Title: Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets
Author:  J. K. Rowling

^^^article

## Chapter 1

The Worst Birthday
Not for the first time, an argument had broken out over breakfast at number four, Privet Drive. Mr. Vernon DursВӯley had been woken in the early hours of the morning by a loud, hooting noise from his nephew HarryвҖҷs room.
вҖңThird time this week!вҖқ he roared across the table. вҖңIf you canвҖҷt control that owl, itвҖҷll have to go!вҖқ
Harry tried, yet again, to explain.
вҖңSheвҖҷs bored,вҖқ he said. вҖңSheвҖҷs used to flying around outside. If I could just let her out at night вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңDo I look stupid?вҖқ snarled Uncle Vernon, a bit of fried egg danВӯgling from his bushy mustache. вҖңI know whatвҖҷll happen if that owlвҖҷs let out.вҖқ
He exchanged dark looks with his wife, Petunia.
Harry tried to argue back but his words were drowned by a long, loud belch from the DursleysвҖҷ son, Dudley.
вҖңI want more bacon.вҖқ
вҖңThereвҖҷs more in the frying pan, sweetums,вҖқ said Aunt Petunia, turning misty eyes on her massive son. вҖңWe must build you up while weвҖҷve got the chance. вҖҰ I donвҖҷt like the sound of that school food. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңNonsense, Petunia, I never went hungry when I was at SmeltВӯings,вҖқ said Uncle Vernon heartily. вҖңDudley gets enough, donвҖҷt you, son?вҖқ
Dudley, who was so large his bottom drooped over either side of the kitchen chair, grinned and turned to Harry.
вҖңPass the frying pan.вҖқ
вҖңYouвҖҷve forgotten the magic word,вҖқ said Harry irritably.
The effect of this simple sentence on the rest of the family was incredible: Dudley gasped and fell off his chair with a crash that shook the whole kitchen; Mrs. Dursley gave a small scream and clapped her hands to her mouth; Mr. Dursley jumped to his feet, veins throbbing in his temples.
вҖңI meant вҖҳpleaseвҖҷ!вҖқ said Harry quickly. вҖңI didnвҖҷt mean вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWHAT HAVE I TOLD YOU,вҖқ thundered his uncle, spraying spit over the table, вҖңABOUT SAYING THE вҖҳMвҖҷ WORD IN OUR HOUSE?вҖқ
вҖңBut I вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHOW DARE YOU THREATEN DUDLEY!вҖқ roared Uncle Vernon, pounding the table with his fist.
вҖңI just вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI WARNED YOU! I WILL NOT TOLERATE MENTION OF YOUR ABNORMALITY UNDER THIS ROOF!вҖқ
Harry stared from his purple-faced uncle to his pale aunt, who was trying to heave Dudley to his feet.
вҖңAll right,вҖқ said Harry, вҖңall right вҖҰвҖқ
Uncle Vernon sat back down, breathing like a winded rhinoceros and watching Harry closely out of the corners of his small, sharp eyes.
Ever since Harry had come home for the summer holidays, UnВӯcle Vernon had been treating him like a bomb that might go off at any moment, because Harry Potter wasnвҖҷt a normal boy. As a matВӯter of fact, he was as not normal as it is possible to be.
Harry Potter was a wizard вҖ” a wizard fresh from his first year at Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry. And if the Dursleys were unhappy to have him back for the holidays, it was nothing to how Harry felt.
He missed Hogwarts so much it was like having a constant stomachache. He missed the castle, with its secret passageways and ghosts, his classes (though perhaps not Snape, the Potions master), the mail arriving by owl, eating banquets in the Great Hall, sleepВӯing in his four-poster bed in the tower dormitory, visiting the gamekeeper, Hagrid, in his cabin next to the Forbidden Forest in the grounds, and, especially, Quidditch, the most popular sport in the wizarding world (six tall goal posts, four flying balls, and fourВӯteen players on broomsticks).
All HarryвҖҷs spellbooks, his wand, robes, cauldron, and top-of-the-line Nimbus Two Thousand broomstick had been locked in a cupboard under the stairs by Uncle Vernon the instant Harry had come home. What did the Dursleys care if Harry lost his place on the House Quidditch team because he hadnвҖҷt practiced all sumВӯmer? What was it to the Dursleys if Harry went back to school without any of his homework done? The Dursleys were what wizВӯards called Muggles (not a drop of magical blood in their veins), and as far as they were concerned, having a wizard in the family was a matter of deepest shame. Uncle Vernon had even padlocked HarryвҖҷs owl, Hedwig, inside her cage, to stop her from carrying messages to anyone in the wizarding world.
Harry looked nothing like the rest of the family. Uncle Vernon was large and neckless, with an enormous black mustache; Aunt Petunia was horse-faced and bony; Dudley was blond, pink, and porky. Harry, on the other hand, was small and skinny, with brilВӯliant green eyes and jet-black hair that was always untidy. He wore round glasses, and on his forehead was a thin, lightning-shaped scar.
It was this scar that made Harry so particularly unusual, even for a wizard. This scar was the only hint of HarryвҖҷs very mysterious past, of the reason he had been left on the DursleysвҖҷ doorstep eleven years before.
At the age of one year old, Harry had somehow survived a curse from the greatest Dark sorcerer of all time, Lord Voldemort, whose name most witches and wizards still feared to speak. HarryвҖҷs parВӯents had died in VoldemortвҖҷs attack, but Harry had escaped with his lightning scar, and somehow вҖ” nobody understood why вҖ” VoldemortвҖҷs powers had been destroyed the instant he had failed to kill Harry.
So Harry had been brought up by his dead motherвҖҷs sister and her husband. He had spent ten years with the Dursleys, never unВӯderstanding why he kept making odd things happen without meaning to, believing the DursleysвҖҷ story that he had got his scar in the car crash that had killed his parents.
And then, exactly a year ago, Hogwarts had written to Harry, and the whole story had come out. Harry had taken up his place at wizard school, where he and his scar were famous вҖҰ but now the school year was over, and he was back with the Dursleys for the summer, back to being treated like a dog that had rolled in someВӯthing smelly.
The Dursleys hadnвҖҷt even remembered that today happened to be HarryвҖҷs twelfth birthday. Of course, his hopes hadnвҖҷt been high; theyвҖҷd never given him a real present, let alone a cake вҖ” but to igВӯnore it completely вҖҰ
At that moment, Uncle Vernon cleared his throat importantly and said, вҖңNow, as we all know, today is a very important day.вҖқ
Harry looked up, hardly daring to believe it.
вҖңThis could well be the day I make the biggest deal of my caВӯreer,вҖқ said Uncle Vernon.
Harry went back to his toast. Of course, he thought bitterly, UnВӯcle Vernon was talking about the stupid dinner party. HeвҖҷd been talkВӯing of nothing else for two weeks. Some rich builder and his wife were coming to dinner and Uncle Vernon was hoping to get a huge order from him (Uncle VernonвҖҷs company made drills).
вҖңI think we should run through the schedule one more time,вҖқ said Uncle Vernon. вҖңWe should all be in position at eight oвҖҷclock. Petunia, you will be вҖ” ?вҖқ
вҖңIn the lounge,вҖқ said Aunt Petunia promptly, вҖңwaiting to welВӯcome them graciously to our home.вҖқ
вҖңGood, good. And Dudley?вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷll be waiting to open the door.вҖқ Dudley put on a foul, simВӯpering smile. вҖңMay I take your coats, Mr. and Mrs. Mason?вҖқ
вҖңTheyвҖҷll love him!вҖқ cried Aunt Petunia rapturously.
вҖңExcellent, Dudley,вҖқ said Uncle Vernon. Then he rounded on Harry. вҖңAnd you?вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷll be in my bedroom, making no noise and pretending IвҖҷm not there,вҖқ said Harry tonelessly.
вҖңExactly,вҖқ said Uncle Vernon nastily. вҖңI will lead them into the lounge, introduce you, Petunia, and pour them drinks. At eight-fifteen вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷll announce dinner,вҖқ said Aunt Petunia.
вҖңAnd, Dudley, youвҖҷll say вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңMay I take you through to the dining room, Mrs. Mason?вҖқ said Dudley, offering his fat arm to an invisible woman.
вҖңMy perfect little gentleman!вҖқ sniffed Aunt Petunia.
вҖңAnd you?вҖқ said Uncle Vernon viciously to Harry.
вҖңIвҖҷll be in my room, making no noise and pretending IвҖҷm not there,вҖқ said Harry dully.
вҖңPrecisely. Now, we should aim to get in a few good compliВӯments at dinner. Petunia, any ideas?вҖқ
вҖңVernon tells me youвҖҷre a wonderful golfer, Mr. Mason. вҖҰ Do tell me where you bought your dress, Mrs. Mason. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңPerfect вҖҰ Dudley?вҖқ
вҖңHow about вҖ” вҖҳWe had to write an essay about our hero at school, Mr. Mason, and I wrote about you.вҖҷ вҖқ
This was too much for both Aunt Petunia and Harry. Aunt PetuВӯnia burst into tears and hugged her son, while Harry ducked under the table so they wouldnвҖҷt see him laughing.
вҖңAnd you, boy?вҖқ
Harry fought to keep his face straight as he emerged.
вҖңIвҖҷll be in my room, making no noise and pretending IвҖҷm not there,вҖқ he said.
вҖңToo right, you will,вҖқ said Uncle Vernon forcefully. вҖңThe MaВӯsons donвҖҷt know anything about you and itвҖҷs going to stay that way. When dinnerвҖҷs over, you take Mrs. Mason back to the lounge for coffee, Petunia, and IвҖҷll bring the subject around to drills. With any luck, IвҖҷll have the deal signed and sealed before the news at ten. WeвҖҷll be shopping for a vacation home in Majorca this time toВӯmorrow.вҖқ
Harry couldnвҖҷt feel too excited about this. He didnвҖҷt think the Dursleys would like him any better in Majorca than they did on Privet Drive.
вҖңRight вҖ” IвҖҷm off into town to pick up the dinner jackets for Dudley and me. And you,вҖқ he snarled at Harry. вҖңYou stay out of your auntвҖҷs way while sheвҖҷs cleaning.вҖқ
Harry left through the back door. It was a brilliant, sunny day. He crossed the lawn, slumped down on the garden bench, and sang under his breath:
вҖңHappy birthday to me вҖҰ happy birthday to me вҖҰвҖқ
No cards, no presents, and he would be spending the evening pretending not to exist. He gazed miserably into the hedge. He had never felt so lonely. More than anything else at Hogwarts, more even than playing Quidditch, Harry missed his best friends, Ron Weasley and Hermione Granger. They, however, didnвҖҷt seem to be missing him at all. Neither of them had written to him all summer, even though Ron had said he was going to ask Harry to come and stay.
Countless times, Harry had been on the point of unlocking HedwigвҖҷs cage by magic and sending her to Ron and Hermione with a letter, but it wasnвҖҷt worth the risk. Underage wizards werenвҖҷt allowed to use magic outside of school. Harry hadnвҖҷt told the Dursleys this; he knew it was only their terror that he might turn them all into dung beetles that stopped them from locking him in the cupboard under the stairs with his wand and broomstick. For the first couple of weeks back, Harry had enjoyed muttering nonВӯsense words under his breath and watching Dudley tearing out of the room as fast as his fat legs would carry him. But the long silence from Ron and Hermione had made Harry feel so cut off from the magical world that even taunting Dudley had lost its appeal вҖ” and now Ron and Hermione had forgotten his birthday.
What wouldnвҖҷt he give now for a message from Hogwarts? From any witch or wizard? HeвҖҷd almost be glad of a sight of his archВӯenemy, Draco Malfoy, just to be sure it hadnвҖҷt all been a dream. вҖҰ
Not that his whole year at Hogwarts had been fun. At the very end of last term, Harry had come face-to-face with none other than Lord Voldemort himself. Voldemort might be a ruin of his former self, but he was still terrifying, still cunning, still determined to reВӯgain power. Harry had slipped through VoldemortвҖҷs clutches for a second time, but it had been a narrow escape, and even now, weeks later, Harry kept waking in the night, drenched in cold sweat, wonВӯdering where Voldemort was now, remembering his livid face, his wide, mad eyes вҖ”
Harry suddenly sat bolt upright on the garden bench. He had been staring absent-mindedly into the hedge вҖ” and the hedge was staring back. Two enormous green eyes had appeared among the leaves.
Harry jumped to his feet just as a jeering voice floated across the lawn.
вҖңI know what day it is,вҖқ sang Dudley, waddling toward him.
The huge eyes blinked and vanished.
вҖңWhat?вҖқ said Harry, not taking his eyes off the spot where they had been.
вҖңI know what day it is,вҖқ Dudley repeated, coming right up to him.
вҖңWell done,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңSo youвҖҷve finally learned the days of the week.вҖқ
вҖңTodayвҖҷs your birthday,вҖқ sneered Dudley. вҖңHow come you havenвҖҷt got any cards? HavenвҖҷt you even got friends at that freak place?вҖқ
вҖңBetter not let your mum hear you talking about my school,вҖқ said Harry coolly.
Dudley hitched up his trousers, which were slipping down his fat bottom.
вҖңWhyвҖҷre you staring at the hedge?вҖқ he said suspiciously.
вҖңIвҖҷm trying to decide what would be the best spell to set it on fire,вҖқ said Harry.
Dudley stumbled backward at once, a look of panic on his fat face.
вҖңYou c-canвҖҷt вҖ” Dad told you youвҖҷre not to do m-magic вҖ” he said heвҖҷll chuck you out of the house вҖ” and you havenвҖҷt got anyВӯwhere else to go вҖ” you havenвҖҷt got any friends to take you вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңJiggery pokery!вҖқ said Harry in a fierce voice. вҖңHocus pocus вҖ” squiggly wiggly вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңMUUUUUUM!вҖқ howled Dudley, tripping over his feet as he dashed back toward the house. вҖңMUUUUM! HeвҖҷs doing you know what!вҖқ
Harry paid dearly for his moment of fun. As neither Dudley nor the hedge was in any way hurt, Aunt Petunia knew he hadnвҖҷt really done magic, but he still had to duck as she aimed a heavy blow at his head with the soapy frying pan. Then she gave him work to do, with the promise he wouldnвҖҷt eat again until heвҖҷd finished.
While Dudley lolled around watching and eating ice cream, Harry cleaned the windows, washed the car, mowed the lawn, trimmed the flowerbeds, pruned and watered the roses, and reВӯpainted the garden bench. The sun blazed overhead, burning the back of his neck. Harry knew he shouldnвҖҷt have risen to DudleyвҖҷs bait, but Dudley had said the very thing Harry had been thinking himself вҖҰ maybe he didnвҖҷt have any friends at Hogwarts. вҖҰ
Wish they could see famous Harry Potter now, he thought savagely as he spread manure on the flower beds, his back aching, sweat runВӯning down his face.
It was half past seven in the evening when at last, exhausted, he heard Aunt Petunia calling him.
вҖңGet in here! And walk on the newspaper!вҖқ
Harry moved gladly into the shade of the gleaming kitchen. On top of the fridge stood tonightвҖҷs pudding: a huge mound of whipped cream and sugared violets. A loin of roast pork was sizВӯzling in the oven.
вҖңEat quickly! The Masons will be here soon!вҖқ snapped Aunt Petunia, pointing to two slices of bread and a lump of cheese on the kitchen table. She was already wearing a salmon-pink cocktail dress.
Harry washed his hands and bolted down his pitiful supper. The moment he had finished, Aunt Petunia whisked away his plate. вҖңUpstairs! Hurry!вҖқ
As he passed the door to the living room, Harry caught a glimpse of Uncle Vernon and Dudley in bow ties and dinner jackВӯets. He had only just reached the upstairs landing when the doorВӯbell rang and Uncle VernonвҖҷs furious face appeared at the foot of the stairs.
вҖңRemember, boy вҖ” one sound вҖ”вҖқ
Harry crossed to his bedroom on tiptoe, slipped inside, closed the door, and turned to collapse on his bed.
The trouble was, there was already someone sitting on it.
## Chapter 2

Dobby's Warning
Harry managed not to shout out, but it was a close thing. The little creature on the bed had large, bat-like ears and bulging green eyes the size of tennis balls. Harry knew instantly that this was what had been watching him out of the garden hedge that morning.
As they stared at each other, Harry heard DudleyвҖҷs voice from the hall.
вҖңMay I take your coats, Mr. and Mrs. Mason?вҖқ
The creature slipped off the bed and bowed so low that the end of its long, thin nose touched the carpet. Harry noticed that it was wearing what looked like an old pillowcase, with rips for arm- and leg-holes.
вҖңEr вҖ” hello,вҖқ said Harry nervously.
вҖңHarry Potter!вҖқ said the creature in a high-pitched voice Harry was sure would carry down the stairs. вҖңSo long has Dobby wanted to meet you, sir вҖҰ Such an honor it is. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңTh-thank you,вҖқ said Harry, edging along the wall and sinking into his desk chair, next to Hedwig, who was asleep in her large cage. He wanted to ask, вҖңWhat are you?вҖқ but thought it would sound too rude, so instead he said, вҖңWho are you?вҖқ
вҖңDobby, sir. Just Dobby. Dobby the house-elf,вҖқ said the creaВӯture.
вҖңOh вҖ” really?вҖқ said Harry. вҖңEr вҖ” I donвҖҷt want to be rude or anything, but вҖ” this isnвҖҷt a great time for me to have a house-elf in my bedroom.вҖқ
Aunt PetuniaвҖҷs high, false laugh sounded from the living room. The elf hung his head.
вҖңNot that IвҖҷm not pleased to meet you,вҖқ said Harry quickly, вҖңbut, er, is there any particular reason youвҖҷre here?вҖқ
вҖңOh, yes, sir,вҖқ said Dobby earnestly. вҖңDobby has come to tell you, sir вҖҰ it is difficult, sir вҖҰ Dobby wonders where to beВӯgin. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңSit down,вҖқ said Harry politely, pointing at the bed.
To his horror, the elf burst into tears вҖ” very noisy tears.
вҖңS-sit down!вҖқ he wailed. вҖңNever вҖҰ never ever вҖҰвҖқ
Harry thought he heard the voices downstairs falter.
вҖңIвҖҷm sorry,вҖқ he whispered, вҖңI didnвҖҷt mean to offend you or anyВӯthing вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңOffend Dobby!вҖқ choked the elf. вҖңDobby has never been asked to sit down by a wizard вҖ” like an equal вҖ”вҖқ
Harry, trying to say вҖңShh!вҖқ and look comforting at the same time, ushered Dobby back onto the bed where he sat hiccoughing, looking like a large and very ugly doll. At last he managed to conВӯtrol himself, and sat with his great eyes fixed on Harry in an exВӯpression of watery adoration.
вҖңYou canвҖҷt have met many decent wizards,вҖқ said Harry, trying to cheer him up.
Dobby shook his head. Then, without warning, he leapt up and started banging his head furiously on the window, shouting, вҖңBad Dobby! Bad Dobby!вҖқ
вҖңDonвҖҷt вҖ” what are you doing?вҖқ Harry hissed, springing up and pulling Dobby back onto the bed вҖ” Hedwig had woken up with a particularly loud screech and was beating her wings wildly against the bars of her cage.
вҖңDobby had to punish himself, sir,вҖқ said the elf, who had gone slightly cross-eyed. вҖңDobby almost spoke ill of his family, sir. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңYour family?вҖқ
вҖңThe wizard family Dobby serves, sir. вҖҰ Dobby is a house-elf вҖ” bound to serve one house and one family forever. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңDo they know youвҖҷre here?вҖқ asked Harry curiously.
Dobby shuddered.
вҖңOh, no, sir, no вҖҰ Dobby will have to punish himself most grievously for coming to see you, sir. Dobby will have to shut his ears in the oven door for this. If they ever knew, sir вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBut wonвҖҷt they notice if you shut your ears in the oven door?вҖқ
вҖңDobby doubts it, sir. Dobby is always having to punish himself for something, sir. They lets Dobby get on with it, sir. Sometimes they reminds me to do extra punishments. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңBut why donвҖҷt you leave? Escape?вҖқ
вҖңA house-elf must be set free, sir. And the family will never set Dobby free вҖҰ Dobby will serve the family until he dies, sir. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry stared.
вҖңAnd I thought I had it bad staying here for another four weeks,вҖқ he said. вҖңThis makes the Dursleys sound almost human. CanвҖҷt anyВӯone help you? CanвҖҷt I?вҖқ
Almost at once, Harry wished he hadnвҖҷt spoken. Dobby disВӯsolved again into wails of gratitude.
вҖңPlease,вҖқ Harry whispered frantically, вҖңplease be quiet. If the Dursleys hear anything, if they know youвҖҷre here вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHarry Potter asks if he can help Dobby вҖҰ Dobby has heard of your greatness, sir, but of your goodness, Dobby never knew. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry, who was feeling distinctly hot in the face, said, вҖңWhatВӯever youвҖҷve heard about my greatness is a load of rubbish. IвҖҷm not even top of my year at Hogwarts; thatвҖҷs Hermione, she вҖ”вҖқ
But he stopped quickly, because thinking about Hermione was painful.
вҖңHarry Potter is humble and modest,вҖқ said Dobby reverently, his orb-like eyes aglow. вҖңHarry Potter speaks not of his triumph over He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңVoldemort?вҖқ said Harry.
Dobby clapped his hands over his bat ears and moaned, вҖңAh, speak not the name, sir! Speak not the name!вҖқ
вҖңSorry,вҖқ said Harry quickly. вҖңI know lots of people donвҖҷt like it. My friend Ron вҖ”вҖқ
He stopped again. Thinking about Ron was painful, too.
Dobby leaned toward Harry, his eyes wide as headlights.
вҖңDobby heard tell,вҖқ he said hoarsely, вҖңthat Harry Potter met the Dark Lord for a second time, just weeks ago вҖҰ that Harry Potter escaped yet again.вҖқ
Harry nodded and DobbyвҖҷs eyes suddenly shone with tears.
вҖңAh, sir,вҖқ he gasped, dabbing his face with a corner of the grubby pillowcase he was wearing. вҖңHarry Potter is valiant and bold! He has braved so many dangers already! But Dobby has come to proВӯtect Harry Potter, to warn him, even if he does have to shut his ears in the oven door later. вҖҰ Harry Potter must not go back to Hogwarts.вҖқ
There was a silence broken only by the chink of knives and forks from downstairs and the distant rumble of Uncle VernonвҖҷs voice.
вҖңW-what?вҖқ Harry stammered. вҖңBut IвҖҷve got to go back вҖ” term starts on September first. ItвҖҷs all thatвҖҷs keeping me going. You donвҖҷt know what itвҖҷs like here. I donвҖҷt belong here. I belong in your world вҖ” at Hogwarts.вҖқ
вҖңNo, no, no,вҖқ squeaked Dobby, shaking his head so hard his ears flapped. вҖңHarry Potter must stay where he is safe. He is too great, too good, to lose. If Harry Potter goes back to Hogwarts, he will be in mortal danger.вҖқ
вҖңWhy?вҖқ said Harry in surprise.
вҖңThere is a plot, Harry Potter. A plot to make most terrible things happen at Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry this year,вҖқ whispered Dobby, suddenly trembling all over. вҖңDobby has known it for months, sir. Harry Potter must not put himself in peril. He is too important, sir!вҖқ
вҖңWhat terrible things?вҖқ said Harry at once. вҖңWhoвҖҷs plotting them?вҖқ
Dobby made a funny choking noise and then banged his head frantically against the wall.
вҖңAll right!вҖқ cried Harry, grabbing the elfвҖҷs arm to stop him. вҖңYou canвҖҷt tell me. I understand. But why are you warning me?вҖқ A sudВӯden, unpleasant thought struck him. вҖңHang on вҖ” this hasnвҖҷt got anything to do with Vol вҖ” sorry вҖ” with You-Know-Who, has it? You could just shake or nod,вҖқ he added hastily as DobbyвҖҷs head tilted worryingly close to the wall again.
Slowly, Dobby shook his head.
вҖңNot вҖ” not He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named, sir вҖ”вҖқ
But DobbyвҖҷs eyes were wide and he seemed to be trying to give Harry a hint. Harry, however, was completely lost.
вҖңHe hasnвҖҷt got a brother, has he?вҖқ
Dobby shook his head, his eyes wider than ever.
вҖңWell then, I canвҖҷt think who else would have a chance of makВӯing horrible things happen at Hogwarts,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңI mean, thereвҖҷs Dumbledore, for one thing вҖ” you know who Dumbledore is, donвҖҷt you?вҖқ
Dobby bowed his head.
вҖңAlbus Dumbledore is the greatest headmaster Hogwarts has ever had. Dobby knows it, sir. Dobby has heard DumbledoreвҖҷs powers rival those of He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named at the height of his strength. But, sirвҖқ вҖ” DobbyвҖҷs voice dropped to an urgent whisper вҖ” вҖңthere are powers Dumbledore doesnвҖҷt вҖҰ powers no decent wizard вҖҰвҖқ
And before Harry could stop him, Dobby bounded off the bed, seized HarryвҖҷs desk lamp, and started beating himself around the head with earsplitting yelps.
A sudden silence fell downstairs. Two seconds later Harry, heart thudding madly, heard Uncle Vernon coming into the hall, calling, вҖңDudley must have left his television on again, the little tyke!вҖқ
вҖңQuick! In the closet!вҖқ hissed Harry, stuffing Dobby in, shutting the door, and flinging himself onto the bed just as the door handle turned.
вҖңWhat вҖ” the вҖ” devil вҖ” are вҖ” you вҖ” doing?вҖқ said Uncle VerВӯnon through gritted teeth, his face horribly close to HarryвҖҷs. вҖңYouвҖҷve just ruined the punch line of my Japanese golfer joke. вҖҰ One more sound and youвҖҷll wish youвҖҷd never been born, boy!вҖқ
He stomped flat-footed from the room.
Shaking, Harry let Dobby out of the closet.
вҖңSee what itвҖҷs like here?вҖқ he said. вҖңSee why IвҖҷve got to go back to Hogwarts? ItвҖҷs the only place IвҖҷve got вҖ” well, I think IвҖҷve got friends.вҖқ
вҖңFriends who donвҖҷt even write to Harry Potter?вҖқ said Dobby slyly.
вҖңI expect theyвҖҷve just been вҖ” wait a minute,вҖқ said Harry, frownВӯing. вҖңHow do you know my friends havenвҖҷt been writing to me?вҖқ
Dobby shuffled his feet.
вҖңHarry Potter mustnвҖҷt be angry with Dobby. Dobby did it for the best вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHave you been stopping my letters?вҖқ
вҖңDobby has them here, sir,вҖқ said the elf. Stepping nimbly out of HarryвҖҷs reach, he pulled a thick wad of envelopes from the inside of the pillowcase he was wearing. Harry could make out HermioneвҖҷs neat writing, RonвҖҷs untidy scrawl, and even a scribble that looked as though it was from the Hogwarts gamekeeper, Hagrid.
Dobby blinked anxiously up at Harry.
вҖңHarry Potter mustnвҖҷt be angry. вҖҰ Dobby hoped вҖҰ if Harry Potter thought his friends had forgotten him вҖҰ Harry Potter might not want to go back to school, sir. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry wasnвҖҷt listening. He made a grab for the letters, but Dobby jumped out of reach.
вҖңHarry Potter will have them, sir, if he gives Dobby his word that he will not return to Hogwarts. Ah, sir, this is a danger you must not face! Say you wonвҖҷt go back, sir!вҖқ
вҖңNo,вҖқ said Harry angrily. вҖңGive me my friendsвҖҷ letters!вҖқ
вҖңThen Harry Potter leaves Dobby no choice,вҖқ said the elf sadly.
Before Harry could move, Dobby had darted to the bedroom door, pulled it open, and sprinted down the stairs.
Mouth dry, stomach lurching, Harry sprang after him, trying not to make a sound. He jumped the last six steps, landing catlike on the hall carpet, looking around for Dobby. From the dining room he heard Uncle Vernon saying, вҖңвҖҰ tell Petunia that very funny story about those American plumbers, Mr. Mason. SheвҖҷs been dying to hear вҖҰвҖқ
Harry ran up the hall into the kitchen and felt his stomach disВӯappear.
Aunt PetuniaвҖҷs masterpiece of a pudding, the mountain of cream and sugared violets, was floating up near the ceiling. On top of a cupboard in the corner crouched Dobby.
вҖңNo,вҖқ croaked Harry. вҖңPlease вҖҰ theyвҖҷll kill me. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңHarry Potter must say heвҖҷs not going back to school вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңDobby вҖҰ please вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңSay it, sir вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI canвҖҷt вҖ”вҖқ
Dobby gave him a tragic look.
вҖңThen Dobby must do it, sir, for Harry PotterвҖҷs own good.вҖқ
The pudding fell to the floor with a heart-stopping crash. Cream splattered the windows and walls as the dish shattered. With a crack like a whip, Dobby vanished.
There were screams from the dining room and Uncle Vernon burst into the kitchen to find Harry, rigid with shock, covered from head to foot in Aunt PetuniaвҖҷs pudding.
At first, it looked as though Uncle Vernon would manage to gloss the whole thing over. (вҖңJust our nephew вҖ” very disturbed вҖ” meeting strangers upsets him, so we kept him upstairs. вҖҰвҖқ) He shooed the shocked Masons back into the dining room, promised Harry he would flay him to within an inch of his life when the MaВӯsons had left, and handed him a mop. Aunt Petunia dug some ice cream out of the freezer and Harry, still shaking, started scrubbing the kitchen clean.
Uncle Vernon might still have been able to make his deal вҖ” if it hadnвҖҷt been for the owl.
Aunt Petunia was just passing around a box of after-dinner mints when a huge barn owl swooped through the dining room window, dropped a letter on Mrs. MasonвҖҷs head, and swooped out again. Mrs. Mason screamed like a banshee and ran from the house shouting about lunatics. Mr. Mason stayed just long enough to tell the Dursleys that his wife was mortally afraid of birds of all shapes and sizes, and to ask whether this was their idea of a joke.
Harry stood in the kitchen, clutching the mop for support, as Uncle Vernon advanced on him, a demonic glint in his tiny eyes.
вҖңRead it!вҖқ he hissed evilly, brandishing the letter the owl had deВӯlivered. вҖңGo on вҖ” read it!вҖқ
Harry took it. It did not contain birthday greetings.
Dear Mr. Potter,
We have received intelligence that a Hover Charm was used at your place of residence this evening at twelve minВӯutes past nine.
As you know, underage wizards are not permitted to perВӯform spells outside school, and further spellwork on your part may lead to expulsion from said school (Decree for the Reasonable Restriction of Underage Sorcery, 1875, ParaВӯgraph C).
We would also ask you to remember that any magical activity that risks notice by members of the non-magical community (Muggles) is a serious offense under section 13 of the International Confederation of WarlocksвҖҷ Statute of Secrecy.
Enjoy your holidays!
Yours sincerely,
Mafalda Hopkirk
IMPROPER USE OF MAGIC OFFICE
Ministry of Magic
Harry looked up from the letter and gulped.
вҖңYou didnвҖҷt tell us you werenвҖҷt allowed to use magic outside school,вҖқ said Uncle Vernon, a mad gleam dancing in his eyes. вҖңForВӯgot to mention it. вҖҰ Slipped your mind, I daresay. вҖҰвҖқ
He was bearing down on Harry like a great bulldog, all his teeth bared. вҖңWell, IвҖҷve got news for you, boy. вҖҰ IвҖҷm locking you up. вҖҰ YouвҖҷre never going back to that school вҖҰ never вҖҰ and if you try and magic yourself out вҖ” theyвҖҷll expel you!вҖқ
And laughing like a maniac, he dragged Harry back upstairs.
Uncle Vernon was as bad as his word. The following morning, he paid a man to fit bars on HarryвҖҷs window. He himself fitted a cat-flap in the bedroom door, so that small amounts of food could be pushed inside three times a day. They let Harry out to use the bathroom morning and evening. Otherwise, he was locked in his room around the clock.
Three days later, the Dursleys were showing no sign of relenting, and Harry couldnвҖҷt see any way out of his situation. He lay on his bed watching the sun sinking behind the bars on the window and wondered miserably what was going to happen to him.
What was the good of magicking himself out of his room if Hogwarts would expel him for doing it? Yet life at Privet Drive had reached an all-time low. Now that the Dursleys knew they werenвҖҷt going to wake up as fruit bats, he had lost his only weapon. Dobby might have saved Harry from horrible happenings at Hogwarts, but the way things were going, heвҖҷd probably starve to death anyВӯway.
The cat-flap rattled and Aunt PetuniaвҖҷs hand appeared, pushing a bowl of canned soup into the room. Harry, whose insides were aching with hunger, jumped off his bed and seized it. The soup was stone-cold, but he drank half of it in one gulp. Then he crossed the room to HedwigвҖҷs cage and tipped the soggy vegetables at the botВӯtom of the bowl into her empty food tray. She ruffled her feathers and gave him a look of deep disgust.
вҖңItвҖҷs no good turning your beak up at it вҖ” thatвҖҷs all weвҖҷve got,вҖқ said Harry grimly.
He put the empty bowl back on the floor next to the cat-flap and lay back down on the bed, somehow even hungrier than he had been before the soup.
Supposing he was still alive in another four weeks, what would happen if he didnвҖҷt turn up at Hogwarts? Would someone be sent to see why he hadnвҖҷt come back? Would they be able to make the Dursleys let him go?
The room was growing dark. Exhausted, stomach rumbling, mind spinning over the same unanswerable questions, Harry fell into an uneasy sleep.
He dreamed that he was on show in a zoo, with a card reading UNDERAGE WIZARD attached to his cage. People goggled through the bars at him as he lay, starving and weak, on a bed of straw. He saw DobbyвҖҷs face in the crowd and shouted out, asking for help, but Dobby called, вҖңHarry Potter is safe there, sir!вҖқ and vanished. Then the Dursleys appeared and Dudley rattled the bars of the cage, laughing at him.
вҖңStop it,вҖқ Harry muttered as the rattling pounded in his sore head. вҖңLeave me alone вҖҰ cut it out вҖҰ IвҖҷm trying to sleep. вҖҰвҖқ
He opened his eyes. Moonlight was shining through the bars on the window. And someone was goggling through the bars at him: a freckle-faced, red-haired, long-nosed someone.
Ron Weasley was outside HarryвҖҷs window.
## Chapter 3

The Burrow
вҖңRon!вҖқ breathed Harry, creeping to the window and pushing it up so they could talk through the bars. вҖңRon, how did you вҖ” What the вҖ” ?вҖқ
HarryвҖҷs mouth fell open as the full impact of what he was seeВӯing hit him. Ron was leaning out of the back window of an old turquoise car, which was parked in midair. Grinning at Harry from the front seats were Fred and George, RonвҖҷs elder twin brothers.
вҖңAll right, Harry?вҖқ asked George.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs been going on?вҖқ said Ron. вҖңWhy havenвҖҷt you been anВӯswering my letters? IвҖҷve asked you to stay about twelve times, and then Dad came home and said youвҖҷd got an official warning for usВӯing magic in front of Muggles вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңIt wasnвҖҷt me вҖ” and how did he know?вҖқ
вҖңHe works for the Ministry,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңYou know weвҖҷre not supВӯposed to do spells outside school вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYou should talk,вҖқ said Harry, staring at the floating car.
вҖңOh, this doesnвҖҷt count,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңWeвҖҷre only borrowing this. ItвҖҷs DadвҖҷs, we didnвҖҷt enchant it. But doing magic in front of those Muggles you live with вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI told you, I didnвҖҷt вҖ” but itвҖҷll take too long to explain now вҖ” look, can you tell them at Hogwarts that the Dursleys have locked me up and wonвҖҷt let me come back, and obviously I canвҖҷt magic myself out, because the MinistryвҖҷll think thatвҖҷs the second spell IвҖҷve done in three days, so вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңStop gibbering,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңWeвҖҷve come to take you home with us.вҖқ
вҖңBut you canвҖҷt magic me out either вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWe donвҖҷt need to,вҖқ said Ron, jerking his head toward the front seat and grinning. вҖңYou forget who IвҖҷve got with me.вҖқ
вҖңTie that around the bars,вҖқ said Fred, throwing the end of a rope to Harry.
вҖңIf the Dursleys wake up, IвҖҷm dead,вҖқ said Harry as he tied the rope tightly around a bar and Fred revved up the car.
вҖңDonвҖҷt worry,вҖқ said Fred, вҖңand stand back.вҖқ
Harry moved back into the shadows next to Hedwig, who seemed to have realized how important this was and kept still and silent. The car revved louder and louder and suddenly, with a crunching noise, the bars were pulled clean out of the window as Fred drove straight up in the air. Harry ran back to the window to see the bars dangling a few feet above the ground. Panting, Ron hoisted them up into the car. Harry listened anxiously, but there was no sound from the DursleysвҖҷ bedroom.
When the bars were safely in the back seat with Ron, Fred reВӯversed as close as possible to HarryвҖҷs window.
вҖңGet in,вҖқ Ron said.
вҖңBut all my Hogwarts stuff вҖ” my wand вҖ” my broomstick вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWhere is it?вҖқ
вҖңLocked in the cupboard under the stairs, and I canвҖҷt get out of this room вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңNo problem,вҖқ said George from the front passenger seat. вҖңOut of the way, Harry.вҖқ
Fred and George climbed catlike through the window into HarryвҖҷs room. You had to hand it to them, thought Harry, as George took an ordinary hairpin from his pocket and started to pick the lock.
вҖңA lot of wizards think itвҖҷs a waste of time, knowing this sort of Muggle trick,вҖқ said Fred, вҖңbut we feel theyвҖҷre skills worth learning, even if they are a bit slow.вҖқ
There was a small click and the door swung open.
вҖңSo вҖ” weвҖҷll get your trunk вҖ” you grab anything you need from your room and hand it out to Ron,вҖқ whispered George.
вҖңWatch out for the bottom stair вҖ” it creaks,вҖқ Harry whispered back as the twins disappeared onto the dark landing.
Harry dashed around his room, collecting his things and passing them out of the window to Ron. Then he went to help Fred and George heave his trunk up the stairs. Harry heard Uncle Vernon cough.
At last, panting, they reached the landing, then carried the trunk through HarryвҖҷs room to the open window. Fred climbed back into the car to pull with Ron, and Harry and George pushed from the bedroom side. Inch by inch, the trunk slid through the window.
Uncle Vernon coughed again.
вҖңA bit more,вҖқ panted Fred, who was pulling from inside the car. вҖңOne good push вҖ”вҖқ
Harry and George threw their shoulders against the trunk and it slid out of the window into the back seat of the car.
вҖңOkay, letвҖҷs go,вҖқ George whispered.
But as Harry climbed onto the windowsill there came a sudden loud screech from behind him, followed immediately by the thunВӯder of Uncle VernonвҖҷs voice.
вҖңTHAT RUDDY OWL!вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷve forgotten Hedwig!вҖқ
Harry tore back across the room as the landing light clicked on вҖ” he snatched up HedwigвҖҷs cage, dashed to the window, and passed it out to Ron. He was scrambling back onto the chest of drawers when Uncle Vernon hammered on the unlocked door вҖ” and it crashed open.
For a split second, Uncle Vernon stood framed in the doorway; then he let out a bellow like an angry bull and dived at Harry, grabbing him by the ankle.
Ron, Fred, and George seized HarryвҖҷs arms and pulled as hard as they could.
вҖңPetunia!вҖқ roared Uncle Vernon. вҖңHeвҖҷs getting away! HEвҖҷS GETTING AWAY!вҖқ
But the Weasleys gave a gigantic tug and HarryвҖҷs leg slid out of Uncle VernonвҖҷs grasp вҖ” Harry was in the car вҖ” heвҖҷd slammed the door shut вҖ”
вҖңPut your foot down, Fred!вҖқ yelled Ron, and the car shot sudВӯdenly toward the moon.
Harry couldnвҖҷt believe it вҖ” he was free. He rolled down the window, the night air whipping his hair, and looked back at the shrinking rooftops of Privet Drive. Uncle Vernon, Aunt PetuВӯnia, and Dudley were all hanging, dumbstruck, out of HarryвҖҷs window.
вҖңSee you next summer!вҖқ Harry yelled.
The Weasleys roared with laughter and Harry settled back in his seat, grinning from ear to ear.
вҖңLet Hedwig out,вҖқ he told Ron. вҖңShe can fly behind us. She hasnвҖҷt had a chance to stretch her wings for ages.вҖқ
George handed the hairpin to Ron and, a moment later, Hedwig soared joyfully out of the window to glide alongside them like a ghost.
вҖңSo вҖ” whatвҖҷs the story, Harry?вҖқ said Ron impatiently. вҖңWhatвҖҷs been happening?вҖқ
Harry told them all about Dobby, the warning heвҖҷd given Harry and the fiasco of the violet pudding. There was a long, shocked siВӯlence when he had finished.
вҖңVery fishy,вҖқ said Fred finally.
вҖңDefinitely dodgy,вҖқ agreed George. вҖңSo he wouldnвҖҷt even tell you whoвҖҷs supposed to be plotting all this stuff?вҖқ
вҖңI donвҖҷt think he could,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңI told you, every time he got close to letting something slip, he started banging his head against the wall.вҖқ
He saw Fred and George look at each other.
вҖңWhat, you think he was lying to me?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңWell,вҖқ said Fred, вҖңput it this way вҖ” house-elves have got powВӯerful magic of their own, but they canвҖҷt usually use it without their masterвҖҷs permission. I reckon old Dobby was sent to stop you coming back to Hogwarts. SomeoneвҖҷs idea of a joke. Can you think of anyone at school with a grudge against you?вҖқ
вҖңYes,вҖқ said Harry and Ron together, instantly.
вҖңDraco Malfoy,вҖқ Harry explained. вҖңHe hates me.вҖқ
вҖңDraco Malfoy?вҖқ said George, turning around. вҖңNot Lucius MalfoyвҖҷs son?вҖқ
вҖңMust be, itвҖҷs not a very common name, is it?вҖқ said Harry. вҖңWhy?вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷve heard Dad talking about him,вҖқ said George. вҖңHe was a big supporter of You-Know-Who.вҖқ
вҖңAnd when You-Know-Who disappeared,вҖқ said Fred, craning around to look at Harry, вҖңLucius Malfoy came back saying heвҖҷd never meant any of it. Load of dung вҖ” Dad reckons he was right in You-Know-WhoвҖҷs inner circle.вҖқ
Harry had heard these rumors about MalfoyвҖҷs family before, and they didnвҖҷt surprise him at all. Malfoy made Dudley Dursley look like a kind, thoughtful, and sensitive boy.
вҖңI donвҖҷt know whether the Malfoys own a house-elf. вҖҰвҖқ said Harry.
вҖңWell, whoever owns him will be an old wizarding family, and theyвҖҷll be rich,вҖқ said Fred.
вҖңYeah, MumвҖҷs always wishing we had a house-elf to do the ironВӯing,вҖқ said George. вҖңBut all weвҖҷve got is a lousy old ghoul in the atВӯtic and gnomes all over the garden. House-elves come with big old manors and castles and places like that; you wouldnвҖҷt catch one in our house. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry was silent. Judging by the fact that Draco Malfoy usually had the best of everything, his family was rolling in wizard gold; he could just see Malfoy strutting around a large manor house. SendВӯing the family servant to stop Harry from going back to Hogwarts also sounded exactly like the sort of thing Malfoy would do. Had Harry been stupid to take Dobby seriously?
вҖңIвҖҷm glad we came to get you, anyway,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңI was getting really worried when you didnвҖҷt answer any of my letters. I thought it was ErrolвҖҷs fault at first вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWhoвҖҷs Errol?вҖқ
вҖңOur owl. HeвҖҷs ancient. It wouldnвҖҷt be the first time heвҖҷd colВӯlapsed on a delivery. So then I tried to borrow Hermes вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWho?вҖқ
вҖңThe owl Mum and Dad bought Percy when he was made preВӯfect,вҖқ said Fred from the front.
вҖңBut Percy wouldnвҖҷt lend him to me,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңSaid he needed him.вҖқ
вҖңPercyвҖҷs been acting very oddly this summer,вҖқ said George, frowning. вҖңAnd he has been sending a lot of letters and spending a load of time shut up in his room. вҖҰ I mean, thereвҖҷs only so many times you can polish a prefect badge. вҖҰ YouвҖҷre driving too far west, Fred,вҖқ he added, pointing at a compass on the dashboard. Fred twiddled the steering wheel.
вҖңSo, does your dad know youвҖҷve got the car?вҖқ said Harry, guessВӯing the answer.
вҖңEr, no,вҖқ said Ron, вҖңhe had to work tonight. Hopefully weвҖҷll be able to get it back in the garage without Mum noticing we flew it.вҖқ
вҖңWhat does your dad do at the Ministry of Magic, anyway?вҖқ
вҖңHe works in the most boring department,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңThe Misuse of Muggle Artifacts Office.вҖқ
вҖңThe what?вҖқ
вҖңItвҖҷs all to do with bewitching things that are Muggle-made, you know, in case they end up back in a Muggle shop or house. Like, last year, some old witch died and her tea set was sold to an anВӯtiques shop. This Muggle woman bought it, took it home, and tried to serve her friends tea in it. It was a nightmare вҖ” Dad was working overtime for weeks.вҖқ
вҖңWhat happened?вҖқ
вҖңThe teapot went berserk and squirted boiling tea all over the place and one man ended up in the hospital with the sugar tongs clamped to his nose. Dad was going frantic вҖ” itвҖҷs only him and an old warlock called Perkins in the office вҖ” and they had to do Memory Charms and all sorts of stuff to cover it up вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBut your dad вҖ” this car вҖ”вҖқ
Fred laughed. вҖңYeah, DadвҖҷs crazy about everything to do with Muggles; our shedвҖҷs full of Muggle stuff. He takes it apart, puts spells on it, and puts it back together again. If he raided our house heвҖҷd have to put himself under arrest. It drives Mum mad.вҖқ
вҖңThatвҖҷs the main road,вҖқ said George, peering down through the windshield. вҖңWeвҖҷll be there in ten minutes. вҖҰ Just as well, itвҖҷs getВӯting light. вҖҰвҖқ
A faint pinkish glow was visible along the horizon to the east.
Fred brought the car lower, and Harry saw a dark patchwork of fields and clumps of trees.
вҖңWeвҖҷre a little way outside the village,вҖқ said George. вҖңOttery St. Catchpole.вҖқ
Lower and lower went the flying car. The edge of a brilliant red sun was now gleaming through the trees.
вҖңTouchdown!вҖқ said Fred as, with a slight bump, they hit the ground. They had landed next to a tumbledown garage in a small yard, and Harry looked out for the first time at RonвҖҷs house.
It looked as though it had once been a large stone pigpen, but extra rooms had been added here and there until it was several stoВӯries high and so crooked it looked as though it were held up by magic (which, Harry reminded himself, it probably was). Four or five chimneys were perched on top of the red roof. A lopsided sign stuck in the ground near the entrance read, THE BURROW. Around the front door lay a jumble of rubber boots and a very rusty caulВӯdron. Several fat brown chickens were pecking their way around the yard.
вҖңItвҖҷs not much,вҖқ said Ron.
вҖңItвҖҷs wonderful,вҖқ said Harry happily, thinking of Privet Drive.
They got out of the car.
вҖңNow, weвҖҷll go upstairs really quietly,вҖқ said Fred, вҖңand wait for Mum to call us for breakfast. Then, Ron, you come bounding downstairs going, вҖҳMum, look who turned up in the night!вҖҷ and sheвҖҷll be all pleased to see Harry and no one need ever know we flew the car.вҖқ
вҖңRight,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңCome on, Harry, I sleep at the вҖ” at the top вҖ”вҖқ
Ron had gone a nasty greenish color, his eyes fixed on the house. The other three wheeled around.
Mrs. Weasley was marching across the yard, scattering chickens, and for a short, plump, kind-faced woman, it was remarkable how much she looked like a saber-toothed tiger.
вҖңAh,вҖқ said Fred.
вҖңOh, dear,вҖқ said George.
Mrs. Weasley came to a halt in front of them, her hands on her hips, staring from one guilty face to the next. She was wearing a flowered apron with a wand sticking out of the pocket.
вҖңSo,вҖқ she said.
вҖң вҖҷMorning, Mum,вҖқ said George, in what he clearly thought was a jaunty, winning voice.
вҖңHave you any idea how worried IвҖҷve been?вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley in a deadly whisper.
вҖңSorry, Mum, but see, we had to вҖ”вҖқ
All three of Mrs. WeasleyвҖҷs sons were taller than she was, but they cowered as her rage broke over them.
вҖңBeds empty! No note! Car gone вҖ” could have crashed вҖ” out of my mind with worry вҖ” did you care? вҖ” never, as long as IвҖҷve lived вҖ” you wait until your father gets home, we never had trouble like this from Bill or Charlie or Percy вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңPerfect Percy,вҖқ muttered Fred.
вҖңYOU COULD DO WITH TAKING A LEAF OUT OF PERCYвҖҷS BOOK!вҖқ yelled Mrs. Weasley, prodding a finger in FredвҖҷs chest. вҖңYou could have died, you could have been seen, you could have lost your father his job вҖ”вҖқ
It seemed to go on for hours. Mrs. Weasley had shouted herself hoarse before she turned on Harry, who backed away.
вҖңIвҖҷm very pleased to see you, Harry, dear,вҖқ she said. вҖңCome in and have some breakfast.вҖқ
She turned and walked back into the house and Harry, after a nervous glance at Ron, who nodded encouragingly, followed her.
The kitchen was small and rather cramped. There was a scrubbed wooden table and chairs in the middle, and Harry sat down on the edge of his seat, looking around. He had never been in a wizard house before.
The clock on the wall opposite him had only one hand and no numbers at all. Written around the edge were things like Time to make tea, Time to feed the chickens, and YouвҖҷre late. Books were stacked three deep on the mantelpiece, books with titles like Charm Your Own Cheese, Enchantment in Baking, and One Minute Feasts вҖ” ItвҖҷs Magic! And unless HarryвҖҷs ears were deceiving him, the old radio next to the sink had just announced that coming up was вҖңWitching Hour, with the popular singing sorceress, Celestina Warbeck.вҖқ
Mrs. Weasley was clattering around, cooking breakfast a little haphazardly, throwing dirty looks at her sons as she threw sausages into the frying pan. Every now and then she muttered things like вҖңdonвҖҷt know what you were thinking of,вҖқ and вҖңnever would have believed it.вҖқ
вҖңI donвҖҷt blame you, dear,вҖқ she assured Harry, tipping eight or nine sausages onto his plate. вҖңArthur and I have been worried about you, too. Just last night we were saying weвҖҷd come and get you ourВӯselves if you hadnвҖҷt written back to Ron by Friday. But reallyвҖқ (she was now adding three fried eggs to his plate), вҖңflying an illegal car halfway across the country вҖ” anyone could have seen you вҖ”вҖқ
She flicked her wand casually at the dishes in the sink, which beВӯgan to clean themselves, clinking gently in the background.
вҖңIt was cloudy, Mum!вҖқ said Fred.
вҖңYou keep your mouth closed while youвҖҷre eating!вҖқ Mrs. Weasley snapped.
вҖңThey were starving him, Mum!вҖқ said George.
вҖңAnd you!вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley, but it was with a slightly softened expression that she started cutting Harry bread and buttering it for him.
At that moment there was a diversion in the form of a small, redВӯheaded figure in a long nightdress, who appeared in the kitchen, gave a small squeal, and ran out again.
вҖңGinny,вҖқ said Ron in an undertone to Harry. вҖңMy sister. SheвҖҷs been talking about you all summer.вҖқ
вҖңYeah, sheвҖҷll be wanting your autograph, Harry,вҖқ Fred said with a grin, but he caught his motherвҖҷs eye and bent his face over his plate without another word. Nothing more was said until all four plates were clean, which took a surprisingly short time.
вҖңBlimey, IвҖҷm tired,вҖқ yawned Fred, setting down his knife and fork at last. вҖңI think IвҖҷll go to bed and вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYou will not,вҖқ snapped Mrs. Weasley. вҖңItвҖҷs your own fault youвҖҷve been up all night. YouвҖҷre going to de-gnome the garden for me; theyвҖҷre getting completely out of hand again вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңOh, Mum вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңAnd you two,вҖқ she said, glaring at Ron and Fred. вҖңYou can go up to bed, dear,вҖқ she added to Harry. вҖңYou didnвҖҷt ask them to fly that wretched car вҖ”вҖқ
But Harry, who felt wide awake, said quickly, вҖңIвҖҷll help Ron. IвҖҷve never seen a de-gnoming вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThatвҖҷs very sweet of you, dear, but itвҖҷs dull work,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley. вҖңNow, letвҖҷs see what LockhartвҖҷs got to say on the subject вҖ”вҖқ
And she pulled a heavy book from the stack on the mantelpiece. George groaned.
вҖңMum, we know how to de-gnome a garden вҖ”вҖқ
Harry looked at the cover of Mrs. WeasleyвҖҷs book. Written across it in fancy gold letters were the words Gilderoy LockhartвҖҷs Guide to Household Pests. There was a big photograph on the front of a very good-looking wizard with wavy blond hair and bright blue eyes. As always in the wizarding world, the photograph was moving; the wizard, who Harry supposed was Gilderoy Lockhart, kept winking cheekily up at them all. Mrs. Weasley beamed down at him.
вҖңOh, he is marvelous,вҖқ she said. вҖңHe knows his household pests, all right, itвҖҷs a wonderful book. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңMum fancies him,вҖқ said Fred, in a very audible whisper.
вҖңDonвҖҷt be so ridiculous, Fred,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley, her cheeks rather pink. вҖңAll right, if you think you know better than Lockhart, you can go and get on with it, and woe betide you if thereвҖҷs a sinВӯgle gnome in that garden when I come out to inspect it.вҖқ
Yawning and grumbling, the Weasleys slouched outside with Harry behind them. The garden was large, and in HarryвҖҷs eyes, exВӯactly what a garden should be. The Dursleys wouldnвҖҷt have liked it вҖ” there were plenty of weeds, and the grass needed cutting вҖ” but there were gnarled trees all around the walls, plants Harry had never seen spilling from every flower bed, and a big green pond full of frogs.
вҖңMuggles have garden gnomes, too, you know,вҖқ Harry told Ron as they crossed the lawn.
вҖңYeah, IвҖҷve seen those things they think are gnomes,вҖқ said Ron, bent double with his head in a peony bush, вҖңlike fat little Santa Clauses with fishing rods. вҖҰвҖқ
There was a violent scuffling noise, the peony bush shuddered, and Ron straightened up. вҖңThis is a gnome,вҖқ he said grimly.
вҖңGerroff me! Gerroff me!вҖқ squealed the gnome.
It was certainly nothing like Santa Claus. It was small and leathВӯery looking, with a large, knobby, bald head exactly like a potato. Ron held it at armвҖҷs length as it kicked out at him with its horny litВӯtle feet; he grasped it around the ankles and turned it upside down.
вҖңThis is what you have to do,вҖқ he said. He raised the gnome above his head (вҖңGerroff me!вҖқ) and started to swing it in great cirВӯcles like a lasso. Seeing the shocked look on HarryвҖҷs face, Ron added, вҖңIt doesnвҖҷt hurt them вҖ” youвҖҷve just got to make them really dizzy so they canвҖҷt find their way back to the gnomeholes.вҖқ
He let go of the gnomeвҖҷs ankles: It flew twenty feet into the air and landed with a thud in the field over the hedge.
вҖңPitiful,вҖқ said Fred. вҖңI bet I can get mine beyond that stump.вҖқ
Harry learned quickly not to feel too sorry for the gnomes. He decided just to drop the first one he caught over the hedge, but the gnome, sensing weakness, sank its razor-sharp teeth into HarryвҖҷs finger and he had a hard job shaking it off вҖ” until вҖ”
вҖңWow, Harry вҖ” that mustвҖҷve been fifty feet. вҖҰвҖқ
The air was soon thick with flying gnomes.
вҖңSee, theyвҖҷre not too bright,вҖқ said George, seizing five or six gnomes at once. вҖңThe moment they know the de-gnomingвҖҷs going on they storm up to have a look. YouвҖҷd think theyвҖҷd have learned by now just to stay put.вҖқ
Soon, the crowd of gnomes in the field started walking away in a straggling line, their little shoulders hunched.
вҖңTheyвҖҷll be back,вҖқ said Ron as they watched the gnomes disapВӯpear into the hedge on the other side of the field. вҖңThey love it here. вҖҰ DadвҖҷs too soft with them; he thinks theyвҖҷre funny. вҖҰвҖқ
Just then, the front door slammed.
вҖңHeвҖҷs back!вҖқ said George. вҖңDadвҖҷs home!вҖқ
They hurried through the garden and back into the house.
Mr. Weasley was slumped in a kitchen chair with his glasses off and his eyes closed. He was a thin man, going bald, but the little hair he had was as red as any of his childrenвҖҷs. He was wearing long green robes, which were dusty and travel-worn.
вҖңWhat a night,вҖқ he mumbled, groping for the teapot as they all sat down around him. вҖңNine raids. Nine! And old Mundungus Fletcher tried to put a hex on me when I had my back turned. вҖҰвҖқ
Mr. Weasley took a long gulp of tea and sighed.
вҖңFind anything, Dad?вҖқ said Fred eagerly.
вҖңAll I got were a few shrinking door keys and a biting kettle,вҖқ yawned Mr. Weasley. вҖңThere was some pretty nasty stuff that wasnвҖҷt my department, though. Mortlake was taken away for quesВӯtioning about some extremely odd ferrets, but thatвҖҷs the CommitВӯtee on Experimental Charms, thank goodness. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңWhy would anyone bother making door keys shrink?вҖқ said George.
вҖңJust Muggle-baiting,вҖқ sighed Mr. Weasley. вҖңSell them a key that keeps shrinking to nothing so they can never find it when they need it. вҖҰ Of course, itвҖҷs very hard to convict anyone because no Muggle would admit their key keeps shrinking вҖ” theyвҖҷll insist they just keep losing it. Bless them, theyвҖҷll go to any lengths to igВӯnore magic, even if itвҖҷs staring them in the face. вҖҰ But the things our lot have taken to enchanting, you wouldnвҖҷt believe вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңLIKE CARS, FOR INSTANCE?вҖқ
Mrs. Weasley had appeared, holding a long poker like a sword. Mr. WeasleyвҖҷs eyes jerked open. He stared guiltily at his wife.
вҖңC-cars, Molly, dear?вҖқ
вҖңYes, Arthur, cars,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley, her eyes flashing. вҖңImagВӯine a wizard buying a rusty old car and telling his wife all he wanted to do with it was take it apart to see how it worked, while really he was enchanting it to make it fly.вҖқ
Mr. Weasley blinked.
вҖңWell, dear, I think youвҖҷll find that he would be quite within the law to do that, even if вҖ” er вҖ” he maybe would have done better to, um, tell his wife the truth. вҖҰ ThereвҖҷs a loophole in the law, youвҖҷll find. вҖҰ As long as he wasnвҖҷt intending to fly the car, the fact that the car could fly wouldnвҖҷt вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңArthur Weasley, you made sure there was a loophole when you wrote that law!вҖқ shouted Mrs. Weasley. вҖңJust so you could carry on tinkering with all that Muggle rubbish in your shed! And for your information, Harry arrived this morning in the car you werenвҖҷt inВӯtending to fly!вҖқ
вҖңHarry?вҖқ said Mr. Weasley blankly. вҖңHarry who?вҖқ
He looked around, saw Harry, and jumped.
вҖңGood lord, is it Harry Potter? Very pleased to meet you, RonвҖҷs told us so much about вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYour sons flew that car to HarryвҖҷs house and back last night!вҖқ shouted Mrs. Weasley. вҖңWhat have you got to say about that, eh?вҖқ
вҖңDid you really?вҖқ said Mr. Weasley eagerly. вҖңDid it go all right? I вҖ” I mean,вҖқ he faltered as sparks flew from Mrs. WeasleyвҖҷs eyes, вҖңthat вҖ” that was very wrong, boys вҖ” very wrong indeed. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңLetвҖҷs leave them to it,вҖқ Ron muttered to Harry as Mrs. Weasley swelled like a bullfrog. вҖңCome on, IвҖҷll show you my bedroom.вҖқ
They slipped out of the kitchen and down a narrow passageway to an uneven staircase, which wound its way, zigzagging up through the house. On the third landing, a door stood ajar. Harry just caught sight of a pair of bright brown eyes staring at him beВӯfore it closed with a snap.
вҖңGinny,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңYou donвҖҷt know how weird it is for her to be this shy. She never shuts up normally вҖ”вҖқ
They climbed two more flights until they reached a door with peeling paint and a small plaque on it, saying RONALDвҖҷS ROOM.
Harry stepped in, his head almost touching the sloping ceiling, and blinked. It was like walking into a furnace: Nearly everything in RonвҖҷs room seemed to be a violent shade of orange: the bedВӯspread, the walls, even the ceiling. Then Harry realized that Ron had covered nearly every inch of the shabby wallpaper with posters of the same seven witches and wizards, all wearing bright orange robes, carrying broomsticks, and waving energetically.
вҖңYour Quidditch team?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңThe Chudley Cannons,вҖқ said Ron, pointing at the orange bedВӯspread, which was emblazoned with two giant black CвҖҷs and a speeding cannonball. вҖңNinth in the league.вҖқ
RonвҖҷs school spellbooks were stacked untidily in a corner, next to a pile of comics that all seemed to feature The Adventures of Martin Miggs, the Mad Muggle. RonвҖҷs magic wand was lying on top of a fish tank full of frog spawn on the windowsill, next to his fat gray rat, Scabbers, who was snoozing in a patch of sun.
Harry stepped over a pack of Self-Shuffling playing cards on the floor and looked out of the tiny window. In the field far below he could see a gang of gnomes sneaking one by one back through the WeasleysвҖҷ hedge. Then he turned to look at Ron, who was watchВӯing him almost nervously, as though waiting for his opinion.
вҖңItвҖҷs a bit small,вҖқ said Ron quickly. вҖңNot like that room you had with the Muggles. And IвҖҷm right underneath the ghoul in the attic; heвҖҷs always banging on the pipes and groaning. вҖҰвҖқ
But Harry, grinning widely, said, вҖңThis is the best house IвҖҷve ever been in.вҖқ
RonвҖҷs ears went pink.
## Chapter 4

At Flourish and Blotts
Life at the Burrow was as different as possible from life on Privet Drive. The Dursleys liked everything neat and ordered; the WeasleysвҖҷ house burst with the strange and unexpected. Harry got a shock the first time he looked in the mirror over the kitchen manВӯtelpiece and it shouted, вҖңTuck your shirt in, scruffy!вҖқ The ghoul in the attic howled and dropped pipes whenever he felt things were getting too quiet, and small explosions from Fred and GeorgeвҖҷs bedroom were considered perfectly normal. What Harry found most unusual about life at RonвҖҷs, however, wasnвҖҷt the talking mirВӯror or the clanking ghoul: It was the fact that everybody there seemed to like him.
Mrs. Weasley fussed over the state of his socks and tried to force him to eat fourth helpings at every meal. Mr. Weasley liked Harry to sit next to him at the dinner table so that he could bombard him with questions about life with Muggles, asking him to explain how things like plugs and the postal service worked.
вҖңFascinating!вҖқ he would say as Harry talked him through using a telephone. вҖңIngenious, really, how many ways Muggles have found of getting along without magic.вҖқ
Harry heard from Hogwarts one sunny morning about a week after he had arrived at the Burrow. He and Ron went down to breakfast to find Mr. and Mrs. Weasley and Ginny already sitting at the kitchen table. The moment she saw Harry, Ginny accidenВӯtally knocked her porridge bowl to the floor with a loud clatter. Ginny seemed very prone to knocking things over whenever Harry entered a room. She dived under the table to retrieve the bowl and emerged with her face glowing like the setting sun. Pretending he hadnвҖҷt noticed this, Harry sat down and took the toast Mrs. Weasley offered him.
вҖңLetters from school,вҖқ said Mr. Weasley, passing Harry and Ron identical envelopes of yellowish parchment, addressed in green ink. вҖңDumbledore already knows youвҖҷre here, Harry вҖ” doesnвҖҷt miss a trick, that man. You twoвҖҷve got them, too,вҖқ he added, as Fred and George ambled in, still in their pajamas.
For a few minutes there was silence as they all read their letters. HarryвҖҷs told him to catch the Hogwarts Express as usual from KingвҖҷs Cross station on September first. There was also a list of the new books heвҖҷd need for the coming year.
SECOND-YEAR STUDENTS WILL REQUIRE:
The Standard Book of Spells, Grade 2
by Miranda Goshawk
Break with a Banshee by Gilderoy Lockhart
Gadding with Ghouls by Gilderoy Lockhart
Holidays with Hags by Gilderoy Lockhart
Travels with Trolls by Gilderoy Lockhart
Voyages with Vampires by Gilderoy Lockhart
Wanderings with Werewolves by Gilderoy Lockhart
Year with the Yeti by Gilderoy Lockhart
Fred, who had finished his own list, peered over at HarryвҖҷs.
вҖңYouвҖҷve been told to get all LockhartвҖҷs books, too!вҖқ he said. вҖңThe new Defense Against the Dark Arts teacher must be a fan вҖ” bet itвҖҷs a witch.вҖқ
At this point, Fred caught his motherвҖҷs eye and quickly busied himself with the marmalade.
вҖңThat lot wonвҖҷt come cheap,вҖқ said George, with a quick look at his parents. вҖңLockhartвҖҷs books are really expensive. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңWell, weвҖҷll manage,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley, but she looked worВӯried. вҖңI expect weвҖҷll be able to pick up a lot of GinnyвҖҷs things secondhand.вҖқ
вҖңOh, are you starting at Hogwarts this year?вҖқ Harry asked Ginny.
She nodded, blushing to the roots of her flaming hair, and put her elbow in the butter dish. Fortunately no one saw this except Harry, because just then RonвҖҷs elder brother Percy walked in. He was already dressed, his Hogwarts prefect badge pinned to his sweater vest.
вҖңMorning, all,вҖқ said Percy briskly. вҖңLovely day.вҖқ
He sat down in the only remaining chair but leapt up again alВӯmost immediately, pulling from underneath him a molting, gray feather duster вҖ” at least, that was what Harry thought it was, unВӯtil he saw that it was breathing.
вҖңErrol!вҖқ said Ron, taking the limp owl from Percy and extracting a letter from under its wing. вҖңFinally вҖ” heвҖҷs got HermioneвҖҷs anВӯswer. I wrote to her saying we were going to try and rescue you from the Dursleys.вҖқ
He carried Errol to a perch just inside the back door and tried to stand him on it, but Errol flopped straight off again so Ron laid him on the draining board instead, muttering, вҖңPathetic.вҖқ Then he ripped open HermioneвҖҷs letter and read it out loud:
вҖң вҖҳDear Ron, and Harry if youвҖҷre there,
вҖң вҖҳI hope everything went all right and that Harry is okay and that you didnвҖҷt do anything illegal to get him out, Ron, because that would get Harry into trouble, too. IвҖҷve been really worried and if Harry is all right, will you please let me know at once, but perhaps it would be betВӯter if you used a different owl, because I think another delivery might finish your one off.
вҖң вҖҳIвҖҷm very busy with schoolwork, of courseвҖҷ вҖ” How can she be?вҖқ said Ron in horror. вҖңWeвҖҷre on vacation! вҖ” вҖҳand weвҖҷre going to LonВӯdon next Wednesday to buy my new books. Why donвҖҷt we meet in DiВӯagon Alley?
вҖң вҖҳLet me know whatвҖҷs happening as soon as you can. Love from Hermione.вҖҷ вҖқ
вҖңWell, that fits in nicely, we can go and get all your things then, too,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley, starting to clear the table. вҖңWhatвҖҷre you all up to today?вҖқ
Harry, Ron, Fred, and George were planning to go up the hill to a small paddock the Weasleys owned. It was surrounded by trees that blocked it from view of the village below, meaning that they could practice Quidditch there, as long as they didnвҖҷt fly too high. They couldnвҖҷt use real Quidditch balls, which would have been hard to explain if they had escaped and flown away over the village; instead they threw apples for one another to catch. They took turns riding HarryвҖҷs Nimbus Two Thousand, which was easily the best broom; RonвҖҷs old Shooting Star was often outstripped by passing butterflies.
Five minutes later they were marching up the hill, broomsticks over their shoulders. They had asked Percy if he wanted to join them, but he had said he was busy. Harry had only seen Percy at mealtimes so far; he stayed shut in his room the rest of the time.
вҖңWish I knew what he was up to,вҖқ said Fred, frowning. вҖңHeвҖҷs not himself. His exam results came the day before you did; twelve O.W.L.s and he hardly gloated at all.вҖқ
вҖңOrdinary Wizarding Levels,вҖқ George explained, seeing HarryвҖҷs puzzled look. вҖңBill got twelve, too. If weвҖҷre not careful, weвҖҷll have another Head Boy in the family. I donвҖҷt think I could stand the shame.вҖқ
Bill was the oldest Weasley brother. He and the next brother, Charlie, had already left Hogwarts. Harry had never met either of them, but knew that Charlie was in Romania studying dragons and Bill in Egypt working for the wizardвҖҷs bank, Gringotts.
вҖңDunno how Mum and Dad are going to afford all our school stuff this year,вҖқ said George after a while. вҖңFive sets of Lockhart books! And Ginny needs robes and a wand and everything. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry said nothing. He felt a bit awkward. Stored in an underВӯground vault at Gringotts in London was a small fortune that his parents had left him. Of course, it was only in the wizarding world that he had money; you couldnвҖҷt use Galleons, Sickles, and Knuts in Muggle shops. He had never mentioned his Gringotts bank acВӯcount to the Dursleys; he didnвҖҷt think their horror of anything conВӯnected with magic would stretch to a large pile of gold.
Mrs. Weasley woke them all early the following Wednesday. After a quick half a dozen bacon sandwiches each, they pulled on their coats and Mrs. Weasley took a flowerpot off the kitchen mantelВӯpiece and peered inside.
вҖңWeвҖҷre running low, Arthur,вҖқ she sighed. вҖңWeвҖҷll have to buy some more today. вҖҰ Ah well, guests first! After you, Harry dear!вҖқ
And she offered him the flowerpot.
Harry stared at them all watching him.
вҖңW-what am I supposed to do?вҖқ he stammered.
вҖңHeвҖҷs never traveled by Floo powder,вҖқ said Ron suddenly. вҖңSorry, Harry, I forgot.вҖқ
вҖңNever?вҖқ said Mr. Weasley. вҖңBut how did you get to Diagon AlВӯley to buy your school things last year?вҖқ
вҖңI went on the Underground вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңReally?вҖқ said Mr. Weasley eagerly. вҖңWere there escapators? How exactly вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңNot now, Arthur,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley. вҖңFloo powderвҖҷs a lot quicker, dear, but goodness me, if youвҖҷve never used it before вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHeвҖҷll be all right, Mum,вҖқ said Fred. вҖңHarry, watch us first.вҖқ
He took a pinch of glittering powder out of the flowerpot, stepped up to the fire, and threw the powder into the flames.
With a roar, the fire turned emerald green and rose higher than Fred, who stepped right into it, shouted, вҖңDiagon Alley!вҖқ and vanВӯished.
вҖңYou must speak clearly, dear,вҖқ Mrs. Weasley told Harry as George dipped his hand into the flowerpot. вҖңAnd be sure to get out at the right grate. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңThe right what?вҖқ said Harry nervously as the fire roared and whipped George out of sight, too.
вҖңWell, there are an awful lot of wizard fires to choose from, you know, but as long as youвҖҷve spoken clearly вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHeвҖҷll be fine, Molly, donвҖҷt fuss,вҖқ said Mr. Weasley, helping himВӯself to Floo powder, too.
вҖңBut, dear, if he got lost, how would we ever explain to his aunt and uncle?вҖқ
вҖңThey wouldnвҖҷt mind,вҖқ Harry reassured her. вҖңDudley would think it was a brilliant joke if I got lost up a chimney, donвҖҷt worry about that вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWell вҖҰ all right вҖҰ you go after Arthur,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley. вҖңNow, when you get into the fire, say where youвҖҷre going вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңAnd keep your elbows tucked in,вҖқ Ron advised.
вҖңAnd your eyes shut,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley. вҖңThe soot вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңDonвҖҷt fidget,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңOr you might well fall out of the wrong fireplace вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBut donвҖҷt panic and get out too early; wait until you see Fred and George.вҖқ
Trying hard to bear all this in mind, Harry took a pinch of Floo powder and walked to the edge of the fire. He took a deep breath, scattered the powder into the flames, and stepped forward; the fire felt like a warm breeze; he opened his mouth and immediately swallowed a lot of hot ash.
вҖңD-Dia-gon Alley,вҖқ he coughed.
It felt as though he were being sucked down a giant drain. He seemed to be spinning very fast вҖ” the roaring in his ears was deafВӯening вҖ” he tried to keep his eyes open but the whirl of green flames made him feel sick вҖ” something hard knocked his elbow and he tucked it in tightly, still spinning and spinning вҖ” now it felt as though cold hands were slapping his face вҖ” squinting through his glasses he saw a blurred stream of fireplaces and snatched glimpses of the rooms beyond вҖ” his bacon sandwiches were churning inside him вҖ” he closed his eyes again wishing it would stop, and then вҖ”
He fell, face forward, onto cold stone and felt the bridge of his glasses snap.
Dizzy and bruised, covered in soot, he got gingerly to his feet, holding his broken glasses up to his eyes. He was quite alone, but where he was, he had no idea. All he could tell was that he was standing in the stone fireplace of what looked like a large, dimly lit wizardвҖҷs shop вҖ” but nothing in here was ever likely to be on a Hogwarts school list.
A glass case nearby held a withered hand on a cushion, a bloodВӯstained pack of cards, and a staring glass eye. Evil-looking masks stared down from the walls, an assortment of human bones lay upon the counter, and rusty, spiked instruments hung from the ceiling. Even worse, the dark, narrow street Harry could see through the dusty shop window was definitely not Diagon Alley.
The sooner he got out of here, the better. Nose still stinging where it had hit the hearth, Harry made his way swiftly and silently toward the door, but before heвҖҷd got halfway toward it, two people appeared on the other side of the glass вҖ” and one of them was the very last person Harry wanted to meet when he was lost, covered in soot, and wearing broken glasses: Draco Malfoy.
Harry looked quickly around and spotted a large black cabinet to his left; he shot inside it and pulled the doors closed, leaving a small crack to peer through. Seconds later, a bell clanged, and MalВӯfoy stepped into the shop.
The man who followed could only be DracoвҖҷs father. He had the same pale, pointed face and identical cold, gray eyes. Mr. Malfoy crossed the shop, looking lazily at the items on display, and rang a bell on the counter before turning to his son and saying, вҖңTouch nothing, Draco.вҖқ
Malfoy, who had reached for the glass eye, said, вҖңI thought you were going to buy me a present.вҖқ
вҖңI said I would buy you a racing broom,вҖқ said his father, drumВӯming his fingers on the counter.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs the good of that if IвҖҷm not on the House team?вҖқ said Malfoy, looking sulky and bad-tempered. вҖңHarry Potter got a Nimbus Two Thousand last year. Special permission from DumВӯbledore so he could play for Gryffindor. HeвҖҷs not even that good, itвҖҷs just because heвҖҷs famous вҖҰ famous for having a stupid scar on his forehead. вҖҰвҖқ
Malfoy bent down to examine a shelf full of skulls.
вҖңвҖҰ everyone thinks heвҖҷs so smart, wonderful Potter with his scar and his broomstick вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYou have told me this at least a dozen times already,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy, with a quelling look at his son. вҖңAnd I would remind you that it is not вҖ” prudent вҖ” to appear less than fond of Harry PotВӯter, not when most of our kind regard him as the hero who made the Dark Lord disappear вҖ” ah, Mr. Borgin.вҖқ
A stooping man had appeared behind the counter, smoothing his greasy hair back from his face.
вҖңMr. Malfoy, what a pleasure to see you again,вҖқ said Mr. Borgin in a voice as oily as his hair. вҖңDelighted вҖ” and young Master MalВӯfoy, too вҖ” charmed. How may I be of assistance? I must show you, just in today, and very reasonably priced вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷm not buying today, Mr. Borgin, but selling,вҖқ said Mr. MalВӯfoy.
вҖңSelling?вҖқ The smile faded slightly from Mr. BorginвҖҷs face.
вҖңYou have heard, of course, that the Ministry is conducting more raids,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy, taking a roll of parchment from his inside pocket and unraveling it for Mr. Borgin to read. вҖңI have a few вҖ” ah вҖ” items at home that might embarrass me, if the MinВӯistry were to call. вҖҰвҖқ
Mr. Borgin fixed a pair of pince-nez to his nose and looked down the list.
вҖңThe Ministry wouldnвҖҷt presume to trouble you, sir, surely?вҖқ
Mr. MalfoyвҖҷs lip curled.
вҖңI have not been visited yet. The name Malfoy still commands a certain respect, yet the Ministry grows ever more meddlesome. There are rumors about a new Muggle Protection Act вҖ” no doubt that flea-bitten, Muggle-loving fool Arthur Weasley is behind it вҖ”вҖқ
Harry felt a hot surge of anger.
вҖңвҖ” and as you see, certain of these poisons might make it apВӯpear вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI understand, sir, of course,вҖқ said Mr. Borgin. вҖңLet me see вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңCan I have that?вҖқ interrupted Draco, pointing at the withered hand on its cushion.
вҖңAh, the Hand of Glory!вҖқ said Mr. Borgin, abandoning Mr. MalfoyвҖҷs list and scurrying over to Draco. вҖңInsert a candle and it gives light only to the holder! Best friend of thieves and plunderers! Your son has fine taste, sir.вҖқ
вҖңI hope my son will amount to more than a thief or a plunderer, Borgin,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy coldly, and Mr. Borgin said quickly, вҖңNo offense, sir, no offense meant вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThough if his grades donвҖҷt pick up,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy, more coldly still, вҖңthat may indeed be all he is fit for вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңItвҖҷs not my fault,вҖқ retorted Draco. вҖңThe teachers all have faВӯvorites, that Hermione Granger вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI would have thought youвҖҷd be ashamed that a girl of no wizard family beat you in every exam,вҖқ snapped Mr. Malfoy.
вҖңHa!вҖқ said Harry under his breath, pleased to see Draco looking both abashed and angry.
вҖңItвҖҷs the same all over,вҖқ said Mr. Borgin, in his oily voice. вҖңWizВӯard blood is counting for less everywhere вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңNot with me,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy, his long nostrils flaring.
вҖңNo, sir, nor with me, sir,вҖқ said Mr. Borgin, with a deep bow.
вҖңIn that case, perhaps we can return to my list,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy shortly. вҖңI am in something of a hurry, Borgin, I have important business elsewhere today вҖ”вҖқ
They started to haggle. Harry watched nervously as Draco drew nearer and nearer to his hiding place, examining the objects for sale. Draco paused to examine a long coil of hangmanвҖҷs rope and to read, smirking, the card propped on a magnificent necklace of opals, Caution: Do Not Touch. Cursed вҖ” Has Claimed the Lives of Nineteen Muggle Owners to Date.
Draco turned away and saw the cabinet right in front of him. He walked forward вҖ” he stretched out his hand for the handle вҖ”
вҖңDone,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy at the counter. вҖңCome, Draco вҖ”вҖқ
Harry wiped his forehead on his sleeve as Draco turned away.
вҖңGood day to you, Mr. Borgin. IвҖҷll expect you at the manor toВӯmorrow to pick up the goods.вҖқ
The moment the door had closed, Mr. Borgin dropped his oily manner.
вҖңGood day yourself, Mister Malfoy, and if the stories are true, you havenвҖҷt sold me half of whatвҖҷs hidden in your manor. вҖҰвҖқ
Muttering darkly, Mr. Borgin disappeared into a back room. Harry waited for a minute in case he came back, then, quietly as he could, slipped out of the cabinet, past the glass cases, and out of the shop door.
Clutching his broken glasses to his face, Harry stared around. He had emerged into a dingy alleyway that seemed to be made up entirely of shops devoted to the Dark Arts. The one heвҖҷd just left, Borgin and Burkes, looked like the largest, but opposite was a nasty window display of shrunken heads and, two doors down, a large cage was alive with gigantic black spiders. Two shabby-looking wizВӯards were watching him from the shadow of a doorway, muttering to each other. Feeling jumpy, Harry set off, trying to hold his glasses on straight and hoping against hope heвҖҷd be able to find a way out of here.
An old wooden street sign hanging over a shop selling poisoВӯnous candles told him he was in Knockturn Alley. This didnвҖҷt help, as Harry had never heard of such a place. He supposed he hadnвҖҷt spoken clearly enough through his mouthful of ashes back in the WeasleysвҖҷ fire. Trying to stay calm, he wondered what to do.
вҖңNot lost are you, my dear?вҖқ said a voice in his ear, making him jump.
An aged witch stood in front of him, holding a tray of what looked horribly like whole human fingernails. She leered at him, showing mossy teeth. Harry backed away.
вҖңIвҖҷm fine, thanks,вҖқ he said. вҖңIвҖҷm just вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHARRY! What dвҖҷyeh think yer doinвҖҷ down there?вҖқ
HarryвҖҷs heart leapt. So did the witch; a load of fingernails casВӯcaded down over her feet and she cursed as the massive form of Hagrid, the Hogwarts gamekeeper, came striding toward them, beetle-black eyes flashing over his great bristling beard.
вҖңHagrid!вҖқ Harry croaked in relief. вҖңI was lost вҖ” Floo powВӯder вҖ”вҖқ
Hagrid seized Harry by the scruff of the neck and pulled him away from the witch, knocking the tray right out of her hands. Her shrieks followed them all the way along the twisting alleyway out into bright sunlight. Harry saw a familiar, snow-white marble building in the distance вҖ” Gringotts Bank. Hagrid had steered him right into Diagon Alley.
вҖңYer a mess!вҖқ said Hagrid gruffly, brushing soot off Harry so forcefully he nearly knocked him into a barrel of dragon dung outВӯside an apothecary. вҖңSkulkinвҖҷ around Knockturn Alley, I dunno вҖ” dodgy place, Harry вҖ” donвҖҷ want no one ter see yeh down there вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI realized that,вҖқ said Harry, ducking as Hagrid made to brush him off again. вҖңI told you, I was lost вҖ” what were you doing down there, anyway?вҖқ
вҖңI was lookinвҖҷ fer a Flesh-EatinвҖҷ Slug Repellent,вҖқ growled HaВӯgrid. вҖңTheyвҖҷre ruininвҖҷ the school cabbages. Yer not on yer own?вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷm staying with the Weasleys but we got separated,вҖқ Harry exВӯplained. вҖңIвҖҷve got to go and find them. вҖҰвҖқ
They set off together down the street.
вҖңHow come yeh never wrote back ter me?вҖқ said Hagrid as Harry jogged alongside him (he had to take three steps to every stride of HagridвҖҷs enormous boots). Harry explained all about Dobby and the Dursleys.
вҖңLousy Muggles,вҖқ growled Hagrid. вҖңIf IвҖҷdвҖҷve known вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHarry! Harry! Over here!вҖқ
Harry looked up and saw Hermione Granger standing at the top of the white flight of steps to Gringotts. She ran down to meet them, her bushy brown hair flying behind her.
вҖңWhat happened to your glasses? Hello, Hagrid вҖ” Oh, itвҖҷs wonderful to see you two again вҖ” Are you coming into Gringotts, Harry?вҖқ
вҖңAs soon as IвҖҷve found the Weasleys,вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңYeh wonвҖҷt have long ter wait,вҖқ Hagrid said with a grin.
Harry and Hermione looked around: Sprinting up the crowded street were Ron, Fred, George, Percy, and Mr. Weasley.
