вҖңHarry,вҖқ Mr. Weasley panted. вҖңWe hoped youвҖҷd only gone one grate too far. вҖҰвҖқ He mopped his glistening bald patch. вҖңMollyвҖҷs frantic вҖ” sheвҖҷs coming now вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWhere did you come out?вҖқ Ron asked.
вҖңKnockturn Alley,вҖқ said Hagrid grimly.
вҖңExcellent!вҖқ said Fred and George together.
вҖңWeвҖҷve never been allowed in,вҖқ said Ron enviously.
вҖңI should ruddy well think not,вҖқ growled Hagrid.
Mrs. Weasley now came galloping into view, her handbag swingВӯing wildly in one hand, Ginny just clinging onto the other.
вҖңOh, Harry вҖ” oh, my dear вҖ” you could have been anyВӯwhere вҖ”вҖқ
Gasping for breath she pulled a large clothes brush out of her bag and began sweeping off the soot Hagrid hadnвҖҷt managed to beat away. Mr. Weasley took HarryвҖҷs glasses, gave them a tap of his wand, and returned them, good as new.
вҖңWell, gotta be off,вҖқ said Hagrid, who was having his hand wrung by Mrs. Weasley (вҖңKnockturn Alley! If you hadnвҖҷt found him, Hagrid!вҖқ). вҖңSee yer at Hogwarts!вҖқ And he strode away, head and shoulders taller than anyone else in the packed street.
вҖңGuess who I saw in Borgin and Burkes?вҖқ Harry asked Ron and Hermione as they climbed the Gringotts steps. вҖңMalfoy and his faВӯther.вҖқ
вҖңDid Lucius Malfoy buy anything?вҖқ said Mr. Weasley sharply behind them.
вҖңNo, he was selling вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңSo heвҖҷs worried,вҖқ said Mr. Weasley with grim satisfaction. вҖңOh, IвҖҷd love to get Lucius Malfoy for something. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңYou be careful, Arthur,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley sharply as they were bowed into the bank by a goblin at the door. вҖңThat familyвҖҷs trouВӯble. DonвҖҷt go biting off more than you can chew вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңSo you donвҖҷt think IвҖҷm a match for Lucius Malfoy?вҖқ said Mr. Weasley indignantly, but he was distracted almost at once by the sight of HermioneвҖҷs parents, who were standing nervously at the counter that ran all along the great marble hall, waiting for Hermione to introduce them.
вҖңBut youвҖҷre Muggles!вҖқ said Mr. Weasley delightedly. вҖңWe must have a drink! WhatвҖҷs that youвҖҷve got there? Oh, youвҖҷre changing Muggle money. Molly, look!вҖқ He pointed excitedly at the ten-pound notes in Mr. GrangerвҖҷs hand.
вҖңMeet you back here,вҖқ Ron said to Hermione as the Weasleys and Harry were led off to their underground vaults by another Gringotts goblin.
The vaults were reached by means of small, goblin-driven carts that sped along minature train tracks through the bankвҖҷs underВӯground tunnels. Harry enjoyed the breakneck journey down to the WeasleysвҖҷ vault, but felt dreadful, far worse than he had in Knock-turn Alley, when it was opened. There was a very small pile of silВӯver Sickles inside, and just one gold Galleon. Mrs. Weasley felt right into the corners before sweeping the whole lot into her bag. Harry felt even worse when they reached his vault. He tried to block the contents from view as he hastily shoved handfuls of coins into a leather bag.
Back outside on the marble steps, they all separated. Percy mutВӯtered vaguely about needing a new quill. Fred and George had spotted their friend from Hogwarts, Lee Jordan. Mrs. Weasley and Ginny were going to a secondhand robe shop. Mr. Weasley was inВӯsisting on taking the Grangers off to the Leaky Cauldron for a drink.
вҖңWeвҖҷll all meet at Flourish and Blotts in an hour to buy your schoolbooks,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley, setting off with Ginny. вҖңAnd not one step down Knockturn Alley!вҖқ she shouted at the twinsвҖҷ retreatВӯing backs.
Harry, Ron, and Hermione strolled off along the winding, cobВӯbled street. The bag of gold, silver, and bronze jangling cheerfully in HarryвҖҷs pocket was clamoring to be spent, so he bought three large strawberry-and-peanut-butter ice creams, which they slurped happily as they wandered up the alley, examining the fascinating shop windows. Ron gazed longingly at a full set of Chudley CanВӯnon robes in the windows of Quality Quidditch Supplies until Hermione dragged them off to buy ink and parchment next door. In Gambol and Japes Wizarding Joke Shop, they met Fred, George, and Lee Jordan, who were stocking up on Dr. FilibusterвҖҷs Fabulous Wet-Start, No-Heat Fireworks, and in a tiny junk shop full of broВӯken wands, lopsided brass scales, and old cloaks covered in potion stains they found Percy, deeply immersed in a small and deeply boring book called Prefects Who Gained Power.
вҖңA study of Hogwarts prefects and their later careers,вҖқ Ron read aloud off the back cover. вҖңThat sounds fascinating. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңGo away,вҖқ Percy snapped.
вҖң вҖҷCourse, heвҖҷs very ambitious, Percy, heвҖҷs got it all planned out. вҖҰ He wants to be Minister of Magic вҖҰвҖқ Ron told Harry and Hermione in an undertone as they left Percy to it.
An hour later, they headed for Flourish and Blotts. They were by no means the only ones making their way to the bookshop. As they approached it, they saw to their surprise a large crowd jostling outВӯside the doors, trying to get in. The reason for this was proclaimed by a large banner stretched across the upper windows:
GILDEROY LOCKHART
will be signing copies of his autobiography
MAGICAL ME
today 12:30 p.m. to 4:30 p.m.
вҖңWe can actually meet him!вҖқ Hermione squealed. вҖңI mean, heвҖҷs written almost the whole booklist!вҖқ
The crowd seemed to be made up mostly of witches around Mrs. WeasleyвҖҷs age. A harassed-looking wizard stood at the door, saying, вҖңCalmly, please, ladies. вҖҰ DonвҖҷt push, there вҖҰ mind the books, now. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry, Ron, and Hermione squeezed inside. A long line wound right to the back of the shop, where Gilderoy Lockhart was signing his books. They each grabbed a copy of The Standard Book of Spells, Grade 2 and sneaked up the line to where the rest of the Weasleys were standing with Mr. and Mrs. Granger.
вҖңOh, there you are, good,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley. She sounded breathless and kept patting her hair. вҖңWeвҖҷll be able to see him in a minute. вҖҰвҖқ
Gilderoy Lockhart came slowly into view, seated at a table surrounded by large pictures of his own face, all winking and flashing dazzlingly white teeth at the crowd. The real Lockhart was wearing robes of forget-me-not blue that exactly matched his eyes; his pointed wizardвҖҷs hat was set at a jaunty angle on his wavy hair.
A short, irritable-looking man was dancing around taking phoВӯtographs with a large black camera that emitted puffs of purple smoke with every blinding flash.
вҖңOut of the way, there,вҖқ he snarled at Ron, moving back to get a better shot. вҖңThis is for the Daily Prophet вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBig deal,вҖқ said Ron, rubbing his foot where the photographer had stepped on it.
Gilderoy Lockhart heard him. He looked up. He saw Ron вҖ” and then he saw Harry. He stared. Then he leapt to his feet and positively shouted, вҖңIt canвҖҷt be Harry Potter?вҖқ
The crowd parted, whispering excitedly; Lockhart dived forВӯward, seized HarryвҖҷs arm, and pulled him to the front. The crowd burst into applause. HarryвҖҷs face burned as Lockhart shook his hand for the photographer, who was clicking away madly, wafting thick smoke over the Weasleys.
вҖңNice big smile, Harry,вҖқ said Lockhart, through his own gleamВӯing teeth. вҖңTogether, you and I are worth the front page.вҖқ
When he finally let go of HarryвҖҷs hand, Harry could hardly feel his fingers. He tried to sidle back over to the Weasleys, but LockВӯhart threw an arm around his shoulders and clamped him tightly to his side.
вҖңLadies and gentlemen,вҖқ he said loudly, waving for quiet. вҖңWhat an extraordinary moment this is! The perfect moment for me to make a little announcement IвҖҷve been sitting on for some time!
вҖңWhen young Harry here stepped into Flourish and Blotts toВӯday, he only wanted to buy my autobiography вҖ” which I shall be happy to present him now, free of charge вҖ”вҖқ The crowd applauded again. вҖңHe had no idea,вҖқ Lockhart continued, giving Harry a little shake that made his glasses slip to the end of his nose, вҖңthat he would shortly be getting much, much more than my book, Magical Me. He and his schoolmates will, in fact, be getting the real magical me. Yes, ladies and gentlemen, I have great pleasure and pride in announcing that this September, I will be taking up the post of Defense Against the Dark Arts teacher at Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry!вҖқ
The crowd cheered and clapped and Harry found himself being presented with the entire works of Gilderoy Lockhart. Staggering slightly under their weight, he managed to make his way out of the limelight to the edge of the room, where Ginny was standing next to her new cauldron.
вҖңYou have these,вҖқ Harry mumbled to her, tipping the books into the cauldron. вҖңIвҖҷll buy my own вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBet you loved that, didnвҖҷt you, Potter?вҖқ said a voice Harry had no trouble recognizing. He straightened up and found himself face-to-face with Draco Malfoy, who was wearing his usual sneer.
вҖңFamous Harry Potter,вҖқ said Malfoy. вҖңCanвҖҷt even go into a bookВӯshop without making the front page.вҖқ
вҖңLeave him alone, he didnвҖҷt want all that!вҖқ said Ginny. It was the first time she had spoken in front of Harry. She was glaring at MalВӯfoy.
вҖңPotter, youвҖҷve got yourself a girlfriend!вҖқ drawled Malfoy. Ginny went scarlet as Ron and Hermione fought their way over, both clutching stacks of LockhartвҖҷs books.
вҖңOh, itвҖҷs you,вҖқ said Ron, looking at Malfoy as if he were someВӯthing unpleasant on the sole of his shoe. вҖңBet youвҖҷre surprised to see Harry here, eh?вҖқ
вҖңNot as surprised as I am to see you in a shop, Weasley,вҖқ retorted Malfoy. вҖңI suppose your parents will go hungry for a month to pay for all those.вҖқ
Ron went as red as Ginny. He dropped his books into the caulВӯdron, too, and started toward Malfoy, but Harry and Hermione grabbed the back of his jacket.
вҖңRon!вҖқ said Mr. Weasley, struggling over with Fred and George. вҖңWhat are you doing? ItвҖҷs too crowded in here, letвҖҷs go outside.вҖқ
вҖңWell, well, well вҖ” Arthur Weasley.вҖқ
It was Mr. Malfoy. He stood with his hand on DracoвҖҷs shoulder, sneering in just the same way.
вҖңLucius,вҖқ said Mr. Weasley, nodding coldly.
вҖңBusy time at the Ministry, I hear,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy. вҖңAll those raids вҖҰ I hope theyвҖҷre paying you overtime?вҖқ
He reached into GinnyвҖҷs cauldron and extracted, from amid the glossy Lockhart books, a very old, very battered copy of A BeginВӯnerвҖҷs Guide to Transfiguration.
вҖңObviously not,вҖқ Mr. Malfoy said. вҖңDear me, whatвҖҷs the use of being a disgrace to the name of wizard if they donвҖҷt even pay you well for it?вҖқ
Mr. Weasley flushed darker than either Ron or Ginny.
вҖңWe have a very different idea of what disgraces the name of wizВӯard, Malfoy,вҖқ he said.
вҖңClearly,вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy, his pale eyes straying to Mr. and Mrs. Granger, who were watching apprehensively. вҖңThe company you keep, Weasley вҖҰ and I thought your family could sink no lower вҖ”вҖқ
There was a thud of metal as GinnyвҖҷs cauldron went flying; Mr. Weasley had thrown himself at Mr. Malfoy, knocking him backВӯward into a bookshelf. Dozens of heavy spellbooks came thunderВӯing down on all their heads; there was a yell of, вҖңGet him, Dad!вҖқ from Fred or George; Mrs. Weasley was shrieking, вҖңNo, Arthur, no!вҖқ; the crowd stampeded backward, knocking more shelves over; вҖңGentlemen, please вҖ” please!вҖқ cried the assistant, and then, louder than all вҖ”
вҖңBreak it up, there, gents, break it up вҖ”вҖқ
Hagrid was wading toward them through the sea of books. In an instant he had pulled Mr. Weasley and Mr. Malfoy apart. Mr. Weasley had a cut lip and Mr. Malfoy had been hit in the eye by an Encyclopedia of Toadstools. He was still holding GinnyвҖҷs old Transfiguration book. He thrust it at her, his eyes glittering with malice.
вҖңHere, girl вҖ” take your book вҖ” itвҖҷs the best your father can give you вҖ”вҖқ Pulling himself out of HagridвҖҷs grip he beckoned to Draco and swept from the shop.
вҖңYeh shouldвҖҷve ignored him, Arthur,вҖқ said Hagrid, almost lifting Mr. Weasley off his feet as he straightened his robes. вҖңRotten ter the core, the whole family, everyone knows that вҖ” no MalfoyвҖҷs worth listeninвҖҷ ter вҖ” bad blood, thatвҖҷs what it is вҖ” come on now вҖ” letвҖҷs get outta here.вҖқ
The assistant looked as though he wanted to stop them from leaving, but he barely came up to HagridвҖҷs waist and seemed to think better of it. They hurried up the street, the Grangers shaking with fright and Mrs. Weasley beside herself with fury.
вҖңA fine example to set for your children вҖҰ brawling in pubВӯlic вҖҰ what Gilderoy Lockhart mustвҖҷve thought вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHe was pleased,вҖқ said Fred. вҖңDidnвҖҷt you hear him as we were leaving? He was asking that bloke from the Daily Prophet if heвҖҷd be able to work the fight into his report вҖ” said it was all publicity вҖ”вҖқ
But it was a subdued group that headed back to the fireside in the Leaky Cauldron, where Harry, the Weasleys, and all their shopВӯping would be traveling back to the Burrow using Floo powder. They said good-bye to the Grangers, who were leaving the pub for the Muggle street on the other side; Mr. Weasley started to ask them how bus stops worked, but stopped quickly at the look on Mrs. WeasleyвҖҷs face.
Harry took off his glasses and put them safely in his pocket beВӯfore helping himself to Floo powder. It definitely wasnвҖҷt his favorite way to travel.
## Chapter 5

The Whomping Willow
The end of the summer vacation came too quickly for HarryвҖҷs liking. He was looking forward to getting back to Hogwarts, but his month at the Burrow had been the happiest of his life. It was difficult not to feel jealous of Ron when he thought of the Dursleys and the sort of welcome he could expect next time he turned up on Privet Drive.
On their last evening, Mrs. Weasley conjured up a sumptuous dinner that included all of HarryвҖҷs favorite things, ending with a mouthwatering treacle pudding. Fred and George rounded off the evening with a display of Filibuster fireworks; they filled the kitchen with red and blue stars that bounced from ceiling to wall for at least half an hour. Then it was time for a last mug of hot chocolate and bed.
It took a long while to get started next morning. They were up at dawn, but somehow they still seemed to have a great deal to do. Mrs. Weasley dashed about in a bad mood looking for spare socks and quills; people kept colliding on the stairs, half-dressed with bits of toast in their hands; and Mr. Weasley nearly broke his neck, tripВӯping over a stray chicken as he crossed the yard carrying GinnyвҖҷs trunk to the car.
Harry couldnвҖҷt see how eight people, six large trunks, two owls, and a rat were going to fit into one small Ford Anglia. He had reckВӯoned, of course, without the special features that Mr. Weasley had added.
вҖңNot a word to Molly,вҖқ he whispered to Harry as he opened the trunk and showed him how it had been magically expanded so that the luggage fitted easily.
When at last they were all in the car, Mrs. Weasley glanced into the back seat, where Harry, Ron, Fred, George, and Percy were all sitting comfortably side by side, and said, вҖңMuggles do know more than we give them credit for, donвҖҷt they?вҖқ She and Ginny got into the front seat, which had been stretched so that it resembled a park bench. вҖңI mean, youвҖҷd never know it was this roomy from the outВӯside, would you?вҖқ
Mr. Weasley started up the engine and they trundled out of the yard, Harry turning back for a last look at the house. He barely had time to wonder when heвҖҷd see it again when they were back вҖ” George had forgotten his box of Filibuster fireworks. Five minutes after that, they skidded to a halt in the yard so that Fred could run in for his broomstick. They had almost reached the highway when Ginny shrieked that sheвҖҷd left her diary. By the time she had clamВӯbered back into the car, they were running very late, and tempers were running high.
Mr. Weasley glanced at his watch and then at his wife.
вҖңMolly, dear вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңNo, Arthur вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңNo one would see вҖ” this little button here is an Invisibility Booster I installed вҖ” thatвҖҷd get us up in the air вҖ” then we fly above the clouds. WeвҖҷd be there in ten minutes and no one would be any the wiser вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI said no, Arthur, not in broad daylight вҖ”вҖқ
They reached KingвҖҷs Cross at a quarter to eleven. Mr. Weasley dashed across the road to get trolleys for their trunks and they all hurried into the station.
Harry had caught the Hogwarts Express the previous year. The tricky part was getting onto platform nine and three-quarters, which wasnвҖҷt visible to the Muggle eye. What you had to do was walk through the solid barrier dividing platforms nine and ten. It didnвҖҷt hurt, but it had to be done carefully so that none of the Muggles noticed you vanishing.
вҖңPercy first,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley, looking nervously at the clock overhead, which showed they had only five minutes to disappear casually through the barrier.
Percy strode briskly forward and vanished. Mr. Weasley went next; Fred and George followed.
вҖңIвҖҷll take Ginny and you two come right after us,вҖқ Mrs. Weasley told Harry and Ron, grabbing GinnyвҖҷs hand and setting off. In the blink of an eye they were gone.
вҖңLetвҖҷs go together, weвҖҷve only got a minute,вҖқ Ron said to Harry.
Harry made sure that HedwigвҖҷs cage was safely wedged on top of his trunk and wheeled his trolley around to face the barrier. He felt perfectly confident; this wasnвҖҷt nearly as uncomfortable as using Floo powder. Both of them bent low over the handles of their trolВӯleys and walked purposefully toward the barrier, gathering speed. A few feet away from it, they broke into a run and вҖ”
CRASH.
Both trolleys hit the barrier and bounced backward; RonвҖҷs trunk fell off with a loud thump, Harry was knocked off his feet, and HedwigвҖҷs cage bounced onto the shiny floor, and she rolled away, shrieking indignantly; people all around them stared and a guard nearby yelled, вҖңWhat in blazes dвҖҷyou think youвҖҷre doing?вҖқ
вҖңLost control of the trolley,вҖқ Harry gasped, clutching his ribs as he got up. Ron ran to pick up Hedwig, who was causing such a scene that there was a lot of muttering about cruelty to animals from the surrounding crowd.
вҖңWhy canвҖҷt we get through?вҖқ Harry hissed to Ron.
вҖңI dunno вҖ”вҖқ
Ron looked wildly around. A dozen curious people were still watching them.
вҖңWeвҖҷre going to miss the train,вҖқ Ron whispered. вҖңI donвҖҷt underВӯstand why the gatewayвҖҷs sealed itself вҖ”вҖқ
Harry looked up at the giant clock with a sickening feeling in the pit of his stomach. Ten seconds вҖҰ nine seconds вҖҰ
He wheeled his trolley forward cautiously until it was right against the barrier and pushed with all his might. The metal reВӯmained solid.
Three seconds вҖҰ two seconds вҖҰ one second вҖҰ
вҖңItвҖҷs gone,вҖқ said Ron, sounding stunned. вҖңThe trainвҖҷs left. What if Mum and Dad canвҖҷt get back through to us? Have you got any Muggle money?вҖқ
Harry gave a hollow laugh. вҖңThe Dursleys havenвҖҷt given me pocket money for about six years.вҖқ
Ron pressed his ear to the cold barrier.
вҖңCanвҖҷt hear a thing,вҖқ he said tensely. вҖңWhatвҖҷre we going to do? I donвҖҷt know how long itвҖҷll take Mum and Dad to get back to us.вҖқ
They looked around. People were still watching them, mainly because of HedwigвҖҷs continuing screeches.
вҖңI think weвҖҷd better go and wait by the car,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңWeвҖҷre attracting too much atten вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHarry!вҖқ said Ron, his eyes gleaming. вҖңThe car!вҖқ
вҖңWhat about it?вҖқ
вҖңWe can fly the car to Hogwarts!вҖқ
вҖңBut I thought вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWeвҖҷre stuck, right? And weвҖҷve got to get to school, havenвҖҷt we? And even underage wizards are allowed to use magic if itвҖҷs a real emergency, section nineteen or something of the Restriction of Thingy вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBut your mum and dad вҖҰвҖқ said Harry, pushing against the barrier again in the vain hope that it would give way. вҖңHow will they get home?вҖқ
вҖңThey donвҖҷt need the car!вҖқ said Ron impatiently. вҖңThey know how to Apparate! You know, just vanish and reappear at home! They only bother with Floo powder and the car because weвҖҷre all underage and weвҖҷre not allowed to Apparate yet. вҖҰвҖқ
HarryвҖҷs feeling of panic turned suddenly to excitement.
вҖңCan you fly it?вҖқ
вҖңNo problem,вҖқ said Ron, wheeling his trolley around to face the exit. вҖңCвҖҷmon, letвҖҷs go. If we hurry weвҖҷll be able to follow the HogВӯwarts Express вҖ”вҖқ
And they marched off through the crowd of curious Muggles, out of the station and back onto the side road where the old Ford Anglia was parked.
Ron unlocked the cavernous trunk with a series of taps from his wand. They heaved their luggage back in, put Hedwig on the back seat, and got into the front.
вҖңCheck that no oneвҖҷs watching,вҖқ said Ron, starting the ignition with another tap of his wand. Harry stuck his head out of the winВӯdow: Traffic was rumbling along the main road ahead, but their street was empty.
вҖңOkay,вҖқ he said.
Ron pressed a tiny silver button on the dashboard. The car around them vanished вҖ” and so did they. Harry could feel the seat vibrating beneath him, hear the engine, feel his hands on his knees and his glasses on his nose, but for all he could see, he had become a pair of eyeballs, floating a few feet above the ground in a dingy street full of parked cars.
вҖңLetвҖҷs go,вҖқ said RonвҖҷs voice from his right.
And the ground and the dirty buildings on either side fell away, dropping out of sight as the car rose; in seconds, the whole of LonВӯdon lay, smoky and glittering, below them.
Then there was a popping noise and the car, Harry, and Ron reappeared.
вҖңUh-oh,вҖқ said Ron, jabbing at the Invisibility Booster. вҖңItвҖҷs faulty вҖ”вҖқ
Both of them pummeled it. The car vanished. Then it flickered back again.
вҖңHold on!вҖқ Ron yelled, and he slammed his foot on the accelerator; they shot straight into the low, woolly clouds and everything turned dull and foggy.
вҖңNow what?вҖқ said Harry, blinking at the solid mass of cloud pressing in on them from all sides.
вҖңWe need to see the train to know what direction to go in,вҖқ said Ron.
вҖңDip back down again вҖ” quickly вҖ”вҖқ
They dropped back beneath the clouds and twisted around in their seats, squinting at the ground.
вҖңI can see it!вҖқ Harry yelled. вҖңRight ahead вҖ” there!вҖқ
The Hogwarts Express was streaking along below them like a scarlet snake.
вҖңDue north,вҖқ said Ron, checking the compass on the dashboard. вҖңOkay, weвҖҷll just have to check on it every half hour or so вҖ” hold on вҖ”вҖқ
And they shot up through the clouds. A minute later, they burst out into a blaze of sunlight.
It was a different world. The wheels of the car skimmed the sea of fluffy cloud, the sky a bright, endless blue under the blinding white sun.
вҖңAll weвҖҷve got to worry about now are airplanes,вҖқ said Ron.
They looked at each other and started to laugh; for a long time, they couldnвҖҷt stop.
It was as though they had been plunged into a fabulous dream. This, thought Harry, was surely the only way to travel вҖ” past swirls and turrets of snowy cloud, in a car full of hot, bright sunВӯlight, with a fat pack of toffees in the glove compartment, and the prospect of seeing FredвҖҷs and GeorgeвҖҷs jealous faces when they landed smoothly and spectacularly on the sweeping lawn in front of Hogwarts castle.
They made regular checks on the train as they flew farther and farther north, each dip beneath the clouds showing them a difВӯferent view. London was soon far behind them, replaced by neat green fields that gave way in turn to wide, purplish moors, a great city alive with cars like multicolored ants, villages with tiny toy churches.
Several uneventful hours later, however, Harry had to admit that some of the fun was wearing off. The toffees had made them exВӯtremely thirsty and they had nothing to drink. He and Ron had pulled off their sweaters, but HarryвҖҷs T-shirt was sticking to the back of his seat and his glasses kept sliding down to the end of his sweaty nose. He had stopped noticing the fantastic cloud shapes now and was thinking longingly of the train miles below, where you could buy ice-cold pumpkin juice from a trolley pushed by a plump witch. Why hadnвҖҷt they been able to get onto platform nine and three-quarters?
вҖңCanвҖҷt be much further, can it?вҖқ croaked Ron, hours later still, as the sun started to sink into their floor of cloud, staining it a deep pink. вҖңReady for another check on the train?вҖқ
It was still right below them, winding its way past a snowcapped mountain. It was much darker beneath the canopy of clouds.
Ron put his foot on the accelerator and drove them upward again, but as he did so, the engine began to whine.
Harry and Ron exchanged nervous glances.
вҖңItвҖҷs probably just tired,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңItвҖҷs never been this far beВӯfore. вҖҰвҖқ
And they both pretended not to notice the whining growing louder and louder as the sky became steadily darker. Stars were blossoming in the blackness. Harry pulled his sweater back on, tryВӯing to ignore the way the windshield wipers were now waving feeВӯbly, as though in protest.
вҖңNot far,вҖқ said Ron, more to the car than to Harry, вҖңnot far now,вҖқ and he patted the dashboard nervously.
When they flew back beneath the clouds a little while later, they had to squint through the darkness for a landmark they knew.
вҖңThere!вҖқ Harry shouted, making Ron and Hedwig jump. вҖңStraight ahead!вҖқ
Silhouetted on the dark horizon, high on the cliff over the lake, stood the many turrets and towers of Hogwarts castle.
But the car had begun to shudder and was losing speed.
вҖңCome on,вҖқ Ron said cajolingly, giving the steering wheel a litВӯtle shake, вҖңnearly there, come on вҖ”вҖқ
The engine groaned. Narrow jets of steam were issuing from unВӯder the hood. Harry found himself gripping the edges of his seat very hard as they flew toward the lake.
The car gave a nasty wobble. Glancing out of his window, Harry saw the smooth, black, glassy surface of the water, a mile below. RonвҖҷs knuckles were white on the steering wheel. The car wobbled again.
вҖңCome on,вҖқ Ron muttered.
They were over the lake вҖ” the castle was right ahead вҖ” Ron put his foot down.
There was a loud clunk, a splutter, and the engine died comВӯpletely.
вҖңUh-oh,вҖқ said Ron, into the silence.
The nose of the car dropped. They were falling, gathering speed, heading straight for the solid castle wall.
вҖңNoooooo!вҖқ Ron yelled, swinging the steering wheel around; they missed the dark stone wall by inches as the car turned in a great arc, soaring over the dark greenhouses, then the vegetable patch, and then out over the black lawns, losing altitude all the time.
Ron let go of the steering wheel completely and pulled his wand out of his back pocket вҖ”
вҖңSTOP! STOP!вҖқ he yelled, whacking the dashboard and the windshield, but they were still plummeting, the ground flying up toward them вҖ”
вҖңWATCH OUT FOR THAT TREE!вҖқ Harry bellowed, lunging for the steering wheel, but too late вҖ”
CRUNCH.
With an earsplitting bang of metal on wood, they hit the thick tree trunk and dropped to the ground with a heavy jolt. Steam was billowing from under the crumpled hood; Hedwig was shrieking in terror; a golf-ball-sized lump was throbbing on HarryвҖҷs head where he had hit the windshield; and to his right, Ron let out a low, deВӯspairing groan.
вҖңAre you okay?вҖқ Harry said urgently.
вҖңMy wand,вҖқ said Ron, in a shaky voice. вҖңLook at my wand вҖ”вҖқ
It had snapped, almost in two; the tip was dangling limply, held on by a few splinters.
Harry opened his mouth to say he was sure theyвҖҷd be able to mend it up at the school, but he never even got started. At that very moment, something hit his side of the car with the force of a charging bull, sending him lurching sideways into Ron, just as an equally heavy blow hit the roof.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs happen вҖ” ?вҖқ
Ron gasped, staring through the windshield, and Harry looked around just in time to see a branch as thick as a python smash into it. The tree they had hit was attacking them. Its trunk was bent alВӯmost double, and its gnarled boughs were pummeling every inch of the car it could reach.
вҖңAaargh!вҖқ said Ron as another twisted limb punched a large dent into his door; the windshield was now trembling under a hail of blows from knuckle-like twigs and a branch as thick as a battering ram was pounding furiously on the roof, which seemed to be cavВӯing вҖ”
вҖңRun for it!вҖқ Ron shouted, throwing his full weight against his door, but next second he had been knocked backward into HarryвҖҷs lap by a vicious uppercut from another branch.
вҖңWeвҖҷre done for!вҖқ he moaned as the ceiling sagged, but suddenly the floor of the car was vibrating вҖ” the engine had restarted.
вҖңReverse!вҖқ Harry yelled, and the car shot backward; the tree was still trying to hit them; they could hear its roots creaking as it alВӯmost ripped itself up, lashing out at them as they sped out of reach.
вҖңThat,вҖқ panted Ron, вҖңwas close. Well done, car вҖ”вҖқ
The car, however, had reached the end of its tether. With two sharp clunks, the doors flew open and Harry felt his seat tip sideВӯways: Next thing he knew he was sprawled on the damp ground. Loud thuds told him that the car was ejecting their luggage from the trunk; HedwigвҖҷs cage flew through the air and burst open; she rose out of it with an angry screech and sped off toward the castle without a backward look. Then, dented, scratched, and steaming, the car rumbled off into the darkness, its rear lights blazing angrily.
вҖңCome back!вҖқ Ron yelled after it, brandishing his broken wand. вҖңDadвҖҷll kill me!вҖқ
But the car disappeared from view with one last snort from its exhaust.
вҖңCan you believe our luck?вҖқ said Ron miserably, bending down to pick up Scabbers. вҖңOf all the trees we couldвҖҷve hit, we had to get one that hits back.вҖқ
He glanced over his shoulder at the ancient tree, which was still flailing its branches threateningly.
вҖңCome on,вҖқ said Harry wearily, вҖңweвҖҷd better get up to the school. вҖҰвҖқ
It wasnвҖҷt at all the triumphant arrival they had pictured. Stiff, cold, and bruised, they seized the ends of their trunks and began dragging them up the grassy slope, toward the great oak front doors.
вҖңI think the feastвҖҷs already started,вҖқ said Ron, dropping his trunk at the foot of the front steps and crossing quietly to look through a brightly lit window. вҖңHey вҖ” Harry вҖ” come and look вҖ” itвҖҷs the Sorting!вҖқ
Harry hurried over and, together, he and Ron peered in at the Great Hall.
Innumerable candles were hovering in midair over four long, crowded tables, making the golden plates and goblets sparkle. Overhead, the bewitched ceiling, which always mirrored the sky outside, sparkled with stars.
Through the forest of pointed black Hogwarts hats, Harry saw a long line of scared-looking first years filing into the Hall. Ginny was among them, easily visible because of her vivid Weasley hair. Meanwhile, Professor McGonagall, a bespectacled witch with her hair in a tight bun, was placing the famous Hogwarts Sorting Hat on a stool before the newcomers.
Every year, this aged old hat, patched, frayed, and dirty, sorted new students into the four Hogwarts houses (Gryffindor, HufВӯflepuff, Ravenclaw, and Slytherin). Harry well remembered putting it on, exactly one year ago, and waiting, petrified, for its decision as it muttered aloud in his ear. For a few horrible seconds he had feared that the hat was going to put him in Slytherin, the House that had turned out more Dark witches and wizards than any other вҖ” but he had ended up in Gryffindor, along with Ron, Hermione, and the rest of the Weasleys. Last term, Harry and Ron had helped Gryffindor win the House Championship, beating Slytherin for the first time in seven years.
A very small, mousy-haired boy had been called forward to place the hat on his head. HarryвҖҷs eyes wandered past him to where ProВӯfessor Dumbledore, the headmaster, sat watching the Sorting from the staff table, his long silver beard and half-moon glasses shining brightly in the candlelight. Several seats along, Harry saw Gilderoy Lockhart, dressed in robes of aquamarine. And there at the end was Hagrid, huge and hairy, drinking deeply from his goblet.
вҖңHang on вҖҰвҖқ Harry muttered to Ron. вҖңThereвҖҷs an empty chair at the staff table. вҖҰ WhereвҖҷs Snape?вҖқ
Professor Severus Snape was HarryвҖҷs least favorite teacher. Harry also happened to be SnapeвҖҷs least favorite student. Cruel, sarcastic, and disliked by everybody except the students from his own House (Slytherin), Snape taught Potions.
вҖңMaybe heвҖҷs ill!вҖқ said Ron hopefully.
вҖңMaybe heвҖҷs left,вҖқ said Harry, вҖңbecause he missed out on the DeВӯfense Against the Dark Arts job again!вҖқ
вҖңOr he might have been sacked!вҖқ said Ron enthusiastically. вҖңI mean, everyone hates him вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңOr maybe,вҖқ said a very cold voice right behind them, вҖңheвҖҷs waiting to hear why you two didnвҖҷt arrive on the school train.вҖқ
Harry spun around. There, his black robes rippling in a cold breeze, stood Severus Snape. He was a thin man with sallow skin, a hooked nose, and greasy, shoulder-length black hair, and at this moment, he was smiling in a way that told Harry he and Ron were in very deep trouble.
вҖңFollow me,вҖқ said Snape.
Not daring even to look at each other, Harry and Ron followed Snape up the steps into the vast, echoing entrance hall, which was lit with flaming torches. A delicious smell of food was wafting from the Great Hall, but Snape led them away from the warmth and light, down a narrow stone staircase that led into the dungeons.
вҖңIn!вҖқ he said, opening a door halfway down the cold passageway and pointing.
They entered SnapeвҖҷs office, shivering. The shadowy walls were lined with shelves of large glass jars, in which floated all manner of revolting things Harry didnвҖҷt really want to know the name of at the moment. The fireplace was dark and empty. Snape closed the door and turned to look at them.
вҖңSo,вҖқ he said softly, вҖңthe train isnвҖҷt good enough for the famous Harry Potter and his faithful sidekick, Weasley. Wanted to arrive with a bang, did we, boys?вҖқ
вҖңNo, sir, it was the barrier at KingвҖҷs Cross, it вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңSilence!вҖқ said Snape coldly. вҖңWhat have you done with the car?вҖқ
Ron gulped. This wasnвҖҷt the first time Snape had given Harry the impression of being able to read minds. But a moment later, he unВӯderstood, as Snape unrolled todayвҖҷs issue of the Evening Prophet.
вҖңYou were seen,вҖқ he hissed, showing them the headline: FLYВӯING FORD ANGLIA MYSTIFIES MUGGLES. He began to read aloud: вҖңTwo Muggles in London, convinced they saw an old car flying over the Post Office tower вҖҰ at noon in Norfolk, Mrs. Hetty Bayliss, while hanging out her washing вҖҰ Mr. Angus Fleet, of Peebles, reported to police вҖҰ Six or seven Muggles in all. I beВӯlieve your father works in the Misuse of Muggle Artifacts Office?вҖқ he said, looking up at Ron and smiling still more nastily. вҖңDear, dear вҖҰ his own son вҖҰвҖқ
Harry felt as though heвҖҷd just been walloped in the stomach by one of the mad treeвҖҷs larger branches. If anyone found out Mr. Weasley had bewitched the car вҖҰ he hadnвҖҷt thought of that. вҖҰ
вҖңI noticed, in my search of the park, that considerable damage seems to have been done to a very valuable Whomping Willow,вҖқ Snape went on.
вҖңThat tree did more damage to us than we вҖ”вҖқ Ron blurted out.
вҖңSilence!вҖқ snapped Snape again. вҖңMost unfortunately, you are not in my House and the decision to expel you does not rest with me. I shall go and fetch the people who do have that happy power. You will wait here.вҖқ
Harry and Ron stared at each other, white-faced. Harry didnвҖҷt feel hungry anymore. He now felt extremely sick. He tried not to look at a large, slimy something suspended in green liquid on a shelf behind SnapeвҖҷs desk. If Snape had gone to fetch Professor McGonagall, head of Gryffindor House, they were hardly any betВӯter off. She might be fairer than Snape, but she was still extremely strict.
Ten minutes later, Snape returned, and sure enough it was ProВӯfessor McGonagall who accompanied him. Harry had seen ProfesВӯsor McGonagall angry on several occasions, but either he had forgotten just how thin her mouth could go, or he had never seen her this angry before. She raised her wand the moment she entered; Harry and Ron both flinched, but she merely pointed it at the empty fireplace, where flames suddenly erupted.
вҖңSit,вҖқ she said, and they both backed into chairs by the fire.
вҖңExplain,вҖқ she said, her glasses glinting ominously.
Ron launched into the story, starting with the barrier at the staВӯtion refusing to let them through.
вҖңвҖ” so we had no choice, Professor, we couldnвҖҷt get on the train.вҖқ
вҖңWhy didnвҖҷt you send us a letter by owl? I believe you have an owl?вҖқ Professor McGonagall said coldly to Harry.
Harry gaped at her. Now sheвҖҷd said it, that seemed the obvious thing to have done.
вҖңI вҖ” I didnвҖҷt think вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThat,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall, вҖңis obvious.вҖқ
There was a knock on the office door and Snape, now looking happier than ever, opened it. There stood the headmaster, Professor Dumbledore.
HarryвҖҷs whole body went numb. Dumbledore was looking unВӯusually grave. He stared down his very crooked nose at them, and Harry suddenly found himself wishing he and Ron were still being beaten up by the Whomping Willow.
There was a long silence. Then Dumbledore said, вҖңPlease exВӯplain why you did this.вҖқ
It would have been better if he had shouted. Harry hated the disВӯappointment in his voice. For some reason, he was unable to look Dumbledore in the eyes, and spoke instead to his knees. He told Dumbledore everything except that Mr. Weasley owned the beВӯwitched car, making it sound as though he and Ron had happened to find a flying car parked outside the station. He knew DumbleВӯdore would see through this at once, but Dumbledore asked no questions about the car. When Harry had finished, he merely conВӯtinued to peer at them through his spectacles.
вҖңWeвҖҷll go and get our stuff,вҖқ said Ron in a hopeless sort of voice.
вҖңWhat are you talking about, Weasley?вҖқ barked Professor McВӯGonagall.
вҖңWell, youвҖҷre expelling us, arenвҖҷt you?вҖқ said Ron.
Harry looked quickly at Dumbledore.
вҖңNot today, Mr. Weasley,вҖқ said Dumbledore. вҖңBut I must imВӯpress upon both of you the seriousness of what you have done. I will be writing to both your families tonight. I must also warn you that if you do anything like this again, I will have no choice but to expel you.вҖқ
Snape looked as though Christmas had been canceled. He cleared his throat and said, вҖңProfessor Dumbledore, these boys have flouted the Decree for the Restriction of Underage Wizardry, caused serious damage to an old and valuable tree вҖ” surely acts of this nature вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңIt will be for Professor McGonagall to decide on these boysвҖҷ punishments, Severus,вҖқ said Dumbledore calmly. вҖңThey are in her House and are therefore her responsibility.вҖқ He turned to Professor McGonagall. вҖңI must go back to the feast, Minerva, IвҖҷve got to give out a few notices. Come, Severus, thereвҖҷs a delicious-looking cusВӯtard tart I want to sample вҖ”вҖқ
Snape shot a look of pure venom at Harry and Ron as he allowed himself to be swept out of his office, leaving them alone with ProВӯfessor McGonagall, who was still eyeing them like a wrathful eagle.
вҖңYouвҖҷd better get along to the hospital wing, Weasley, youвҖҷre bleeding.вҖқ
вҖңNot much,вҖқ said Ron, hastily wiping the cut over his eye with his sleeve. вҖңProfessor, I wanted to watch my sister being Sorted вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThe Sorting Ceremony is over,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall. вҖңYour sister is also in Gryffindor.вҖқ
вҖңOh, good,вҖқ said Ron.
вҖңAnd speaking of Gryffindor вҖ”вҖқ Professor McGonagall said sharply, but Harry cut in: вҖңProfessor, when we took the car, term hadnвҖҷt started, so вҖ” so Gryffindor shouldnвҖҷt really have points taken from it вҖ” should it?вҖқ he finished, watching her anxiously.
Professor McGonagall gave him a piercing look, but he was sure she had almost smiled. Her mouth looked less thin, anyway.
вҖңI will not take any points from Gryffindor,вҖқ she said, and HarryвҖҷs heart lightened considerably. вҖңBut you will both get a deВӯtention.вҖқ
It was better than Harry had expected. As for DumbledoreвҖҷs writing to the Dursleys, that was nothing. Harry knew perfectly well theyвҖҷd just be disappointed that the Whomping Willow hadnвҖҷt squashed him flat.
Professor McGonagall raised her wand again and pointed it at SnapeвҖҷs desk. A large plate of sandwiches, two silver goblets, and a jug of iced pumpkin juice appeared with a pop.
вҖңYou will eat in here and then go straight up to your dormitory,вҖқ she said. вҖңI must also return to the feast.вҖқ
When the door had closed behind her, Ron let out a long, low whistle.
вҖңI thought weвҖҷd had it,вҖқ he said, grabbing a sandwich.
вҖңSo did I,вҖқ said Harry, taking one, too.
вҖңCan you believe our luck, though?вҖқ said Ron thickly through a mouthful of chicken and ham. вҖңFred and George mustвҖҷve flown that car five or six times and no Muggle ever saw them.вҖқ He swalВӯlowed and took another huge bite. вҖңWhy couldnвҖҷt we get through the barrier?вҖқ
Harry shrugged. вҖңWeвҖҷll have to watch our step from now on, though,вҖқ he said, taking a grateful swig of pumpkin juice. вҖңWish we couldвҖҷve gone up to the feast. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңShe didnвҖҷt want us showing off,вҖқ said Ron sagely. вҖңDoesnвҖҷt want people to think itвҖҷs clever, arriving by flying car.вҖқ
When they had eaten as many sandwiches as they could (the plate kept refilling itself), they rose and left the office, treading the familiar path to Gryffindor Tower. The castle was quiet; it seemed that the feast was over. They walked past muttering portraits and creaking suits of armor, and climbed narrow flights of stone stairs, until at last they reached the passage where the secret entrance to Gryffindor Tower was hidden, behind an oil painting of a very fat woman in a pink silk dress.
вҖңPassword?вҖқ she said as they approached.
вҖңEr вҖ”вҖқ said Harry.
They didnвҖҷt know the new yearвҖҷs password, not having met a Gryffindor prefect yet, but help came almost immediately; they heard hurrying feet behind them and turned to see Hermione dashing toward them.
вҖңThere you are! Where have you been? The most ridiculous ruВӯmors вҖ” someone said youвҖҷd been expelled for crashing a flying car вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWell, we havenвҖҷt been expelled,вҖқ Harry assured her.
вҖңYouвҖҷre not telling me you did fly here?вҖқ said Hermione, soundВӯing almost as severe as Professor McGonagall.
вҖңSkip the lecture,вҖқ said Ron impatiently, вҖңand tell us the new password.вҖқ
вҖңItвҖҷs вҖҳwattlebird,вҖҷ вҖқ said Hermione impatiently, вҖңbut thatвҖҷs not the point вҖ”вҖқ
Her words were cut short, however, as the portrait of the fat lady swung open and there was a sudden storm of clapping. It looked as though the whole of Gryffindor House was still awake, packed into the circular common room, standing on the lopsided tables and squashy armchairs, waiting for them to arrive. Arms reached through the portrait hole to pull Harry and Ron inside, leaving Hermione to scramble in after them.
вҖңBrilliant!вҖқ yelled Lee Jordan. вҖңInspired! What an entrance! FlyВӯing a car right into the Whomping Willow, peopleвҖҷll be talking about that one for years вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңGood for you,вҖқ said a fifth year Harry had never spoken to; someone was patting him on the back as though heвҖҷd just won a marathon; Fred and George pushed their way to the front of the crowd and said together, вҖңWhy couldnвҖҷt weвҖҷve come in the car, eh?вҖқ Ron was scarlet in the face, grinning embarrassedly, but Harry could see one person who didnвҖҷt look happy at all. Percy was visible over the heads of some excited first years, and he seemed to be tryВӯing to get near enough to start telling them off. Harry nudged Ron in the ribs and nodded in PercyвҖҷs direction. Ron got the point at once.
вҖңGot to get upstairs вҖ” bit tired,вҖқ he said, and the two of them started pushing their way toward the door on the other side of the room, which led to a spiral staircase and the dormitories.
вҖң вҖҷNight,вҖқ Harry called back to Hermione, who was wearing a scowl just like PercyвҖҷs.
They managed to get to the other side of the common room, still having their backs slapped, and gained the peace of the stairВӯcase. They hurried up it, right to the top, and at last reached the door of their old dormitory, which now had a sign on it saying SECOND YEARS. They entered the familiar, circular room, with its five four-posters hung with red velvet and its high, narrow winВӯdows. Their trunks had been brought up for them and stood at the ends of their beds.
Ron grinned guiltily at Harry.
вҖңI know I shouldnвҖҷtвҖҷve enjoyed that or anything, but вҖ”вҖқ
The dormitory door flew open and in came the other second year Gryffindor boys, Seamus Finnigan, Dean Thomas, and Neville Longbottom.
вҖңUnbelievable!вҖқ beamed Seamus.
вҖңCool,вҖқ said Dean.
вҖңAmazing,вҖқ said Neville, awestruck.
Harry couldnвҖҷt help it. He grinned, too.
## Chapter 6

Gilderoy Lockhart
The next day, however, Harry barely grinned once. Things started to go downhill from breakfast in the Great Hall. The four long House tables were laden with tureens of porridge, plates of kippers, mountains of toast, and dishes of eggs and bacon, beВӯneath the enchanted ceiling (today, a dull, cloudy gray). Harry and Ron sat down at the Gryffindor table next to Hermione, who had her copy of Voyages with Vampires propped open against a milk jug. There was a slight stiffness in the way she said вҖң вҖҷMorning,вҖқ which told Harry that she was still disapproving of the way they had arВӯrived. Neville Longbottom, on the other hand, greeted them cheerВӯfully. Neville was a round-faced and accident-prone boy with the worst memory of anyone Harry had ever met.
вҖңMailвҖҷs due any minute вҖ” I think GranвҖҷs sending a few things I forgot.вҖқ
Harry had only just started his porridge when, sure enough, there was a rushing sound overhead and a hundred or so owls streamed in, circling the hall and dropping letters and packages into the chattering crowd. A big, lumpy package bounced off NevilleвҖҷs head and, a second later, something large and gray fell into HermioneвҖҷs jug, spraying them all with milk and feathers.
вҖңErrol!вҖқ said Ron, pulling the bedraggled owl out by the feet. ErВӯrol slumped, unconscious, onto the table, his legs in the air and a damp red envelope in his beak.
вҖңOh, no вҖ”вҖқ Ron gasped.
вҖңItвҖҷs all right, heвҖҷs still alive,вҖқ said Hermione, prodding Errol gently with the tip of her finger.
вҖңItвҖҷs not that вҖ” itвҖҷs that.вҖқ
Ron was pointing at the red envelope. It looked quite ordinary to Harry, but Ron and Neville were both looking at it as though they expected it to explode.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs the matter?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңSheвҖҷs вҖ” sheвҖҷs sent me a Howler,вҖқ said Ron faintly.
вҖңYouвҖҷd better open it, Ron,вҖқ said Neville in a timid whisper. вҖңItвҖҷll be worse if you donвҖҷt. My gran sent me one once, and I ignored it andвҖқ вҖ” he gulped вҖ” вҖңit was horrible.вҖқ
Harry looked from their petrified faces to the red envelope.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs a Howler?вҖқ he said.
But RonвҖҷs whole attention was fixed on the letter, which had beВӯgun to smoke at the corners.
вҖңOpen it,вҖқ Neville urged. вҖңItвҖҷll all be over in a few minutes вҖ”вҖқ
Ron stretched out a shaking hand, eased the envelope from ErВӯrolвҖҷs beak, and slit it open. Neville stuffed his fingers in his ears. A split second later, Harry knew why. He thought for a moment it had exploded; a roar of sound filled the huge hall, shaking dust from the ceiling.
вҖңвҖ” STEALING THE CAR, I WOULDNвҖҷT HAVE BEEN SURВӯPRISED IF THEYвҖҷD EXPELLED YOU, YOU WAIT TILL I GET HOLD OF YOU, I DONвҖҷT SUPPOSE YOU STOPPED TO THINK WHAT YOUR FATHER AND I WENT THROUGH WHEN WE SAW IT WAS GONE вҖ”вҖқ
Mrs. WeasleyвҖҷs yells, a hundred times louder than usual, made the plates and spoons rattle on the table, and echoed deafeningly off the stone walls. People throughout the hall were swiveling around to see who had received the Howler, and Ron sank so low in his chair that only his crimson forehead could be seen.
вҖңвҖ” LETTER FROM DUMBLEDORE LAST NIGHT, I THOUGHT YOUR FATHER WOULD DIE OF SHAME, WE DIDNвҖҷT BRING YOU UP TO BEHAVE LIKE THIS, YOU AND HARRY COULD BOTH HAVE DIED вҖ”вҖқ
Harry had been wondering when his name was going to crop up. He tried very hard to look as though he couldnвҖҷt hear the voice that was making his eardrums throb.
вҖңвҖ” ABSOLUTELY DISGUSTED вҖ” YOUR FATHERвҖҷS FACВӯING AN INQUIRY AT WORK, ITвҖҷS ENTIRELY YOUR FAULT AND IF YOU PUT ANOTHER TOE OUT OF LINE WEвҖҷLL BRING YOU STRAIGHT BACK HOME.вҖқ
A ringing silence fell. The red envelope, which had dropped from RonвҖҷs hand, burst into flames and curled into ashes. Harry and Ron sat stunned, as though a tidal wave had just passed over them. A few people laughed and, gradually, a babble of talk broke out again.
Hermione closed Voyages with Vampires and looked down at the top of RonвҖҷs head.
вҖңWell, I donвҖҷt know what you expected, Ron, but you вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңDonвҖҷt tell me I deserved it,вҖқ snapped Ron.
Harry pushed his porridge away. His insides were burning with guilt. Mr. Weasley was facing an inquiry at work. After all Mr. and Mrs. Weasley had done for him over the summer вҖҰ
But he had no time to dwell on this; Professor McGonagall was moving along the Gryffindor table, handing out course schedules. Harry took his and saw that they had double Herbology with the Hufflepuffs first.
Harry, Ron, and Hermione left the castle together, crossed the vegetable patch, and made for the greenhouses, where the magical plants were kept. At least the Howler had done one good thing: Hermione seemed to think they had now been punished enough and was being perfectly friendly again.
As they neared the greenhouses they saw the rest of the class standing outside, waiting for Professor Sprout. Harry, Ron, and Hermione had only just joined them when she came striding into view across the lawn, accompanied by Gilderoy Lockhart. ProfesВӯsor SproutвҖҷs arms were full of bandages, and with another twinge of guilt, Harry spotted the Whomping Willow in the distance, several of its branches now in slings.
Professor Sprout was a squat little witch who wore a patched hat over her flyaway hair; there was usually a large amount of earth on her clothes and her fingernails would have made Aunt Petunia faint. Gilderoy Lockhart, however, was immaculate in sweeping robes of turquoise, his golden hair shining under a perfectly posiВӯtioned turquoise hat with gold trimming.
вҖңOh, hello there!вҖқ he called, beaming around at the assembled students. вҖңJust been showing Professor Sprout the right way to docВӯtor a Whomping Willow! But I donвҖҷt want you running away with the idea that IвҖҷm better at Herbology than she is! I just happen to have met several of these exotic plants on my travels вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңGreenhouse three today, chaps!вҖқ said Professor Sprout, who was looking distinctly disgruntled, not at all her usual cheerful self.
There was a murmur of interest. They had only ever worked in greenhouse one before вҖ” greenhouse three housed far more inВӯteresting and dangerous plants. Professor Sprout took a large key from her belt and unlocked the door. Harry caught a whiff of damp earth and fertilizer mingling with the heavy perfume of some giant, umbrella-sized flowers dangling from the ceiling. He was about to follow Ron and Hermione inside when LockhartвҖҷs hand shot out.
вҖңHarry! IвҖҷve been wanting a word вҖ” you donвҖҷt mind if heвҖҷs a couple of minutes late, do you, Professor Sprout?вҖқ
Judging by Professor SproutвҖҷs scowl, she did mind, but Lockhart said, вҖңThatвҖҷs the ticket,вҖқ and closed the greenhouse door in her face.
вҖңHarry,вҖқ said Lockhart, his large white teeth gleaming in the sunlight as he shook his head. вҖңHarry, Harry, Harry.вҖқ
Completely nonplussed, Harry said nothing.
вҖңWhen I heard вҖ” well, of course, it was all my fault. Could have kicked myself.вҖқ
Harry had no idea what he was talking about. He was about to say so when Lockhart went on, вҖңDonвҖҷt know when IвҖҷve been more shocked. Flying a car to Hogwarts! Well, of course, I knew at once why youвҖҷd done it. Stood out a mile. Harry, Harry, Harry.вҖқ
It was remarkable how he could show every one of those brilliant teeth even when he wasnвҖҷt talking.
вҖңGave you a taste for publicity, didnвҖҷt I?вҖқ said Lockhart. вҖңGave you the bug. You got onto the front page of the paper with me and you couldnвҖҷt wait to do it again.вҖқ
вҖңOh, no, Professor, see вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHarry, Harry, Harry,вҖқ said Lockhart, reaching out and grasping his shoulder. вҖңI understand. Natural to want a bit more once youвҖҷve had that first taste вҖ” and I blame myself for giving you that, beВӯcause it was bound to go to your head вҖ” but see here, young man, you canвҖҷt start flying cars to try and get yourself noticed. Just calm down, all right? Plenty of time for all that when youвҖҷre older. Yes, yes, I know what youвҖҷre thinking! вҖҳItвҖҷs all right for him, heвҖҷs an inВӯternationally famous wizard already!вҖҷ But when I was twelve, I was just as much of a nobody as you are now. In fact, IвҖҷd say I was even more of a nobody! I mean, a few people have heard of you, havenвҖҷt they? All that business with He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named!вҖқ He glanced at the lightning scar on HarryвҖҷs forehead. вҖңI know, I know вҖ” itвҖҷs not quite as good as winning Witch WeeklyвҖҷs Most-Charming-Smile Award five times in a row, as I have вҖ” but itвҖҷs a start, Harry, itвҖҷs a start.вҖқ
He gave Harry a hearty wink and strode off. Harry stood stunned for a few seconds, then, remembering he was supposed to be in the greenhouse, he opened the door and slid inside.
Professor Sprout was standing behind a trestle bench in the cenВӯter of the greenhouse. About twenty pairs of different-colored ear-muffs were lying on the bench. When Harry had taken his place between Ron and Hermione, she said, вҖңWeвҖҷll be repotting ManВӯdrakes today. Now, who can tell me the properties of the ManВӯdrake?вҖқ
To nobodyвҖҷs surprise, HermioneвҖҷs hand was first into the air.
вҖңMandrake, or Mandragora, is a powerful restorative,вҖқ said HerВӯmione, sounding as usual as though she had swallowed the textВӯbook. вҖңIt is used to return people who have been transfigured or cursed to their original state.вҖқ
вҖңExcellent. Ten points to Gryffindor,вҖқ said Professor Sprout. вҖңThe Mandrake forms an essential part of most antidotes. It is also, however, dangerous. Who can tell me why?вҖқ
HermioneвҖҷs hand narrowly missed HarryвҖҷs glasses as it shot up again.
вҖңThe cry of the Mandrake is fatal to anyone who hears it,вҖқ she said promptly.
вҖңPrecisely. Take another ten points,вҖқ said Professor Sprout. вҖңNow, the Mandrakes we have here are still very young.вҖқ
She pointed to a row of deep trays as she spoke, and everyone shuffled forward for a better look. A hundred or so tufty little plants, purplish green in color, were growing there in rows. They looked quite unremarkable to Harry, who didnвҖҷt have the slightest idea what Hermione meant by the вҖңcryвҖқ of the Mandrake.
вҖңEveryone take a pair of earmuffs,вҖқ said Professor Sprout.
There was a scramble as everyone tried to seize a pair that wasnвҖҷt pink and fluffy.
вҖңWhen I tell you to put them on, make sure your ears are comВӯpletely covered,вҖқ said Professor Sprout. вҖңWhen it is safe to remove them, I will give you the thumbs-up. Right вҖ” earmuffs on.вҖқ
Harry snapped the earmuffs over his ears. They shut out sound completely. Professor Sprout put the pink, fluffy pair over her own ears, rolled up the sleeves of her robes, grasped one of the tufty plants firmly, and pulled hard.
Harry let out a gasp of surprise that no one could hear.
Instead of roots, a small, muddy, and extremely ugly baby popped out of the earth. The leaves were growing right out of his head. He had pale green, mottled skin, and was clearly bawling at the top of his lungs.
Professor Sprout took a large plant pot from under the table and plunged the Mandrake into it, burying him in dark, damp comВӯpost until only the tufted leaves were visible. Professor Sprout dusted off her hands, gave them all the thumbs-up, and removed her own earmuffs.
вҖңAs our Mandrakes are only seedlings, their cries wonвҖҷt kill yet,вҖқ she said calmly as though sheвҖҷd just done nothing more exciting than water a begonia. вҖңHowever, they will knock you out for sevВӯeral hours, and as IвҖҷm sure none of you want to miss your first day back, make sure your earmuffs are securely in place while you work. I will attract your attention when it is time to pack up.
вҖңFour to a tray вҖ” there is a large supply of pots here вҖ” comВӯpost in the sacks over there вҖ” and be careful of the Venomous Tentacula, itвҖҷs teething.вҖқ
She gave a sharp slap to a spiky, dark red plant as she spoke, making it draw in the long feelers that had been inching sneakily over her shoulder.
Harry, Ron, and Hermione were joined at their tray by a curly-haired Hufflepuff boy Harry knew by sight but had never spoken to.
вҖңJustin Finch-Fletchley,вҖқ he said brightly, shaking Harry by the hand. вҖңKnow who you are, of course, the famous Harry Potter. вҖҰ And youвҖҷre Hermione Granger вҖ” always top in everythingвҖқ (Hermione beamed as she had her hand shaken too) вҖңвҖ” and Ron Weasley. WasnвҖҷt that your flying car?вҖқ
Ron didnвҖҷt smile. The Howler was obviously still on his mind.
вҖңThat LockhartвҖҷs something, isnвҖҷt he?вҖқ said Justin happily as they began filling their plant pots with dragon dung compost. вҖңAwfully brave chap. Have you read his books? IвҖҷd have died of fear if IвҖҷd been cornered in a telephone booth by a werewolf, but he stayed cool and вҖ” zap вҖ” just fantastic.
вҖңMy name was down for Eton, you know. I canвҖҷt tell you how glad I am I came here instead. Of course, Mother was slightly disВӯappointed, but since I made her read LockhartвҖҷs books I think sheвҖҷs begun to see how useful itвҖҷll be to have a fully trained wizard in the family. вҖҰвҖқ
After that they didnвҖҷt have much chance to talk. Their earmuffs were back on and they needed to concentrate on the Mandrakes. Professor Sprout had made it look extremely easy, but it wasnвҖҷt. The Mandrakes didnвҖҷt like coming out of the earth, but didnвҖҷt seem to want to go back into it either. They squirmed, kicked, flailed their sharp little fists, and gnashed their teeth; Harry spent ten whole minutes trying to squash a particularly fat one into a pot.
By the end of the class, Harry, like everyone else, was sweaty, aching, and covered in earth. Everyone traipsed back to the castle for a quick wash and then the Gryffindors hurried off to TransfigВӯuration.
Professor McGonagallвҖҷs classes were always hard work, but today was especially difficult. Everything Harry had learned last year seemed to have leaked out of his head during the summer. He was supposed to be turning a beetle into a button, but all he managed to do was give his beetle a lot of exercise as it scuttled over the deskВӯtop avoiding his wand.
Ron was having far worse problems. He had patched up his wand with some borrowed Spellotape, but it seemed to be damaged beyond repair. It kept crackling and sparking at odd moments, and every time Ron tried to transfigure his beetle it engulfed him in thick gray smoke that smelled of rotten eggs. Unable to see what he was doing, Ron accidentally squashed his beetle with his elВӯbow and had to ask for a new one. Professor McGonagall wasnвҖҷt pleased.
Harry was relieved to hear the lunch bell. His brain felt like a wrung sponge. Everyone filed out of the classroom except him and Ron, who was whacking his wand furiously on the desk.
вҖңStupid вҖ” useless вҖ” thing вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWrite home for another one,вҖқ Harry suggested as the wand let off a volley of bangs like a firecracker.
вҖңOh, yeah, and get another Howler back,вҖқ said Ron, stuffing the now hissing wand into his bag. вҖң вҖҳItвҖҷs your own fault your wand got snapped вҖ”вҖҷ вҖқ
They went down to lunch, where RonвҖҷs mood was not improved by HermioneвҖҷs showing them the handful of perfect coat buttons she had produced in Transfiguration.
вҖңWhatвҖҷve we got this afternoon?вҖқ said Harry, hastily changing the subject.
вҖңDefense Against the Dark Arts,вҖқ said Hermione at once.
вҖңWhy,вҖқ demanded Ron, seizing her schedule, вҖңhave you outlined all LockhartвҖҷs lessons in little hearts?вҖқ
Hermione snatched the schedule back, blushing furiously.
They finished lunch and went outside into the overcast courtВӯyard. Hermione sat down on a stone step and buried her nose in Voyages with Vampires again. Harry and Ron stood talking about Quidditch for several minutes before Harry became aware that he was being closely watched. Looking up, he saw the very small, mousy-haired boy heвҖҷd seen trying on the Sorting Hat last night staring at Harry as though transfixed. He was clutching what looked like an ordinary Muggle camera, and the moment Harry looked at him, he went bright red.
вҖңAll right, Harry? IвҖҷm вҖ” IвҖҷm Colin Creevey,вҖқ he said breathВӯlessly, taking a tentative step forward. вҖңIвҖҷm in Gryffindor, too. DвҖҷyou think вҖ” would it be all right if вҖ” can I have a picture?вҖқ he said, raising the camera hopefully.
вҖңA picture?вҖқ Harry repeated blankly.
вҖңSo I can prove IвҖҷve met you,вҖқ said Colin Creevey eagerly, edgВӯing further forward. вҖңI know all about you. EveryoneвҖҷs told me. About how you survived when You-Know-Who tried to kill you and how he disappeared and everything and how youвҖҷve still got a lightning scar on your foreheadвҖқ (his eyes raked HarryвҖҷs hairline) вҖңand a boy in my dormitory said if I develop the film in the right potion, the picturesвҖҷll move.вҖқ Colin drew a great shuddering breath of excitement and said, вҖңItвҖҷs amazing here, isnвҖҷt it? I never knew all the odd stuff I could do was magic till I got the letter from HogВӯwarts. My dadвҖҷs a milkman, he couldnвҖҷt believe it either. So IвҖҷm takВӯing loads of pictures to send home to him. And itвҖҷd be really good if I had one of youвҖқ вҖ” he looked imploringly at Harry вҖ” вҖңmaybe your friend could take it and I could stand next to you? And then, could you sign it?вҖқ
вҖңSigned photos? YouвҖҷre giving out signed photos, Potter?вҖқ
Loud and scathing, Draco MalfoyвҖҷs voice echoed around the courtyard. He had stopped right behind Colin, flanked, as he alВӯways was at Hogwarts, by his large and thuggish cronies, Crabbe and Goyle.
вҖңEveryone line up!вҖқ Malfoy roared to the crowd. вҖңHarry PotterвҖҷs giving out signed photos!вҖқ
вҖңNo, IвҖҷm not,вҖқ said Harry angrily, his fists clenching. вҖңShut up, Malfoy.вҖқ
вҖңYouвҖҷre just jealous,вҖқ piped up Colin, whose entire body was about as thick as CrabbeвҖҷs neck.
вҖңJealous?вҖқ said Malfoy, who didnвҖҷt need to shout anymore: Half the courtyard was listening in. вҖңOf what? I donвҖҷt want a foul scar right across my head, thanks. I donвҖҷt think getting your head cut open makes you that special, myself.вҖқ
Crabbe and Goyle were sniggering stupidly.
вҖңEat slugs, Malfoy,вҖқ said Ron angrily. Crabbe stopped laughing and started rubbing his knuckles in a menacing way.
вҖңBe careful, Weasley,вҖқ sneered Malfoy. вҖңYou donвҖҷt want to start any trouble or your mommyвҖҷll have to come and take you away from school.вҖқ He put on a shrill, piercing voice. вҖңIf you put another toe out of line вҖ”вҖқ
A knot of Slytherin fifth years nearby laughed loudly at this.
вҖңWeasley would like a signed photo, Potter,вҖқ smirked Malfoy. вҖңItвҖҷd be worth more than his familyвҖҷs whole house вҖ”вҖқ
Ron whipped out his Spellotaped wand, but Hermione shut Voyages with Vampires with a snap and whispered, вҖңLook out!вҖқ
вҖңWhatвҖҷs all this, whatвҖҷs all this?вҖқ Gilderoy Lockhart was striding toward them, his turquoise robes swirling behind him. вҖңWhoвҖҷs givВӯing out signed photos?вҖқ
Harry started to speak but he was cut short as Lockhart flung an arm around his shoulders and thundered jovially, вҖңShouldnвҖҷt have asked! We meet again, Harry!вҖқ
Pinned to LockhartвҖҷs side and burning with humiliation, Harry saw Malfoy slide smirking back into the crowd.
вҖңCome on then, Mr. Creevey,вҖқ said Lockhart, beaming at Colin. вҖңA double portrait, canвҖҷt do better than that, and weвҖҷll both sign it for you.вҖқ
Colin fumbled for his camera and took the picture as the bell rang behind them, signaling the start of afternoon classes.
вҖңOff you go, move along there,вҖқ Lockhart called to the crowd, and he set off back to the castle with Harry, who was wishing he knew a good Vanishing Spell, still clasped to his side.
вҖңA word to the wise, Harry,вҖқ said Lockhart paternally as they entered the building through a side door. вҖңI covered up for you back there with young Creevey вҖ” if he was photographing me, too, your schoolmates wonвҖҷt think youвҖҷre setting yourself up so much. вҖҰвҖқ
Deaf to HarryвҖҷs stammers, Lockhart swept him down a corridor lined with staring students and up a staircase.
вҖңLet me just say that handing out signed pictures at this stage of your career isnвҖҷt sensible вҖ” looks a tad bigheaded, Harry, to be frank. There may well come a time when, like me, youвҖҷll need to keep a stack handy wherever you go, butвҖқ вҖ” he gave a little chorВӯtle вҖ” вҖңI donвҖҷt think youвҖҷre quite there yet.вҖқ
They had reached LockhartвҖҷs classroom and he let Harry go at last. Harry yanked his robes straight and headed for a seat at the very back of the class, where he busied himself with piling all seven of LockhartвҖҷs books in front of him, so that he could avoid looking at the real thing.
The rest of the class came clattering in, and Ron and Hermione sat down on either side of Harry.
вҖңYou couldвҖҷve fried an egg on your face,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңYouвҖҷd better hope Creevey doesnвҖҷt meet Ginny, or theyвҖҷll be starting a Harry Potter fan club.вҖқ
вҖңShut up,вҖқ snapped Harry. The last thing he needed was for Lockhart to hear the phrase вҖңHarry Potter fan club.вҖқ
When the whole class was seated, Lockhart cleared his throat loudly and silence fell. He reached forward, picked up Neville LongbottomвҖҷs copy of Travels with Trolls, and held it up to show his own, winking portrait on the front.
вҖңMe,вҖқ he said, pointing at it and winking as well. вҖңGilderoy Lockhart, Order of Merlin, Third Class, Honorary Member of the Dark Force Defense League, and five-time winner of Witch WeeklyвҖҷs Most-Charming-Smile Award вҖ” but I donвҖҷt talk about that. I didnвҖҷt get rid of the Bandon Banshee by smiling at her!вҖқ
He waited for them to laugh; a few people smiled weakly.
вҖңI see youвҖҷve all bought a complete set of my books вҖ” well done. I thought weвҖҷd start today with a little quiz. Nothing to worry about вҖ” just to check how well youвҖҷve read them, how much youвҖҷve taken in вҖ”вҖқ
When he had handed out the test papers he returned to the front of the class and said, вҖңYou have thirty minutes вҖ” start вҖ” now!вҖқ
Harry looked down at his paper and read:
1. What is Gilderoy LockhartвҖҷs favorite color?
2. What is Gilderoy LockhartвҖҷs secret ambition?
3. What, in your opinion, is Gilderoy LockhartвҖҷs
greatest achievement to date?
On and on it went, over three sides of paper, right down to:
54. When is Gilderoy LockhartвҖҷs birthday, and what
would his ideal gift be?
Half an hour later, Lockhart collected the papers and rifled through them in front of the class.
вҖңTut, tut вҖ” hardly any of you remembered that my favorite color is lilac. I say so in Year with the Yeti. And a few of you need to read Wanderings with Werewolves more carefully вҖ” I clearly state in chapter twelve that my ideal birthday gift would be harmony beВӯtween all magic and non-magic peoples вҖ” though I wouldnвҖҷt say no to a large bottle of OgdenвҖҷs Old Firewhisky!вҖқ
He gave them another roguish wink. Ron was now staring at Lockhart with an expression of disbelief on his face; Seamus FinniВӯgan and Dean Thomas, who were sitting in front, were shaking with silent laughter. Hermione, on the other hand, was listening to Lockhart with rapt attention and gave a start when he mentioned her name.
вҖңвҖҰ but Miss Hermione Granger knew my secret ambition is to rid the world of evil and market my own range of hair-care poВӯtions вҖ” good girl! In factвҖқ вҖ” he flipped her paper over вҖ” вҖңfull marks! Where is Miss Hermione Granger?вҖқ
Hermione raised a trembling hand.
вҖңExcellent!вҖқ beamed Lockhart. вҖңQuite excellent! Take ten points for Gryffindor! And so вҖ” to business вҖ”вҖқ
He bent down behind his desk and lifted a large, covered cage onto it.
вҖңNow вҖ” be warned! It is my job to arm you against the foulest creatures known to wizardkind! You may find yourselves facing your worst fears in this room. Know only that no harm can befall you whilst I am here. All I ask is that you remain calm.вҖқ
In spite of himself, Harry leaned around his pile of books for a better look at the cage. Lockhart placed a hand on the cover. Dean and Seamus had stopped laughing now. Neville was cowering in his front row seat.
вҖңI must ask you not to scream,вҖқ said Lockhart in a low voice. вҖңIt might provoke them.вҖқ
As the whole class held its breath, Lockhart whipped off the cover.
вҖңYes,вҖқ he said dramatically. вҖңFreshly caught Cornish pixies.вҖқ
Seamus Finnigan couldnвҖҷt control himself. He let out a snort of laughter that even Lockhart couldnвҖҷt mistake for a scream of terror.
вҖңYes?вҖқ He smiled at Seamus.
вҖңWell, theyвҖҷre not вҖ” theyвҖҷre not very вҖ” dangerous, are they?вҖқ Seamus choked.
вҖңDonвҖҷt be so sure!вҖқ said Lockhart, waggling a finger annoyingly at Seamus. вҖңDevilish tricky little blighters they can be!вҖқ
The pixies were electric blue and about eight inches high, with pointed faces and voices so shrill it was like listening to a lot of budgies arguing. The moment the cover had been removed, they had started jabbering and rocketing around, rattling the bars and making bizarre faces at the people nearest them.
вҖңRight, then,вҖқ Lockhart said loudly. вҖңLetвҖҷs see what you make of them!вҖқ And he opened the cage.
It was pandemonium. The pixies shot in every direction like rockets. Two of them seized Neville by the ears and lifted him into the air. Several shot straight through the window, showering the back row with broken glass. The rest proceeded to wreck the classВӯroom more effectively than a rampaging rhino. They grabbed ink bottles and sprayed the class with them, shredded books and paВӯpers, tore pictures from the walls, up-ended the waste basket, grabbed bags and books and threw them out of the smashed winВӯdow; within minutes, half the class was sheltering under desks and Neville was swinging from the iron chandelier in the ceiling.
вҖңCome on now вҖ” round them up, round them up, theyвҖҷre only pixies,вҖқ Lockhart shouted.
He rolled up his sleeves, brandished his wand, and bellowed, вҖңPeskipiksi Pesternomi!вҖқ
It had absolutely no effect; one of the pixies seized his wand and threw it out of the window, too. Lockhart gulped and dived under his own desk, narrowly avoiding being squashed by Neville, who fell a second later as the chandelier gave way.
The bell rang and there was a mad rush toward the exit. In the relative calm that followed, Lockhart straightened up, caught sight of Harry, Ron, and Hermione, who were almost at the door, and said, вҖңWell, IвҖҷll ask you three to just nip the rest of them back into their cage.вҖқ He swept past them and shut the door quickly behind him.
вҖңCan you believe him?вҖқ roared Ron as one of the remaining pixВӯies bit him painfully on the ear.
вҖңHe just wants to give us some hands-on experience,вҖқ said Hermione, immobilizing two pixies at once with a clever Freezing Charm and stuffing them back into their cage.
вҖңHands on?вҖқ said Harry, who was trying to grab a pixie dancing out of reach with its tongue out. вҖңHermione, he didnвҖҷt have a clue what he was doing вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңRubbish,вҖқ said Hermione. вҖңYouвҖҷve read his books вҖ” look at all those amazing things heвҖҷs done вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHe says heвҖҷs done,вҖқ Ron muttered.
## Chapter 7

Mudbloods and Murmurs
Harry spent a lot of time over the next few days dodging out of sight whenever he saw Gilderoy Lockhart coming down a corridor. Harder to avoid was Colin Creevey, who seemed to have memorized HarryвҖҷs schedule. Nothing seemed to give Colin a bigger thrill than to say, вҖңAll right, Harry?вҖқ six or seven times a day and hear, вҖңHello, Colin,вҖқ back, however exasperated Harry sounded when he said it.
Hedwig was still angry with Harry about the disasterous car journey and RonвҖҷs wand was still malfunctioning, surpassing itself on Friday morning by shooting out of RonвҖҷs hand in Charms and hitting tiny old Professor Flitwick squarely between the eyes, creatВӯing a large, throbbing green boil where it had struck. So with one thing and another, Harry was quite glad to reach the weekend. He, Ron, and Hermione were planning to visit Hagrid on Saturday morning. Harry, however, was shaken awake several hours earlier than he would have liked by Oliver Wood, Captain of the GryfВӯfindor Quidditch team.
вҖңWhassamatter?вҖқ said Harry groggily.
вҖңQuidditch practice!вҖқ said Wood. вҖңCome on!вҖқ
Harry squinted at the window. There was a thin mist hanging across the pink-and-gold sky. Now that he was awake, he couldnвҖҷt understand how he could have slept through the racket the birds were making.
вҖңOliver,вҖқ Harry croaked. вҖңItвҖҷs the crack of dawn.вҖқ
вҖңExactly,вҖқ said Wood. He was a tall and burly sixth year and, at the moment, his eyes were gleaming with a crazed enthusiasm. вҖңItвҖҷs part of our new training program. Come on, grab your broom, and letвҖҷs go,вҖқ said Wood heartily. вҖңNone of the other teams have started training yet; weвҖҷre going to be first off the mark this year вҖ”вҖқ
Yawning and shivering slightly, Harry climbed out of bed and tried to find his Quidditch robes.
вҖңGood man,вҖқ said Wood. вҖңMeet you on the field in fifteen minВӯutes.вҖқ
When heвҖҷd found his scarlet team robes and pulled on his cloak for warmth, Harry scribbled a note to Ron explaining where heвҖҷd gone and went down the spiral staircase to the common room, his Nimbus Two Thousand on his shoulder. He had just reached the portrait hole when there was a clatter behind him and Colin Creevey came dashing down the spiral staircase, his camera swinging madly around his neck and something clutched in his hand.
вҖңI heard someone saying your name on the stairs, Harry! Look what IвҖҷve got here! IвҖҷve had it developed, I wanted to show you вҖ”вҖқ
Harry looked bemusedly at the photograph Colin was brandishВӯing under his nose.
A moving, black-and-white Lockhart was tugging hard on an arm Harry recognized as his own. He was pleased to see that his photographic self was putting up a good fight and refusing to be dragged into view. As Harry watched, Lockhart gave up and slumped, panting, against the white edge of the picture.
вҖңWill you sign it?вҖқ said Colin eagerly.
вҖңNo,вҖқ said Harry flatly, glancing around to check that the room was really deserted. вҖңSorry, Colin, IвҖҷm in a hurry вҖ” Quidditch practice вҖ”вҖқ
He climbed through the portrait hole.
вҖңOh, wow! Wait for me! IвҖҷve never watched a Quidditch game before!вҖқ
Colin scrambled through the hole after him.
вҖңItвҖҷll be really boring,вҖқ Harry said quickly, but Colin ignored him, his face shining with excitement.
вҖңYou were the youngest House player in a hundred years, werenвҖҷt you, Harry? WerenвҖҷt you?вҖқ said Colin, trotting alongside him. вҖңYou must be brilliant. IвҖҷve never flown. Is it easy? Is that your own broom? Is that the best one there is?вҖқ
Harry didnвҖҷt know how to get rid of him. It was like having an extremely talkative shadow.
вҖңI donвҖҷt really understand Quidditch,вҖқ said Colin breathlessly. вҖңIs it true there are four balls? And two of them fly around trying to knock people off their brooms?вҖқ
вҖңYes,вҖқ said Harry heavily, resigned to explaining the complicated rules of Quidditch. вҖңTheyвҖҷre called Bludgers. There are two Beaters on each team who carry clubs to beat the Bludgers away from their side. Fred and George Weasley are the Gryffindor Beaters.вҖқ
вҖңAnd what are the other balls for?вҖқ Colin asked, tripping down a couple of steps because he was gazing open-mouthed at Harry.
вҖңWell, the Quaffle вҖ” thatвҖҷs the biggish red one вҖ” is the one that scores goals. Three Chasers on each team throw the Quaffle to each other and try and get it through the goal posts at the end of the pitch вҖ” theyвҖҷre three long poles with hoops on the end.вҖқ
вҖңAnd the fourth ball вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңвҖ” is the Golden Snitch,вҖқ said Harry, вҖңand itвҖҷs very small, very fast, and difficult to catch. But thatвҖҷs what the SeekerвҖҷs got to do, because a game of Quidditch doesnвҖҷt end until the Snitch has been caught. And whichever teamвҖҷs Seeker gets the Snitch earns his team an extra hundred and fifty points.вҖқ
вҖңAnd youвҖҷre the Gryffindor Seeker, arenвҖҷt you?вҖқ said Colin in awe.
вҖңYes,вҖқ said Harry as they left the castle and started across the dew-drenched grass. вҖңAnd thereвҖҷs the Keeper, too. He guards the goal posts. ThatвҖҷs it, really.вҖқ
But Colin didnвҖҷt stop questioning Harry all the way down the sloping lawns to the Quidditch field, and Harry only shook him off when he reached the changing rooms; Colin called after him in a piping voice, вҖңIвҖҷll go and get a good seat, Harry!вҖқ and hurried off to the stands.
The rest of the Gryffindor team were already in the changВӯing room. Wood was the only person who looked truly awake. Fred and George Weasley were sitting, puffy-eyed and tousle-haired, next to fourth year Alicia Spinnet, who seemed to be nodВӯding off against the wall behind her. Her fellow Chasers, Katie Bell and Angelina Johnson, were yawning side by side opposite them.
вҖңThere you are, Harry, what kept you?вҖқ said Wood briskly. вҖңNow, I wanted a quick talk with you all before we actually get onto the field, because I spent the summer devising a whole new training program, which I really think will make all the differВӯence. вҖҰвҖқ
Wood was holding up a large diagram of a Quidditch field, on which were drawn many lines, arrows, and crosses in different-colored inks. He took out his wand, tapped the board, and the arrows began to wiggle over the diagram like caterpillars. As Wood launched into a speech about his new tactics, Fred WeasleyвҖҷs head drooped right onto Alicia SpinnetвҖҷs shoulder and he began to snore.
The first board took nearly twenty minutes to explain, but there was another board under that, and a third under that one. Harry sank into a stupor as Wood droned on and on.
вҖңSo,вҖқ said Wood, at long last, jerking Harry from a wistful fanВӯtasy about what he could be eating for breakfast at this very moВӯment up at the castle. вҖңIs that clear? Any questions?вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷve got a question, Oliver,вҖқ said George, who had woken with a start. вҖңWhy couldnвҖҷt you have told us all this yesterday when we were awake?вҖқ
Wood wasnвҖҷt pleased.
вҖңNow, listen here, you lot,вҖқ he said, glowering at them all. вҖңWe should have won the Quidditch Cup last year. WeвҖҷre easily the best team. But unfortunately вҖ” owing to circumstances beyond our control вҖ”вҖқ
