Harry shifted guiltily in his seat. He had been unconscious in the hospital wing for the final match of the previous year, meaning that Gryffindor had been a player short and had suffered their worst defeat in three hundred years.
Wood took a moment to regain control of himself. Their last deВӯfeat was clearly still torturing him.
вҖңSo this year, we train harder than ever before. вҖҰ Okay, letвҖҷs go and put our new theories into practice!вҖқ Wood shouted, seizing his broomstick and leading the way out of the locker rooms. Stiff-legged and still yawning, his team followed.
They had been in the locker room so long that the sun was up completely now, although remnants of mist hung over the grass in the stadium. As Harry walked onto the field, he saw Ron and HerВӯmione sitting in the stands.
вҖңArenвҖҷt you finished yet?вҖқ called Ron incredulously.
вҖңHavenвҖҷt even started,вҖқ said Harry, looking jealously at the toast and marmalade Ron and Hermione had brought out of the Great Hall. вҖңWoodвҖҷs been teaching us new moves.вҖқ
He mounted his broomstick and kicked at the ground, soaring up into the air. The cool morning air whipped his face, waking him far more effectively than WoodвҖҷs long talk. It felt wonderful to be back on the Quidditch field. He soared right around the stadium at full speed, racing Fred and George.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs that funny clicking noise?вҖқ called Fred as they hurtled around the corner.
Harry looked into the stands. Colin was sitting in one of the highest seats, his camera raised, taking picture after picture, the sound strangely magnified in the deserted stadium.
вҖңLook this way, Harry! This way!вҖқ he cried shrilly.
вҖңWhoвҖҷs that?вҖқ said Fred.
вҖңNo idea,вҖқ Harry lied, putting on a spurt of speed that took him as far away as possible from Colin.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs going on?вҖқ said Wood, frowning, as he skimmed through the air toward them. вҖңWhyвҖҷs that first year taking pictures? I donвҖҷt like it. He could be a Slytherin spy, trying to find out about our new training program.вҖқ
вҖңHeвҖҷs in Gryffindor,вҖқ said Harry quickly.
вҖңAnd the Slytherins donвҖҷt need a spy, Oliver,вҖқ said George.
вҖңWhat makes you say that?вҖқ said Wood testily.
вҖңBecause theyвҖҷre here in person,вҖқ said George, pointing.
Several people in green robes were walking onto the field, broomsticks in their hands.
вҖңI donвҖҷt believe it!вҖқ Wood hissed in outrage. вҖңI booked the field for today! WeвҖҷll see about this!вҖқ
Wood shot toward the ground, landing rather harder than he meant to in his anger, staggering slightly as he dismounted. Harry, Fred, and George followed.
вҖңFlint!вҖқ Wood bellowed at the Slytherin Captain. вҖңThis is our practice time! We got up specially! You can clear off now!вҖқ
Marcus Flint was even larger than Wood. He had a look of trollВӯish cunning on his face as he replied, вҖңPlenty of room for all of us, Wood.вҖқ
Angelina, Alicia, and Katie had come over, too. There were no girls on the Slytherin team, who stood shoulder to shoulder, facing the Gryffindors, leering to a man.
вҖңBut I booked the field!вҖқ said Wood, positively spitting with rage. вҖңI booked it!вҖқ
вҖңAh,вҖқ said Flint. вҖңBut IвҖҷve got a specially signed note here from Professor Snape. вҖҳI, Professor S. Snape, give the Slytherin team perВӯmission to practice today on the Quidditch field owing to the need to train their new Seeker.вҖҷ вҖқ
вҖңYouвҖҷve got a new Seeker?вҖқ said Wood, distracted. вҖңWhere?вҖқ
And from behind the six large figures before them came a sevВӯenth, smaller boy, smirking all over his pale, pointed face. It was Draco Malfoy.
вҖңArenвҖҷt you Lucius MalfoyвҖҷs son?вҖқ said Fred, looking at Malfoy with dislike.
вҖңFunny you should mention DracoвҖҷs father,вҖқ said Flint as the whole Slytherin team smiled still more broadly. вҖңLet me show you the generous gift heвҖҷs made to the Slytherin team.вҖқ
All seven of them held out their broomsticks. Seven highly polВӯished, brand-new handles and seven sets of fine gold lettering spelling the words Nimbus Two Thousand and One gleamed under the GryffindorsвҖҷ noses in the early morning sun.
вҖңVery latest model. Only came out last month,вҖқ said Flint carelessly, flicking a speck of dust from the end of his own. вҖңI beВӯlieve it outstrips the old Two Thousand series by a considerable amount. As for the old CleansweepsвҖқ вҖ” he smiled nastily at Fred and George, who were both clutching Cleansweep Fives вҖ” вҖңsweeps the board with them.вҖқ
None of the Gryffindor team could think of anything to say for a moment. Malfoy was smirking so broadly his cold eyes were reВӯduced to slits.
вҖңOh, look,вҖқ said Flint. вҖңA field invasion.вҖқ
Ron and Hermione were crossing the grass to see what was goВӯing on.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs happening?вҖқ Ron asked Harry. вҖңWhy arenвҖҷt you playВӯing? And whatвҖҷs he doing here?вҖқ
He was looking at Malfoy, taking in his Slytherin Quidditch robes.
вҖңIвҖҷm the new Slytherin Seeker, Weasley,вҖқ said Malfoy, smugly. вҖңEveryoneвҖҷs just been admiring the brooms my fatherвҖҷs bought our team.вҖқ
Ron gaped, openmouthed, at the seven superb broomsticks in front of him.
вҖңGood, arenвҖҷt they?вҖқ said Malfoy smoothly. вҖңBut perhaps the Gryffindor team will be able to raise some gold and get new brooms, too. You could raffle off those Cleansweep Fives; I expect a museum would bid for them.вҖқ
The Slytherin team howled with laughter.
вҖңAt least no one on the Gryffindor team had to buy their way in,вҖқ said Hermione sharply. вҖңThey got in on pure talent.вҖқ
The smug look on MalfoyвҖҷs face flickered.
вҖңNo one asked your opinion, you filthy little Mudblood,вҖқ he spat.
Harry knew at once that Malfoy had said something really bad because there was an instant uproar at his words. Flint had to dive in front of Malfoy to stop Fred and George jumping on him, AliВӯcia shrieked, вҖңHow dare you!вҖқ, and Ron plunged his hand into his robes, pulled out his wand, yelling, вҖңYouвҖҷll pay for that one, MalВӯfoy!вҖқ and pointed it furiously under FlintвҖҷs arm at MalfoyвҖҷs face.
A loud bang echoed around the stadium and a jet of green light shot out of the wrong end of RonвҖҷs wand, hitting him in the stomВӯach and sending him reeling backward onto the grass.
вҖңRon! Ron! Are you all right?вҖқ squealed Hermione.
Ron opened his mouth to speak, but no words came out. Instead he gave an almighty belch and several slugs dribbled out of his mouth onto his lap.
The Slytherin team were paralyzed with laughter. Flint was douВӯbled up, hanging onto his new broomstick for support. Malfoy was on all fours, banging the ground with his fist. The Gryffindors were gathered around Ron, who kept belching large, glistening slugs. Nobody seemed to want to touch him.
вҖңWeвҖҷd better get him to HagridвҖҷs, itвҖҷs nearest,вҖқ said Harry to Hermione, who nodded bravely, and the pair of them pulled Ron up by the arms.
вҖңWhat happened, Harry? What happened? Is he ill? But you can cure him, canвҖҷt you?вҖқ Colin had run down from his seat and was now dancing alongside them as they left the field. Ron gave a huge heave and more slugs dribbled down his front.
вҖңOooh,вҖқ said Colin, fascinated and raising his camera. вҖңCan you hold him still, Harry?вҖқ
вҖңGet out of the way, Colin!вҖқ said Harry angrily. He and HerВӯmione supported Ron out of the stadium and across the grounds toward the edge of the forest.
вҖңNearly there, Ron,вҖқ said Hermione as the gamekeeperвҖҷs cabin came into view. вҖңYouвҖҷll be all right in a minute вҖ” almost there вҖ”вҖқ
They were within twenty feet of HagridвҖҷs house when the front door opened, but it wasnвҖҷt Hagrid who emerged. Gilderoy LockВӯhart, wearing robes of palest mauve today, came striding out.
вҖңQuick, behind here,вҖқ Harry hissed, dragging Ron behind a nearby bush. Hermione followed, somewhat reluctantly.
вҖңItвҖҷs a simple matter if you know what youвҖҷre doing!вҖқ Lockhart was saying loudly to Hagrid. вҖңIf you need help, you know where I am! IвҖҷll let you have a copy of my book. IвҖҷm surprised you havenвҖҷt already got one вҖ” IвҖҷll sign one tonight and send it over. Well, good-bye!вҖқ And he strode away toward the castle.
Harry waited until Lockhart was out of sight, then pulled Ron out of the bush and up to HagridвҖҷs front door. They knocked urВӯgently.
Hagrid appeared at once, looking very grumpy, but his expresВӯsion brightened when he saw who it was.
вҖңBin wonderinвҖҷ when youвҖҷd come ter see me вҖ” come in, come in вҖ” thought you mighta bin Professor Lockhart back again вҖ”вҖқ
Harry and Hermione supported Ron over the threshold into the one-roomed cabin, which had an enormous bed in one corner, a fire crackling merrily in the other. Hagrid didnвҖҷt seem perturbed by RonвҖҷs slug problem, which Harry hastily explained as he lowered Ron into a chair.
вҖңBetter out than in,вҖқ he said cheerfully, plunking a large copper basin in front of him. вҖңGet вҖҷem all up, Ron.вҖқ
вҖңI donвҖҷt think thereвҖҷs anything to do except wait for it to stop,вҖқ said Hermione anxiously, watching Ron bend over the basin. вҖңThatвҖҷs a difficult curse to work at the best of times, but with a broВӯken wand вҖ”вҖқ
Hagrid was bustling around making them tea. His boarhound, Fang, was slobbering over Harry.
вҖңWhat did Lockhart want with you, Hagrid?вҖқ Harry asked, scratching FangвҖҷs ears.
вҖңGivinвҖҷ me advice on gettinвҖҷ kelpies out of a well,вҖқ growled Hagrid, moving a half-plucked rooster off his scrubbed table and setting down the teapot. вҖңLike I donвҖҷ know. AnвҖҷ banginвҖҷ on about some banshee he banished. If one word of it was true, IвҖҷll eat my kettle.вҖқ
It was most unlike Hagrid to criticize a Hogwarts teacher, and Harry looked at him in surprise. Hermione, however, said in a voice somewhat higher than usual, вҖңI think youвҖҷre being a bit unВӯfair. Professor Dumbledore obviously thought he was the best man for the job вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHe was the onвҖҷy man for the job,вҖқ said Hagrid, offering them a plate of treacle toffee, while Ron coughed squelchily into his basin. вҖңAnвҖҷ I mean the onвҖҷy one. GettinвҖҷ very difficult ter find anyone fer the Dark Arts job. People arenвҖҷt too keen ter take it on, see. TheyвҖҷre startinвҖҷ ter think itвҖҷs jinxed. No oneвҖҷs lasted long fer a while now. So tell me,вҖқ said Hagrid, jerking his head at Ron. вҖңWho was he tryinвҖҷ ter curse?вҖқ
вҖңMalfoy called Hermione something вҖ” it mustвҖҷve been really bad, because everyone went wild.вҖқ
вҖңIt was bad,вҖқ said Ron hoarsely, emerging over the tabletop lookВӯing pale and sweaty. вҖңMalfoy called her вҖҳMudblood,вҖҷ Hagrid вҖ”вҖқ
Ron dived out of sight again as a fresh wave of slugs made their appearance. Hagrid looked outraged.
вҖңHe didnвҖҷ!вҖқ he growled at Hermione.
вҖңHe did,вҖқ she said. вҖңBut I donвҖҷt know what it means. I could tell it was really rude, of course вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңItвҖҷs about the most insulting thing he could think of,вҖқ gasped Ron, coming back up. вҖңMudbloodвҖҷs a really foul name for someone who is Muggle-born вҖ” you know, non-magic parents. There are some wizards вҖ” like MalfoyвҖҷs family вҖ” who think theyвҖҷre better than everyone else because theyвҖҷre what people call pure-blood.вҖқ He gave a small burp, and a single slug fell into his outstretched hand. He threw it into the basin and continued, вҖңI mean, the rest of us know it doesnвҖҷt make any difference at all. Look at Neville Longbottom вҖ” heвҖҷs pure-blood and he can hardly stand a caulВӯdron the right way up.вҖқ
вҖңAnвҖҷ they havenвҖҷt invented a spell our Hermione canвҖҷ do,вҖқ said Hagrid proudly, making Hermione go a brilliant shade of magenta.
вҖңItвҖҷs a disgusting thing to call someone,вҖқ said Ron, wiping his sweaty brow with a shaking hand. вҖңDirty blood, see. Common blood. ItвҖҷs ridiculous. Most wizards these days are half-blood anyВӯway. If we hadnвҖҷt married Muggles weвҖҷdвҖҷve died out.вҖқ
He retched and ducked out of sight again.
вҖңWell, I donвҖҷ blame yeh fer tryinвҖҷ ter curse him, Ron,вҖқ said HaВӯgrid loudly over the thuds of more slugs hitting the basin. вҖңBuвҖҷ maybe it was a good thing yer wand backfired. вҖҷSpect Lucius MalВӯfoy wouldвҖҷve come marchinвҖҷ up ter school if yehвҖҷd cursed his son. Least yer not in trouble.вҖқ
Harry would have pointed out that trouble didnвҖҷt come much worse than having slugs pouring out of your mouth, but he couldnвҖҷt; HagridвҖҷs treacle toffee had cemented his jaws together.
вҖңHarry,вҖқ said Hagrid abruptly as though struck by a sudden thought. вҖңGotta bone ter pick with yeh. IвҖҷve heard youвҖҷve bin givinвҖҷ out signed photos. How come I havenвҖҷt got one?вҖқ
Furious, Harry wrenched his teeth apart.
вҖңI have not been giving out signed photos,вҖқ he said hotly. вҖңIf LockhartвҖҷs still spreading that around вҖ”вҖқ
But then he saw that Hagrid was laughing.
вҖңIвҖҷm onвҖҷy jokinвҖҷ,вҖқ he said, patting Harry genially on the back and sending him face first into the table. вҖңI knew yeh hadnвҖҷt really. I told Lockhart yeh didnвҖҷ need teh. Yer more famous than him withВӯout tryinвҖҷ.вҖқ
вҖңBet he didnвҖҷt like that,вҖқ said Harry, sitting up and rubbing his chin.
вҖңDonвҖҷ think he did,вҖқ said Hagrid, his eyes twinkling. вҖңAnвҖҷ then I told him IвҖҷd never read one oвҖҷ his books anвҖҷ he decided ter go. Treacle toffee, Ron?вҖқ he added as Ron reappeared.
вҖңNo thanks,вҖқ said Ron weakly. вҖңBetter not risk it.вҖқ
вҖңCome anвҖҷ see what IвҖҷve bin growinвҖҷ,вҖқ said Hagrid as Harry and Hermione finished the last of their tea.
In the small vegetable patch behind HagridвҖҷs house were a dozen of the largest pumpkins Harry had ever seen. Each was the size of a large boulder.
вҖңGettinвҖҷ on well, arenвҖҷt they?вҖқ said Hagrid happily. вҖңFer the HalВӯloween feast вҖҰ should be big enough by then.вҖқ
вҖңWhatвҖҷve you been feeding them?вҖқ said Harry.
Hagrid looked over his shoulder to check that they were alone.
вҖңWell, IвҖҷve bin givinвҖҷ them вҖ” you know вҖ” a bit oвҖҷ help вҖ”вҖқ
Harry noticed HagridвҖҷs flowery pink umbrella leaning against the back wall of the cabin. Harry had had reason to believe before now that this umbrella was not all it looked; in fact, he had the strong impression that HagridвҖҷs old school wand was concealed inВӯside it. Hagrid wasnвҖҷt supposed to use magic. He had been expelled from Hogwarts in his third year, but Harry had never found out why вҖ” any mention of the matter and Hagrid would clear his throat loudly and become mysteriously deaf until the subject was changed.
вҖңAn Engorgement Charm, I suppose?вҖқ said Hermione, halfway between disapproval and amusement. вҖңWell, youвҖҷve done a good job on them.вҖқ
вҖңThatвҖҷs what yer little sister said,вҖқ said Hagrid, nodding at Ron. вҖңMet her jusвҖҷ yesterday.вҖқ Hagrid looked sideways at Harry, his beard twitching. вҖңSaid she was jusвҖҷ lookinвҖҷ round the grounds, but I reckon she was hopinвҖҷ she might run inter someone else at my house.вҖқ He winked at Harry. вҖңIf yeh ask me, she wouldnвҖҷ say no ter a signed вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңOh, shut up,вҖқ said Harry. Ron snorted with laughter and the ground was sprayed with slugs.
вҖңWatch it!вҖқ Hagrid roared, pulling Ron away from his precious pumpkins.
It was nearly lunchtime and as Harry had only had one bit of treacle toffee since dawn, he was keen to go back to school to eat. They said good-bye to Hagrid and walked back up to the castle, Ron hiccoughing occasionally, but only bringing up two very small slugs.
They had barely set foot in the cool entrance hall when a voice rang out, вҖңThere you are, Potter вҖ” Weasley.вҖқ Professor McGonaВӯgall was walking toward them, looking stern. вҖңYou will both do your detentions this evening.вҖқ
вҖңWhatвҖҷre we doing, Professor?вҖқ said Ron, nervously suppressing a burp.
вҖңYou will be polishing the silver in the trophy room with Mr. Filch,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall. вҖңAnd no magic, Weasley вҖ” elВӯbow grease.вҖқ
Ron gulped. Argus Filch, the caretaker, was loathed by every stuВӯdent in the school.
вҖңAnd you, Potter, will be helping Professor Lockhart answer his fan mail,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall.
вҖңOh n вҖ” Professor, canвҖҷt I go and do the trophy room, too?вҖқ said Harry desperately.
вҖңCertainly not,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall, raising her eyebrows. вҖңProfessor Lockhart requested you particularly. Eight oвҖҷclock sharp, both of you.вҖқ
Harry and Ron slouched into the Great Hall in states of deepest gloom, Hermione behind them, wearing a well-you-did-break-school-rules sort of expression. Harry didnвҖҷt enjoy his shepherdвҖҷs pie as much as heвҖҷd thought. Both he and Ron felt theyвҖҷd got the worse deal.
вҖңFilchвҖҷll have me there all night,вҖқ said Ron heavily. вҖңNo magic! There must be about a hundred cups in that room. IвҖҷm no good at Muggle cleaning.вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷd swap anytime,вҖқ said Harry hollowly. вҖңIвҖҷve had loads of pracВӯtice with the Dursleys. Answering LockhartвҖҷs fan mail вҖҰ heвҖҷll be a nightmare. вҖҰвҖқ
Saturday afternoon seemed to melt away, and in what seemed like no time, it was five minutes to eight, and Harry was dragging his feet along the second-floor corridor to LockhartвҖҷs office. He gritted his teeth and knocked.
The door flew open at once. Lockhart beamed down at him.
вҖңAh, hereвҖҷs the scalawag!вҖқ he said. вҖңCome in, Harry, come in вҖ”вҖқ
Shining brightly on the walls by the light of many candles were countless framed photographs of Lockhart. He had even signed a few of them. Another large pile lay on his desk.
вҖңYou can address the envelopes!вҖқ Lockhart told Harry, as though this was a huge treat. вҖңThis first oneвҖҷs to Gladys Gudgeon, bless her вҖ” huge fan of mine вҖ”вҖқ
The minutes snailed by. Harry let LockhartвҖҷs voice wash over him, occasionally saying, вҖңMmmвҖқ and вҖңRightвҖқ and вҖңYeah.вҖқ Now and then he caught a phrase like, вҖңFameвҖҷs a fickle friend, Harry,вҖқ or вҖңCelebrity is as celebrity does, remember that.вҖқ
The candles burned lower and lower, making the light dance over the many moving faces of Lockhart watching him. Harry moved his aching hand over what felt like the thousandth enveВӯlope, writing out Veronica SmethleyвҖҷs address. It must be nearly time to leave, Harry thought miserably, please let it be nearly time. вҖҰ
And then he heard something вҖ” something quite apart from the spitting of the dying candles and LockhartвҖҷs prattle about his fans.
It was a voice, a voice to chill the bone marrow, a voice of breathВӯtaking, ice-cold venom.
вҖңCome вҖҰ come to me. вҖҰ Let me rip you. вҖҰ Let me tear you. вҖҰ Let me kill you. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry gave a huge jump and a large lilac blot appeared on Veronica SmethleyвҖҷs street.
вҖңWhat?вҖқ he said loudly.
вҖңI know!вҖқ said Lockhart. вҖңSix solid months at the top of the best-seller list! Broke all records!вҖқ
вҖңNo,вҖқ said Harry frantically. вҖңThat voice!вҖқ
вҖңSorry?вҖқ said Lockhart, looking puzzled. вҖңWhat voice?вҖқ
вҖңThat вҖ” that voice that said вҖ” didnвҖҷt you hear it?вҖқ
Lockhart was looking at Harry in high astonishment.
вҖңWhat are you talking about, Harry? Perhaps youвҖҷre getting a litВӯtle drowsy? Great Scott вҖ” look at the time! вҖңWeвҖҷve been here nearly four hours! IвҖҷd never have believed it вҖ” the timeвҖҷs flown, hasnвҖҷt it?вҖқ
Harry didnвҖҷt answer. He was straining his ears to hear the voice again, but there was no sound now except for Lockhart telling him he mustnвҖҷt expect a treat like this every time he got detention. FeelВӯing dazed, Harry left.
It was so late that the Gryffindor common room was almost empty. Harry went straight up to the dormitory. Ron wasnвҖҷt back yet. Harry pulled on his pajamas, got into bed, and waited. Half an hour later, Ron arrived, nursing his right arm and bringing a strong smell of polish into the darkened room.
вҖңMy muscles have all seized up,вҖқ he groaned, sinking on his bed. вҖңFourteen times he made me buff up that Quidditch Cup before he was satisfied. And then I had another slug attack all over a Special Award for Services to the School. Took ages to get the slime off. вҖҰ How was it with Lockhart?вҖқ
Keeping his voice low so as not to wake Neville, Dean, and SeaВӯmus, Harry told Ron exactly what he had heard.
вҖңAnd Lockhart said he couldnвҖҷt hear it?вҖқ said Ron. Harry could see him frowning in the moonlight. вҖңDвҖҷyou think he was lying? But I donвҖҷt get it вҖ” even someone invisible wouldвҖҷve had to open the door.вҖқ
вҖңI know,вҖқ said Harry, lying back in his four-poster and staring at the canopy above him. вҖңI donвҖҷt get it either.вҖқ
## Chapter 8

The Deathday Party
October arrived, spreading a damp chill over the grounds and into the castle. Madam Pomfrey, the nurse, was kept busy by a sudden spate of colds among the staff and students. Her Pepperup Potion worked instantly, though it left the drinker smokВӯing at the ears for several hours afterward. Ginny Weasley, who had been looking pale, was bullied into taking some by Percy. The steam pouring from under her vivid hair gave the impression that her whole head was on fire.
Raindrops the size of bullets thundered on the castle windows for days on end; the lake rose, the flower beds turned into muddy streams, and HagridвҖҷs pumpkins swelled to the size of garden sheds. Oliver WoodвҖҷs enthusiasm for regular training sessions, however, was not dampened, which was why Harry was to be found, late one stormy Saturday afternoon a few days before Halloween, returning to Gryffindor Tower, drenched to the skin and splattered with mud. Even aside from the rain and wind it hadnвҖҷt been a happy pracВӯtice session. Fred and George, who had been spying on the SlythВӯerin team, had seen for themselves the speed of those new Nimbus Two Thousand and Ones. They reported that the Slytherin team was no more than seven greenish blurs, shooting through the air like missiles.
As Harry squelched along the deserted corridor he came across somebody who looked just as preoccupied as he was. Nearly HeadВӯless Nick, the ghost of Gryffindor Tower, was staring morosely out of a window, muttering under his breath, вҖңвҖҰ donвҖҷt fulfill their reВӯquirements вҖҰ half an inch, if that вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңHello, Nick,вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңHello, hello,вҖқ said Nearly Headless Nick, starting and looking round. He wore a dashing, plumed hat on his long curly hair, and a tunic with a ruff, which concealed the fact that his neck was alВӯmost completely severed. He was pale as smoke, and Harry could see right through him to the dark sky and torrential rain outside.
вҖңYou look troubled, young Potter,вҖқ said Nick, folding a transВӯparent letter as he spoke and tucking it inside his doublet.
вҖңSo do you,вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңAh,вҖқ Nearly Headless Nick waved an elegant hand, вҖңa matter of no importance. вҖҰ ItвҖҷs not as though I really wanted to join. вҖҰ Thought IвҖҷd apply, but apparently I вҖҳdonвҖҷt fulfill requirementsвҖҷ вҖ”вҖқ
In spite of his airy tone, there was a look of great bitterness on his face.
вҖңBut you would think, wouldnвҖҷt you,вҖқ he erupted suddenly, pulling the letter back out of his pocket, вҖңthat getting hit forty-five times in the neck with a blunt axe would qualify you to join the Headless Hunt?вҖқ
вҖңOh вҖ” yes,вҖқ said Harry, who was obviously supposed to agree.
вҖңI mean, nobody wishes more than I do that it had all been quick and clean, and my head had come off properly, I mean, it would have saved me a great deal of pain and ridicule. However вҖ”вҖқ Nearly Headless Nick shook his letter open and read furiously:
вҖң вҖҳWe can only accept huntsmen whose heads have parted company with their bodies. You will appreciate that it would be impossible otherwise for members to participate in hunt activities such as Horseback Head-Juggling and Head Polo. It is with the greatest regret, therefore, that I must inform you that you do not fulВӯfill our requirements. With very best wishes, Sir Patrick Delaney-Podmore.вҖҷ вҖқ
Fuming, Nearly Headless Nick stuffed the letter away.
вҖңHalf an inch of skin and sinew holding my neck on, Harry! Most people would think thatвҖҷs good and beheaded, but oh, no, itвҖҷs not enough for Sir Properly Decapitated-Podmore.вҖқ
Nearly Headless Nick took several deep breaths and then said, in a far calmer tone, вҖңSo вҖ” whatвҖҷs bothering you? Anything I can do?вҖқ
вҖңNo,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңNot unless you know where we can get seven free Nimbus Two Thousand and Ones for our match against Sly вҖ”вҖқ
The rest of HarryвҖҷs sentence was drowned out by a high-pitched mewling from somewhere near his ankles. He looked down and found himself gazing into a pair of lamp-like yellow eyes. It was Mrs. Norris, the skeletal gray cat who was used by the caretaker, ArВӯgus Filch, as a sort of deputy in his endless battle against students.
вҖңYouвҖҷd better get out of here, Harry,вҖқ said Nick quickly. вҖңFilch isnвҖҷt in a good mood вҖ” heвҖҷs got the flu and some third years acciВӯdentally plastered frog brains all over the ceiling in dungeon five. HeвҖҷs been cleaning all morning, and if he sees you dripping mud all over the place вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңRight,вҖқ said Harry, backing away from the accusing stare of Mrs. Norris, but not quickly enough. Drawn to the spot by the mysteriВӯous power that seemed to connect him with his foul cat, Argus Filch burst suddenly through a tapestry to HarryвҖҷs right, wheezing and looking wildly about for the rule-breaker. There was a thick tartan scarf bound around his head, and his nose was unusually purple.
вҖңFilth!вҖқ he shouted, his jowls aquiver, his eyes popping alarmВӯingly as he pointed at the muddy puddle that had dripped from HarryвҖҷs Quidditch robes. вҖңMess and muck everywhere! IвҖҷve had enough of it, I tell you! Follow me, Potter!вҖқ
So Harry waved a gloomy good-bye to Nearly Headless Nick and followed Filch back downstairs, doubling the number of muddy footprints on the floor.
Harry had never been inside FilchвҖҷs office before; it was a place most students avoided. The room was dingy and windowless, lit by a single oil lamp dangling from the low ceiling. A faint smell of fried fish lingered about the place. Wooden filing cabinets stood around the walls; from their labels, Harry could see that they contained deВӯtails of every pupil Filch had ever punished. Fred and George Weasley had an entire drawer to themselves. A highly polished colВӯlection of chains and manacles hung on the wall behind FilchвҖҷs desk. It was common knowledge that he was always begging Dumbledore to let him suspend students by their ankles from the ceiling.
Filch grabbed a quill from a pot on his desk and began shuffling around looking for parchment.
вҖңDung,вҖқ he muttered furiously, вҖңgreat sizzling dragon bogies вҖҰ frog brains вҖҰ rat intestines вҖҰ IвҖҷve had enough of it вҖҰ make an example вҖҰ whereвҖҷs the form вҖҰ yes вҖҰвҖқ
He retrieved a large roll of parchment from his desk drawer and stretched it out in front of him, dipping his long black quill into the ink pot.
вҖңName вҖҰ Harry Potter. Crime вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңIt was only a bit of mud!вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңItвҖҷs only a bit of mud to you, boy, but to me itвҖҷs an extra hour scrubbing!вҖқ shouted Filch, a drip shivering unpleasantly at the end of his bulbous nose. вҖңCrime вҖҰ befouling the castle вҖҰ suggested sentence вҖҰвҖқ
Dabbing at his streaming nose, Filch squinted unpleasantly at Harry, who waited with bated breath for his sentence to fall.
But as Filch lowered his quill, there was a great BANG! on the ceiling of the office, which made the oil lamp rattle.
вҖңPEEVES!вҖқ Filch roared, flinging down his quill in a transport of rage. вҖңIвҖҷll have you this time, IвҖҷll have you!вҖқ
And without a backward glance at Harry, Filch ran flat-footed from the office, Mrs. Norris streaking alongside him.
Peeves was the school poltergeist, a grinning, airborne menace who lived to cause havoc and distress. Harry didnвҖҷt much like Peeves, but couldnвҖҷt help feeling grateful for his timing. HopeВӯfully, whatever Peeves had done (and it sounded as though heвҖҷd wrecked something very big this time) would distract Filch from Harry.
Thinking that he should probably wait for Filch to come back, Harry sank into a moth-eaten chair next to the desk. There was only one thing on it apart from his half-completed form: a large, glossy, purple envelope with silver lettering on the front. With a quick glance at the door to check that Filch wasnвҖҷt on his way back, Harry picked up the envelope and read:
KWIKSPELL
A Correspondence Course in BeginnersвҖҷ Magic
Intrigued, Harry flicked the envelope open and pulled out the sheaf of parchment inside. More curly silver writing on the front page said:
Feel out of step in the world of modern magic? Find yourself making excuses not to perform simple spells? Ever been taunted for your woeВӯful wandwork?
There is an answer!
Kwikspell is an all-new, fail-safe, quick-result, easy-learn course. Hundreds of witches and wizards have benefited from the Kwikspell method!
Madam Z. Nettles of Topsham writes:
вҖңI had no memory for incantations and my potions were a family joke! Now, after a Kwikspell course, I am the center of attention at parties and friends beg for the recipe of my Scintillation Solution!вҖқ
Warlock D. J. Prod of Didsbury says:
вҖңMy wife used to sneer at my feeble charms, but one month into your fabulous Kwikspell course and I succeeded in turning her into a yak!
Thank you, Kwikspell!вҖқ
Fascinated, Harry thumbed through the rest of the envelopeвҖҷs contents. Why on earth did Filch want a Kwikspell course? Did this mean he wasnвҖҷt a proper wizard? Harry was just reading вҖңLesВӯson One: Holding Your Wand (Some Useful Tips)вҖқ when shuffling footsteps outside told him Filch was coming back. Stuffing the parchment back into the envelope, Harry threw it back onto the desk just as the door opened.
Filch was looking triumphant.
вҖңThat vanishing cabinet was extremely valuable!вҖқ he was saying gleefully to Mrs. Norris. вҖңWeвҖҷll have Peeves out this time, my sweet вҖ”вҖқ
His eyes fell on Harry and then darted to the Kwikspell enveВӯlope, which, Harry realized too late, was lying two feet away from where it had started.
FilchвҖҷs pasty face went brick red. Harry braced himself for a tidal wave of fury. Filch hobbled across to his desk, snatched up the enВӯvelope, and threw it into a drawer.
вҖңHave you вҖ” did you read вҖ” ?вҖқ he sputtered.
вҖңNo,вҖқ Harry lied quickly.
FilchвҖҷs knobbly hands were twisting together.
вҖңIf I thought youвҖҷd read my private вҖ” not that itвҖҷs mine вҖ” for a friend вҖ” be that as it may вҖ” however вҖ”вҖқ
Harry was staring at him, alarmed; Filch had never looked madВӯder. His eyes were popping, a tic was going in one of his pouchy cheeks, and the tartan scarf didnвҖҷt help.
вҖңVery well вҖ” go вҖ” and donвҖҷt breathe a word вҖ” not that вҖ” however, if you didnвҖҷt read вҖ” go now, I have to write up PeevesвҖҷ reВӯport вҖ” go вҖ”вҖқ
Amazed at his luck, Harry sped out of the office, up the corridor, and back upstairs. To escape from FilchвҖҷs office without punishВӯment was probably some kind of school record.
вҖңHarry! Harry! Did it work?вҖқ
Nearly Headless Nick came gliding out of a classroom. Behind him, Harry could see the wreckage of a large black-and-gold cabiВӯnet that appeared to have been dropped from a great height.
вҖңI persuaded Peeves to crash it right over FilchвҖҷs office,вҖқ said Nick eagerly. вҖңThought it might distract him вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWas that you?вҖқ said Harry gratefully. вҖңYeah, it worked, I didnвҖҷt even get detention. Thanks, Nick!вҖқ
They set off up the corridor together. Nearly Headless Nick, Harry noticed, was still holding Sir PatrickвҖҷs rejection letter.
вҖңI wish there was something I could do for you about the HeadВӯless Hunt,вҖқ Harry said.
Nearly Headless Nick stopped in his tracks and Harry walked right through him. He wished he hadnвҖҷt; it was like stepping through an icy shower.

вҖңWhat is it?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңWell, this Halloween will be my five hundredth deathday,вҖқ said Nearly Headless Nick, drawing himself up and looking dignified.
вҖңOh,вҖқ said Harry, not sure whether he should look sorry or happy about this. вҖңRight.вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷm holding a party down in one of the roomier dungeons. Friends will be coming from all over the country. It would be such an honor if you would attend. Mr. Weasley and Miss Granger would be most welcome, too, of course вҖ” but I daresay youвҖҷd rather go to the school feast?вҖқ He watched Harry on tenterhooks.
вҖңNo,вҖқ said Harry quickly, вҖңIвҖҷll come вҖ”вҖқ

вҖңOf вҖ” of course,вҖқ said Harry.
Nearly Headless Nick beamed at him.
вҖңA deathday party?вҖқ said Hermione keenly when Harry had changed at last and joined her and Ron in the common room. вҖңI bet there arenвҖҷt many living people who can say theyвҖҷve been to one of those вҖ” itвҖҷll be fascinating!вҖқ
вҖңWhy would anyone want to celebrate the day they died?вҖқ said Ron, who was halfway through his Potions homework and grumpy. вҖңSounds dead depressing to me. вҖҰвҖқ
Rain was still lashing the windows, which were now inky black, but inside all looked bright and cheerful. The firelight glowed over the countless squashy armchairs where people sat reading, talking, doing homework or, in the case of Fred and George Weasley, trying to find out what would happen if you fed a Filibuster firework to a salamander. Fred had вҖңrescuedвҖқ the brilliant orange, fire-dwelling lizard from a Care of Magical Creatures class and it was now smoldering gently on a table surrounded by a knot of curious people.
Harry was at the point of telling Ron and Hermione about Filch and the Kwikspell course when the salamander suddenly whizzed into the air, emitting loud sparks and bangs as it whirled wildly round the room. The sight of Percy bellowing himself hoarse at Fred and George, the spectacular display of tangerine stars showerВӯing from the salamanderвҖҷs mouth, and its escape into the fire, with accompanying explosions, drove both Filch and the Kwikspell enВӯvelope from HarryвҖҷs mind.
By the time Halloween arrived, Harry was regretting his rash promise to go to the deathday party. The rest of the school was happily anticipating their Halloween feast; the Great Hall had been decorated with the usual live bats, HagridвҖҷs vast pumpkins had been carved into lanterns large enough for three men to sit in, and there were rumors that Dumbledore had booked a troupe of dancВӯing skeletons for the entertainment.
вҖңA promise is a promise,вҖқ Hermione reminded Harry bossily. вҖңYou said youвҖҷd go to the deathday party.вҖқ
So at seven oвҖҷclock, Harry, Ron, and Hermione walked straight past the doorway to the packed Great Hall, which was glittering invitingly with gold plates and candles, and directed their steps inВӯstead toward the dungeons.
The passageway leading to Nearly Headless NickвҖҷs party had been lined with candles, too, though the effect was far from cheerВӯful: These were long, thin, jet-black tapers, all burning bright blue, casting a dim, ghostly light even over their own living faces. The temperature dropped with every step they took. As Harry shivered and drew his robes tightly around him, he heard what sounded like a thousand fingernails scraping an enormous blackboard.
вҖңIs that supposed to be music?вҖқ Ron whispered. They turned a corner and saw Nearly Headless Nick standing at a doorway hung with black velvet drapes.
вҖңMy dear friends,вҖқ he said mournfully. вҖңWelcome, welcome вҖҰ so pleased you could come. вҖҰвҖқ
He swept off his plumed hat and bowed them inside.
It was an incredible sight. The dungeon was full of hundreds of pearly-white, translucent people, mostly drifting around a crowded dance floor, waltzing to the dreadful, quavering sound of thirty musical saws, played by an orchestra on a raised, black-draped platВӯform. A chandelier overhead blazed midnight-blue with a thouВӯsand more black candles. Their breath rose in a mist before them; it was like stepping into a freezer.
вҖңShall we have a look around?вҖқ Harry suggested, wanting to warm up his feet.
вҖңCareful not to walk through anyone,вҖқ said Ron nervously, and they set off around the edge of the dance floor. They passed a group of gloomy nuns, a ragged man wearing chains, and the Fat Friar, a cheerful Hufflepuff ghost, who was talking to a knight with an arrow sticking out of his forehead. Harry wasnвҖҷt surprised to see that the Bloody Baron, a gaunt, staring Slytherin ghost covered in silver bloodstains, was being given a wide berth by the other ghosts.
вҖңOh, no,вҖқ said Hermione, stopping abruptly. вҖңTurn back, turn back, I donвҖҷt want to talk to Moaning Myrtle вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWho?вҖқ said Harry as they backtracked quickly.
вҖңShe haunts one of the toilets in the girlsвҖҷ bathroom on the first floor,вҖқ said Hermione.
вҖңShe haunts a toilet?вҖқ
вҖңYes. ItвҖҷs been out-of-order all year because she keeps having tantrums and flooding the place. I never went in there anyway if I could avoid it; itвҖҷs awful trying to have a pee with her wailing at you вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңLook, food!вҖқ said Ron.
On the other side of the dungeon was a long table, also covered in black velvet. They approached it eagerly but next moment had stopped in their tracks, horrified. The smell was quite disgusting. Large, rotten fish were laid on handsome silver platters; cakes, burned charcoal-black, were heaped on salvers; there was a great maggoty haggis, a slab of cheese covered in furry green mold and, in pride of place, an enormous gray cake in the shape of a tombВӯstone, with tar-like icing forming the words,
SIR NICHOLAS DE MIMSY-PORPINGTON
DIED 31ST OCTOBER, 1492
Harry watched, amazed, as a portly ghost approached the table, crouched low, and walked through it, his mouth held wide so that it passed through one of the stinking salmon.
вҖңCan you taste it if you walk through it?вҖқ Harry asked him.
вҖңAlmost,вҖқ said the ghost sadly, and he drifted away.
вҖңI expect theyвҖҷve let it rot to give it a stronger flavor,вҖқ said HerВӯmione knowledgeably, pinching her nose and leaning closer to look at the putrid haggis.
вҖңCan we move? I feel sick,вҖқ said Ron.
They had barely turned around, however, when a little man swooped suddenly from under the table and came to a halt in midair before them.
вҖңHello, Peeves,вҖқ said Harry cautiously.
Unlike the ghosts around them, Peeves the Poltergeist was the very reverse of pale and transparent. He was wearing a bright orВӯange party hat, a revolving bow tie, and a broad grin on his wide, wicked face.
вҖңNibbles?вҖқ he said sweetly, offering them a bowl of peanuts covВӯered in fungus.
вҖңNo thanks,вҖқ said Hermione.
вҖңHeard you talking about poor Myrtle,вҖқ said Peeves, his eyes dancing. вҖңRude you was about poor Myrtle.вҖқ He took a deep breath and bellowed, вҖңOY! MYRTLE!вҖқ
вҖңOh, no, Peeves, donвҖҷt tell her what I said, sheвҖҷll be really upset,вҖқ Hermione whispered frantically. вҖңI didnвҖҷt mean it, I donвҖҷt mind her вҖ” er, hello, Myrtle.вҖқ
The squat ghost of a girl had glided over. She had the glummest face Harry had ever seen, half-hidden behind lank hair and thick, pearly spectacles.
вҖңWhat?вҖқ she said sulkily.
вҖңHow are you, Myrtle?вҖқ said Hermione in a falsely bright voice. вҖңItвҖҷs nice to see you out of the toilet.вҖқ
Myrtle sniffed.
вҖңMiss Granger was just talking about you вҖ”вҖқ said Peeves slyly in MyrtleвҖҷs ear.
вҖңJust saying вҖ” saying вҖ” how nice you look tonight,вҖқ said HerВӯmione, glaring at Peeves.
Myrtle eyed Hermione suspiciously.
вҖңYouвҖҷre making fun of me,вҖқ she said, silver tears welling rapidly in her small, see-through eyes.
вҖңNo вҖ” honestly вҖ” didnвҖҷt I just say how nice MyrtleвҖҷs looking?вҖқ said Hermione, nudging Harry and Ron painfully in the ribs.
вҖңOh, yeah вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңShe did вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңDonвҖҷt lie to me,вҖқ Myrtle gasped, tears now flooding down her face, while Peeves chuckled happily over her shoulder. вҖңDвҖҷyou think I donвҖҷt know what people call me behind my back? Fat MyrВӯtle! Ugly Myrtle! Miserable, moaning, moping Myrtle!вҖқ
вҖңYouвҖҷve forgotten pimply,вҖқ Peeves hissed in her ear.
Moaning Myrtle burst into anguished sobs and fled from the dungeon. Peeves shot after her, pelting her with moldy peanuts, yelling, вҖңPimply! Pimply!вҖқ
вҖңOh, dear,вҖқ said Hermione sadly.
Nearly Headless Nick now drifted toward them through the crowd.
вҖңEnjoying yourselves?вҖқ
вҖңOh, yes,вҖқ they lied.
вҖңNot a bad turnout,вҖқ said Nearly Headless Nick proudly. вҖңThe Wailing Widow came all the way up from Kent. вҖҰ ItвҖҷs nearly time for my speech, IвҖҷd better go and warn the orchestra. вҖҰвҖқ
The orchestra, however, stopped playing at that very moment. They, and everyone else in the dungeon, fell silent, looking around in excitement, as a hunting horn sounded.
вҖңOh, here we go,вҖқ said Nearly Headless Nick bitterly.
Through the dungeon wall burst a dozen ghost horses, each ridden by a headless horseman. The assembly clapped wildly; Harry started to clap, too, but stopped quickly at the sight of NickвҖҷs face.
The horses galloped into the middle of the dance floor and halted, rearing and plunging. At the front of the pack was a large ghost who held his bearded head under his arm, from which posiВӯtion he was blowing the horn. The ghost leapt down, lifted his head high in the air so he could see over the crowd (everyone laughed), and strode over to Nearly Headless Nick, squashing his head back onto his neck.
вҖңNick!вҖқ he roared. вҖңHow are you? Head still hanging in there?вҖқ
He gave a hearty guffaw and clapped Nearly Headless Nick on the shoulder.
вҖңWelcome, Patrick,вҖқ said Nick stiffly.
вҖңLive вҖҷuns!вҖқ said Sir Patrick, spotting Harry, Ron, and Hermione and giving a huge, fake jump of astonishment, so that his head fell off again (the crowd howled with laughter).
вҖңVery amusing,вҖқ said Nearly Headless Nick darkly.
вҖңDonвҖҷt mind Nick!вҖқ shouted Sir PatrickвҖҷs head from the floor. вҖңStill upset we wonвҖҷt let him join the Hunt! But I mean to say вҖ” look at the fellow вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI think,вҖқ said Harry hurriedly, at a meaningful look from Nick, вҖңNickвҖҷs very вҖ” frightening and вҖ” er вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHa!вҖқ yelled Sir PatrickвҖҷs head. вҖңBet he asked you to say that!вҖқ
вҖңIf I could have everyoneвҖҷs attention, itвҖҷs time for my speech!вҖқ said Nearly Headless Nick loudly, striding toward the podium and climbing into an icy blue spotlight.
вҖңMy late lamented lords, ladies, and gentlemen, it is my great sorrow вҖҰвҖқ
But nobody heard much more. Sir Patrick and the rest of the Headless Hunt had just started a game of Head Hockey and the crowd were turning to watch. Nearly Headless Nick tried vainly to recapture his audience, but gave up as Sir PatrickвҖҷs head went sailВӯing past him to loud cheers.
Harry was very cold by now, not to mention hungry.
вҖңI canвҖҷt stand much more of this,вҖқ Ron muttered, his teeth chatВӯtering, as the orchestra ground back into action and the ghosts swept back onto the dance floor.
вҖңLetвҖҷs go,вҖқ Harry agreed.
They backed toward the door, nodding and beaming at anyone who looked at them, and a minute later were hurrying back up the passageway full of black candles.
вҖңPudding might not be finished yet,вҖқ said Ron hopefully, leadВӯing the way toward the steps to the entrance hall.
And then Harry heard it.
вҖңвҖҰ rip вҖҰ tear вҖҰ kill вҖҰвҖқ
It was the same voice, the same cold, murderous voice he had heard in LockhartвҖҷs office.
He stumbled to a halt, clutching at the stone wall, listening with all his might, looking around, squinting up and down the dimly lit passageway.
вҖңHarry, whatвҖҷre you вҖ” ?вҖқ
вҖңItвҖҷs that voice again вҖ” shut up a minute вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңвҖҰ soo hungry вҖҰ for so long вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңListen!вҖқ said Harry urgently, and Ron and Hermione froze, watching him.
вҖңвҖҰ kill вҖҰ time to kill вҖҰвҖқ
The voice was growing fainter. Harry was sure it was moving away вҖ” moving upward. A mixture of fear and excitement gripped him as he stared at the dark ceiling; how could it be moving upВӯward? Was it a phantom, to whom stone ceilings didnвҖҷt matter?
вҖңThis way,вҖқ he shouted, and he began to run, up the stairs, into the entrance hall. It was no good hoping to hear anything here, the babble of talk from the Halloween feast was echoing out of the Great Hall. Harry sprinted up the marble staircase to the first floor, Ron and Hermione clattering behind him.
вҖңHarry, whatвҖҷre we вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңSHH!вҖқ
Harry strained his ears. Distantly, from the floor above, and growing fainter still, he heard the voice: вҖңвҖҰ I smell blood. вҖҰ I SMELL BLOOD!вҖқ
His stomach lurched вҖ”
вҖңItвҖҷs going to kill someone!вҖқ he shouted, and ignoring RonвҖҷs and HermioneвҖҷs bewildered faces, he ran up the next flight of steps three at a time, trying to listen over his own pounding footsteps вҖ”
Harry hurtled around the whole of the second floor, Ron and Hermione panting behind him, not stopping until they turned a corner into the last, deserted passage.
вҖңHarry, what was that all about?вҖқ said Ron, wiping sweat off his face. вҖңI couldnвҖҷt hear anything. вҖҰвҖқ
But Hermione gave a sudden gasp, pointing down the corridor.
вҖңLook!вҖқ
Something was shining on the wall ahead. They approached slowly, squinting through the darkness. Foot-high words had been daubed on the wall between two windows, shimmering in the light cast by the flaming torches.
THE CHAMBER OF SECRETS HAS BEEN
OPENED. ENEMIES OF THE HEIR, BEWARE.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs that thing вҖ” hanging underneath?вҖқ said Ron, a slight quiver in his voice.
As they edged nearer, Harry almost slipped вҖ” there was a large puddle of water on the floor; Ron and Hermione grabbed him, and they inched toward the message, eyes fixed on a dark shadow beВӯneath it. All three of them realized what it was at once, and leapt backward with a splash.
Mrs. Norris, the caretakerвҖҷs cat, was hanging by her tail from the torch bracket. She was stiff as a board, her eyes wide and staring.
For a few seconds, they didnвҖҷt move. Then Ron said, вҖңLetвҖҷs get out of here.вҖқ
вҖңShouldnвҖҷt we try and help вҖ”вҖқ Harry began awkwardly.
вҖңTrust me,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңWe donвҖҷt want to be found here.вҖқ
But it was too late. A rumble, as though of distant thunder, told them that the feast had just ended. From either end of the corridor where they stood came the sound of hundreds of feet climbing the stairs, and the loud, happy talk of well-fed people; next moment, students were crashing into the passage from both ends.
The chatter, the bustle, the noise died suddenly as the people in front spotted the hanging cat. Harry, Ron, and Hermione stood alone, in the middle of the corridor, as silence fell among the mass of students pressing forward to see the grisly sight.
Then someone shouted through the quiet.
вҖңEnemies of the Heir, beware! YouвҖҷll be next, Mudbloods!вҖқ
It was Draco Malfoy. He had pushed to the front of the crowd, his cold eyes alive, his usually bloodless face flushed, as he grinned at the sight of the hanging, immobile cat.
## Chapter 9

The Writing on the Wall
вҖңWhatвҖҷs going on here? WhatвҖҷs going on?вҖқ
Attracted no doubt by MalfoyвҖҷs shout, Argus Filch came shouldering his way through the crowd. Then he saw Mrs. Norris and fell back, clutching his face in horror.
вҖңMy cat! My cat! WhatвҖҷs happened to Mrs. Norris?вҖқ he shrieked.
And his popping eyes fell on Harry.
вҖңYou!вҖқ he screeched. вҖңYou! YouвҖҷve murdered my cat! YouвҖҷve killed her! IвҖҷll kill you! IвҖҷll вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңArgus!вҖқ
Dumbledore had arrived on the scene, followed by a number of other teachers. In seconds, he had swept past Harry, Ron, and Hermione and detached Mrs. Norris from the torch bracket.
вҖңCome with me, Argus,вҖқ he said to Filch. вҖңYou, too, Mr. Potter, Mr. Weasley, Miss Granger.вҖқ
Lockhart stepped forward eagerly.
вҖңMy office is nearest, Headmaster вҖ” just upstairs вҖ” please feel free вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThank you, Gilderoy,вҖқ said Dumbledore.
The silent crowd parted to let them pass. Lockhart, looking exВӯcited and important, hurried after Dumbledore; so did Professors McGonagall and Snape.
As they entered LockhartвҖҷs darkened office there was a flurry of movement across the walls; Harry saw several of the Lockharts in the pictures dodging out of sight, their hair in rollers. The real Lockhart lit the candles on his desk and stood back. Dumbledore laid Mrs. Norris on the polished surface and began to examine her. Harry, Ron, and Hermione exchanged tense looks and sank into chairs outside the pool of candlelight, watching.
The tip of DumbledoreвҖҷs long, crooked nose was barely an inch from Mrs. NorrisвҖҷs fur. He was looking at her closely through his half-moon spectacles, his long fingers gently prodding and poking. Professor McGonagall was bent almost as close, her eyes narrowed. Snape loomed behind them, half in shadow, wearing a most pecuВӯliar expression: It was as though he was trying hard not to smile. And Lockhart was hovering around all of them, making suggesВӯtions.
вҖңIt was definitely a curse that killed her вҖ” probably the Trans-mogrifian Torture вҖ” IвҖҷve seen it used many times, so unlucky I wasnвҖҷt there, I know the very countercurse that would have saved her. вҖҰвҖқ
LockhartвҖҷs comments were punctuated by FilchвҖҷs dry, racking sobs. He was slumped in a chair by the desk, unable to look at Mrs. Norris, his face in his hands. Much as he detested Filch, Harry couldnвҖҷt help feeling a bit sorry for him, though not nearly as sorry as he felt for himself. If Dumbledore believed Filch, he would be expelled for sure.
Dumbledore was now muttering strange words under his breath and tapping Mrs. Norris with his wand but nothing happened: She continued to look as though she had been recently stuffed.
вҖңвҖҰ I remember something very similar happening in Oua-gadogou,вҖқ said Lockhart, вҖңa series of attacks, the full storyвҖҷs in my autobiography, I was able to provide the townsfolk with various amulets, which cleared the matter up at once. вҖҰвҖқ
The photographs of Lockhart on the walls were all nodding in agreement as he talked. One of them had forgotten to remove his hair net.
At last Dumbledore straightened up.
вҖңSheвҖҷs not dead, Argus,вҖқ he said softly.
Lockhart stopped abruptly in the middle of counting the numВӯber of murders he had prevented.
вҖңNot dead?вҖқ choked Filch, looking through his fingers at Mrs. Norris. вҖңBut whyвҖҷs she all вҖ” all stiff and frozen?вҖқ
вҖңShe has been Petrified,вҖқ said Dumbledore (вҖңAh! I thought so!вҖқ said Lockhart). вҖңBut how, I cannot say. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңAsk him!вҖқ shrieked Filch, turning his blotched and tearstained face to Harry.
вҖңNo second year could have done this,вҖқ said Dumbledore firmly. вҖңIt would take Dark Magic of the most advanced вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHe did it, he did it!вҖқ Filch spat, his pouchy face purpling. вҖңYou saw what he wrote on the wall! He found вҖ” in my office вҖ” he knows IвҖҷm a вҖ” IвҖҷm a вҖ”вҖқ FilchвҖҷs face worked horribly. вҖңHe knows IвҖҷm a Squib!вҖқ he finished.
вҖңI never touched Mrs. Norris!вҖқ Harry said loudly, uncomfortably aware of everyone looking at him, including all the Lockharts on the walls. вҖңAnd I donвҖҷt even know what a Squib is.вҖқ
вҖңRubbish!вҖқ snarled Filch. вҖңHe saw my Kwikspell letter!вҖқ
вҖңIf I might speak, Headmaster,вҖқ said Snape from the shadows, and HarryвҖҷs sense of foreboding increased; he was sure nothing Snape had to say was going to do him any good.
вҖңPotter and his friends may have simply been in the wrong place at the wrong time,вҖқ he said, a slight sneer curling his mouth as though he doubted it. вҖңBut we do have a set of suspicious circumВӯstances here. Why was he in the upstairs corridor at all? Why wasnвҖҷt he at the Halloween feast?вҖқ
Harry, Ron and Hermione all launched into an explanation about the deathday party. вҖңвҖҰ there were hundreds of ghosts, theyвҖҷll tell you we were there вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBut why not join the feast afterward?вҖқ said Snape, his black eyes glittering in the candlelight. вҖңWhy go up to that corridor?вҖқ
Ron and Hermione looked at Harry.
вҖңBecause вҖ” because вҖ”вҖқ Harry said, his heart thumping very fast; something told him it would sound very far-fetched if he told them he had been led there by a bodiless voice no one but he could hear, вҖңbecause we were tired and wanted to go to bed,вҖқ he said.
вҖңWithout any supper?вҖқ said Snape, a triumphant smile flickerВӯing across his gaunt face. вҖңI didnвҖҷt think ghosts provided food fit for living people at their parties.вҖқ
вҖңWe werenвҖҷt hungry,вҖқ said Ron loudly as his stomach gave a huge rumble.
SnapeвҖҷs nasty smile widened.
вҖңI suggest, Headmaster, that Potter is not being entirely truthВӯful,вҖқ he said. вҖңIt might be a good idea if he were deprived of certain privileges until he is ready to tell us the whole story. I personally feel he should be taken off the Gryffindor Quidditch team until he is ready to be honest.вҖқ
вҖңReally, Severus,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall sharply, вҖңI see no reason to stop the boy playing Quidditch. This cat wasnвҖҷt hit over the head with a broomstick. There is no evidence at all that Potter has done anything wrong.вҖқ
Dumbledore was giving Harry a searching look. His twinkling light-blue gaze made Harry feel as though he were being X-rayed.
вҖңInnocent until proven guilty, Severus,вҖқ he said firmly.
Snape looked furious. So did Filch.
вҖңMy cat has been Petrified!вҖқ he shrieked, his eyes popping. вҖңI want to see some punishment!вҖқ
вҖңWe will be able to cure her, Argus,вҖқ said Dumbledore patiently. вҖңProfesser Sprout recently managed to procure some Mandrakes. As soon as they have reached their full size, I will have a potion made that will revive Mrs. Norris.вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷll make it,вҖқ Lockhart butted in. вҖңI must have done it a hunВӯdred times. I could whip up a Mandrake Restorative Draught in my sleep вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңExcuse me,вҖқ said Snape icily. вҖңBut I believe I am the Potions master at this school.вҖқ
There was a very awkward pause.
вҖңYou may go,вҖқ Dumbledore said to Harry, Ron, and Hermione.
They went, as quickly as they could without actually running. When they were a floor up from LockhartвҖҷs office, they turned into an empty classroom and closed the door quietly behind them. Harry squinted at his friendsвҖҷ darkened faces.
вҖңDвҖҷyou think I should have told them about that voice I heard?вҖқ
вҖңNo,вҖқ said Ron, without hesitation. вҖңHearing voices no one else can hear isnвҖҷt a good sign, even in the wizarding world.вҖқ
Something in RonвҖҷs voice made Harry ask, вҖңYou do believe me, donвҖҷt you?вҖқ
вҖң вҖҷCourse I do,вҖқ said Ron quickly. вҖңBut вҖ” you must admit itвҖҷs weird. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңI know itвҖҷs weird,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңThe whole thingвҖҷs weird. What was that writing on the wall about? вҖҳThe Chamber Has Been OpenedвҖҷ. вҖҰ WhatвҖҷs that supposed to mean?вҖқ
вҖңYou know, it rings a sort of bell,вҖқ said Ron slowly. вҖңI think someone told me a story about a secret chamber at Hogwarts once вҖҰ mightвҖҷve been Bill. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңAnd what on earthвҖҷs a Squib?вҖқ said Harry.
To his surprise, Ron stifled a snigger.
вҖңWell вҖ” itвҖҷs not funny really вҖ” but as itвҖҷs Filch,вҖқ he said. вҖңA Squib is someone who was born into a wizarding family but hasnвҖҷt got any magic powers. Kind of the opposite of Muggle-born wizВӯards, but Squibs are quite unusual. If FilchвҖҷs trying to learn magic from a Kwikspell course, I reckon he must be a Squib. It would exВӯplain a lot. Like why he hates students so much.вҖқ Ron gave a satisВӯfied smile. вҖңHeвҖҷs bitter.вҖқ
A clock chimed somewhere.
вҖңMidnight,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңWeвҖҷd better get to bed before Snape comes along and tries to frame us for something else.вҖқ
* * *
For a few days, the school could talk of little else but the attack on Mrs. Norris. Filch kept it fresh in everyoneвҖҷs minds by pacing the spot where she had been attacked, as though he thought the atВӯtacker might come back. Harry had seen him scrubbing the mesВӯsage on the wall with Mrs. SkowerвҖҷs All-Purpose Magical Mess Remover, but to no effect; the words still gleamed as brightly as ever on the stone. When Filch wasnвҖҷt guarding the scene of the crime, he was skulking red-eyed through the corridors, lunging out at unsuspecting students and trying to put them in detention for things like вҖңbreathing loudlyвҖқ and вҖңlooking happy.вҖқ
Ginny Weasley seemed very disturbed by Mrs. NorrisвҖҷs fate. AcВӯcording to Ron, she was a great cat lover.
вҖңBut you havenвҖҷt really got to know Mrs. Norris,вҖқ Ron told her bracingly. вҖңHonestly, weвҖҷre much better off without her.вҖқ GinnyвҖҷs lip trembled. вҖңStuff like this doesnвҖҷt often happen at Hogwarts,вҖқ Ron assured her. вҖңTheyвҖҷll catch the maniac who did it and have him out of here in no time. I just hope heвҖҷs got time to Petrify Filch before heвҖҷs expelled. IвҖҷm only joking вҖ”вҖқ Ron added hastily as Ginny blanched.
The attack had also had an effect on Hermione. It was quite usual for Hermione to spend a lot of time reading, but she was now doing almost nothing else. Nor could Harry and Ron get much reВӯsponse from her when they asked what she was up to, and not unВӯtil the following Wednesday did they find out.
Harry had been held back in Potions, where Snape had made him stay behind to scrape tubeworms off the desks. After a hurried lunch, he went upstairs to meet Ron in the library, and saw JusВӯtin Finch-Fletchley, the Hufflepuff boy from Herbology, coming toward him. Harry had just opened his mouth to say hello when Justin caught sight of him, turned abruptly, and sped off in the opВӯposite direction.
Harry found Ron at the back of the library, measuring his HisВӯtory of Magic homework. Professor Binns had asked for a three-foot-long composition on вҖңThe Medieval Assembly of European Wizards.вҖқ
вҖңI donвҖҷt believe it, IвҖҷm still eight inches short. вҖҰвҖқ said Ron fuВӯriously, letting go of his parchment, which sprang back into a roll. вҖңAnd HermioneвҖҷs done four feet seven inches and her writingвҖҷs tiny.вҖқ
вҖңWhere is she?вҖқ asked Harry, grabbing the tape measure and unВӯrolling his own homework.
вҖңSomewhere over there,вҖқ said Ron, pointing along the shelves. вҖңLooking for another book. I think sheвҖҷs trying to read the whole library before Christmas.вҖқ
Harry told Ron about Justin Finch-Fletchley running away from him.
вҖңDunno why you care. I thought he was a bit of an idiot,вҖқ said Ron, scribbling away, making his writing as large as possible. вҖңAll that junk about Lockhart being so great вҖ”вҖқ
Hermione emerged from between the bookshelves. She looked irritable and at last seemed ready to talk to them.
вҖңAll the copies of Hogwarts, A History have been taken out,вҖқ she said, sitting down next to Harry and Ron. вҖңAnd thereвҖҷs a two-week waiting list. I wish I hadnвҖҷt left my copy at home, but I couldnвҖҷt fit it in my trunk with all the Lockhart books.вҖқ
вҖңWhy do you want it?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңThe same reason everyone else wants it,вҖқ said Hermione, вҖңto read up on the legend of the Chamber of Secrets.вҖқ
вҖңWhatвҖҷs that?вҖқ said Harry quickly.
вҖңThatвҖҷs just it. I canвҖҷt remember,вҖқ said Hermione, biting her lip. вҖңAnd I canвҖҷt find the story anywhere else вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHermione, let me read your composition,вҖқ said Ron desperВӯately, checking his watch.
вҖңNo, I wonвҖҷt,вҖқ said Hermione, suddenly severe. вҖңYouвҖҷve had ten days to finish it вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI only need another two inches, come on вҖ”вҖқ
The bell rang. Ron and Hermione led the way to History of Magic, bickering.
History of Magic was the dullest subject on their schedule. ProВӯfessor Binns, who taught it, was their only ghost teacher, and the most exciting thing that ever happened in his classes was his enterВӯing the room through the blackboard. Ancient and shriveled, many people said he hadnвҖҷt noticed he was dead. He had simply got up to teach one day and left his body behind him in an armchair in front of the staffroom fire; his routine had not varied in the slightest since.
Today was as boring as ever. Professor Binns opened his notes and began to read in a flat drone like an old vacuum cleaner until nearly everyone in the class was in a deep stupor, occasionally comВӯing to long enough to copy down a name or date, then falling asleep again. He had been speaking for half an hour when someВӯthing happened that had never happened before. Hermione put up her hand.
Professor Binns, glancing up in the middle of a deadly dull lecture on the International Warlock Convention of 1289, looked amazed.
вҖңMiss вҖ” er вҖ” ?вҖқ
вҖңGranger, Professor. I was wondering if you could tell us anyВӯthing about the Chamber of Secrets,вҖқ said Hermione in a clear voice.
Dean Thomas, who had been sitting with his mouth hanging open, gazing out of the window, jerked out of his trance; Lavender BrownвҖҷs head came up off her arms and Neville LongbottomвҖҷs elВӯbow slipped off his desk.
Professor Binns blinked.
вҖңMy subject is History of Magic,вҖқ he said in his dry, wheezy voice. вҖңI deal with, facts, Miss Granger, not myths and legends.вҖқ He cleared his throat with a small noise like chalk snapping and conВӯtinued, вҖңIn September of that year, a subcommittee of Sardinian sorcerers вҖ”вҖқ
He stuttered to a halt. HermioneвҖҷs hand was waving in the air again.
вҖңMiss Grant?вҖқ
вҖңPlease, sir, donвҖҷt legends always have a basis in fact?вҖқ
Professor Binns was looking at her in such amazement, Harry was sure no student had ever interrupted him before, alive or dead.
вҖңWell,вҖқ said Professor Binns slowly, вҖңyes, one could argue that, I suppose.вҖқ He peered at Hermione as though he had never seen a student properly before. вҖңHowever, the legend of which you speak is such a very sensational, even ludicrous tale вҖ”вҖқ
But the whole class was now hanging on Professor BinnsвҖҷs every word. He looked dimly at them all, every face turned to his. Harry could tell he was completely thrown by such an unusual show of interest.
вҖңOh, very well,вҖқ he said slowly. вҖңLet me see вҖҰ the Chamber of Secrets вҖҰ
вҖңYou all know, of course, that Hogwarts was founded over a thousand years ago вҖ” the precise date is uncertain вҖ” by the four greatest witches and wizards of the age. The four school Houses are named after them: Godric Gryffindor, Helga Hufflepuff, Rowena Ravenclaw, and Salazar Slytherin. They built this castle together, far from prying Muggle eyes, for it was an age when magic was feared by common people, and witches and wizards suffered much persecution.вҖқ
He paused, gazed blearily around the room, and continued.
вҖңFor a few years, the founders worked in harmony together, seeking out youngsters who showed signs of magic and bringing them to the castle to be educated. But then disagreements sprang up between them. A rift began to grow between Slytherin and the others. Slytherin wished to be more selective about the students adВӯmitted to Hogwarts. He believed that magical learning should be kept within all-magic families. He disliked taking students of MugВӯgle parentage, believing them to be untrustworthy. After a while, there was a serious argument on the subject between Slytherin and Gryffindor, and Slytherin left the school.вҖқ
Professor Binns paused again, pursing his lips, looking like a wrinkled old tortoise.
вҖңReliable historical sources tell us this much,вҖқ he said. вҖңBut these honest facts have been obscured by the fanciful legend of the Chamber of Secrets. The story goes that Slytherin had built a hidden chamber in the castle, of which the other founders knew nothing.
вҖңSlytherin, according to the legend, sealed the Chamber of SeВӯcrets so that none would be able to open it until his own true heir arrived at the school. The heir alone would be able to unseal the Chamber of Secrets, unleash the horror within, and use it to purge the school of all who were unworthy to study magic.вҖқ
There was silence as he finished telling the story, but it wasnвҖҷt the usual, sleepy silence that filled Professor BinnsвҖҷs classes. There was unease in the air as everyone continued to watch him, hoping for more. Professor Binns looked faintly annoyed.
вҖңThe whole thing is arrant nonsense, of course,вҖқ he said. вҖңNatuВӯrally, the school has been searched for evidence of such a chamber, many times, by the most learned witches and wizards. It does not exist. A tale told to frighten the gullible.вҖқ
HermioneвҖҷs hand was back in the air.
вҖңSir вҖ” what exactly do you mean by the вҖҳhorror withinвҖҷ the Chamber?вҖқ
вҖңThat is believed to be some sort of monster, which the Heir of Slytherin alone can control,вҖқ said Professor Binns in his dry, reedy voice.
The class exchanged nervous looks.
вҖңI tell you, the thing does not exist,вҖқ said Professor Binns, shufВӯfling his notes. вҖңThere is no Chamber and no monster.вҖқ
вҖңBut, sir,вҖқ said Seamus Finnigan, вҖңif the Chamber can only be opened by SlytherinвҖҷs true heir, no one else would be able to find it, would they?вҖқ
вҖңNonsense, OвҖҷFlaherty,вҖқ said Professor Binns in an aggravated tone. вҖңIf a long succession of Hogwarts headmasters and headВӯmistresses havenвҖҷt found the thing вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBut, Professor,вҖқ piped up Parvati Patil, вҖңyouвҖҷd probably have to use Dark Magic to open it вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңJust because a wizard doesnвҖҷt use Dark Magic doesnвҖҷt mean he canвҖҷt, Miss Pennyfeather,вҖқ snapped Professor Binns. вҖңI repeat, if the likes of Dumbledore вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBut maybe youвҖҷve got to be related to Slytherin, so DumbleВӯdore couldnвҖҷt вҖ”вҖқ began Dean Thomas, but Professor Binns had had enough.
вҖңThat will do,вҖқ he said sharply. вҖңIt is a myth! It does not exist! There is not a shred of evidence that Slytherin ever built so much as a secret broom cupboard! I regret telling you such a foolish story! We will return, if you please, to history, to solid, believable, verifiВӯable fact!вҖқ
And within five minutes, the class had sunk back into its usual torpor.
вҖңI always knew Salazar Slytherin was a twisted old loony,вҖқ Ron told Harry and Hermione as they fought their way through the teeming corridors at the end of the lesson to drop off their bags before dinner. вҖңBut I never knew he started all this pure-blood stuff. I wouldnвҖҷt be in his House if you paid me. Honestly, if the Sorting Hat had tried to put me in Slytherin, IвҖҷdвҖҷve got the train straight back home. вҖҰвҖқ
Hermione nodded fervently, but Harry didnвҖҷt say anything. His stomach had just dropped unpleasantly.
Harry had never told Ron and Hermione that the Sorting Hat had seriously considered putting him in Slytherin. He could reВӯmember, as though it were yesterday, the small voice that had spoВӯken in his ear when heвҖҷd placed the hat on his head a year before: You could be great, you know, itвҖҷs all here in your head, and Slytherin would help you on the way to greatness, no doubt about that. вҖҰ
But Harry, who had already heard of Slytherin HouseвҖҷs reputaВӯtion for turning out Dark wizards, had thought desperately, Not Slytherin! and the hat had said, Oh, well, if youвҖҷre sure вҖҰ better be Gryffindor. вҖҰ
As they were shunted along in the throng, Colin Creevey went past.
вҖңHiya, Harry!вҖқ
вҖңHullo, Colin,вҖқ said Harry automatically.
вҖңHarry вҖ” Harry вҖ” a boy in my class has been saying youвҖҷre вҖ”вҖқ
But Colin was so small he couldnвҖҷt fight against the tide of people bearing him toward the Great Hall; they heard him squeak, вҖңSee you, Harry!вҖқ and he was gone.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs a boy in his class saying about you?вҖқ Hermione wonВӯdered.
вҖңThat IвҖҷm SlytherinвҖҷs heir, I expect,вҖқ said Harry, his stomach dropping another inch or so as he suddenly remembered the way Justin Finch-Fletchley had run away from him at lunchtime.
вҖңPeople hereвҖҷll believe anything,вҖқ said Ron in disgust.
The crowd thinned and they were able to climb the next stairВӯcase without difficulty.
вҖңDвҖҷyou really think thereвҖҷs a Chamber of Secrets?вҖқ Ron asked Hermione.
вҖңI donвҖҷt know,вҖқ she said, frowning. вҖңDumbledore couldnвҖҷt cure Mrs. Norris, and that makes me think that whatever attacked her might not be вҖ” well вҖ” human.вҖқ
As she spoke, they turned a corner and found themselves at the end of the very corridor where the attack had happened. They stopped and looked. The scene was just as it had been that night, except that there was no stiff cat hanging from the torch bracket, and an empty chair stood against the wall bearing the message вҖңThe Chamber of Secrets Has Been Opened.вҖқ
вҖңThatвҖҷs where Filch has been keeping guard,вҖқ Ron muttered.
They looked at each other. The corridor was deserted.
вҖңCanвҖҷt hurt to have a poke around,вҖқ said Harry, dropping his bag and getting to his hands and knees so that he could crawl along, searching for clues.
вҖңScorch marks!вҖқ he said. вҖңHere вҖ” and here вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңCome and look at this!вҖқ said Hermione. вҖңThis is funny. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry got up and crossed to the window next to the message on the wall. Hermione was pointing at the topmost pane, where around twenty spiders were scuttling, apparently fighting to get through a small crack. A long, silvery thread was dangling like a rope, as though they had all climbed it in their hurry to get outside.
вҖңHave you ever seen spiders act like that?вҖқ said Hermione wonВӯderingly.
вҖңNo,вҖқ said Harry, вҖңhave you, Ron? Ron?вҖқ
He looked over his shoulder. Ron was standing well back and seemed to be fighting the impulse to run.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs up?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңI вҖ” donвҖҷt вҖ” like вҖ” spiders,вҖқ said Ron tensely.
вҖңI never knew that,вҖқ said Hermione, looking at Ron in surprise. вҖңYouвҖҷve used spiders in Potions loads of times. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңI donвҖҷt mind them dead,вҖқ said Ron, who was carefully lookВӯing anywhere but at the window. вҖңI just donвҖҷt like the way they move. вҖҰвҖқ
Hermione giggled.
вҖңItвҖҷs not funny,вҖқ said Ron, fiercely. вҖңIf you must know, when I was three, Fred turned my вҖ” my teddy bear into a great big filthy spider because I broke his toy broomstick. вҖҰ You wouldnвҖҷt like them either if youвҖҷd been holding your bear and suddenly it had too many legs and вҖҰвҖқ
He broke off, shuddering. Hermione was obviously still trying not to laugh. Feeling they had better get off the subject, Harry said, вҖңRemember all that water on the floor? Where did that come from? SomeoneвҖҷs mopped it up.вҖқ
вҖңIt was about here,вҖқ said Ron, recovering himself to walk a few paces past FilchвҖҷs chair and pointing. вҖңLevel with this door.вҖқ
He reached for the brass doorknob but suddenly withdrew his hand as though heвҖҷd been burned.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs the matter?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңCanвҖҷt go in there,вҖқ said Ron gruffly. вҖңThatвҖҷs a girlsвҖҷ toilet.вҖқ
вҖңOh, Ron, there wonвҖҷt be anyone in there,вҖқ said Hermione, standing up and coming over. вҖңThatвҖҷs Moaning MyrtleвҖҷs place. Come on, letвҖҷs have a look.вҖқ
And ignoring the large OUT OF ORDER sign, she opened the door.
It was the gloomiest, most depressing bathroom Harry had ever set foot in. Under a large, cracked, and spotted mirror were a row of chipped sinks. The floor was damp and reflected the dull light given off by the stubs of a few candles, burning low in their holdВӯers; the wooden doors to the stalls were flaking and scratched and one of them was dangling off its hinges.
Hermione put her fingers to her lips and set off toward the end stall. When she reached it she said, вҖңHello, Myrtle, how are you?вҖқ
Harry and Ron went to look. Moaning Myrtle was floating above the tank of the toilet, picking a spot on her chin.
вҖңThis is a girlsвҖҷ bathroom,вҖқ she said, eyeing Ron and Harry susВӯpiciously. вҖңTheyвҖҷre not girls.вҖқ
вҖңNo,вҖқ Hermione agreed. вҖңI just wanted to show them how вҖ” er вҖ” nice it is in here.вҖқ
She waved vaguely at the dirty old mirror and the damp floor.
вҖңAsk her if she saw anything,вҖқ Harry mouthed at Hermione.
вҖңWhat are you whispering?вҖқ said Myrtle, staring at him.
вҖңNothing,вҖқ said Harry quickly. вҖңWe wanted to ask вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI wish people would stop talking behind my back!вҖқ said Myrtle, in a voice choked with tears. вҖңI do have feelings, you know, even if I am dead вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңMyrtle, no one wants to upset you,вҖқ said Hermione. вҖңHarry only вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңNo one wants to upset me! ThatвҖҷs a good one!вҖқ howled Myrtle. вҖңMy life was nothing but misery at this place and now people come along ruining my death!вҖқ
вҖңWe wanted to ask you if youвҖҷve seen anything funny lately,вҖқ said Hermione quickly. вҖңBecause a cat was attacked right outside your front door on Halloween.вҖқ
вҖңDid you see anyone near here that night?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңI wasnвҖҷt paying attention,вҖқ said Myrtle dramatically. вҖңPeeves upset me so much I came in here and tried to kill myself. Then, of course, I remembered that IвҖҷm вҖ” that IвҖҷm вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңAlready dead,вҖқ said Ron helpfully.
Myrtle gave a tragic sob, rose up in the air, turned over, and dived headfirst into the toilet, splashing water all over them and vanishing from sight, although from the direction of her muffled sobs, she had come to rest somewhere in the U-bend.
Harry and Ron stood with their mouths open, but Hermione shrugged wearily and said, вҖңHonestly, that was almost cheerful for Myrtle. вҖҰ Come on, letвҖҷs go.вҖқ
Harry had barely closed the door on MyrtleвҖҷs gurgling sobs when a loud voice made all three of them jump.
вҖңRON!вҖқ
Percy Weasley had stopped dead at the head of the stairs, prefect badge agleam, an expression of complete shock on his face.
вҖңThatвҖҷs a girlsвҖҷ bathroom!вҖқ he gasped. вҖңWhat were you вҖ” ?вҖқ
вҖңJust having a look around,вҖқ Ron shrugged. вҖңClues, you know вҖ”вҖқ
Percy swelled in a manner that reminded Harry forcefully of Mrs. Weasley.
вҖңGet вҖ” away вҖ” from вҖ” there вҖ”вҖқ Percy said, striding toward them and starting to bustle them along, flapping his arms. вҖңDonвҖҷt you care what this looks like? Coming back here while everyoneвҖҷs at dinner вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWhy shouldnвҖҷt we be here?вҖқ said Ron hotly, stopping short and glaring at Percy. вҖңListen, we never laid a finger on that cat!вҖқ
вҖңThatвҖҷs what I told Ginny,вҖқ said Percy fiercely, вҖңbut she still seems to think youвҖҷre going to be expelled, IвҖҷve never seen her so upset, crying her eyes out, you might think of her, all the first years are thoroughly overexcited by this business вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYou donвҖҷt care about Ginny,вҖқ said Ron, whose ears were now reddening. вҖңYouвҖҷre just worried IвҖҷm going to mess up your chances of being Head Boy вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңFive points from Gryffindor!вҖқ Percy said tersely, fingering his prefect badge. вҖңAnd I hope it teaches you a lesson! No more detecВӯtive work, or IвҖҷll write to Mum!вҖқ
And he strode off, the back of his neck as red as RonвҖҷs ears.
Harry, Ron, and Hermione chose seats as far as possible from Percy in the common room that night. Ron was still in a very bad temВӯper and kept blotting his Charms homework. When he reached absently for his wand to remove the smudges, it ignited the parchВӯment. Fuming almost as much as his homework, Ron slammed The Standard Book of Spells, Grade 2 shut. To HarryвҖҷs surprise, Hermione followed suit.
вҖңWho can it be, though?вҖқ she said in a quiet voice, as though continuing a conversation they had just been having. вҖңWhoвҖҷd want to frighten all the Squibs and Muggle-borns out of Hogwarts?вҖқ
вҖңLetвҖҷs think,вҖқ said Ron in mock puzzlement. вҖңWho do we know who thinks Muggle-borns are scum?вҖқ
He looked at Hermione. Hermione looked back, unconvinced.
вҖңIf youвҖҷre talking about Malfoy вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңOf course I am!вҖқ said Ron. вҖңYou heard him вҖ” вҖҳYouвҖҷll be next, Mudbloods!вҖҷ вҖ” come on, youвҖҷve only got to look at his foul rat face to know itвҖҷs him вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңMalfoy, the Heir of Slytherin?вҖқ said Hermione skeptically.
вҖңLook at his family,вҖқ said Harry, closing his books, too. вҖңThe whole lot of them have been in Slytherin; heвҖҷs always boasting about it. They could easily be SlytherinвҖҷs descendants. His fatherвҖҷs definitely evil enough.вҖқ
вҖңThey couldвҖҷve had the key to the Chamber of Secrets for cenВӯturies!вҖқ said Ron. вҖңHanding it down, father to son. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңWell,вҖқ said Hermione cautiously, вҖңI suppose itвҖҷs possible. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңBut how do we prove it?вҖқ said Harry darkly.
вҖңThere might be a way,вҖқ said Hermione slowly, dropping her voice still further with a quick glance across the room at Percy. вҖңOf course, it would be difficult. And dangerous, very dangerous. WeвҖҷd be breaking about fifty school rules, I expect вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңIf, in a month or so, you feel like explaining, you will let us know, wonвҖҷt you?вҖқ said Ron irritably.
вҖңAll right,вҖқ said Hermione coldly. вҖңWhat weвҖҷd need to do is to get inside the Slytherin common room and ask Malfoy a few quesВӯtions without him realizing itвҖҷs us.вҖқ
вҖңBut thatвҖҷs impossible,вҖқ Harry said as Ron laughed.
вҖңNo, itвҖҷs not,вҖқ said Hermione. вҖңAll weвҖҷd need would be some Polyjuice Potion.вҖқ
вҖңWhatвҖҷs that?вҖқ said Ron and Harry together.
вҖңSnape mentioned it in class a few weeks ago вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңDвҖҷyou think weвҖҷve got nothing better to do in Potions than lisВӯten to Snape?вҖқ muttered Ron.
вҖңIt transforms you into somebody else. Think about it! We could change into three of the Slytherins. No one would know it was us. Malfoy would probably tell us anything. HeвҖҷs probably boasting about it in the Slytherin common room right now, if only we could hear him.вҖқ
вҖңThis Polyjuice stuff sounds a bit dodgy to me,вҖқ said Ron, frowning. вҖңWhat if we were stuck looking like three of the Slytherins forever?вҖқ
вҖңIt wears off after a while,вҖқ said Hermione, waving her hand impatiently. вҖңBut getting hold of the recipe will be very difficult. Snape said it was in a book called Moste Potente Potions and itвҖҷs bound to be in the Restricted Section of the library.вҖқ
There was only one way to get out a book from the Restricted Section: You needed a signed note of permission from a teacher.
вҖңHard to see why weвҖҷd want the book, really,вҖқ said Ron, вҖңif we werenвҖҷt going to try and make one of the potions.вҖқ
вҖңI think,вҖқ said Hermione, вҖңthat if we made it sound as though we were just interested in the theory, we might stand a chance. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңOh, come on, no teacherвҖҷs going to fall for that,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңTheyвҖҷd have to be really thick. вҖҰвҖқ
## Chapter 10

The Rogue Bludger
Since the disastrous episode of the pixies, Professor Lockhart had not brought live creatures to class. Instead, he read passages from his books to them, and sometimes reenacted some of the more dramatic bits. He usually picked Harry to help him with these reconstructions; so far, Harry had been forced to play a simВӯple Transylvanian villager whom Lockhart had cured of a Babbling Curse, a yeti with a head cold, and a vampire who had been unable to eat anything except lettuce since Lockhart had dealt with him.
Harry was hauled to the front of the class during their very next Defense Against the Dark Arts lesson, this time acting a werewolf. If he hadnвҖҷt had a very good reason for keeping Lockhart in a good mood, he would have refused to do it.
вҖңNice loud howl, Harry вҖ” exactly вҖ” and then, if youвҖҷll believe it, I pounced вҖ” like this вҖ” slammed him to the floor вҖ” thus вҖ” with one hand, I managed to hold him down вҖ” with my other, I put my wand to his throat вҖ” I then screwed up my remainВӯing strength and performed the immensely complex Homorphus Charm вҖ” he let out a piteous moan вҖ” go on, Harry вҖ” higher than that вҖ” good вҖ” the fur vanished вҖ” the fangs shrank вҖ” and he turned back into a man. Simple, yet effective вҖ” and another village will remember me forever as the hero who delivered them from the monthly terror of werewolf attacks.вҖқ
The bell rang and Lockhart got to his feet.
