вҖңHomework вҖ” compose a poem about my defeat of the Wagga Wagga Werewolf! Signed copies of Magical Me to the author of the best one!вҖқ
The class began to leave. Harry returned to the back of the room, where Ron and Hermione were waiting.
вҖңReady?вҖқ Harry muttered.
вҖңWait till everyoneвҖҷs gone,вҖқ said Hermione nervously. вҖңAll right вҖҰвҖқ
She approached LockhartвҖҷs desk, a piece of paper clutched tightly in her hand, Harry and Ron right behind her.
вҖңEr вҖ” Professor Lockhart?вҖқ Hermione stammered. вҖңI wanted to вҖ” to get this book out of the library. Just for background readВӯing.вҖқ She held out the piece of paper, her hand shaking slightly. вҖңBut the thing is, itвҖҷs in the Restricted Section of the library, so I need a teacher to sign for it вҖ” IвҖҷm sure it would help me underВӯstand what you say in Gadding with Ghouls about slow-acting venВӯoms вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңAh, Gadding with Ghouls!вҖқ said Lockhart, taking the note from Hermione and smiling widely at her. вҖңPossibly my very favorite book. You enjoyed it?вҖқ
вҖңOh, yes,вҖқ said Hermione eagerly. вҖңSo clever, the way you trapped that last one with the tea-strainer вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWell, IвҖҷm sure no one will mind me giving the best student of the year a little extra help,вҖқ said Lockhart warmly, and he pulled out an enormous peacock quill. вҖңYes, nice, isnвҖҷt it?вҖқ he said, misreading the revolted look on RonвҖҷs face. вҖңI usually save it for book signings.вҖқ
He scrawled an enormous loopy signature on the note and handed it back to Hermione.
вҖңSo, Harry,вҖқ said Lockhart, while Hermione folded the note with fumbling fingers and slipped it into her bag. вҖңTomorrowвҖҷs the first Quidditch match of the season, I believe? Gryffindor against Slytherin, is it not? I hear youвҖҷre a useful player. I was a Seeker, too. I was asked to try for the National Squad, but preferred to dedicate my life to the eradication of the Dark Forces. Still, if ever you feel the need for a little private training, donвҖҷt hesitate to ask. Always happy to pass on my expertise to less able players. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry made an indistinct noise in his throat and then hurried off after Ron and Hermione.
вҖңI donвҖҷt believe it,вҖқ he said as the three of them examined the signature on the note. вҖңHe didnвҖҷt even look at the book we wanted.вҖқ
вҖңThatвҖҷs because heвҖҷs a brainless git,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңBut who cares, weвҖҷve got what we needed вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHe is not a brainless git,вҖқ said Hermione shrilly as they half ran toward the library.
вҖңJust because he said you were the best student of the year вҖ”вҖқ
They dropped their voices as they entered the muffled stillness of the library. Madam Pince, the librarian, was a thin, irritable woman who looked like an underfed vulture.
вҖңMoste Potente Potions?вҖқ she repeated suspiciously, trying to take the note from Hermione; but Hermione wouldnвҖҷt let go.
вҖңI was wondering if I could keep it,вҖқ she said breathlessly.
вҖңOh, come on,вҖқ said Ron, wrenching it from her grasp and thrusting it at Madam Pince. вҖңWeвҖҷll get you another autograph. LockhartвҖҷll sign anything if it stands still long enough.вҖқ
Madam Pince held the note up to the light, as though deterВӯmined to detect a forgery, but it passed the test. She stalked away between the lofty shelves and returned several minutes later carryВӯing a large and moldy-looking book. Hermione put it carefully into her bag and they left, trying not to walk too quickly or look too guilty.
Five minutes later, they were barricaded in Moaning MyrtleвҖҷs out-of-order bathroom once again. Hermione had overridden RonвҖҷs objections by pointing out that it was the last place anyone in their right minds would go, so they were guaranteed some privacy. Moaning Myrtle was crying noisily in her stall, but they were igВӯnoring her, and she them.
Hermione opened Moste Potente Potions carefully, and the three of them bent over the damp-spotted pages. It was clear from a glance why it belonged in the Restricted Section. Some of the poВӯtions had effects almost too gruesome to think about, and there were some very unpleasant illustrations, which included a man who seemed to have been turned inside out and a witch sprouting several extra pairs of arms out of her head.
вҖңHere it is,вҖқ said Hermione excitedly as she found the page headed The Polyjuice Potion. It was decorated with drawings of people halfway through transforming into other people. Harry sincerely hoped the artist had imagined the looks of intense pain on their faces.
вҖңThis is the most complicated potion IвҖҷve ever seen,вҖқ said Hermione as they scanned the recipe. вҖңLacewing flies, leeches, fluxweed, and knotgrass,вҖқ she murmured, running her finger down the list of ingredients. вҖңWell, theyвҖҷre easy enough, theyвҖҷre in the student store-cupboard, we can help ourselves. вҖҰ Oooh, look, powdered horn of a bicorn вҖ” donвҖҷt know where weвҖҷre going to get that вҖ” shredded skin of a boomslang вҖ” thatвҖҷll be tricky, too вҖ” and of course a bit of whoever we want to change into.вҖқ
вҖңExcuse me?вҖқ said Ron sharply. вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou mean, a bit of whoever weвҖҷre changing into? IвҖҷm drinking nothing with CrabbeвҖҷs toenails in it вҖ”вҖқ
Hermione continued as though she hadnвҖҷt heard him.
вҖңWe donвҖҷt have to worry about that yet, though, because we add those bits last. вҖҰвҖқ
Ron turned, speechless, to Harry, who had another worry.
вҖңDвҖҷyou realize how much weвҖҷre going to have to steal, HerВӯmione? Shredded skin of a boomslang, thatвҖҷs definitely not in the studentsвҖҷ cupboard. WhatвҖҷre we going to do, break into SnapeвҖҷs priВӯvate stores? I donвҖҷt know if this is a good idea. вҖҰвҖқ
Hermione shut the book with a snap.
вҖңWell, if you two are going to chicken out, fine,вҖқ she said. There were bright pink patches on her cheeks and her eyes were brighter than usual. вҖңI donвҖҷt want to break rules, you know. I think threatВӯening Muggle-borns is far worse than brewing up a difficult poВӯtion. But if you donвҖҷt want to find out if itвҖҷs Malfoy, IвҖҷll go straight to Madam Pince now and hand the book back in вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI never thought IвҖҷd see the day when youвҖҷd be persuading us to break rules,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңAll right, weвҖҷll do it. But not toenails, okay?вҖқ
вҖңHow long will it take to make, anyway?вҖқ said Harry as HerВӯmione, looking happier, opened the book again.
вҖңWell, since the fluxweed has got to be picked at the full moon and the lacewings have got to be stewed for twenty-one days вҖҰ IвҖҷd say itвҖҷd be ready in about a month, if we can get all the ingredients.вҖқ
вҖңA month?вҖқ said Ron. вҖңMalfoy could have attacked half the Muggle-borns in the school by then!вҖқ But HermioneвҖҷs eyes narВӯrowed dangerously again, and he added swiftly, вҖңBut itвҖҷs the best plan weвҖҷve got, so full steam ahead, I say.вҖқ
However, while Hermione was checking that the coast was clear for them to leave the bathroom, Ron muttered to Harry, вҖңItвҖҷll be a lot less hassle if you can just knock Malfoy off his broom tomorВӯrow.вҖқ
Harry woke early on Saturday morning and lay for a while thinkВӯing about the coming Quidditch match. He was nervous, mainly at the thought of what Wood would say if Gryffindor lost, but also at the idea of facing a team mounted on the fastest racing brooms gold could buy. He had never wanted to beat Slytherin so badly. After half an hour of lying there with his insides churning, he got up, dressed, and went down to breakfast early, where he found the rest of the Gryffindor team huddled at the long, empty table, all looking uptight and not speaking much.
As eleven oвҖҷclock approached, the whole school started to make its way down to the Quidditch stadium. It was a muggy sort of day with a hint of thunder in the air. Ron and Hermione came hurryВӯing over to wish Harry good luck as he entered the locker rooms. The team pulled on their scarlet Gryffindor robes, then sat down to listen to WoodвҖҷs usual pre-match pep talk.
вҖңSlytherin has better brooms than us,вҖқ he began. вҖңNo point deВӯnying it. But weвҖҷve got better people on our brooms. WeвҖҷve trained harder than they have, weвҖҷve been flying in all weathers вҖ”вҖқ (вҖңToo true,вҖқ muttered George Weasley. вҖңI havenвҖҷt been properly dry since AugustвҖқ) вҖңвҖ” and weвҖҷre going to make them rue the day they let that little bit of slime, Malfoy, buy his way onto their team.вҖқ
Chest heaving with emotion, Wood turned to Harry.
вҖңItвҖҷll be down to you, Harry, to show them that a Seeker has to have something more than a rich father. Get to that Snitch before Malfoy or die trying, Harry, because weвҖҷve got to win today, weвҖҷve got to.вҖқ
вҖңSo no pressure, Harry,вҖқ said Fred, winking at him.
As they walked out onto the field, a roar of noise greeted them; mainly cheers, because Ravenclaw and Hufflepuff were anxious to see Slytherin beaten, but the Slytherins in the crowd made their boos and hisses heard, too. Madam Hooch, the Quidditch teacher, asked Flint and Wood to shake hands, which they did, giving each other threatening stares and gripping rather harder than was necesВӯsary.
вҖңOn my whistle,вҖқ said Madam Hooch. вҖңThree вҖҰ two вҖҰ one вҖҰвҖқ
With a roar from the crowd to speed them upward, the fourteen players rose toward the leaden sky. Harry flew higher than any of them, squinting around for the Snitch.
вҖңAll right there, Scarhead?вҖқ yelled Malfoy, shooting underneath him as though to show off the speed of his broom.
Harry had no time to reply. At that very moment, a heavy black Bludger came pelting toward him; he avoided it so narrowly that he felt it ruffle his hair as it passed.
вҖңClose one, Harry!вҖқ said George, streaking past him with his club in his hand, ready to knock the Bludger back toward a SlythВӯerin. Harry saw George give the Bludger a powerful whack in the direction of Adrian Pucey, but the Bludger changed direction in midair and shot straight for Harry again.
Harry dropped quickly to avoid it, and George managed to hit it hard toward Malfoy. Once again, the Bludger swerved like a boomerang and shot at HarryвҖҷs head.
Harry put on a burst of speed and zoomed toward the other end of the field. He could hear the Bludger whistling along behind him. What was going on? Bludgers never concentrated on one player like this; it was their job to try and unseat as many people as possible. вҖҰ
Fred Weasley was waiting for the Bludger at the other end. Harry ducked as Fred swung at the Bludger with all his might; the Bludger was knocked off course.
вҖңGotcha!вҖқ Fred yelled happily, but he was wrong; as though it was magnetically attracted to Harry, the Bludger pelted after him once more and Harry was forced to fly off at full speed.
It had started to rain; Harry felt heavy drops fall onto his face, splattering onto his glasses. He didnвҖҷt have a clue what was going on in the rest of the game until he heard Lee Jordan, who was comВӯmentating, say, вҖңSlytherin lead, sixty points to zero вҖ”вҖқ
The SlytherinsвҖҷ superior brooms were clearly doing their jobs, and meanwhile the mad Bludger was doing all it could to knock Harry out of the air. Fred and George were now flying so close to him on either side that Harry could see nothing at all except their flailing arms and had no chance to look for the Snitch, let alone catch it.
вҖңSomeoneвҖҷs вҖ” tampered вҖ” with вҖ” this вҖ” Bludger вҖ”вҖқ Fred grunted, swinging his bat with all his might at it as it launched a new attack on Harry.
вҖңWe need time out,вҖқ said George, trying to signal to Wood and stop the Bludger breaking HarryвҖҷs nose at the same time.
Wood had obviously got the message. Madam HoochвҖҷs whistle rang out and Harry, Fred, and George dived for the ground, still trying to avoid the mad Bludger.
вҖңWhatвҖҷs going on?вҖқ said Wood as the Gryffindor team huddled together, while Slytherins in the crowd jeered. вҖңWeвҖҷre being flatВӯtened. Fred, George, where were you when that Bludger stopped Angelina scoring?вҖқ
вҖңWe were twenty feet above her, stopping the other Bludger from murdering Harry, Oliver,вҖқ said George angrily. вҖңSomeoneвҖҷs fixed it вҖ” it wonвҖҷt leave Harry alone. It hasnвҖҷt gone for anyone else all game. The Slytherins must have done something to it.вҖқ
вҖңBut the Bludgers have been locked in Madam HoochвҖҷs office since our last practice, and there was nothing wrong with them then. вҖҰвҖқ said Wood, anxiously.
Madam Hooch was walking toward them. Over her shoulder, Harry could see the Slytherin team jeering and pointing in his diВӯrection.
вҖңListen,вҖқ said Harry as she came nearer and nearer, вҖңwith you two flying around me all the time the only way IвҖҷm going to catch the Snitch is if it flies up my sleeve. Go back to the rest of the team and let me deal with the rogue one.вҖқ
вҖңDonвҖҷt be thick,вҖқ said Fred. вҖңItвҖҷll take your head off.вҖқ
Wood was looking from Harry to the Weasleys.
вҖңOliver, this is insane,вҖқ said Alicia Spinnet angrily. вҖңYou canвҖҷt let Harry deal with that thing on his own. LetвҖҷs ask for an inquiry вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңIf we stop now, weвҖҷll have to forfeit the match!вҖқ said Harry. вҖңAnd weвҖҷre not losing to Slytherin just because of a crazy Bludger! Come on, Oliver, tell them to leave me alone!вҖқ
вҖңThis is all your fault,вҖқ George said angrily to Wood. вҖң вҖҳGet the Snitch or die trying,вҖҷ what a stupid thing to tell him вҖ”вҖқ
Madam Hooch had joined them.
вҖңReady to resume play?вҖқ she asked Wood.
Wood looked at the determined look on HarryвҖҷs face.
вҖңAll right,вҖқ he said. вҖңFred, George, you heard Harry вҖ” leave him alone and let him deal with the Bludger on his own.вҖқ
The rain was falling more heavily now. On Madam HoochвҖҷs whistle, Harry kicked hard into the air and heard the telltale whoosh of the Bludger behind him. Higher and higher Harry climbed; he looped and swooped, spiraled, zigzagged, and rolled. Slightly dizzy, he nevertheless kept his eyes wide open, rain was speckling his glasses and ran up his nostrils as he hung upside down, avoiding another fierce dive from the Bludger. He could hear laughter from the crowd; he knew he must look very stupid, but the rogue Bludger was heavy and couldnвҖҷt change direction as quickly as Harry could; he began a kind of roller-coaster ride around the edges of the stadium, squinting through the silver sheets of rain to the Gryffindor goal posts, where Adrian Pucey was trying to get past Wood вҖ”
A whistling in HarryвҖҷs ear told him the Bludger had just missed him again; he turned right over and sped in the opposite direction.
вҖңTraining for the ballet, Potter?вҖқ yelled Malfoy as Harry was forced to do a stupid kind of twirl in midair to dodge the Bludger, and he fled, the Bludger trailing a few feet behind him; and then, glaring back at Malfoy in hatred, he saw it вҖ” the Golden Snitch. It was hovering inches above MalfoyвҖҷs left ear вҖ” and Malfoy, busy laughing at Harry, hadnвҖҷt seen it.
For an agonizing moment, Harry hung in midair, not daring to speed toward Malfoy in case he looked up and saw the Snitch.
WHAM.
He had stayed still a second too long. The Bludger had hit him at last, smashed into his elbow, and Harry felt his arm break. Dimly, dazed by the searing pain in his arm, he slid sideways on his rain-drenched broom, one knee still crooked over it, his right arm dangling useless at his side вҖ” the Bludger came pelting back for a second attack, this time aiming at his face вҖ” Harry swerved out of the way, one idea firmly lodged in his numb brain: get to Malfoy.
Through a haze of rain and pain he dived for the shimmering, sneering face below him and saw its eyes widen with fear: Malfoy thought Harry was attacking him.
вҖңWhat the вҖ”вҖқ he gasped, careening out of HarryвҖҷs way.
Harry took his remaining hand off his broom and made a wild snatch; he felt his fingers close on the cold Snitch but was now only gripping the broom with his legs, and there was a yell from the crowd below as he headed straight for the ground, trying hard not to pass out.
With a splattering thud he hit the mud and rolled off his broom. His arm was hanging at a very strange angle; riddled with pain, he heard, as though from a distance, a good deal of whistling and shouting. He focused on the Snitch clutched in his good hand.
вҖңAha,вҖқ he said vaguely. вҖңWeвҖҷve won.вҖқ
And he fainted.
He came around, rain falling on his face, still lying on the field, with someone leaning over him. He saw a glitter of teeth.
вҖңOh, no, not you,вҖқ he moaned.
вҖңDoesnвҖҷt know what heвҖҷs saying,вҖқ said Lockhart loudly to the anxious crowd of Gryffindors pressing around them. вҖңNot to worry, Harry. IвҖҷm about to fix your arm.вҖқ
вҖңNo!вҖқ said Harry. вҖңIвҖҷll keep it like this, thanks. вҖҰвҖқ
He tried to sit up, but the pain was terrible. He heard a familiar clicking noise nearby.
вҖңI donвҖҷt want a photo of this, Colin,вҖқ he said loudly.
вҖңLie back, Harry,вҖқ said Lockhart soothingly. вҖңItвҖҷs a simple charm IвҖҷve used countless times вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWhy canвҖҷt I just go to the hospital wing?вҖқ said Harry through clenched teeth.
вҖңHe should really, Professor,вҖқ said a muddy Wood, who couldnвҖҷt help grinning even though his Seeker was injured. вҖңGreat capture, Harry, really spectacular, your best yet, IвҖҷd say вҖ”вҖқ
Through the thicket of legs around him, Harry spotted Fred and George Weasley, wrestling the rogue Bludger into a box. It was still putting up a terrific fight.
вҖңStand back,вҖқ said Lockhart, who was rolling up his jade-green sleeves.
вҖңNo вҖ” donвҖҷt вҖ”вҖқ said Harry weakly, but Lockhart was twirling his wand and a second later had directed it straight at HarryвҖҷs arm.
A strange and unpleasant sensation started at HarryвҖҷs shoulder and spread all the way down to his fingertips. It felt as though his arm was being deflated. He didnвҖҷt dare look at what was happenВӯing. He had shut his eyes, his face turned away from his arm, but his worst fears were realized as the people above him gasped and Colin Creevey began clicking away madly. His arm didnвҖҷt hurt anyВӯmore вҖ” nor did it feel remotely like an arm.
вҖңAh,вҖқ said Lockhart. вҖңYes. Well, that can sometimes happen. But the point is, the bones are no longer broken. ThatвҖҷs the thing to bear in mind. So, Harry, just toddle up to the hospital wing вҖ” ah, Mr. Weasley, Miss Granger, would you escort him? вҖ” and Madam Pomfrey will be able to вҖ” er вҖ” tidy you up a bit.вҖқ
As Harry got to his feet, he felt strangely lopsided. Taking a deep breath he looked down at his right side. What he saw nearly made him pass out again.
Poking out of the end of his robes was what looked like a thick, flesh-colored rubber glove. He tried to move his fingers. Nothing happened.
Lockhart hadnвҖҷt mended HarryвҖҷs bones. He had removed them.
Madam Pomfrey wasnвҖҷt at all pleased.
вҖңYou should have come straight to me!вҖқ she raged, holding up the sad, limp remainder of what, half an hour before, had been a working arm. вҖңI can mend bones in a second вҖ” but growing them back вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYou will be able to, wonвҖҷt you?вҖқ said Harry desperately.
вҖңIвҖҷll be able to, certainly, but it will be painful,вҖқ said Madam Pomfrey grimly, throwing Harry a pair of pajamas. вҖңYouвҖҷll have to stay the night. вҖҰвҖқ
Hermione waited outside the curtain drawn around HarryвҖҷs bed while Ron helped him into his pajamas. It took a while to stuff the rubbery, boneless arm into a sleeve.
вҖңHow can you stick up for Lockhart now, Hermione, eh?вҖқ Ron called through the curtain as he pulled HarryвҖҷs limp fingers through the cuff. вҖңIf Harry had wanted deboning he would have asked.вҖқ
вҖңAnyone can make a mistake,вҖқ said Hermione. вҖңAnd it doesnвҖҷt hurt anymore, does it, Harry?вҖқ
вҖңNo,вҖқ said Harry, getting into bed. вҖңBut it doesnвҖҷt do anything else either.вҖқ
As he swung himself onto the bed, his arm flapped pointlessly.
Hermione and Madam Pomfrey came around the curtain. Madam Pomfrey was holding a large bottle of something labeled Skele-Gro.
вҖңYouвҖҷre in for a rough night,вҖқ she said, pouring out a steaming beakerful and handing it to him. вҖңRegrowing bones is a nasty busiВӯness.вҖқ
So was taking the Skele-Gro. It burned HarryвҖҷs mouth and throat as it went down, making him cough and splutter. Still tut-tutting about dangerous sports and inept teachers, Madam Pomfrey retreated, leaving Ron and Hermione to help Harry gulp down some water.
вҖңWe won, though,вҖқ said Ron, a grin breaking across his face. вҖңThat was some catch you made. MalfoyвҖҷs face вҖҰ he looked ready to kill. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңI want to know how he fixed that Bludger,вҖқ said Hermione darkly.
вҖңWe can add that to the list of questions weвҖҷll ask him when weвҖҷve taken the Polyjuice Potion,вҖқ said Harry, sinking back onto his pillows. вҖңI hope it tastes better than this stuff. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңIf itвҖҷs got bits of Slytherins in it? YouвҖҷve got to be joking,вҖқ said Ron.
The door of the hospital wing burst open at that moment. Filthy and soaking wet, the rest of the Gryffindor team had arrived to see Harry.
вҖңUnbelievable flying, Harry,вҖқ said George. вҖңIвҖҷve just seen MarВӯcus Flint yelling at Malfoy. Something about having the Snitch on top of his head and not noticing. Malfoy didnвҖҷt seem too happy.вҖқ
They had brought cakes, sweets, and bottles of pumpkin juice; they gathered around HarryвҖҷs bed and were just getting started on what promised to be a good party when Madam Pomfrey came storming over, shouting, вҖңThis boy needs rest, heвҖҷs got thirty-three bones to regrow! Out! OUT!вҖқ
And Harry was left alone, with nothing to distract him from the stabbing pains in his limp arm.
Hours and hours later, Harry woke quite suddenly in the pitch blackness and gave a small yelp of pain: His arm now felt full of large splinters. For a second, he thought that was what had woken him. Then, with a thrill of horror, he realized that someone was sponging his forehead in the dark.
вҖңGet off!вҖқ he said loudly, and then, вҖңDobby!вҖқ
The house-elfвҖҷs goggling tennis ball eyes were peering at Harry through the darkness. A single tear was running down his long, pointed nose.
вҖңHarry Potter came back to school,вҖқ he whispered miserably. вҖңDobby warned and warned Harry Potter. Ah sir, why didnвҖҷt you heed Dobby? Why didnвҖҷt Harry Potter go back home when he missed the train?вҖқ
Harry heaved himself up on his pillows and pushed DobbyвҖҷs sponge away.
вҖңWhatвҖҷre you doing here?вҖқ he said. вҖңAnd how did you know I missed the train?вҖқ
DobbyвҖҷs lip trembled and Harry was seized by a sudden suspiВӯcion.
вҖңIt was you!вҖқ he said slowly. вҖңYou stopped the barrier from letting us through!вҖқ
вҖңIndeed yes, sir,вҖқ said Dobby, nodding his head vigorously, ears flapping. вҖңDobby hid and watched for Harry Potter and sealed the gateway and Dobby had to iron his hands afterwardвҖқ вҖ” he showed Harry ten long, bandaged fingers вҖ” вҖңbut Dobby didnвҖҷt care, sir, for he thought Harry Potter was safe, and never did Dobby dream that Harry Potter would get to school another way!вҖқ
He was rocking backward and forward, shaking his ugly head.
вҖңDobby was so shocked when he heard Harry Potter was back at Hogwarts, he let his masterвҖҷs dinner burn! Such a flogging Dobby never had, sir. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry slumped back onto his pillows.
вҖңYou nearly got Ron and me expelled,вҖқ he said fiercely. вҖңYouвҖҷd better get lost before my bones come back, Dobby, or I might strangle you.вҖқ
Dobby smiled weakly.
вҖңDobby is used to death threats, sir. Dobby gets them five times a day at home.вҖқ
He blew his nose on a corner of the filthy pillowcase he wore, looking so pathetic that Harry felt his anger ebb away in spite of himself.
вҖңWhy dвҖҷyou wear that thing, Dobby?вҖқ he asked curiously.
вҖңThis, sir?вҖқ said Dobby, plucking at the pillowcase. вҖң вҖҷTis a mark of the house-elfвҖҷs enslavement, sir. Dobby can only be freed if his masters present him with clothes, sir. The family is careful not to pass Dobby even a sock, sir, for then he would be free to leave their house forever.вҖқ
Dobby mopped his bulging eyes and said suddenly, вҖңHarry PotВӯter must go home! Dobby thought his Bludger would be enough to make вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYour Bludger?вҖқ said Harry, anger rising once more. вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou mean, your Bludger? You made that Bludger try and kill me?вҖқ
вҖңNot kill you, sir, never kill you!вҖқ said Dobby, shocked. вҖңDobby wants to save Harry PotterвҖҷs life! Better sent home, grievously inВӯjured, than remain here, sir! Dobby only wanted Harry Potter hurt enough to be sent home!вҖқ
вҖңOh, is that all?вҖқ said Harry angrily. вҖңI donвҖҷt suppose youвҖҷre goВӯing to tell me why you wanted me sent home in pieces?вҖқ
вҖңAh, if Harry Potter only knew!вҖқ Dobby groaned, more tears dripping onto his ragged pillowcase. вҖңIf he knew what he means to us, to the lowly, the enslaved, we dregs of the magical world! Dobby remembers how it was when He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named was at the height of his powers, sir! We house-elves were treated like vermin, sir! Of course, Dobby is still treated like that, sir,вҖқ he admitted, drying his face on the pillowcase. вҖңBut mostly, sir, life has improved for my kind since you triumphed over He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named. Harry Potter survived, and the Dark LordвҖҷs power was broken, and it was a new dawn, sir, and Harry Potter shone like a beacon of hope for those of us who thought the Dark days would never end, sir. вҖҰ And now, at Hogwarts, terrible things are to happen, are perhaps happening already, and Dobby cannot let Harry Potter stay here now that history is to repeat itself, now that the Chamber of Secrets is open once more вҖ”вҖқ
Dobby froze, horrorstruck, then grabbed HarryвҖҷs water jug from his bedside table and cracked it over his own head, toppling out of sight. A second later, he crawled back onto the bed, cross-eyed, muttering, вҖңBad Dobby, very bad Dobby вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңSo there is a Chamber of Secrets?вҖқ Harry whispered. вҖңAnd вҖ” did you say itвҖҷs been opened before? Tell me, Dobby!вҖқ
He seized the elfвҖҷs bony wrist as DobbyвҖҷs hand inched toward the water jug. вҖңBut IвҖҷm not Muggle-born вҖ” how can I be in danВӯger from the Chamber?вҖқ
вҖңAh, sir, ask no more, ask no more of poor Dobby,вҖқ stammered the elf, his eyes huge in the dark. вҖңDark deeds are planned in this place, but Harry Potter must not be here when they happen вҖ” go home, Harry Potter, go home. Harry Potter must not meddle in this, sir, вҖҷtis too dangerous вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWho is it, Dobby?вҖқ Harry said, keeping a firm hold on DobbyвҖҷs wrist to stop him from hitting himself with the water jug again. вҖңWhoвҖҷs opened it? Who opened it last time?вҖқ
вҖңDobby canвҖҷt, sir, Dobby canвҖҷt, Dobby mustnвҖҷt tell!вҖқ squealed the elf. вҖңGo home, Harry Potter, go home!вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷm not going anywhere!вҖқ said Harry fiercely. вҖңOne of my best friends is Muggle-born; sheвҖҷll be first in line if the Chamber really has been opened вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHarry Potter risks his own life for his friends!вҖқ moaned Dobby in a kind of miserable ecstasy. вҖңSo noble! So valiant! But he must save himself, he must, Harry Potter must not вҖ”вҖқ
Dobby suddenly froze, his bat ears quivering. Harry heard it, too. There were footsteps coming down the passageway outside.
вҖңDobby must go!вҖқ breathed the elf, terrified. There was a loud crack, and HarryвҖҷs fist was suddenly clenched on thin air. He slumped back into bed, his eyes on the dark doorway to the hospiВӯtal wing as the footsteps drew nearer.
Next moment, Dumbledore was backing into the dormitory, wearing a long woolly dressing gown and a nightcap. He was carryВӯing one end of what looked like a statue. Professor McGonagall appeared a second later, carrying its feet. Together, they heaved it onto a bed.
вҖңGet Madam Pomfrey,вҖқ whispered Dumbledore, and Professor McGonagall hurried past the end of HarryвҖҷs bed out of sight. Harry lay quite still, pretending to be asleep. He heard urgent voices, and then Professor McGonagall swept back into view, closely followed by Madam Pomfrey, who was pulling a cardigan on over her nightВӯdress. He heard a sharp intake of breath.
вҖңWhat happened?вҖқ Madam Pomfrey whispered to Dumbledore, bending over the statue on the bed.
вҖңAnother attack,вҖқ said Dumbledore. вҖңMinerva found him on the stairs.вҖқ
вҖңThere was a bunch of grapes next to him,вҖқ said Professor McВӯGonagall. вҖңWe think he was trying to sneak up here to visit Potter.вҖқ
HarryвҖҷs stomach gave a horrible lurch. Slowly and carefully, he raised himself a few inches so he could look at the statue on the bed. A ray of moonlight lay across its staring face.
It was Colin Creevey. His eyes were wide and his hands were stuck up in front of him, holding his camera.
вҖңPetrified?вҖқ whispered Madam Pomfrey.
вҖңYes,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall. вҖңBut I shudder to think вҖҰ If Albus hadnвҖҷt been on the way downstairs for hot chocolate вҖ” who knows what might have вҖ”вҖқ
The three of them stared down at Colin. Then Dumbledore leaned forward and wrenched the camera out of ColinвҖҷs rigid grip.
вҖңYou donвҖҷt think he managed to get a picture of his attacker?вҖқ said Professor McGonagall eagerly.
Dumbledore didnвҖҷt answer. He opened the back of the camera.
вҖңGood gracious!вҖқ said Madam Pomfrey.
A jet of steam had hissed out of the camera. Harry, three beds away, caught the acrid smell of burnt plastic.
вҖңMelted,вҖқ said Madam Pomfrey wonderingly. вҖңAll melted вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңWhat does this mean, Albus?вҖқ Professor McGonagall asked urВӯgently.
вҖңIt means,вҖқ said Dumbledore, вҖңthat the Chamber of Secrets is indeed open again.вҖқ
Madam Pomfrey clapped a hand to her mouth. Professor McGonagall stared at Dumbledore.
вҖңBut, Albus вҖҰ surely вҖҰ who?вҖқ
вҖңThe question is not who,вҖқ said Dumbledore, his eyes on Colin. вҖңThe question is, how. вҖҰвҖқ
And from what Harry could see of Professor McGonagallвҖҷs shadВӯowy face, she didnвҖҷt understand this any better than he did.
## Chapter 11

The Dueling Club
Harry woke up on Sunday morning to find the dormitory blazing with winter sunlight and his arm reboned but very stiff. He sat up quickly and looked over at ColinвҖҷs bed, but it had been blocked from view by the high curtains Harry had changed behind yesterday. Seeing that he was awake, Madam PomВӯfrey came bustling over with a breakfast tray and then began bendВӯing and stretching his arm and fingers.
вҖңAll in order,вҖқ she said as he clumsily fed himself porridge left-handed. вҖңWhen youвҖҷve finished eating, you may leave.вҖқ
Harry dressed as quickly as he could and hurried off to GryfВӯfindor Tower, desperate to tell Ron and Hermione about Colin and Dobby, but they werenвҖҷt there. Harry left to look for them, wondering where they could have got to and feeling slightly hurt that they werenвҖҷt interested in whether he had his bones back or not.
As Harry passed the library, Percy Weasley strolled out of it, looking in far better spirits than last time theyвҖҷd met.
вҖңOh, hello, Harry,вҖқ he said. вҖңExcellent flying yesterday, really exВӯcellent. Gryffindor has just taken the lead for the House Cup вҖ” you earned fifty points!вҖқ
вҖңYou havenвҖҷt seen Ron or Hermione, have you?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңNo, I havenвҖҷt,вҖқ said Percy, his smile fading. вҖңI hope RonвҖҷs not in another girlsвҖҷ toilet. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry forced a laugh, watched Percy walk out of sight, and then headed straight for Moaning MyrtleвҖҷs bathroom. He couldnвҖҷt see why Ron and Hermione would be in there again, but after making sure that neither Filch nor any prefects were around, he opened the door and heard their voices coming from a locked stall.
вҖңItвҖҷs me,вҖқ he said, closing the door behind him. There was a clunk, a splash, and a gasp from within the stall and he saw HermioneвҖҷs eye peering through the keyhole.
вҖңHarry!вҖқ she said. вҖңYou gave us such a fright вҖ” come in вҖ” howвҖҷs your arm?вҖқ
вҖңFine,вҖқ said Harry, squeezing into the stall. An old cauldron was perched on the toilet, and a crackling from under the rim told Harry they had lit a fire beneath it. Conjuring up portable, waterВӯproof fires was a speciality of HermioneвҖҷs.
вҖңWeвҖҷdвҖҷve come to meet you, but we decided to get started on the Polyjuice Potion,вҖқ Ron explained as Harry, with difficulty, locked the stall again. вҖңWeвҖҷve decided this is the safest place to hide it.вҖқ
Harry started to tell them about Colin, but Hermione interВӯrupted.
вҖңWe already know вҖ” we heard Professor McGonagall telling Professor Flitwick this morning. ThatвҖҷs why we decided weвҖҷd better get going вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThe sooner we get a confession out of Malfoy, the better,вҖқ snarled Ron. вҖңDвҖҷyou know what I think? He was in such a foul temper after the Quidditch match, he took it out on Colin.вҖқ
вҖңThereвҖҷs something else,вҖқ said Harry, watching Hermione tearВӯing bundles of knotgrass and throwing them into the potion. вҖңDobby came to visit me in the middle of the night.вҖқ
Ron and Hermione looked up, amazed. Harry told them everyВӯthing Dobby had told him вҖ” or hadnвҖҷt told him. Hermione and Ron listened with their mouths open.
вҖңThe Chamber of Secrets has been opened before?вҖқ Hermione said.
вҖңThis settles it,вҖқ said Ron in a triumphant voice. вҖңLucius Malfoy mustвҖҷve opened the Chamber when he was at school here and now heвҖҷs told dear old Draco how to do it. ItвҖҷs obvious. Wish DobbyвҖҷd told you what kind of monsterвҖҷs in there, though. I want to know how come nobodyвҖҷs noticed it sneaking around the school.вҖқ
вҖңMaybe it can make itself invisible,вҖқ said Hermione, prodding leeches to the bottom of the cauldron. вҖңOr maybe it can disguise itself вҖ” pretend to be a suit of armor or something вҖ” IвҖҷve read about Chameleon Ghouls вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYou read too much, Hermione,вҖқ said Ron, pouring dead lacewings on top of the leeches. He crumpled up the empty lacewing bag and looked at Harry.
вҖңSo Dobby stopped us from getting on the train and broke your arm. вҖҰвҖқ He shook his head. вҖңYou know what, Harry? If he doesnвҖҷt stop trying to save your life heвҖҷs going to kill you.вҖқ
* * *
The news that Colin Creevey had been attacked and was now lying as though dead in the hospital wing had spread through the entire school by Monday morning. The air was suddenly thick with ruВӯmor and suspicion. The first years were now moving around the castle in tight-knit groups, as though scared they would be attacked if they ventured forth alone.
Ginny Weasley, who sat next to Colin Creevey in Charms, was distraught, but Harry felt that Fred and George were going the wrong way about cheering her up. They were taking turns covering themselves with fur or boils and jumping out at her from behind statues. They only stopped when Percy, apoplectic with rage, told them he was going to write to Mrs. Weasley and tell her Ginny was having nightmares.
Meanwhile, hidden from the teachers, a roaring trade in talisВӯmans, amulets, and other protective devices was sweeping the school. Neville Longbottom bought a large, evil-smelling green onion, a pointed purple crystal, and a rotting newt tail before the other Gryffindor boys pointed out that he was in no danger; he was a pureblood, and therefore unlikely to be attacked.
вҖңThey went for Filch first,вҖқ Neville said, his round face fearful. вҖңAnd everyone knows IвҖҷm almost a Squib.вҖқ
In the second week of December Professor McGonagall came around as usual, collecting names of those who would be staying at school for Christmas. Harry, Ron, and Hermione signed her list; they had heard that Malfoy was staying, which struck them as very suspicious. The holidays would be the perfect time to use the Polyjuice Potion and try to worm a confession out of him.
Unfortunately, the potion was only half finished. They still needed the bicorn horn and the boomslang skin, and the only place they were going to get them was from SnapeвҖҷs private stores. Harry privately felt heвҖҷd rather face SlytherinвҖҷs legendary monster than let Snape catch him robbing his office.
вҖңWhat we need,вҖқ said Hermione briskly as Thursday afternoonвҖҷs double Potions lesson loomed nearer, вҖңis a diversion. Then one of us can sneak into SnapeвҖҷs office and take what we need.вҖқ
Harry and Ron looked at her nervously.
вҖңI think IвҖҷd better do the actual stealing,вҖқ Hermione continued in a matter-of-fact tone. вҖңYou two will be expelled if you get into any more trouble, and IвҖҷve got a clean record. So all you need to do is cause enough mayhem to keep Snape busy for five minutes or so.вҖқ
Harry smiled feebly. Deliberately causing mayhem in SnapeвҖҷs Potions class was about as safe as poking a sleeping dragon in the eye.
Potions lessons took place in one of the large dungeons. ThursВӯday afternoonвҖҷs lesson proceeded in the usual way. Twenty caulВӯdrons stood steaming between the wooden desks, on which stood brass scales and jars of ingredients. Snape prowled through the fumes, making waspish remarks about the GryffindorsвҖҷ work while the Slytherins sniggered appreciatively. Draco Malfoy, who was SnapeвҖҷs favorite student, kept flicking puffer-fish eyes at Ron and Harry, who knew that if they retaliated they would get detention faster than you could say вҖңUnfair.вҖқ
HarryвҖҷs Swelling Solution was far too runny, but he had his mind on more important things. He was waiting for HermioneвҖҷs signal, and he hardly listened as Snape paused to sneer at his watery potion. When Snape turned and walked off to bully Neville, Hermione caught HarryвҖҷs eye and nodded.
Harry ducked swiftly down behind his cauldron, pulled one of FredвҖҷs Filibuster fireworks out of his pocket, and gave it a quick prod with his wand. The firework began to fizz and sputter. Knowing he had only seconds, Harry straightened up, took aim, and lobbed it into the air; it landed right on target in GoyleвҖҷs cauldron.
GoyleвҖҷs potion exploded, showering the whole class. People shrieked as splashes of the Swelling Solution hit them. Malfoy got a faceful and his nose began to swell like a balloon; Goyle blunВӯdered around, his hands over his eyes, which had expanded to the size of a dinner plate вҖ” Snape was trying to restore calm and find out what had happened. Through the confusion, Harry saw HerВӯmione slip quietly into SnapeвҖҷs office.
вҖңSilence! SILENCE!вҖқ Snape roared. вҖңAnyone who has been splashed, come here for a Deflating Draught вҖ” when I find out who did this вҖ”вҖқ
Harry tried not to laugh as he watched Malfoy hurry forward, his head drooping with the weight of a nose like a small melon. As half the class lumbered up to SnapeвҖҷs desk, some weighted down with arms like clubs, others unable to talk through gigantic puffed-up lips, Harry saw Hermione slide back into the dungeon, the front of her robes bulging.
When everyone had taken a swig of antidote and the various swellings had subsided, Snape swept over to GoyleвҖҷs cauldron and scooped out the twisted black remains of the firework. There was a sudden hush.
вҖңIf I ever find out who threw this,вҖқ Snape whispered, вҖңI shall make sure that person is expelled.вҖқ
Harry arranged his face into what he hoped was a puzzled exВӯpression. Snape was looking right at him, and the bell that rang ten minutes later could not have been more welcome.
вҖңHe knew it was me,вҖқ Harry told Ron and Hermione as they hurried back to Moaning MyrtleвҖҷs bathroom. вҖңI could tell.вҖқ
Hermione threw the new ingredients into the cauldron and beВӯgan to stir feverishly.
вҖңItвҖҷll be ready in two weeks,вҖқ she said happily.
вҖңSnape canвҖҷt prove it was you,вҖқ said Ron reassuringly to Harry. вҖңWhat can he do?вҖқ
вҖңKnowing Snape, something foul,вҖқ said Harry as the potion frothed and bubbled.
A week later, Harry, Ron, and Hermione were walking across the entrance hall when they saw a small knot of people gathered around the notice board, reading a piece of parchment that had just been pinned up. Seamus Finnigan and Dean Thomas beckВӯoned them over, looking excited.
вҖңTheyвҖҷre starting a Dueling Club!вҖқ said Seamus. вҖңFirst meeting tonight! I wouldnвҖҷt mind dueling lessons; they might come in handy one of these days. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңWhat, you reckon SlytherinвҖҷs monster can duel?вҖқ said Ron, but he, too, read the sign with interest.
вҖңCould be useful,вҖқ he said to Harry and Hermione as they went into dinner. вҖңShall we go?вҖқ
Harry and Hermione were all for it, so at eight oвҖҷclock that evening they hurried back to the Great Hall. The long dining tables had vanished and a golden stage had appeared along one wall, lit by thousands of candles floating overhead. The ceiling was velvety black once more and most of the school seemed to be packed beВӯneath it, all carrying their wands and looking excited.
вҖңI wonder whoвҖҷll be teaching us?вҖқ said Hermione as they edged into the chattering crowd. вҖңSomeone told me Flitwick was a duelВӯing champion when he was young вҖ” maybe itвҖҷll be him.вҖқ
вҖңAs long as itвҖҷs not вҖ”вҖқ Harry began, but he ended on a groan: Gilderoy Lockhart was walking onto the stage, resplendent in robes of deep plum and accompanied by none other than Snape, wearing his usual black.
Lockhart waved an arm for silence and called, вҖңGather round, gather round! Can everyone see me? Can you all hear me? ExcelВӯlent!
вҖңNow, Professor Dumbledore has granted me permission to start this little dueling club, to train you all in case you ever need to deВӯfend yourselves as I myself have done on countless occasions вҖ” for full details, see my published works.
вҖңLet me introduce my assistant, Professor Snape,вҖқ said Lockhart, flashing a wide smile. вҖңHe tells me he knows a tiny little bit about dueling himself and has sportingly agreed to help me with a short demonstration before we begin. Now, I donвҖҷt want any of you youngsters to worry вҖ” youвҖҷll still have your Potions master when IвҖҷm through with him, never fear!вҖқ
вҖңWouldnвҖҷt it be good if they finished each other off?вҖқ Ron mutВӯtered in HarryвҖҷs ear.
SnapeвҖҷs upper lip was curling. Harry wondered why Lockhart was still smiling; if Snape had been looking at him like that heвҖҷd have been running as fast as he could in the opposite direction.
Lockhart and Snape turned to face each other and bowed; at least, Lockhart did, with much twirling of his hands, whereas Snape jerked his head irritably. Then they raised their wands like swords in front of them.
вҖңAs you see, we are holding our wands in the accepted combatВӯive position,вҖқ Lockhart told the silent crowd. вҖңOn the count of three, we will cast our first spells. Neither of us will be aiming to kill, of course.вҖқ
вҖңI wouldnвҖҷt bet on that,вҖқ Harry murmured, watching Snape barВӯing his teeth.
вҖңOne вҖ” two вҖ” three вҖ”вҖқ
Both of them swung their wands above their heads and pointed them at their opponent; Snape cried: вҖңExpelliarmus!вҖқ There was a dazzling flash of scarlet light and Lockhart was blasted off his feet: He flew backward off the stage, smashed into the wall, and slid down it to sprawl on the floor.
Malfoy and some of the other Slytherins cheered. Hermione was dancing on tiptoes. вҖңDo you think heвҖҷs all right?вҖқ she squealed through her fingers.
вҖңWho cares?вҖқ said Harry and Ron together.
Lockhart was getting unsteadily to his feet. His hat had fallen off and his wavy hair was standing on end.
вҖңWell, there you have it!вҖқ he said, tottering back onto the platВӯform. вҖңThat was a Disarming Charm вҖ” as you see, IвҖҷve lost my wand вҖ” ah, thank you, Miss Brown вҖ” yes, an excellent idea to show them that, Professor Snape, but if you donвҖҷt mind my saying so, it was very obvious what you were about to do. If I had wanted to stop you it would have been only too easy вҖ” however, I felt it would be instructive to let them see вҖҰвҖқ
Snape was looking murderous. Possibly Lockhart had noticed, because he said, вҖңEnough demonstrating! IвҖҷm going to come amongst you now and put you all into pairs. Professor Snape, if youвҖҷd like to help me вҖ”вҖқ
They moved through the crowd, matching up partners. LockВӯhart teamed Neville with Justin Finch-Fletchley, but Snape reached Harry and Ron first.
вҖңTime to split up the dream team, I think,вҖқ he sneered. вҖңWeasley, you can partner Finnigan. Potter вҖ”вҖқ
Harry moved automatically toward Hermione.
вҖңI donвҖҷt think so,вҖқ said Snape, smiling coldly. вҖңMr. Malfoy, come over here. LetвҖҷs see what you make of the famous Potter. And you, Miss Granger вҖ” you can partner Miss Bulstrode.вҖқ
Malfoy strutted over, smirking. Behind him walked a Slytherin girl who reminded Harry of a picture heвҖҷd seen in Holidays with Hags. She was large and square and her heavy jaw jutted aggresВӯsively. Hermione gave her a weak smile that she did not return.
вҖңFace your partners!вҖқ called Lockhart, back on the platform. вҖңAnd bow!вҖқ
Harry and Malfoy barely inclined their heads, not taking their eyes off each other.
вҖңWands at the ready!вҖқ shouted Lockhart. вҖңWhen I count to three, cast your charms to disarm your opponents вҖ” only to disВӯarm them вҖ” we donвҖҷt want any accidents вҖ” one вҖҰ two вҖҰ three вҖ”вҖқ
Harry swung his wand high, but Malfoy had already started on вҖңtwoвҖқ: His spell hit Harry so hard he felt as though heвҖҷd been hit over the head with a saucepan. He stumbled, but everything still seemed to be working, and wasting no more time, Harry pointed his wand straight at Malfoy and shouted, вҖңRictusempra!вҖқ
A jet of silver light hit Malfoy in the stomach and he doubled up, wheezing.
вҖңI said disarm only!вҖқ Lockhart shouted in alarm over the heads of the battling crowd, as Malfoy sank to his knees; Harry had hit him with a Tickling Charm, and he could barely move for laughВӯing. Harry hung back, with a vague feeling it would be unsporting to bewitch Malfoy while he was on the floor, but this was a misВӯtake; gasping for breath, Malfoy pointed his wand at HarryвҖҷs knees, choked, вҖңTarantallegra!вҖқ and the next second HarryвҖҷs legs began to jerk around out of his control in a kind of quickstep.
вҖңStop! Stop!вҖқ screamed Lockhart, but Snape took charge.
вҖңFinite Incantatem!вҖқ he shouted; HarryвҖҷs feet stopped dancing, Malfoy stopped laughing, and they were able to look up.
A haze of greenish smoke was hovering over the scene. Both Neville and Justin were lying on the floor, panting; Ron was holdВӯing up an ashen-faced Seamus, apologizing for whatever his broken wand had done; but Hermione and Millicent Bulstrode were still moving; Millicent had Hermione in a headlock and Hermione was whimpering in pain; both their wands lay forgotten on the floor. Harry leapt forward and pulled Millicent off. It was difficult: She was a lot bigger than he was.
вҖңDear, dear,вҖқ said Lockhart, skittering through the crowd, lookВӯing at the aftermath of the duels. вҖңUp you go, Macmillan. вҖҰ Careful there, Miss Fawcett. вҖҰ Pinch it hard, itвҖҷll stop bleeding in a second, Boot вҖ”
вҖңI think IвҖҷd better teach you how to block unfriendly spells,вҖқ said Lockhart, standing flustered in the midst of the hall. He glanced at Snape, whose black eyes glinted, and looked quickly away. вҖңLetвҖҷs have a volunteer pair вҖ” Longbottom and Finch-Fletchley, how about you вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңA bad idea, Professor Lockhart,вҖқ said Snape, gliding over like a large and malevolent bat. вҖңLongbottom causes devastation with the simplest spells. WeвҖҷll be sending whatвҖҷs left of Finch-Fletchley up to the hospital wing in a matchbox.вҖқ NevilleвҖҷs round, pink face went pinker. вҖңHow about Malfoy and Potter?вҖқ said Snape with a twisted smile.
вҖңExcellent idea!вҖқ said Lockhart, gesturing Harry and Malfoy into the middle of the hall as the crowd backed away to give them room.
вҖңNow, Harry,вҖқ said Lockhart. вҖңWhen Draco points his wand at you, you do this.вҖқ
He raised his own wand, attempted a complicated sort of wigВӯgling action, and dropped it. Snape smirked as Lockhart quickly picked it up, saying, вҖңWhoops вҖ” my wand is a little overexВӯcited вҖ”вҖқ
Snape moved closer to Malfoy, bent down, and whispered someВӯthing in his ear. Malfoy smirked, too. Harry looked up nervously at Lockhart and said, вҖңProfessor, could you show me that blocking thing again?вҖқ
вҖңScared?вҖқ muttered Malfoy, so that Lockhart couldnвҖҷt hear him.
вҖңYou wish,вҖқ said Harry out of the corner of his mouth.
Lockhart cuffed Harry merrily on the shoulder. вҖңJust do what I did, Harry!вҖқ
вҖңWhat, drop my wand?вҖқ
But Lockhart wasnвҖҷt listening.
вҖңThree вҖ” two вҖ” one вҖ” go!вҖқ he shouted.
Malfoy raised his wand quickly and bellowed, вҖңSerpensortia!вҖқ
The end of his wand exploded. Harry watched, aghast, as a long black snake shot out of it, fell heavily onto the floor between them, and raised itself, ready to strike. There were screams as the crowd backed swiftly away, clearing the floor.
вҖңDonвҖҷt move, Potter,вҖқ said Snape lazily, clearly enjoying the sight of Harry standing motionless, eye to eye with the angry snake. вҖңIвҖҷll get rid of it. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңAllow me!вҖқ shouted Lockhart. He brandished his wand at the snake and there was a loud bang; the snake, instead of vanishing, flew ten feet into the air and fell back to the floor with a loud smack. Enraged, hissing furiously, it slithered straight toward Justin Finch-Fletchley and raised itself again, fangs exposed, poised to strike.
Harry wasnвҖҷt sure what made him do it. He wasnвҖҷt even aware of deciding to do it. All he knew was that his legs were carrying him forward as though he was on casters and that he had shouted stuВӯpidly at the snake, вҖңLeave him alone!вҖқ And miraculously вҖ” inexВӯplicably вҖ” the snake slumped to the floor, docile as a thick, black garden hose, its eyes now on Harry. Harry felt the fear drain out of him. He knew the snake wouldnвҖҷt attack anyone now, though how he knew it, he couldnвҖҷt have explained.
He looked up at Justin, grinning, expecting to see Justin looking relieved, or puzzled, or even grateful вҖ” but certainly not angry and scared.
вҖңWhat do you think youвҖҷre playing at?вҖқ he shouted, and before Harry could say anything, Justin had turned and stormed out of the hall.
Snape stepped forward, waved his wand, and the snake vanished in a small puff of black smoke. Snape, too, was looking at Harry in an unexpected way: It was a shrewd and calculating look, and Harry didnвҖҷt like it. He was also dimly aware of an ominous muttering all around the walls. Then he felt a tugging on the back of his robes.
вҖңCome on,вҖқ said RonвҖҷs voice in his ear. вҖңMove вҖ” come on вҖ”вҖқ
Ron steered him out of the hall, Hermione hurrying alongside them. As they went through the doors, the people on either side drew away as though they were frightened of catching something. Harry didnвҖҷt have a clue what was going on, and neither Ron nor Hermione explained anything until they had dragged him all the way up to the empty Gryffindor common room. Then Ron pushed Harry into an armchair and said, вҖңYouвҖҷre a Parselmouth. Why didnвҖҷt you tell us?вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷm a what?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңA Parselmouth!вҖқ said Ron. вҖңYou can talk to snakes!вҖқ
вҖңI know,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңI mean, thatвҖҷs only the second time IвҖҷve ever done it. I accidentally set a boa constrictor on my cousin DudВӯley at the zoo once вҖ” long story вҖ” but it was telling me it had never seen Brazil and I sort of set it free without meaning to вҖ” that was before I knew I was a wizard вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңA boa constrictor told you it had never seen Brazil?вҖқ Ron reВӯpeated faintly.
вҖңSo?вҖқ said Harry. вҖңI bet loads of people here can do it.вҖқ
вҖңOh, no they canвҖҷt,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңItвҖҷs not a very common gift. Harry, this is bad.вҖқ
вҖңWhatвҖҷs bad?вҖқ said Harry, starting to feel quite angry. вҖңWhatвҖҷs wrong with everyone? Listen, if I hadnвҖҷt told that snake not to atВӯtack Justin вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңOh, thatвҖҷs what you said to it?вҖқ
вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou mean? You were there вҖ” you heard me вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI heard you speaking Parseltongue,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңSnake language. You could have been saying anything вҖ” no wonder Justin panВӯicked, you sounded like you were egging the snake on or someВӯthing вҖ” it was creepy, you know вҖ”вҖқ
Harry gaped at him.
вҖңI spoke a different language? But вҖ” I didnвҖҷt realize вҖ” how can I speak a language without knowing I can speak it?вҖқ
Ron shook his head. Both he and Hermione were looking as though someone had died. Harry couldnвҖҷt see what was so terrible.
вҖңDвҖҷyou want to tell me whatвҖҷs wrong with stopping a massive snake biting off JustinвҖҷs head?вҖқ he said. вҖңWhat does it matter how I did it as long as Justin doesnвҖҷt have to join the Headless Hunt?вҖқ
вҖңIt matters,вҖқ said Hermione, speaking at last in a hushed voice, вҖңbecause being able to talk to snakes was what Salazar Slytherin was famous for. ThatвҖҷs why the symbol of Slytherin House is a serpent.вҖқ
HarryвҖҷs mouth fell open.
вҖңExactly,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңAnd now the whole schoolвҖҷs going to think youвҖҷre his great-great-great-great-grandson or something вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBut IвҖҷm not,вҖқ said Harry, with a panic he couldnвҖҷt quite explain.
вҖңYouвҖҷll find that hard to prove,вҖқ said Hermione. вҖңHe lived about a thousand years ago; for all we know, you could be.вҖқ
* * *
Harry lay awake for hours that night. Through a gap in the curВӯtains around his four-poster he watched snow starting to drift past the tower window and wondered вҖҰ
Could he be a descendant of Salazar Slytherin? He didnвҖҷt know anything about his fatherвҖҷs family, after all. The Dursleys had alВӯways forbidden questions about his wizarding relatives.
Quietly, Harry tried to say something in Parseltongue. The words wouldnвҖҷt come. It seemed he had to be face-to-face with a snake to do it.
But IвҖҷm in Gryffindor, Harry thought. The Sorting Hat wouldnвҖҷt have put me in here if I had Slytherin blood. вҖҰ
Ah, said a nasty little voice in his brain, but the Sorting Hat wanted to put you in Slytherin, donвҖҷt you remember?
Harry turned over. HeвҖҷd see Justin the next day in Herbology and heвҖҷd explain that heвҖҷd been calling the snake off, not egging it on, which (he thought angrily, pummeling his pillow) any fool should have realized.
By next morning, however, the snow that had begun in the night had turned into a blizzard so thick that the last Herbology lesson of the term was canceled: Professor Sprout wanted to fit socks and scarves on the Mandrakes, a tricky operation she would entrust to no one else, now that it was so important for the Mandrakes to grow quickly and revive Mrs. Norris and Colin Creevey.
Harry fretted about this next to the fire in the Gryffindor comВӯmon room, while Ron and Hermione used their time off to play a game of wizard chess.
вҖңFor heavenвҖҷs sake, Harry,вҖқ said Hermione, exasperated, as one of RonвҖҷs bishops wrestled her knight off his horse and dragged him off the board. вҖңGo and find Justin if itвҖҷs so important to you.вҖқ
So Harry got up and left through the portrait hole, wondering where Justin might be.
The castle was darker than it usually was in daytime because of the thick, swirling gray snow at every window. Shivering, Harry walked past classrooms where lessons were taking place, catching snatches of what was happening within. Professor McGonagall was shouting at someone who, by the sound of it, had turned his friend into a badger. Resisting the urge to take a look, Harry walked on by, thinking that Justin might be using his free time to catch up on some work, and deciding to check the library first.
A group of the Hufflepuffs who should have been in Herbology were indeed sitting at the back of the library, but they didnвҖҷt seem to be working. Between the long lines of high bookshelves, Harry could see that their heads were close together and they were havВӯing what looked like an absorbing conversation. He couldnвҖҷt see whether Justin was among them. He was walking toward them when something of what they were saying met his ears, and he paused to listen, hidden in the Invisibility section.
вҖңSo anyway,вҖқ a stout boy was saying, вҖңI told Justin to hide up in our dormitory. I mean to say, if PotterвҖҷs marked him down as his next victim, itвҖҷs best if he keeps a low profile for a while. Of course, JustinвҖҷs been waiting for something like this to happen ever since he let slip to Potter he was Muggle-born. Justin actually told him heвҖҷd been down for Eton. ThatвҖҷs not the kind of thing you bandy about with SlytherinвҖҷs heir on the loose, is it?вҖқ
вҖңYou definitely think it is Potter, then, Ernie?вҖқ said a girl with blonde pigtails anxiously.
вҖңHannah,вҖқ said the stout boy solemnly, вҖңheвҖҷs a Parselmouth. Everyone knows thatвҖҷs the mark of a Dark wizard. Have you ever heard of a decent one who could talk to snakes? They called Slytherin himself Serpent-tongue.вҖқ
There was some heavy murmuring at this, and Ernie went on, вҖңRemember what was written on the wall? Enemies of the Heir, BeВӯware. Potter had some sort of run-in with Filch. Next thing we know, FilchвҖҷs catвҖҷs attacked. That first year, Creevey, was annoying Potter at the Quidditch match, taking pictures of him while he was lying in the mud. Next thing we know вҖ” CreeveyвҖҷs been attacked.вҖқ
вҖңHe always seems so nice, though,вҖқ said Hannah uncertainly, вҖңand, well, heвҖҷs the one who made You-Know-Who disappear. He canвҖҷt be all bad, can he?вҖқ
Ernie lowered his voice mysteriously, the Hufflepuffs bent closer, and Harry edged nearer so that he could catch ErnieвҖҷs words.
вҖңNo one knows how he survived that attack by You-Know-Who. I mean to say, he was only a baby when it happened. He should have been blasted into smithereens. Only a really powerful Dark wizard could have survived a curse like that.вҖқ He dropped his voice until it was barely more than a whisper, and said, вҖңThatвҖҷs probably why You-Know-Who wanted to kill him in the first place. DidnвҖҷt want another Dark Lord competing with him. I wonder what other powers PotterвҖҷs been hiding?вҖқ
Harry couldnвҖҷt take anymore. Clearing his throat loudly, he stepped out from behind the bookshelves. If he hadnвҖҷt been feeling so angry, he would have found the sight that greeted him funny: Every one of the Hufflepuffs looked as though they had been PetВӯrified by the sight of him, and the color was draining out of ErnieвҖҷs face.
вҖңHello,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңIвҖҷm looking for Justin Finch-Fletchley.вҖқ
The HufflepuffsвҖҷ worst fears had clearly been confirmed. They all looked fearfully at Ernie.
вҖңWhat do you want with him?вҖқ said Ernie in a quavering voice.
вҖңI wanted to tell him what really happened with that snake at the Dueling Club,вҖқ said Harry.
Ernie bit his white lips and then, taking a deep breath, said, вҖңWe were all there. We saw what happened.вҖқ
вҖңThen you noticed that after I spoke to it, the snake backed off?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңAll I saw,вҖқ said Ernie stubbornly, though he was trembling as he spoke, вҖңwas you speaking Parseltongue and chasing the snake toward Justin.вҖқ
вҖңI didnвҖҷt chase it at him!вҖқ Harry said, his voice shaking with anger. вҖңIt didnвҖҷt even touch him!вҖқ
вҖңIt was a very near miss,вҖқ said Ernie. вҖңAnd in case youвҖҷre getting ideas,вҖқ he added hastily, вҖңI might tell you that you can trace my family back through nine generations of witches and warlocks and my bloodвҖҷs as pure as anyoneвҖҷs, so вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI donвҖҷt care what sort of blood youвҖҷve got!вҖқ said Harry fiercely. вҖңWhy would I want to attack Muggle-borns?вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷve heard you hate those Muggles you live with,вҖқ said Ernie swiftly.
вҖңItвҖҷs not possible to live with the Dursleys and not hate them,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңIвҖҷd like to see you try it.вҖқ
He turned on his heel and stormed out of the library, earning himself a reproving glare from Madam Pince, who was polishing the gilded cover of a large spellbook.
Harry blundered up the corridor, barely noticing where he was going, he was in such a fury. The result was that he walked into something very large and solid, which knocked him backward onto the floor.
вҖңOh, hello, Hagrid,вҖқ Harry said, looking up.
HagridвҖҷs face was entirely hidden by a woolly, snow-covered balВӯaclava, but it couldnвҖҷt possibly be anyone else, as he filled most of the corridor in his moleskin overcoat. A dead rooster was hanging from one of his massive, gloved hands.
вҖңAll righвҖҷ, Harry?вҖқ he said, pulling up the balaclava so he could speak. вҖңWhy arenвҖҷt yeh in class?вҖқ
вҖңCanceled,вҖқ said Harry, getting up. вҖңWhatвҖҷre you doing in here?вҖқ
Hagrid held up the limp rooster.
вҖңSecond one killed this term,вҖқ he explained. вҖңItвҖҷs either foxes or a Blood-SuckinвҖҷ Bugbear, anвҖҷ I need the headmasterвҖҷs permission ter put a charm around the hen coop.вҖқ
He peered more closely at Harry from under his thick, snow-flecked eyebrows.
вҖңYeh sure yehвҖҷre all righвҖҷ? Yeh look all hot anвҖҷ bothered вҖ”вҖқ
Harry couldnвҖҷt bring himself to repeat what Ernie and the rest of the Hufflepuffs had been saying about him.
вҖңItвҖҷs nothing,вҖқ he said. вҖңIвҖҷd better get going, Hagrid, itвҖҷs TransВӯfiguration next and IвҖҷve got to pick up my books.вҖқ
He walked off, his mind still full of what Ernie had said about him.
вҖңJustinвҖҷs been waiting for something like this to happen ever since he let slip to Potter he was Muggle-born. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry stamped up the stairs and turned along another corridor, which was particularly dark; the torches had been extinguished by a strong, icy draft that was blowing through a loose windowpane. He was halfway down the passage when he tripped headlong over something lying on the floor.
He turned to squint at what heвҖҷd fallen over and felt as though his stomach had dissolved.
Justin Finch-Fletchley was lying on the floor, rigid and cold, a look of shock frozen on his face, his eyes staring blankly at the ceilВӯing. And that wasnвҖҷt all. Next to him was another figure, the strangest sight Harry had ever seen.
It was Nearly Headless Nick, no longer pearly-white and transВӯparent, but black and smoky, floating immobile and horizontal, six inches off the floor. His head was half off and his face wore an exВӯpression of shock identical to JustinвҖҷs.
Harry got to his feet, his breathing fast and shallow, his heart doВӯing a kind of drumroll against his ribs. He looked wildly up and down the deserted corridor and saw a line of spiders scuttling as fast as they could away from the bodies. The only sounds were the muffled voices of teachers from the classes on either side.
He could run, and no one would ever know he had been there. But he couldnвҖҷt just leave them lying here. вҖҰ He had to get help. вҖҰ Would anyone believe he hadnвҖҷt had anything to do with this?
As he stood there, panicking, a door right next to him opened with a bang. Peeves the Poltergeist came shooting out.
вҖңWhy, itвҖҷs potty wee Potter!вҖқ cackled Peeves, knocking HarryвҖҷs glasses askew as he bounced past him. вҖңWhatвҖҷs Potter up to? WhyвҖҷs Potter lurking вҖ”вҖқ
Peeves stopped, halfway through a midair somersault. Upside down, he spotted Justin and Nearly Headless Nick. He flipped the right way up, filled his lungs and, before Harry could stop him, screamed, вҖңATTACK! ATTACK! ANOTHER ATTACK! NO MORTAL OR GHOST IS SAFE! RUN FOR YOUR LIVES! ATTAAAACK!вҖқ
Crash вҖ” crash вҖ” crash вҖ” door after door flew open along the corridor and people flooded out. For several long minutes, there was a scene of such confusion that Justin was in danger of being squashed and people kept standing in Nearly Headless Nick. Harry found himself pinned against the wall as the teachers shouted for quiet. Professor McGonagall came running, followed by her own class, one of whom still had black-and-white-striped hair. She used her wand to set off a loud bang, which restored silence, and ordered everyone back into their classes. No sooner had the scene cleared somewhat than Ernie the Hufflepuff arrived, panting, on the scene.
вҖңCaught in the act!вҖқ Ernie yelled, his face stark white, pointing his finger dramatically at Harry.
вҖңThat will do, Macmillan!вҖқ said Professor McGonagall sharply.
Peeves was bobbing overhead, now grinning wickedly, surveying the scene; Peeves always loved chaos. As the teachers bent over Justin and Nearly Headless Nick, examining them, Peeves broke into song:
вҖңOh, Potter, you rotter, oh, what have you done,
YouвҖҷre killing off students, you think itвҖҷs good fun вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThatвҖҷs enough, Peeves!вҖқ barked Professor McGonagall, and Peeves zoomed away backward, with his tongue out at Harry.
Justin was carried up to the hospital wing by Professor Flitwick and Professor Sinistra of the Astronomy department, but nobody seemed to know what to do for Nearly Headless Nick. In the end, Professor McGonagall conjured a large fan out of thin air, which she gave to Ernie with instructions to waft Nearly Headless Nick up the stairs. This Ernie did, fanning Nick along like a silent black hovercraft. This left Harry and Professor McGonagall alone toВӯgether.
вҖңThis way, Potter,вҖқ she said.
вҖңProfessor,вҖқ said Harry at once, вҖңI swear I didnвҖҷt вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThis is out of my hands, Potter,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall curtly.
They marched in silence around a corner and she stopped before a large and extremely ugly stone gargoyle.
вҖңLemon drop!вҖқ she said. This was evidently a password, because the gargoyle sprang suddenly to life and hopped aside as the wall behind him split in two. Even full of dread for what was coming, Harry couldnвҖҷt fail to be amazed. Behind the wall was a spiral stairВӯcase that was moving smoothly upward, like an escalator. As he and Professor McGonagall stepped onto it, Harry heard the wall thud closed behind them. They rose upward in circles, higher and higher, until at last, slightly dizzy, Harry saw a gleaming oak door ahead, with a brass knocker in the shape of a griffin.
He knew now where he was being taken. This must be where Dumbledore lived.
## Chapter 12

The Polyjuice Potion
They stepped off the stone staircase at the top, and Professor McGonagall rapped on the door. It opened silently and they entered. Professor McGonagall told Harry to wait and left him there, alone.
Harry looked around. One thing was certain: of all the teachersвҖҷ offices Harry had visited so far this year, DumbledoreвҖҷs was by far the most interesting. If he hadnвҖҷt been scared out of his wits that he was about to be thrown out of school, he would have been very pleased to have a chance to look around it.
It was a large and beautiful circular room, full of funny little noises. A number of curious silver instruments stood on spindle-legged tables, whirring and emitting little puffs of smoke. The walls were covered with portraits of old headmasters and headmistresses, all of whom were snoozing gently in their frames. There was also an enormous, claw-footed desk, and, sitting on a shelf behind it, a shabby, tattered wizardвҖҷs hat вҖ” the Sorting Hat.
Harry hesitated. He cast a wary eye around the sleeping witches and wizards on the walls. Surely it couldnвҖҷt hurt if he took the hat down and tried it on again? Just to see вҖҰ just to make sure it had put him in the right House вҖ”
He walked quietly around the desk, lifted the hat from its shelf, and lowered it slowly onto his head. It was much too large and slipped down over his eyes, just as it had done the last time heвҖҷd put it on. Harry stared at the black inside of the hat, waiting. Then a small voice said in his ear, вҖңBee in your bonnet, Harry Potter?вҖқ
вҖңEr, yes,вҖқ Harry muttered. вҖңEr вҖ” sorry to bother you вҖ” I wanted to ask вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYouвҖҷve been wondering whether I put you in the right House,вҖқ said the hat smartly. вҖңYes вҖҰ you were particularly difficult to place. But I stand by what I said beforeвҖқ вҖ” HarryвҖҷs heart leapt вҖ” вҖңyou would have done well in Slytherin вҖ”вҖқ
HarryвҖҷs stomach plummeted. He grabbed the point of the hat and pulled it off. It hung limply in his hand, grubby and faded. Harry pushed it back onto its shelf, feeling sick.
вҖңYouвҖҷre wrong,вҖқ he said aloud to the still and silent hat. It didnвҖҷt move. Harry backed away, watching it. Then a strange, gagging noise behind him made him wheel around.
He wasnвҖҷt alone after all. Standing on a golden perch behind the door was a decrepit-looking bird that resembled a half-plucked turkey. Harry stared at it and the bird looked balefully back, makВӯing its gagging noise again. Harry thought it looked very ill. Its eyes were dull and, even as Harry watched, a couple more feathers fell out of its tail.
Harry was just thinking that all he needed was for DumbledoreвҖҷs pet bird to die while he was alone in the office with it, when the bird burst into flames.
Harry yelled in shock and backed away into the desk. He looked feverishly around in case there was a glass of water somewhere but couldnвҖҷt see one; the bird, meanwhile, had become a fireball; it gave one loud shriek and next second there was nothing but a smolderВӯing pile of ash on the floor.
The office door opened. Dumbledore came in, looking very somber.
вҖңProfessor,вҖқ Harry gasped. вҖңYour bird вҖ” I couldnвҖҷt do anyВӯthing вҖ” he just caught fire вҖ”вҖқ
To HarryвҖҷs astonishment, Dumbledore smiled.
вҖңAbout time, too,вҖқ he said. вҖңHeвҖҷs been looking dreadful for days; IвҖҷve been telling him to get a move on.вҖқ
He chuckled at the stunned look on HarryвҖҷs face.
вҖңFawkes is a phoenix, Harry. Phoenixes burst into flame when it is time for them to die and are reborn from the ashes. Watch him вҖҰвҖқ
Harry looked down in time to see a tiny, wrinkled, newborn bird poke its head out of the ashes. It was quite as ugly as the old one.
вҖңItвҖҷs a shame you had to see him on a Burning Day,вҖқ said Dumbledore, seating himself behind his desk. вҖңHeвҖҷs really very handsome most of the time, wonderful red and gold plumage. FasВӯcinating creatures, phoenixes. They can carry immensely heavy loads, their tears have healing powers, and they make highly faithВӯful pets.вҖқ
In the shock of Fawkes catching fire, Harry had forgotten what he was there for, but it all came back to him as Dumbledore settled himself in the high chair behind the desk and fixed Harry with his penetrating, light-blue stare.
Before Dumbledore could speak another word, however, the door of the office flew open with an almighty bang and Hagrid burst in, a wild look in his eyes, his balaclava perched on top of his shaggy black head and the dead rooster still swinging from his hand.
вҖңIt wasnвҖҷ Harry, Professor Dumbledore!вҖқ said Hagrid urgently. вҖңI was talkinвҖҷ ter him seconds before that kid was found, he never had time, sir вҖ”вҖқ
Dumbledore tried to say something, but Hagrid went ranting on, waving the rooster around in his agitation, sending feathers everywhere.
вҖңвҖ” it canвҖҷtвҖҷve bin him, IвҖҷll swear it in front oвҖҷ the Ministry oвҖҷ Magic if I have to вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHagrid, I вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңвҖ” yehвҖҷve got the wrong boy, sir, I know Harry never вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHagrid!вҖқ said Dumbledore loudly. вҖңI do not think that Harry atВӯtacked those people.вҖқ
вҖңOh,вҖқ said Hagrid, the rooster falling limply at his side. вҖңRight. IвҖҷll wait outside then, Headmaster.вҖқ
And he stomped out looking embarrassed.
вҖңYou donвҖҷt think it was me, Professor?вҖқ Harry repeated hopefully as Dumbledore brushed rooster feathers off his desk.
вҖңNo, Harry, I donвҖҷt,вҖқ said Dumbledore, though his face was somber again. вҖңBut I still want to talk to you.вҖқ

вҖңI must ask you, Harry, whether there is anything youвҖҷd like to tell me,вҖқ he said gently. вҖңAnything at all.вҖқ
Harry didnвҖҷt know what to say. He thought of Malfoy shouting, вҖңYouвҖҷll be next, Mudbloods!вҖқ and of the Polyjuice Potion simmerВӯing away in Moaning MyrtleвҖҷs bathroom. вҖңNo,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңThere isnвҖҷt anything, Professor. вҖҰвҖқ
The double attack on Justin and Nearly Headless Nick turned what had hitherto been nervousness into real panic. Curiously, it was Nearly Headless NickвҖҷs fate that seemed to worry people most. What could possibly do that to a ghost? people asked each other; what terrible power could harm someone who was already dead? There was almost a stampede to book seats on the Hogwarts ExВӯpress so that students could go home for Christmas.
вҖңAt this rate, weвҖҷll be the only ones left,вҖқ Ron told Harry and Hermione. вҖңUs, Malfoy, Crabbe, and Goyle. What a jolly holiday itвҖҷs going to be.вҖқ
Crabbe and Goyle, who always did whatever Malfoy did, had signed up to stay over the holidays, too. But Harry was glad that most people were leaving. He was tired of people skirting around him in the corridors, as though he were about to sprout fangs or spit poison; tired of all the muttering, pointing, and hissing as he passed.
Fred and George, however, found all this very funny. They went out of their way to march ahead of Harry down the corridors, shouting, вҖңMake way for the Heir of Slytherin, seriously evil wizВӯard coming through. вҖҰвҖқ
Percy was deeply disapproving of this behavior.
вҖңIt is not a laughing matter,вҖқ he said coldly.
вҖңOh, get out of the way, Percy,вҖқ said Fred. вҖңHarryвҖҷs in a hurry.вҖқ
вҖңYeah, heвҖҷs off to the Chamber of Secrets for a cup of tea with his fanged servant,вҖқ said George, chortling.
Ginny didnвҖҷt find it amusing either.
вҖңOh, donвҖҷt,вҖқ she wailed every time Fred asked Harry loudly who he was planning to attack next, or when George pretended to ward Harry off with a large clove of garlic when they met.
Harry didnвҖҷt mind; it made him feel better that Fred and George, at least, thought the idea of his being SlytherinвҖҷs heir was quite ludicrous. But their antics seemed to be aggravating Draco Malfoy, who looked increasingly sour each time he saw them at it.
вҖңItвҖҷs because heвҖҷs bursting to say itвҖҷs really him,вҖқ said Ron knowВӯingly. вҖңYou know how he hates anyone beating him at anything, and youвҖҷre getting all the credit for his dirty work.вҖқ
вҖңNot for long,вҖқ said Hermione in a satisfied tone. вҖңThe PolyВӯjuice PotionвҖҷs nearly ready. WeвҖҷll be getting the truth out of him any day now.вҖқ
At last the term ended, and a silence deep as the snow on the grounds descended on the castle. Harry found it peaceful, rather than gloomy, and enjoyed the fact that he, Hermione, and the Weasleys had the run of Gryffindor Tower, which meant they could play Exploding Snap loudly without bothering anyone, and pracВӯtice dueling in private. Fred, George, and Ginny had chosen to stay at school rather than visit Bill in Egypt with Mr. and Mrs. Weasley. Percy, who disapproved of what he termed their childish behavior, didnвҖҷt spend much time in the Gryffindor common room. He had already told them pompously that he was only staying over ChristВӯmas because it was his duty as a prefect to support the teachers durВӯing this troubled time.
Christmas morning dawned, cold and white. Harry and Ron, the only ones left in their dormitory, were woken very early by Hermione, who burst in, fully dressed and carrying presents for them both.
вҖңWake up,вҖқ she said loudly, pulling back the curtains at the winВӯdow.
вҖңHermione вҖ” youвҖҷre not supposed to be in here вҖ”вҖқ said Ron, shielding his eyes against the light.
вҖңMerry Christmas to you, too,вҖқ said Hermione, throwing him his present. вҖңIвҖҷve been up for nearly an hour, adding more lace-wings to the potion. ItвҖҷs ready.вҖқ
Harry sat up, suddenly wide awake.
вҖңAre you sure?вҖқ
вҖңPositive,вҖқ said Hermione, shirting Scabbers the rat so that she could sit down on the end of RonвҖҷs four-poster. вҖңIf weвҖҷre going to do it, I say it should be tonight.вҖқ
At that moment, Hedwig swooped into the room, carrying a very small package in her beak.
вҖңHello,вҖқ said Harry happily as she landed on his bed. вҖңAre you speaking to me again?вҖқ
She nibbled his ear in an affectionate sort of way, which was a far better present than the one that she had brought him, which turned out to be from the Dursleys. They had sent Harry a toothВӯpick and a note telling him to find out whether heвҖҷd be able to stay at Hogwarts for the summer vacation, too.
The rest of HarryвҖҷs Christmas presents were far more satisfacВӯtory. Hagrid had sent him a large tin of treacle toffee, which Harry decided to soften by the fire before eating; Ron had given him a book called Flying with the Cannons, a book of interesting facts about his favorite Quidditch team, and Hermione had bought him a luxury eagle-feather quill. Harry opened the last present to find a new, hand-knitted sweater from Mrs. Weasley and a large plum cake. He read her card with a fresh surge of guilt, thinking about Mr. WeasleyвҖҷs car (which hadnвҖҷt been seen since its crash with the Whomping Willow), and the bout of rule-breaking he and Ron were planning next.
No one, not even someone dreading taking Polyjuice Potion later, could fail to enjoy Christmas dinner at Hogwarts.
The Great Hall looked magnificent. Not only were there a dozen frost-covered Christmas trees and thick streamers of holly and mistletoe crisscrossing the ceiling, but enchanted snow was falling, warm and dry, from the ceiling. Dumbledore led them in a few of his favorite carols, Hagrid booming more and more loudly with every goblet of eggnog he consumed. Percy, who hadnвҖҷt noticed that Fred had bewitched his prefect badge so that it now read вҖңPin-head,вҖқ kept asking them all what they were sniggering at. Harry didnвҖҷt even care that Draco Malfoy was making loud, snide remarks about his new sweater from the Slytherin table. With a bit of luck, Malfoy would be getting his comeuppance in a few hoursвҖҷ time.
Harry and Ron had barely finished their third helpings of Christmas pudding when Hermione ushered them out of the hall to finalize their plans for the evening.
вҖңWe still need a bit of the people youвҖҷre changing into,вҖқ said Hermione matter-of-factly, as though she were sending them to the supermarket for laundry detergent. вҖңAnd obviously, itвҖҷll be best if you can get something of CrabbeвҖҷs and GoyleвҖҷs; theyвҖҷre MalfoyвҖҷs best friends, heвҖҷll tell them anything. You know how greedy they are, theyвҖҷre bound to eat them. Once theyвҖҷre asleep, pull out a few of their hairs and hide them in a broom closet.вҖқ
Harry and Ron looked incredulously at each other.
вҖңHermione, I donвҖҷt think вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңThat could go seriously wrong вҖ”вҖқ
But Hermione had a steely glint in her eye not unlike the one Professor McGonagall sometimes had.
вҖңThe potion will be useless without CrabbeвҖҷs and GoyleвҖҷs hair,вҖқ she said sternly. вҖңYou do want to investigate Malfoy, donвҖҷt you?вҖқ

вҖңHave you ever heard of a plan where so many things could go wrong?вҖқ
But to HarryвҖҷs and RonвҖҷs utter amazement, stage one of the operaВӯtion went just as smoothly as Hermione had said. They lurked in the deserted entrance hall after Christmas tea, waiting for Crabbe and Goyle who had remained alone at the Slytherin table, shovelВӯing down fourth helpings of trifle. Harry had perched the chocoВӯlate cakes on the end of the banisters. вҖңHow thick can you get?вҖқ Ron whispered ecstatically as Crabbe gleefully pointed out the cakes to Goyle and grabbed them. GrinВӯning stupidly, they stuffed the cakes whole into their large mouths. For a moment, both of them chewed greedily, looks of triumph on their faces. Then, without the smallest change of expression, they both keeled over backward onto the floor.
By far the hardest part was hiding them in the closet across the hall. Once they were safely stowed among the buckets and mops, Harry yanked out a couple of the bristles that covered GoyleвҖҷs forehead and Ron pulled out several of CrabbeвҖҷs hairs.
