HarryвҖҷs eyes narrowed as he focused on the spiders. If they purВӯsued their fixed course, there could be no doubt about where they would end up.
вҖңLooks like theyвҖҷre heading for the Forbidden Forest. вҖҰвҖқ
And Ron looked even unhappier about that.
At the end of the lesson Professor Sprout escorted the class to their Defense Against the Dark Arts lesson. Harry and Ron lagged behind the others so they could talk out of earshot.
вҖңWeвҖҷll have to use the Invisibility Cloak again,вҖқ Harry told Ron. вҖңWe can take Fang with us. HeвҖҷs used to going into the forest with Hagrid, he might be some help.вҖқ
вҖңRight,вҖқ said Ron, who was twirling his wand nervously in his fingers. вҖңEr вҖ” arenвҖҷt there вҖ” arenвҖҷt there supposed to be wereВӯwolves in the forest?вҖқ he added as they took their usual places at the back of LockhartвҖҷs classroom.
Preferring not to answer that question, Harry said, вҖңThere are good things in there, too. The centaurs are all right, and the uniВӯcorns вҖҰвҖқ
Ron had never been into the Forbidden Forest before. Harry had entered it only once and had hoped never to do so again.
Lockhart bounded into the room and the class stared at him. Every other teacher in the place was looking grimmer than usual, but Lockhart appeared nothing short of buoyant.
вҖңCome now,вҖқ he cried, beaming around him. вҖңWhy all these long faces?вҖқ
People swapped exasperated looks, but nobody answered.
вҖңDonвҖҷt you people realize,вҖқ said Lockhart, speaking slowly, as though they were all a bit dim, вҖңthe danger has passed! The culprit has been taken away вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңSays who?вҖқ said Dean Thomas loudly.
вҖңMy dear young man, the Minister of Magic wouldnвҖҷt have taken Hagrid if he hadnвҖҷt been one hundred percent sure that he was guilty,вҖқ said Lockhart, in the tone of someone explaining that one and one made two.
вҖңOh, yes he would,вҖқ said Ron, even more loudly than Dean.
вҖңI flatter myself I know a touch more about HagridвҖҷs arrest than you do, Mr. Weasley,вҖқ said Lockhart in a self-satisfied tone.
Ron started to say that he didnвҖҷt think so, somehow, but stopped in midsentence when Harry kicked him hard under the desk.
вҖңWe werenвҖҷt there, remember?вҖқ Harry muttered.
But LockhartвҖҷs disgusting cheeriness, his hints that he had alВӯways thought Hagrid was no good, his confidence that the whole business was now at an end, irritated Harry so much that he yearned to throw Gadding with Ghouls right in LockhartвҖҷs stupid face. Instead he contented himself with scrawling a note to Ron: LetвҖҷs do it tonight.
Ron read the message, swallowed hard, and looked sideways at the empty seat usually filled by Hermione. The sight seemed to stiffen his resolve, and he nodded.
The Gryffindor common room was always very crowded these days, because from six oвҖҷclock onward the Gryffindors had noВӯwhere else to go. They also had plenty to talk about, with the result that the common room often didnвҖҷt empty until past midnight.
Harry went to get the Invisibility Cloak out of his trunk right afВӯter dinner, and spent the evening sitting on it, waiting for the room to clear. Fred and George challenged Harry and Ron to a few games of Exploding Snap, and Ginny sat watching them, very subВӯdued in HermioneвҖҷs usual chair. Harry and Ron kept losing on purВӯpose, trying to finish the games quickly, but even so, it was well past midnight when Fred, George, and Ginny finally went to bed.
Harry and Ron waited for the distant sounds of two dormitory doors closing before seizing the cloak, throwing it over themselves, and climbing through the portrait hole.
It was another difficult journey through the castle, dodging all the teachers. At last they reached the entrance hall, slid back the lock on the oak front doors, squeezed between them, trying to stop any creaking, and stepped out into the moonlit grounds.
вҖң вҖҷCourse,вҖқ said Ron abruptly as they strode across the black grass, вҖңwe might get to the forest and find thereвҖҷs nothing to follow. Those spiders might notвҖҷve been going there at all. I know it looked like they were moving in that sort of general direction, but вҖҰвҖқ
His voice trailed away hopefully.
They reached HagridвҖҷs house, sad and sorry-looking with its blank windows. When Harry pushed the door open, Fang went mad with joy at the sight of them. Worried he might wake everyone at the castle with his deep, booming barks, they hastily fed him treacle toffee from a tin on the mantelpiece, which glued his teeth together.
Harry left the Invisibility Cloak on HagridвҖҷs table. There would be no need for it in the pitch-dark forest.
вҖңCвҖҷmon, Fang, weвҖҷre going for a walk,вҖқ said Harry, patting his leg, and Fang bounded happily out of the house behind them, dashed to the edge of the forest, and lifted his leg against a large sycamore tree.
Harry took out his wand, murmured, вҖңLumos!вҖқ and a tiny light appeared at the end of it, just enough to let them watch the path for signs of spiders.
вҖңGood thinking,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңIвҖҷd light mine, too, but you know вҖ” itвҖҷd probably blow up or something. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry tapped Ron on the shoulder, pointing at the grass. Two solitary spiders were hurrying away from the wandlight into the shade of the trees.
вҖңOkay,вҖқ Ron sighed as though resigned to the worst, вҖңIвҖҷm ready. LetвҖҷs go.вҖқ
So, with Fang scampering around them, sniffing tree roots and leaves, they entered the forest. By the glow of HarryвҖҷs wand, they followed the steady trickle of spiders moving along the path. They walked behind them for about twenty minutes, not speaking, lisВӯtening hard for noises other than breaking twigs and rustling leaves. Then, when the trees had become thicker than ever, so that the stars overhead were no longer visible, and HarryвҖҷs wand shone alone in the sea of dark, they saw their spider guides leaving the path.
Harry paused, trying to see where the spiders were going, but everything outside his little sphere of light was pitch-black. He had never been this deep into the forest before. He could vividly remember Hagrid advising him not to leave the forest path last time heвҖҷd been in here. But Hagrid was miles away now, probably sitting in a cell in Azkaban, and he had also said to follow the spiders.
Something wet touched HarryвҖҷs hand and he jumped backward, crushing RonвҖҷs foot, but it was only FangвҖҷs nose.
вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou reckon?вҖқ Harry said to Ron, whose eyes he could just make out, reflecting the light from his wand.
вҖңWeвҖҷve come this far,вҖқ said Ron.
So they followed the darting shadows of the spiders into the trees. They couldnвҖҷt move very quickly now; there were tree roots and stumps in their way, barely visible in the near blackness. Harry could feel FangвҖҷs hot breath on his hand. More than once, they had to stop, so that Harry could crouch down and find the spiders in the wandlight.
They walked for what seemed like at least half an hour, their robes snagging on low-slung branches and brambles. After a while, they noticed that the ground seemed to be sloping downward, though the trees were as thick as ever.
Then Fang suddenly let loose a great, echoing bark, making both Harry and Ron jump out of their skins.
вҖңWhat?вҖқ said Ron loudly, looking around into the pitch-dark, and gripping HarryвҖҷs elbow very hard.
вҖңThereвҖҷs something moving over there,вҖқ Harry breathed. вҖңLisВӯten вҖҰ sounds like something big. вҖҰвҖқ
They listened. Some distance to their right, the something big was snapping branches as it carved a path through the trees.
вҖңOh, no,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңOh, no, oh, no, oh вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңShut up,вҖқ said Harry frantically. вҖңItвҖҷll hear you.вҖқ
вҖңHear me?вҖқ said Ron in an unnaturally high voice. вҖңItвҖҷs already heard Fang!вҖқ
The darkness seemed to be pressing on their eyeballs as they stood, terrified, waiting. There was a strange rumbling noise and then silence.
вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou think itвҖҷs doing?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңProbably getting ready to pounce,вҖқ said Ron.
They waited, shivering, hardly daring to move.
вҖңDвҖҷyou think itвҖҷs gone?вҖқ Harry whispered.
вҖңDunno вҖ”вҖқ
Then, to their right, came a sudden blaze of light, so bright in the darkness that both of them flung up their hands to shield their eyes. Fang yelped and tried to run, but got lodged in a tangle of thorns and yelped even louder.
вҖңHarry!вҖқ Ron shouted, his voice breaking with relief. вҖңHarry, itвҖҷs our car!вҖқ
вҖңWhat?вҖқ
вҖңCome on!вҖқ
Harry blundered after Ron toward the light, stumbling and tripВӯping, and a moment later they had emerged into a clearing.
Mr. WeasleyвҖҷs car was standing, empty, in the middle of a circle of thick trees under a roof of dense branches, its headlights ablaze. As Ron walked, openmouthed, toward it, it moved slowly toward him, exactly like a large, turquoise dog greeting its owner.
вҖңItвҖҷs been here all the time!вҖқ said Ron delightedly, walking around the car. вҖңLook at it. The forestвҖҷs turned it wild. вҖҰвҖқ
The sides of the car were scratched and smeared with mud. ApВӯparently it had taken to trundling around the forest on its own. Fang didnвҖҷt seem at all keen on it; he kept close to Harry, who could feel him quivering. His breathing slowing down again, Harry stuffed his wand back into his robes.
вҖңAnd we thought it was going to attack us!вҖқ said Ron, leaning against the car and patting it. вҖңI wondered where it had gone!вҖқ
Harry squinted around on the floodlit ground for signs of more spiders, but they had all scuttled away from the glare of the headВӯlights.
вҖңWeвҖҷve lost the trail,вҖқ he said. вҖңCвҖҷmon, letвҖҷs go and find them.вҖқ
Ron didnвҖҷt speak. He didnвҖҷt move. His eyes were fixed on a point some ten feet above the forest floor, right behind Harry. His face was livid with terror.
Harry didnвҖҷt even have time to turn around. There was a loud clicking noise and suddenly he felt something long and hairy seize him around the middle and lift him off the ground, so that he was hanging facedown. Struggling, terrified, he heard more clicking, and saw RonвҖҷs legs leave the ground, too, heard Fang whimpering and howling вҖ” next moment, he was being swept away into the dark trees.
Head hanging, Harry saw that what had hold of him was marchВӯing on six immensely long, hairy legs, the front two clutching him tightly below a pair of shining black pincers. Behind him, he could hear another of the creatures, no doubt carrying Ron. They were moving into the very heart of the forest. Harry could hear Fang fighting to free himself from a third monster, whining loudly, but Harry couldnвҖҷt have yelled even if he had wanted to; he seemed to have left his voice back with the car in the clearing.
He never knew how long he was in the creatureвҖҷs clutches; he only knew that the darkness suddenly lifted enough for him to see that the leaf-strewn ground was now swarming with spiders. CranВӯing his neck sideways, he realized that they had reached the ridge of a vast hollow, a hollow that had been cleared of trees, so that the stars shone brightly onto the worst scene he had ever laid eyes on.
Spiders. Not tiny spiders like those surging over the leaves below. Spiders the size of carthorses, eight-eyed, eight-legged, black, hairy, gigantic. The massive specimen that was carrying Harry made its way down the steep slope toward a misty, domed web in the very center of the hollow, while its fellows closed in all around it, clickВӯing their pincers excitedly at the sight of its load.
Harry fell to the ground on all fours as the spider released him. Ron and Fang thudded down next to him. Fang wasnвҖҷt howling anymore, but cowering silently on the spot. Ron looked exactly like Harry felt. His mouth was stretched wide in a kind of silent scream and his eyes were popping.
Harry suddenly realized that the spider that had dropped him was saying something. It had been hard to tell, because he clicked his pincers with every word he spoke.
вҖңAragog!вҖқ it called. вҖңAragog!вҖқ
And from the middle of the misty, domed web, a spider the size of a small elephant emerged, very slowly. There was gray in the black of his body and legs, and each of the eyes on his ugly, pinВӯcered head was milky white. He was blind.
вҖңWhat is it?вҖқ he said, clicking his pincers rapidly.
вҖңMen,вҖқ clicked the spider who had caught Harry.
вҖңIs it Hagrid?вҖқ said Aragog, moving closer, his eight milky eyes wandering vaguely.
вҖңStrangers,вҖқ clicked the spider who had brought Ron.
вҖңKill them,вҖқ clicked Aragog fretfully. вҖңI was sleeping. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңWeвҖҷre friends of HagridвҖҷs,вҖқ Harry shouted. His heart seemed to have left his chest to pound in his throat.
Click, click, click went the pincers of the spiders all around the hollow.
Aragog paused.
вҖңHagrid has never sent men into our hollow before,вҖқ he said slowly.
вҖңHagridвҖҷs in trouble,вҖқ said Harry, breathing very fast. вҖңThatвҖҷs why weвҖҷve come.вҖқ
вҖңIn trouble?вҖқ said the aged spider, and Harry thought he heard concern beneath the clicking pincers. вҖңBut why has he sent you?вҖқ
Harry thought of getting to his feet but decided against it; he didnвҖҷt think his legs would support him. So he spoke from the ground, as calmly as he could.
вҖңThey think, up at the school, that HagridвҖҷs been setting a вҖ” a вҖ” something on students. TheyвҖҷve taken him to Azkaban.вҖқ
Aragog clicked his pincers furiously, and all around the holВӯlow the sound was echoed by the crowd of spiders; it was like applause, except applause didnвҖҷt usually make Harry feel sick with fear.
вҖңBut that was years ago,вҖқ said Aragog fretfully. вҖңYears and years ago. I remember it well. ThatвҖҷs why they made him leave the school. They believed that I was the monster that dwells in what they call the Chamber of Secrets. They thought that Hagrid had opened the Chamber and set me free.вҖқ
вҖңAnd you вҖҰ you didnвҖҷt come from the Chamber of Secrets?вҖқ said Harry, who could feel cold sweat on his forehead.
вҖңI!вҖқ said Aragog, clicking angrily. вҖңI was not born in the castle. I come from a distant land. A traveler gave me to Hagrid when I was an egg. Hagrid was only a boy, but he cared for me, hidden in a cupboard in the castle, feeding me on scraps from the table. Hagrid is my good friend, and a good man. When I was discovered, and blamed for the death of a girl, he protected me. I have lived here in the forest ever since, where Hagrid still visits me. He even found me a wife, Mosag, and you see how our family has grown, all through HagridвҖҷs goodness. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry summoned what remained of his courage.
вҖңSo you never вҖ” never attacked anyone?вҖқ
вҖңNever,вҖқ croaked the old spider. вҖңIt would have been my inВӯstinct, but out of respect for Hagrid, I never harmed a human. The body of the girl who was killed was discovered in a bathroom. I never saw any part of the castle but the cupboard in which I grew up. Our kind like the dark and the quiet. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңBut then вҖҰ Do you know what did kill that girl?вҖқ said Harry. вҖңBecause whatever it is, itвҖҷs back and attacking people again вҖ”вҖқ
His words were drowned by a loud outbreak of clicking and the rustling of many long legs shifting angrily; large black shapes shifted all around him.
вҖңThe thing that lives in the castle,вҖқ said Aragog, вҖңis an ancient creature we spiders fear above all others. Well do I remember how I pleaded with Hagrid to let me go, when I sensed the beast movВӯing about the school.вҖқ
вҖңWhat is it?вҖқ said Harry urgently.
More loud clicking, more rustling; the spiders seemed to be closВӯing in.
вҖңWe do not speak of it!вҖқ said Aragog fiercely. вҖңWe do not name it! I never even told Hagrid the name of that dread creature, though he asked me, many times.вҖқ
Harry didnвҖҷt want to press the subject, not with the spiders pressing closer on all sides. Aragog seemed to be tired of talking. He was backing slowly into his domed web, but his fellow spiders continued to inch slowly toward Harry and Ron.
вҖңWeвҖҷll just go, then,вҖқ Harry called desperately to Aragog, hearВӯing leaves rustling behind him.
вҖңGo?вҖқ said Aragog slowly. вҖңI think not. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңBut вҖ” but вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңMy sons and daughters do not harm Hagrid, on my command. But I cannot deny them fresh meat, when it wanders so willingly into our midst. Good-bye, friend of Hagrid.вҖқ
Harry spun around. Feet away, towering above him, was a solid wall of spiders, clicking, their many eyes gleaming in their ugly black heads.
Even as he reached for his wand, Harry knew it was no good, there were too many of them, but as he tried to stand, ready to die fighting, a loud, long note sounded, and a blaze of light flamed through the hollow.
Mr. WeasleyвҖҷs car was thundering down the slope, headlights glaring, its horn screeching, knocking spiders aside; several were thrown onto their backs, their endless legs waving in the air. The car screeched to a halt in front of Harry and Ron and the doors flew open.
вҖңGet Fang!вҖқ Harry yelled, diving into the front seat; Ron seized the boarhound around the middle and threw him, yelping, into the back of the car вҖ” the doors slammed shut вҖ” Ron didnвҖҷt touch the accelerator but the car didnвҖҷt need him; the engine roared and they were off, hitting more spiders. They sped up the slope, out of the hollow, and they were soon crashing through the forest, branches whipping the windows as the car wound its way cleverly through the widest gaps, following a path it obviously knew.
Harry looked sideways at Ron. His mouth was still open in the silent scream, but his eyes werenвҖҷt popping anymore.
вҖңAre you okay?вҖқ
Ron stared straight ahead, unable to speak.
They smashed their way through the undergrowth, Fang howlВӯing loudly in the back seat, and Harry saw the side mirror snap off as they squeezed past a large oak. After ten noisy, rocky minutes, the trees thinned, and Harry could again see patches of sky.
The car stopped so suddenly that they were nearly thrown into the windshield. They had reached the edge of the forest. Fang flung himself at the window in his anxiety to get out, and when Harry opened the door, he shot off through the trees to HagridвҖҷs house, tail between his legs. Harry got out too, and after a minute or so, Ron seemed to regain the feeling in his limbs and followed, still stiff-necked and staring. Harry gave the car a grateful pat as it reВӯversed back into the forest and disappeared from view.
Harry went back into HagridвҖҷs cabin to get the Invisibility Cloak. Fang was trembling under a blanket in his basket. When Harry got outside again, he found Ron being violently sick in the pumpkin patch.
вҖңFollow the spiders,вҖқ said Ron weakly, wiping his mouth on his sleeve. вҖңIвҖҷll never forgive Hagrid. WeвҖҷre lucky to be alive.вҖқ
вҖңI bet he thought Aragog wouldnвҖҷt hurt friends of his,вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңThatвҖҷs exactly HagridвҖҷs problem!вҖқ said Ron, thumping the wall of the cabin. вҖңHe always thinks monsters arenвҖҷt as bad as theyвҖҷre made out, and look where itвҖҷs got him! A cell in Azkaban!вҖқ He was shivering uncontrollably now. вҖңWhat was the point of sending us in there? What have we found out, IвҖҷd like to know?вҖқ
вҖңThat Hagrid never opened the Chamber of Secrets,вҖқ said Harry, throwing the cloak over Ron and prodding him in the arm to make him walk. вҖңHe was innocent.вҖқ
Ron gave a loud snort. Evidently, hatching Aragog in a cupboard wasnвҖҷt his idea of being innocent.
As the castle loomed nearer Harry twitched the cloak to make sure their feet were hidden, then pushed the creaking front doors ajar. At last they reached the safety of the Gryffindor common room, where the fire had burned itself into glowing ash. They took off the cloak and climbed the winding stair to their dormitory.
Ron fell onto his bed without bothering to get undressed. Harry, however, didnвҖҷt feel very sleepy. He sat on the edge of his fourВӯposter, thinking hard about everything Aragog had said.

вҖңYou donвҖҷt think вҖ” not Moaning Myrtle?вҖқ
## Chapter 16

The Chamber of Secrets

вҖңYouвҖҷre the Defense Against the Dark Arts teacher!вҖқ said Harry. вҖңYou canвҖҷt go now! Not with all the Dark stuff going on here!вҖқ
вҖңWell вҖ” I must say вҖ” when I took the job вҖ”вҖқ Lockhart mutВӯtered, now piling socks on top of his robes. вҖңnothing in the job deВӯscription вҖ” didnвҖҷt expect вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңYou mean youвҖҷre running away? said Harry disbelievingly. вҖңAfВӯter all that stuff you did in your books вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңBooks can be misleading,вҖқ said Lockhart delicately.
вҖңYou wrote them!вҖқ Harry shouted.
вҖңMy dear boy,вҖқ said Lockhart, straightening up and frowning at Harry. вҖңDo use your common sense. My books wouldnвҖҷt have sold half as well if people didnвҖҷt think IвҖҷd done all those things. No one wants to read about some ugly old Armenian warlock, even if he did save a village from werewolves. HeвҖҷd look dreadful on the front cover. No dress sense at all. And the witch who banished the BanВӯdon Banshee had a hairy chin. I mean, come on вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңSo youвҖҷve just been taking credit for what a load of other people have done?вҖқ said Harry incredulously.
вҖңHarry, Harry,вҖқ said Lockhart, shaking his head impatiently, вҖңitвҖҷs not nearly as simple as that. There was work involved. I had to track these people down. Ask them exactly how they managed to do what they did. Then I had to put a Memory Charm on them so they wouldnвҖҷt remember doing it. If thereвҖҷs one thing I pride myself on, itвҖҷs my Memory Charms. No, itвҖҷs been a lot of work, Harry. ItвҖҷs not all book signings and publicity photos, you know. You want fame, you have to be prepared for a long hard slog.вҖқ
He banged the lids of his trunks shut and locked them.
вҖңLetвҖҷs see,вҖқ he said. вҖңI think thatвҖҷs everything. Yes. Only one thing left.вҖқ
He pulled out his wand and turned to them.
вҖңAwfully sorry, boys, but IвҖҷll have to put a Memory Charm on you now. CanвҖҷt have you blabbing my secrets all over the place. IвҖҷd never sell another book вҖ”вҖқ
Harry reached his wand just in time. Lockhart had barely raised his, when Harry bellowed, вҖңExpelliarmus!вҖқ
Lockhart was blasted backward, falling over his trunk; his wand flew high into the air; Ron caught it, and flung it out of the open window.
вҖңShouldnвҖҷt have let Professor Snape teach us that one,вҖқ said Harry furiously, kicking LockhartвҖҷs trunk aside. Lockhart was lookВӯing up at him, feeble once more. Harry was still pointing his wand at him.
вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou want me to do?вҖқ said Lockhart weakly. вҖңI donвҖҷt know where the Chamber of Secrets is. ThereвҖҷs nothing I can do.вҖқ
вҖңYouвҖҷre in luck,вҖқ said Harry, forcing Lockhart to his feet at wandpoint. вҖңWe think we know where it is. And whatвҖҷs inside it. LetвҖҷs go.вҖқ
They marched Lockhart out of his office and down the nearest stairs, along the dark corridor where the messages shone on the wall, to the door of Moaning MyrtleвҖҷs bathroom.
They sent Lockhart in first. Harry was pleased to see that he was shaking.
Moaning Myrtle was sitting on the tank of the end toilet.
вҖңOh, itвҖҷs you,вҖқ she said when she saw Harry. вҖңWhat do you want this time?вҖқ
вҖңTo ask you how you died,вҖқ said Harry.
MyrtleвҖҷs whole aspect changed at once. She looked as though she had never been asked such a flattering question.
вҖңOoooh, it was dreadful,вҖқ she said with relish. вҖңIt happened right in here. I died in this very stall. I remember it so well. IвҖҷd hidВӯden because Olive Hornby was teasing me about my glasses. The door was locked, and I was crying, and then I heard somebody come in. They said something funny. A different language, I think it must have been. Anyway, what really got me was that it was a boy speaking. So I unlocked the door, to tell him to go and use his own toilet, and then вҖ”вҖқ Myrtle swelled importantly, her face shining. вҖңI died.вҖқ
вҖңHow?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңNo idea,вҖқ said Myrtle in hushed tones. вҖңI just remember seeing a pair of great, big, yellow eyes. My whole body sort of seized up, and then I was floating away. вҖҰвҖқ She looked dreamily at Harry. вҖңAnd then I came back again. I was determined to haunt Olive Hornby, you see. Oh, she was sorry sheвҖҷd ever laughed at my glasses.вҖқ
вҖңWhere exactly did you see the eyes?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңSomewhere there,вҖқ said Myrtle, pointing vaguely toward the sink in front of her toilet.
Harry and Ron hurried over to it. Lockhart was standing well back, a look of utter terror on his face.
It looked like an ordinary sink. They examined every inch of it, inside and out, including the pipes below. And then Harry saw it: Scratched on the side of one of the copper taps was a tiny snake.
вҖңThat tapвҖҷs never worked,вҖқ said Myrtle brightly as he tried to turn it.
вҖңHarry,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңSay something. Something in Parseltongue.вҖқ
вҖңBut вҖ”вҖқ Harry thought hard. The only times heвҖҷd ever manВӯaged to speak Parseltongue were when heвҖҷd been faced with a real snake. He stared hard at the tiny engraving, trying to imagine it was real.
вҖңOpen up,вҖқ he said.
He looked at Ron, who shook his head.
вҖңEnglish,вҖқ he said.
Harry looked back at the snake, willing himself to believe it was alive. If he moved his head, the candlelight made it look as though it were moving.
вҖңOpen up,вҖқ he said.
Except that the words werenвҖҷt what he heard; a strange hissing had escaped him, and at once the tap glowed with a brilliant white light and began to spin. Next second, the sink began to move; the sink, in fact, sank, right out of sight, leaving a large pipe exposed, a pipe wide enough for a man to slide into.
Harry heard Ron gasp and looked up again. He had made up his mind what he was going to do.
вҖңIвҖҷm going down there,вҖқ he said.
He couldnвҖҷt not go, not now they had found the entrance to the Chamber, not if there was even the faintest, slimmest, wildest chance that Ginny might be alive.
вҖңMe too,вҖқ said Ron.
There was a pause.
вҖңWell, you hardly seem to need me,вҖқ said Lockhart, with a shadow of his old smile. вҖңIвҖҷll just вҖ”вҖқ
He put his hand on the door knob, but Ron and Harry both pointed their wands at him.
вҖңYou can go first,вҖқ Ron snarled.
White-faced and wandless, Lockhart approached the opening.
вҖңBoys,вҖқ he said, his voice feeble. вҖңBoys, what good will it do?вҖқ
Harry jabbed him in the back with his wand. Lockhart slid his legs into the pipe.
вҖңI really donвҖҷt think вҖ”вҖқ he started to say, but Ron gave him a push, and he slid out of sight. Harry followed quickly. He lowered himself slowly into the pipe, then let go.
It was like rushing down an endless, slimy, dark slide. He could see more pipes branching off in all directions, but none as large as theirs, which twisted and turned, sloping steeply downward, and he knew that he was falling deeper below the school than even the dungeons. Behind him he could hear Ron, thudding slightly at the curves.
And then, just as he had begun to worry about what would hapВӯpen when he hit the ground, the pipe leveled out, and he shot out of the end with a wet thud, landing on the damp floor of a dark stone tunnel large enough to stand in. Lockhart was getting to his feet a little ways away, covered in slime and white as a ghost. Harry stood aside as Ron came whizzing out of the pipe, too.
вҖңWe must be miles under the school,вҖқ said Harry, his voice echoВӯing in the black tunnel.
вҖңUnder the lake, probably,вҖқ said Ron, squinting around at the dark, slimy walls.
All three of them turned to stare into the darkness ahead.
вҖңLumos!вҖқ Harry muttered to his wand and it lit again. вҖңCвҖҷmon,вҖқ he said to Ron and Lockhart, and off they went, their footsteps slapping loudly on the wet floor.
The tunnel was so dark that they could only see a little distance ahead. Their shadows on the wet walls looked monstrous in the wandlight.
вҖңRemember,вҖқ Harry said quietly as they walked cautiously forВӯward, вҖңany sign of movement, close your eyes right away. вҖҰвҖқ
But the tunnel was quiet as the grave, and the first unexpected sound they heard was a loud crunch as Ron stepped on what turned out to be a ratвҖҷs skull. Harry lowered his wand to look at the floor and saw that it was littered with small animal bones. Trying very hard not to imagine what Ginny might look like if they found her, Harry led the way forward, around a dark bend in the tunnel.
вҖңHarry вҖ” thereвҖҷs something up there вҖ”вҖқ said Ron hoarsely, grabbing HarryвҖҷs shoulder.
They froze, watching. Harry could just see the outline of someВӯthing huge and curved, lying right across the tunnel. It wasnвҖҷt movВӯing.
вҖңMaybe itвҖҷs asleep,вҖқ he breathed, glancing back at the other two. LockhartвҖҷs hands were pressed over his eyes. Harry turned back to look at the thing, his heart beating so fast it hurt.
Very slowly, his eyes as narrow as he could make them and still see, Harry edged forward, his wand held high.
The light slid over a gigantic snake skin, of a vivid, poisonous green, lying curled and empty across the tunnel floor. The creature that had shed it must have been twenty feet long at least.
вҖңBlimey,вҖқ said Ron weakly.
There was a sudden movement behind them. Gilderoy LockВӯhartвҖҷs knees had given way.
вҖңGet up,вҖқ said Ron sharply, pointing his wand at Lockhart.
Lockhart got to his feet вҖ” then he dived at Ron, knocking him to the ground.
Harry jumped forward, but too late вҖ” Lockhart was straightenВӯing up, panting, RonвҖҷs wand in his hand and a gleaming smile back on his face.
вҖңThe adventure ends here, boys!вҖқ he said. вҖңI shall take a bit of this skin back up to the school, tell them I was too late to save the girl, and that you two tragically lost your minds at the sight of her mangled body вҖ” say good-bye to your memories!вҖқ
He raised RonвҖҷs Spellotaped wand high over his head and yelled, вҖңObliviate!вҖқ
The wand exploded with the force of a small bomb. Harry flung his arms over his head and ran, slipping over the coils of snake skin, out of the way of great chunks of tunnel ceiling that were thunderВӯing to the floor. Next moment, he was standing alone, gazing at a solid wall of broken rock.
вҖңRon!вҖқ he shouted. вҖңAre you okay? Ron!вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷm here!вҖқ came RonвҖҷs muffled voice from behind the rock-fall. вҖңIвҖҷm okay вҖ” this gitвҖҷs not, though вҖ” he got blasted by the wand вҖ”вҖқ
There was a dull thud and a loud вҖңow!вҖқ It sounded as though Ron had just kicked Lockhart in the shins.
вҖңWhat now?вҖқ RonвҖҷs voice said, sounding desperate. вҖңWe canвҖҷt get through вҖ” itвҖҷll take ages. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry looked up at the tunnel ceiling. Huge cracks had apВӯpeared in it. He had never tried to break apart anything as large as these rocks by magic, and now didnвҖҷt seem a good moment to try вҖ” what if the whole tunnel caved in?
There was another thud and another вҖңow!вҖқ from behind the rocks. They were wasting time. Ginny had already been in the Chamber of Secrets for hours. вҖҰ Harry knew there was only one thing to do.
вҖңWait there,вҖқ he called to Ron. вҖңWait with Lockhart. IвҖҷll go on. вҖҰ If IвҖҷm not back in an hour вҖҰвҖқ
There was a very pregnant pause.
вҖңIвҖҷll try and shift some of this rock,вҖқ said Ron, who seemed to be trying to keep his voice steady. вҖңSo you can вҖ” can get back through. And, Harry вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңSee you in a bit,вҖқ said Harry, trying to inject some confidence into his shaking voice.
And he set off alone past the giant snake skin.
Soon the distant noise of Ron straining to shift the rocks was gone. The tunnel turned and turned again. Every nerve in HarryвҖҷs body was tingling unpleasantly. He wanted the tunnel to end, yet dreaded what heвҖҷd find when it did. And then, at last, as he crept around yet another bend, he saw a solid wall ahead on which two entwined serpents were carved, their eyes set with great, glinting emeralds.
Harry approached, his throat very dry. There was no need to pretend these stone snakes were real; their eyes looked strangely alive.
He could guess what he had to do. He cleared his throat, and the emerald eyes seemed to flicker.
вҖңOpen,вҖқ said Harry, in a low, faint hiss.
The serpents parted as the wall cracked open, the halves slid smoothly out of sight, and Harry, shaking from head to foot, walked inside.
## Chapter 17

The Heir of Slytherin
He was standing at the end of a very long, dimly lit chamВӯber. Towering stone pillars entwined with more carved serpents rose to support a ceiling lost in darkness, casting long, black shadows through the odd, greenish gloom that filled the place.
His heart beating very fast, Harry stood listening to the chill siВӯlence. Could the basilisk be lurking in a shadowy corner, behind a pillar? And where was Ginny?
He pulled out his wand and moved forward between the serВӯpentine columns. Every careful footstep echoed loudly off the shadowy walls. He kept his eyes narrowed, ready to clamp them shut at the smallest sign of movement. The hollow eye sockets of the stone snakes seemed to be following him. More than once, with a jolt of the stomach, he thought he saw one stir.
Then, as he drew level with the last pair of pillars, a statue high as the Chamber itself loomed into view, standing against the back wall.
Harry had to crane his neck to look up into the giant face above: It was ancient and monkeyish, with a long, thin beard that fell alВӯmost to the bottom of the wizardвҖҷs sweeping stone robes, where two enormous gray feet stood on the smooth Chamber floor. And between the feet, facedown, lay a small, black-robed figure with flaming-red hair.
вҖңGinny!вҖқ Harry muttered, sprinting to her and dropping to his knees. вҖңGinny вҖ” donвҖҷt be dead вҖ” please donвҖҷt be dead вҖ”вҖқ He flung his wand aside, grabbed GinnyвҖҷs shoulders, and turned her over. Her face was white as marble, and as cold, yet her eyes were closed, so she wasnвҖҷt Petrified. But then she must be вҖ”
вҖңGinny, please wake up,вҖқ Harry muttered desperately, shaking her. GinnyвҖҷs head lolled hopelessly from side to side.
вҖңShe wonвҖҷt wake,вҖқ said a soft voice.
Harry jumped and spun around on his knees.
A tall, black-haired boy was leaning against the nearest pillar, watching. He was strangely blurred around the edges, as though Harry were looking at him through a misted window. But there was no mistaking him вҖ”
вҖңTom вҖ” Tom Riddle?вҖқ
Riddle nodded, not taking his eyes off HarryвҖҷs face.
вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou mean, she wonвҖҷt wake?вҖқ Harry said desperately. вҖңSheвҖҷs not вҖ” sheвҖҷs not вҖ” ?вҖқ
вҖңSheвҖҷs still alive,вҖқ said Riddle. вҖңBut only just.вҖқ
Harry stared at him. Tom Riddle had been at Hogwarts fifty years ago, yet here he stood, a weird, misty light shining about him, not a day older than sixteen.
вҖңAre you a ghost?вҖқ Harry said uncertainly.
вҖңA memory,вҖқ said Riddle quietly. вҖңPreserved in a diary for fifty years.вҖқ
He pointed toward the floor near the statueвҖҷs giant toes. Lying open there was the little black diary Harry had found in Moaning MyrtleвҖҷs bathroom. For a second, Harry wondered how it had got there вҖ” but there were more pressing matters to deal with.
вҖңYouвҖҷve got to help me, Tom,вҖқ Harry said, raising GinnyвҖҷs head again. вҖңWeвҖҷve got to get her out of here. ThereвҖҷs a basilisk вҖҰ I donвҖҷt know where it is, but it could be along any moment. вҖҰ Please, help me вҖ”вҖқ
Riddle didnвҖҷt move. Harry, sweating, managed to hoist Ginny half off the floor, and bent to pick up his wand again.
But his wand had gone.
вҖңDid you see вҖ” ?вҖқ
He looked up. Riddle was still watching him вҖ” twirling HarryвҖҷs wand between his long fingers.
вҖңThanks,вҖқ said Harry, stretching out his hand for it.
A smile curled the corners of RiddleвҖҷs mouth. He continued to stare at Harry, twirling the wand idly.
вҖңListen,вҖқ said Harry urgently, his knees sagging with GinnyвҖҷs dead weight. вҖңWeвҖҷve got to go! If the basilisk comes вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңIt wonвҖҷt come until it is called,вҖқ said Riddle calmly.
Harry lowered Ginny back onto the floor, unable to hold her up any longer.
вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou mean?вҖқ he said. вҖңLook, give me my wand, I might need it вҖ”вҖқ
RiddleвҖҷs smile broadened.
вҖңYou wonвҖҷt be needing it,вҖқ he said.
Harry stared at him.
вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou mean, I wonвҖҷt be вҖ” ?вҖқ
вҖңIвҖҷve waited a long time for this, Harry Potter,вҖқ said Riddle. вҖңFor the chance to see you. To speak to you.вҖқ
вҖңLook,вҖқ said Harry, losing patience, вҖңI donвҖҷt think you get it. WeвҖҷre in the Chamber of Secrets. We can talk later вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңWeвҖҷre going to talk now,вҖқ said Riddle, still smiling broadly, and he pocketed HarryвҖҷs wand.
Harry stared at him. There was something very funny going on here. вҖҰ
вҖңHow did Ginny get like this?вҖқ he asked slowly.
вҖңWell, thatвҖҷs an interesting question,вҖқ said Riddle pleasantly. вҖңAnd quite a long story. I suppose the real reason Ginny WeasleyвҖҷs like this is because she opened her heart and spilled all her secrets to an invisible stranger.вҖқ
вҖңWhat are you talking about?вҖқ said Harry.
вҖңThe diary,вҖқ said Riddle. вҖңMy diary. Little GinnyвҖҷs been writing in it for months and months, telling me all her pitiful worries and woes вҖ” how her brothers tease her, how she had to come to school with secondhand robes and books, howвҖқ вҖ” RiddleвҖҷs eyes glinted вҖ” вҖңhow she didnвҖҷt think famous, good, great Harry Potter would ever like her. вҖҰвҖқ
All the time he spoke, RiddleвҖҷs eyes never left HarryвҖҷs face. There was an almost hungry look in them.
вҖңItвҖҷs very boring, having to listen to the silly little troubles of an eleven-year-old girl,вҖқ he went on. вҖңBut I was patient. I wrote back. I was sympathetic, I was kind. Ginny simply loved me. No oneвҖҷs ever understood me like you, Tom. вҖҰ IвҖҷm so glad IвҖҷve got this diary to confide in. вҖҰ ItвҖҷs like having a friend I can carry around in my pocket. вҖҰвҖқ
Riddle laughed, a high, cold laugh that didnвҖҷt suit him. It made the hairs stand up on the back of HarryвҖҷs neck.
вҖңIf I say it myself, Harry, IвҖҷve always been able to charm the people I needed. So Ginny poured out her soul to me, and her soul happened to be exactly what I wanted. вҖҰ I grew stronger and stronger on a diet of her deepest fears, her darkest secrets. I grew powerful, far more powerful than little Miss Weasley. Powerful enough to start feeding Miss Weasley a few of my secrets, to start pouring a little of my soul back into her вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңWhat dвҖҷyou mean?вҖқ said Harry, whose mouth had gone very dry.
вҖңHavenвҖҷt you guessed yet, Harry Potter?вҖқ said Riddle softly. вҖңGinny Weasley opened the Chamber of Secrets. She strangled the school roosters and daubed threatening messages on the walls. She set the Serpent of Slytherin on four Mudbloods, and the SquibвҖҷs cat.вҖқ
вҖңNo,вҖқ Harry whispered.
вҖңYes,вҖқ said Riddle, calmly. вҖңOf course, she didnвҖҷt know what she was doing at first. It was very amusing. I wish you could have seen her new diary entries вҖҰ far more interesting, they became. вҖҰ Dear Tom,вҖқ he recited, watching HarryвҖҷs horrified face, вҖңI think IвҖҷm losing my memory. There are rooster feathers all over my robes and I donвҖҷt know how they got there. Dear Tom, I canвҖҷt remember what I did on the night of Halloween, but a cat was attacked and IвҖҷve got paint all down my front. Dear Tom, Percy keeps telling me IвҖҷm pale and IвҖҷm not myself. I think he suspects me. вҖҰ There was another attack today and I donвҖҷt know where I was. Tom, what am I going to do? I think IвҖҷm going mad. вҖҰ I think IвҖҷm the one attacking everyone, Tom!вҖқ
HarryвҖҷs fists were clenched, the nails digging deep into his palms.
вҖңIt took a very long time for stupid little Ginny to stop trusting her diary,вҖқ said Riddle. вҖңBut she finally became suspicious and tried to dispose of it. And thatвҖҷs where you came in, Harry. You found it, and I couldnвҖҷt have been more delighted. Of all the people who could have picked it up, it was you, the very person I was most anxious to meet. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңAnd why did you want to meet me?вҖқ said Harry. Anger was coursing through him, and it was an effort to keep his voice steady.
вҖңWell, you see, Ginny told me all about you, Harry,вҖқ said RidВӯdle. вҖңYour whole fascinating history.вҖқ His eyes roved over the lightВӯning scar on HarryвҖҷs forehead, and their expression grew hungrier. вҖңI knew I must find out more about you, talk to you, meet you if I could. So I decided to show you my famous capture of that great oaf, Hagrid, to gain your trust вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHagridвҖҷs my friend,вҖқ said Harry, his voice now shaking. вҖңAnd you framed him, didnвҖҷt you? I thought you made a mistake, but вҖ”вҖқ
Riddle laughed his high laugh again.
вҖңIt was my word against HagridвҖҷs, Harry. Well, you can imagine how it looked to old Armando Dippet. On the one hand, Tom Riddle, poor but brilliant, parentless but so brave, school prefect, model student вҖҰ on the other hand, big, blundering Hagrid, in trouble every other week, trying to raise werewolf cubs under his bed, sneaking off to the Forbidden Forest to wrestle trolls вҖҰ but I admit, even I was surprised how well the plan worked. I thought someone must realize that Hagrid couldnвҖҷt possibly be the Heir of Slytherin. It had taken me five whole years to find out everything I could about the Chamber of Secrets and discover the secret enВӯtrance вҖҰ as though Hagrid had the brains, or the power!
вҖңOnly the Transfiguration teacher, Dumbledore, seemed to think Hagrid was innocent. He persuaded Dippet to keep Hagrid and train him as gamekeeper. Yes, I think Dumbledore might have guessed. вҖҰ Dumbledore never seemed to like me as much as the other teachers did. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңI bet Dumbledore saw right through you,вҖқ said Harry, his teeth gritted.
вҖңWell, he certainly kept an annoyingly close watch on me after Hagrid was expelled,вҖқ said Riddle carelessly. вҖңI knew it wouldnвҖҷt be safe to open the Chamber again while I was still at school. But I wasnвҖҷt going to waste those long years IвҖҷd spent searching for it. I decided to leave behind a diary, preserving my sixteen-year-old self in its pages, so that one day, with luck, I would be able to lead anВӯother in my footsteps, and finish Salazar SlytherinвҖҷs noble work.вҖқ
вҖңWell, you havenвҖҷt finished it,вҖқ said Harry triumphantly. вҖңNo oneвҖҷs died this time, not even the cat. In a few hours the Mandrake Draught will be ready and everyone who was Petrified will be all right again вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңHavenвҖҷt I already told you,вҖқ said Riddle quietly, вҖңthat killing Mudbloods doesnвҖҷt matter to me anymore? For many months now, my new target has been вҖ” you.вҖқ
Harry stared at him.
вҖңImagine how angry I was when the next time my diary was opened, it was Ginny who was writing to me, not you. She saw you with the diary, you see, and panicked. What if you found out how to work it, and I repeated all her secrets to you? What if, even worse, I told you whoвҖҷd been strangling roosters? So the foolish litВӯtle brat waited until your dormitory was deserted and stole it back. But I knew what I must do. It was clear to me that you were on the trail of SlytherinвҖҷs heir. From everything Ginny had told me about you, I knew you would go to any lengths to solve the mystery вҖ” particularly if one of your best friends was attacked. And Ginny had told me the whole school was buzzing because you could speak Parseltongue. вҖҰ
вҖңSo I made Ginny write her own farewell on the wall and come down here to wait. She struggled and cried and became very boring. But there isnвҖҷt much life left in her. вҖҰ She put too much into the diary, into me. Enough to let me leave its pages at last. вҖҰ I have been waiting for you to appear since we arrived here. I knew youвҖҷd come. I have many questions for you, Harry Potter.вҖқ
вҖңLike what?вҖқ Harry spat, fists still clenched.
вҖңWell,вҖқ said Riddle, smiling pleasantly, вҖңhow is it that you вҖ” a skinny boy with no extraordinary magical talent вҖ” managed to defeat the greatest wizard of all time? How did you escape with nothing but a scar, while Lord VoldemortвҖҷs powers were deВӯstroyed?вҖқ
There was an odd red gleam in his hungry eyes now.
вҖңWhy do you care how I escaped?вҖқ said Harry slowly. вҖңVoldeВӯmort was after your time. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңVoldemort,вҖқ said Riddle softly, вҖңis my past, present, and future, Harry Potter. вҖҰвҖқ
He pulled HarryвҖҷs wand from his pocket and began to trace it through the air, writing three shimmering words:
tom marvolo riddle
Then he waved the wand once, and the letters of his name reВӯarranged themselves:
i am lord voldemort
вҖңYou see?вҖқ he whispered. вҖңIt was a name I was already using at Hogwarts, to my most intimate friends only, of course. You think I was going to use my filthy Muggle fatherвҖҷs name forever? I, in whose veins runs the blood of Salazar Slytherin himself, through my motherвҖҷs side? No, Harry вҖ” I fashioned myself a new name, a name I knew wizards everywhere would one day fear to speak, when I had become the greatest sorcerer in the world!вҖқ
HarryвҖҷs brain seemed to have jammed. He stared numbly at RidВӯdle, at the orphaned boy who had grown up to murder HarryвҖҷs own parents, and so many others. вҖҰ At last he forced himself to speak.
вҖңYouвҖҷre not,вҖқ he said, his quiet voice full of hatred.
вҖңNot what?вҖқ snapped Riddle.
вҖңNot the greatest sorcerer in the world,вҖқ said Harry, breathing fast. вҖңSorry to disappoint you and all that, but the greatest wizard in the world is Albus Dumbledore. Everyone says so. Dumbledore saw through you when you were at school and he still frightens you now, wherever youвҖҷre hiding these days вҖ”вҖқ
The smile had gone from RiddleвҖҷs face, to be replaced by a very ugly look.
вҖңDumbledoreвҖҷs been driven out of this castle by the mere memВӯory of me!вҖқ he hissed.
вҖңHeвҖҷs not as gone as you might think!вҖқ Harry retorted. He was speaking at random, wanting to scare Riddle, wishing rather than believing it to be true вҖ”

Music was coming from somewhere. Riddle whirled around to stare down the empty Chamber. The music was growing louder. It was eerie, spine-tingling, unearthly; it lifted the hair on HarryвҖҷs scalp and made his heart feel as though it was swelling to twice its normal size. Then, as the music reached such a pitch that Harry felt it vibrating inside his own ribs, flames erupted at the top of the nearest pillar.
A crimson bird the size of a swan had appeared, piping its weird music to the vaulted ceiling. It had a glittering golden tail as long as a peacockвҖҷs and gleaming golden talons, which were gripping a ragged bundle.
A second later, the bird was flying straight at Harry. It dropped the ragged thing it was carrying at his feet, then landed heavily on his shoulder. As it folded its great wings, Harry looked up and saw it had a long, sharp golden beak and a beady black eye.

вҖңThatвҖҷs a phoenix. вҖҰвҖқ said Riddle, staring shrewdly back at it.

вҖңAnd that вҖ”вҖқ said Riddle, now eyeing the ragged thing that Fawkes had dropped, вҖңthatвҖҷs the old school Sorting Hat вҖ”вҖқ

ThatвҖҷs where all your power got you. YouвҖҷre in hiding. YouвҖҷre ugly, youвҖҷre foul вҖ”вҖқ

Riddle opened his mouth wide and hissed вҖ” but Harry understood what he was sayВӯing. вҖҰ
вҖңSpeak to me, Slytherin, greatest of the Hogwarts Four.вҖқ

And something was stirring inside the statueвҖҷs mouth. Something was slithering up from its depths.
Harry backed away until he hit the dark Chamber wall, and as he shut his eyes tight he felt FawkesвҖҷ wing sweep his cheek as he took flight. Harry wanted to shout, вҖңDonвҖҷt leave me!вҖқ but what chance did a phoenix have against the king of serpents?

вҖңKill him.вҖқ

The enormous serpent, bright, poisonous green, thick as an oak trunk, had raised itself high in the air and its great blunt head was weaving drunkenly between the pillars. As Harry trembled, ready to close his eyes if it turned, he saw what had distracted the snake.

вҖңNO!вҖқ Harry heard Riddle screaming. вҖңLEAVE THE BIRD! LEAVE THE BIRD! THE BOY IS BEHIND YOU! YOU CAN STILL SMELL HIM! KILL HIM!вҖқ

вҖңKILL THE BOY! LEAVE THE BIRD! THE BOY IS BEHIND YOU! SNIFF вҖ” SMELL HIM!вҖқ
Harry was on his feet, ready. The basiliskвҖҷs head was falling, its body coiling around, hitting pillars as it twisted to face him. The ChamВӯber was dissolving in a whirl of dull color.

вҖңYouвҖҷre dead, Harry Potter,вҖқ said RiddleвҖҷs voice above him. вҖңDead. Even DumbledoreвҖҷs bird knows it. Do you see what heвҖҷs doing, PotВӯter? HeвҖҷs crying.вҖқ

вҖңSo ends the famous Harry Potter,вҖқ said RiddleвҖҷs distant voice. вҖңAlone in the Chamber of Secrets, forsaken by his friends, defeated at last by the Dark Lord he so unwisely challenged. He raised the wand вҖ”
Then, in a rush of wings, Fawkes had soared back overhead and something fell into HarryвҖҷs lap вҖ” the diary.

вҖңHarry вҖ” oh, Harry вҖ” I tried to tell you at b-breakfast, but I c-couldnвҖҷt say it in front of Percy вҖ” it was me, Harry вҖ” but I вҖ” I s-swear I d-didnвҖҷt mean to вҖ” R-Riddle made me, he t-took me over вҖ” and вҖ” how did you kill that вҖ” that thing? Fawkes was waiting for them, hovering in the Chamber entrance. Harry urged Ginny forward; they stepped over the motionless coils of the dead basilisk, through the echoing gloom, and back into the tunnel. Harry heard the stone doors close behind them with a soft hiss.
After a few minutesвҖҷ progress up the dark tunnel, a distant sound of slowly shifting rock reached HarryвҖҷs ears.
вҖңRon!вҖқ Harry yelled, speeding up. вҖңGinnyвҖҷs okay! IвҖҷve got her!вҖқ

вҖңBut вҖ”вҖқ

вҖңHis memoryвҖҷs gone,вҖқ said Ron. вҖңThe Memory Charm backfired. Hit him instead of us. HasnвҖҷt got a clue who he is, or where he is, or who we are. I told him to come and wait here. HeвҖҷs a danger to himВӯself.вҖқ

вҖңYou hold GinnyвҖҷs other hand вҖ”вҖқ
Harry tucked the sword and the Sorting Hat into his belt, Ron took hold of the back of HarryвҖҷs robes, and Harry reached out and took hold of FawkesвҖҷs strangely hot tail feathers.
An extraordinary lightness seemed to spread through his whole body and the next second, in a rush of wings, they were flying upward through the pipe. Harry could hear Lockhart dangling below him, saying, вҖңAmazing! Amazing! This is just like magic!вҖқ The chill air was whipping through HarryвҖҷs hair, and before heвҖҷd stopped enjoying the ride, it was over вҖ” all four of them were hitВӯting the wet floor of Moaning MyrtleвҖҷs bathroom, and as Lockhart straightened his hat, the sink that hid the pipe was sliding back into place.
Myrtle goggled at them.
вҖңYouвҖҷre alive,вҖқ she said blankly to Harry.
вҖңThereвҖҷs no need to sound so disappointed,вҖқ he said grimly, wipВӯing flecks of blood and slime off his glasses.
вҖңOh, well вҖҰ IвҖҷd just been thinking вҖҰ if you had died, youвҖҷd have been welcome to share my toilet,вҖқ said Myrtle, blushing silver.
вҖңUrgh!вҖқ said Ron as they left the bathroom for the dark, deserted corridor outside. вҖңHarry! I think MyrtleвҖҷs grown fond of you! YouвҖҷve got competition, Ginny!вҖқ
But tears were still flooding silently down GinnyвҖҷs face.
вҖңWhere now?вҖқ said Ron, with an anxious look at Ginny. Harry pointed.
Fawkes was leading the way, glowing gold along the corridor. They strode after him, and moments later, found themselves outside Professor McGonagallвҖҷs office.
Harry knocked and pushed the door open.
## Chapter 18

Dobby's Reward
For a moment there was silence as Harry, Ron, Ginny, and Lockhart stood in the doorway, covered in muck and slime and (in HarryвҖҷs case) blood. Then there was a scream.
вҖңGinny!вҖқ
It was Mrs. Weasley, who had been sitting crying in front of the fire. She leapt to her feet, closely followed by Mr. Weasley, and both of them flung themselves on their daughter.
Harry, however, was looking past them. Professor Dumbledore was standing by the mantelpiece, beaming, next to Professor McВӯGonagall, who was taking great, steadying gasps, clutching her chest. Fawkes went whooshing past HarryвҖҷs ear and settled on DumbledoreвҖҷs shoulder, just as Harry found himself and Ron being swept into Mrs. WeasleyвҖҷs tight embrace.
вҖңYou saved her! You saved her! How did you do it?вҖқ
вҖңI think weвҖҷd all like to know that,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall weakly.
Mrs. Weasley let go of Harry, who hesitated for a moment, then walked over to the desk and laid upon it the Sorting Hat, the ruby-encrusted sword, and what remained of RiddleвҖҷs diary.
Then he started telling them everything. For nearly a quarter of an hour he spoke into the rapt silence: He told them about hearing the disembodied voice, how Hermione had finally realized that he was hearing a basilisk in the pipes; how he and Ron had followed the spiders into the forest, that Aragog had told them where the last victim of the basilisk had died; how he had guessed that Moaning Myrtle had been the victim, and that the entrance to the Chamber of Secrets might be in her bathroom. вҖҰ
вҖңVery well,вҖқ Professor McGonagall prompted him as he paused, вҖңso you found out where the entrance was вҖ” breaking a hundred school rules into pieces along the way, I might add вҖ” but how on earth did you all get out of there alive, Potter?вҖқ
So Harry, his voice now growing hoarse from all this talking, told them about FawkesвҖҷs timely arrival and about the Sorting Hat giving him the sword. But then he faltered. He had so far avoided mentioning RiddleвҖҷs diary вҖ” or Ginny. She was standing with her head against Mrs. WeasleyвҖҷs shoulder, and tears were still coursing silently down her cheeks. What if they expelled her? Harry thought in panic. RiddleвҖҷs diary didnвҖҷt work anymore. вҖҰ How could they prove it had been he whoвҖҷd made her do it all?
Instinctively, Harry looked at Dumbledore, who smiled faintly, the firelight glancing off his half-moon spectacles.
вҖңWhat interests me most,вҖқ said Dumbledore gently, вҖңis how Lord Voldemort managed to enchant Ginny, when my sources tell me he is currently in hiding in the forests of Albania.вҖқ
Relief вҖ” warm, sweeping, glorious relief вҖ” swept over Harry.
вҖңW-whatвҖҷs that?вҖқ said Mr. Weasley in a stunned voice. вҖңYou-Know-Who? En-enchant Ginny? But GinnyвҖҷs not вҖҰ Ginny hasnвҖҷt been вҖҰ has she?вҖқ
вҖңIt was this diary,вҖқ said Harry quickly, picking it up and showВӯing it to Dumbledore. вҖңRiddle wrote it when he was sixteen. вҖҰвҖқ
Dumbledore took the diary from Harry and peered keenly down his long, crooked nose at its burnt and soggy pages.
вҖңBrilliant,вҖқ he said softly. вҖңOf course, he was probably the most brilliant student Hogwarts has ever seen.вҖқ He turned around to the Weasleys, who were looking utterly bewildered.
вҖңVery few people know that Lord Voldemort was once called Tom Riddle. I taught him myself, fifty years ago, at Hogwarts. He disappeared after leaving the school вҖҰ traveled far and wide вҖҰ sank so deeply into the Dark Arts, consorted with the very worst of our kind, underwent so many dangerous, magical transformations, that when he resurfaced as Lord Voldemort, he was barely recogВӯnizable. Hardly anyone connected Lord Voldemort with the clever, handsome boy who was once Head Boy here.вҖқ
вҖңBut, Ginny,вҖқ said Mrs. Weasley. вҖңWhatвҖҷs our Ginny got to do with вҖ” with вҖ” him?вҖқ
вҖңHis d-diary!вҖқ Ginny sobbed. вҖңIвҖҷve b-been writing in it, and heвҖҷs been w-writing back all year вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңGinny!вҖқ said Mr. Weasley, flabbergasted. вҖңHavenвҖҷt I taught you anything? What have I always told you? Never trust anything that can think for itself if you canвҖҷt see where it keeps its brain. Why didnвҖҷt you show the diary to me, or your mother? A suspicious object like that, it was clearly full of Dark Magic вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңI d-didnвҖҷt know,вҖқ sobbed Ginny. вҖңI found it inside one of the books Mum got me. I th-thought someone had just left it in there and forgotten about it вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңMiss Weasley should go up to the hospital wing right away,вҖқ Dumbledore interrupted in a firm voice. вҖңThis has been a terrible ordeal for her. There will be no punishment. Older and wiser wizВӯards than she have been hoodwinked by Lord Voldemort.вҖқ He strode over to the door and opened it. вҖңBed rest and perhaps a large, steaming mug of hot chocolate. I always find that cheers me up,вҖқ he added, twinkling kindly down at her. вҖңYou will find that Madam Pomfrey is still awake. SheвҖҷs just giving out Mandrake juice вҖ” I daresay the basiliskвҖҷs victims will be waking up any moment.вҖқ
вҖңSo HermioneвҖҷs okay!вҖқ said Ron brightly.
вҖңThere has been no lasting harm done, Ginny,вҖқ said DumbleВӯdore.
Mrs. Weasley led Ginny out, and Mr. Weasley followed, still looking deeply shaken.
вҖңYou know, Minerva,вҖқ Professor Dumbledore said thoughtfully to Professor McGonagall, вҖңI think all this merits a good feast. Might I ask you to go and alert the kitchens?вҖқ
вҖңRight,вҖқ said Professor McGonagall crisply, also moving to the door. вҖңIвҖҷll leave you to deal with Potter and Weasley, shall I?вҖқ
вҖңCertainly,вҖқ said Dumbledore.
She left, and Harry and Ron gazed uncertainly at Dumbledore. What exactly had Professor McGonagall meant, deal with them? Surely вҖ” surely вҖ” they werenвҖҷt about to be punished?
вҖңI seem to remember telling you both that I would have to expel you if you broke any more school rules,вҖқ said Dumbledore.
Ron opened his mouth in horror.
вҖңWhich goes to show that the best of us must sometimes eat our words,вҖқ Dumbledore went on, smiling. вҖңYou will both receive SpeВӯcial Awards for Services to the School and вҖ” let me see вҖ” yes, I think two hundred points apiece for Gryffindor.вҖқ
Ron went as brightly pink as LockhartвҖҷs valentine flowers and closed his mouth again.
вҖңBut one of us seems to be keeping mightily quiet about his part in this dangerous adventure,вҖқ Dumbledore added. вҖңWhy so modВӯest, Gilderoy?вҖқ
Harry gave a start. He had completely forgotten about Lockhart. He turned and saw that Lockhart was standing in a corner of the room, still wearing his vague smile. When Dumbledore addressed him, Lockhart looked over his shoulder to see who he was talking to.
вҖңProfessor Dumbledore,вҖқ Ron said quickly, вҖңthere was an accident down in the Chamber of Secrets. Professor Lockhart вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңAm I a professor?вҖқ said Lockhart in mild surprise. вҖңGoodness. I expect I was hopeless, was I?вҖқ
вҖңHe tried to do a Memory Charm and the wand backfired,вҖқ Ron explained quietly to Dumbledore.
вҖңDear me,вҖқ said Dumbledore, shaking his head, his long silver mustache quivering. вҖңImpaled upon your own sword, Gilderoy!вҖқ
вҖңSword?вҖқ said Lockhart dimly. вҖңHavenвҖҷt got a sword. That boy has, though.вҖқ He pointed at Harry. вҖңHeвҖҷll lend you one.вҖқ
вҖңWould you mind taking Professor Lockhart up to the infirВӯmary, too?вҖқ Dumbledore said to Ron. вҖңIвҖҷd like a few more words with Harry. вҖҰвҖқ
Lockhart ambled out. Ron cast a curious look back at DumbleВӯdore and Harry as he closed the door.
Dumbledore crossed to one of the chairs by the fire.
вҖңSit down, Harry,вҖқ he said, and Harry sat, feeling unaccountably nervous.
вҖңFirst of all, Harry, I want to thank you,вҖқ said Dumbledore, eyes twinkling again. вҖңYou must have shown me real loyalty down in the Chamber. Nothing but that could have called Fawkes to you.вҖқ
He stroked the phoenix, which had fluttered down onto his knee. Harry grinned awkwardly as Dumbledore watched him.
вҖңAnd so you met Tom Riddle,вҖқ said Dumbledore thoughtfully. вҖңI imagine he was most interested in you. вҖҰвҖқ
Suddenly, something that was nagging at Harry came tumbling out of his mouth.
вҖңProfessor Dumbledore вҖҰ Riddle said IвҖҷm like him. Strange likenesses, he said. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңDid he, now?вҖқ said Dumbledore, looking thoughtfully at Harry from under his thick silver eyebrows. вҖңAnd what do you think, Harry?вҖқ
вҖңI donвҖҷt think IвҖҷm like him!вҖқ said Harry, more loudly than heвҖҷd intended. вҖңI mean, IвҖҷm вҖ” IвҖҷm in Gryffindor, IвҖҷm вҖҰвҖқ
But he fell silent, a lurking doubt resurfacing in his mind.
вҖңProfessor,вҖқ he started again after a moment. вҖңThe Sorting Hat told me IвҖҷd вҖ” IвҖҷd have done well in Slytherin. Everyone thought I was SlytherinвҖҷs heir for a while вҖҰ because I can speak ParselВӯtongue. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңYou can speak Parseltongue, Harry,вҖқ said Dumbledore calmly, вҖңbecause Lord Voldemort вҖ” who is the last remaining descendant of Salazar Slytherin вҖ” can speak Parseltongue. Unless IвҖҷm much mistaken, he transferred some of his own powers to you the night he gave you that scar. Not something he intended to do, IвҖҷm sure. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңVoldemort put a bit of himself in me?вҖқ Harry said, thunderВӯstruck.
вҖңIt certainly seems so.вҖқ
вҖңSo I should be in Slytherin,вҖқ Harry said, looking desperately into DumbledoreвҖҷs face. вҖңThe Sorting Hat could see SlytherinвҖҷs power in me, and it вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңPut you in Gryffindor,вҖқ said Dumbledore calmly. вҖңListen to me, Harry. You happen to have many qualities Salazar Slytherin prized in his hand-picked students. His own very rare gift, ParselВӯtongue вҖ” resourcefulness вҖ” determination вҖ” a certain disregard for rules,вҖқ he added, his mustache quivering again. вҖңYet the Sorting Hat placed you in Gryffindor. You know why that was. Think.вҖқ
вҖңIt only put me in Gryffindor,вҖқ said Harry in a defeated voice, вҖңbecause I asked not to go in Slytherin. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңExactly,вҖқ said Dumbledore, beaming once more. вҖңWhich makes you very different from Tom Riddle. It is our choices, Harry, that show what we truly are, far more than our abilities.вҖқ Harry sat moВӯtionless in his chair, stunned. вҖңIf you want proof, Harry, that you belong in Gryffindor, I suggest you look more closely at this.вҖқ
Dumbledore reached across to Professor McGonagallвҖҷs desk, picked up the blood-stained silver sword, and handed it to Harry. Dully, Harry turned it over, the rubies blazing in the firelight. And then he saw the name engraved just below the hilt.
Godric Gryffindor.
вҖңOnly a true Gryffindor could have pulled that out of the hat, Harry,вҖқ said Dumbledore simply.
For a minute, neither of them spoke. Then Dumbledore pulled open one of the drawers in Professor McGonagallвҖҷs desk and took out a quill and a bottle of ink.
вҖңWhat you need, Harry, is some food and sleep. I suggest you go down to the feast, while I write to Azkaban вҖ” we need our gameВӯkeeper back. And I must draft an advertisement for the Daily Prophet, too,вҖқ he added thoughtfully. вҖңWeвҖҷll be needing a new DeВӯfense Against the Dark Arts teacher. вҖҰ Dear me, we do seem to run through them, donвҖҷt we?вҖқ
Harry got up and crossed to the door. He had just reached for the handle, however, when the door burst open so violently that it bounced back off the wall.
Lucius Malfoy stood there, fury in his face. And cowering beВӯhind his legs, heavily wrapped in bandages, was Dobby.
вҖңGood evening, Lucius,вҖқ said Dumbledore pleasantly.
Mr. Malfoy almost knocked Harry over as he swept into the room. Dobby went scurrying in after him, crouching at the hem of his cloak, a look of abject terror on his face.
The elf was carrying a stained rag with which he was attempting to finish cleaning Mr. MalfoyвҖҷs shoes. Apparently Mr. Malfoy had set out in a great hurry, for not only were his shoes half-polished, but his usually sleek hair was disheveled. Ignoring the elf bobbing apologetically around his ankles, he fixed his cold eyes upon DumВӯbledore.
вҖңSo!вҖқ he said вҖңYouвҖҷve come back. The governors suspended you, but you still saw fit to return to Hogwarts.вҖқ
вҖңWell, you see, Lucius,вҖқ said Dumbledore, smiling serenely, вҖңthe other eleven governors contacted me today. It was something like being caught in a hailstorm of owls, to tell the truth. TheyвҖҷd heard that Arthur WeasleyвҖҷs daughter had been killed and wanted me back here at once. They seemed to think I was the best man for the job after all. Very strange tales they told me, too. вҖҰ Several of them seemed to think that you had threatened to curse their famiВӯlies if they didnвҖҷt agree to suspend me in the first place.вҖқ
Mr. Malfoy went even paler than usual, but his eyes were still slits of fury.
вҖңSo вҖ” have you stopped the attacks yet?вҖқ he sneered. вҖңHave you caught the culprit?вҖқ
вҖңWe have,вҖқ said Dumbledore, with a smile.
вҖңWell?вҖқ said Mr. Malfoy sharply. вҖңWho is it?вҖқ
вҖңThe same person as last time, Lucius,вҖқ said Dumbledore. вҖңBut this time, Lord Voldemort was acting through somebody else. By means of this diary.вҖқ
He held up the small black book with the large hole through the center, watching Mr. Malfoy closely. Harry, however, was watching Dobby.
The elf was doing something very odd. His great eyes fixed meaningfully on Harry, he kept pointing at the diary, then at Mr. Malfoy, and then hitting himself hard on the head with his fist.
вҖңI see вҖҰвҖқ said Mr. Malfoy slowly to Dumbledore.
вҖңA clever plan,вҖқ said Dumbledore in a level voice, still staring Mr. Malfoy straight in the eye. вҖңBecause if Harry hereвҖқ вҖ” Mr. Malfoy shot Harry a swift, sharp look вҖ” вҖңand his friend Ron hadnвҖҷt discovered this book, why вҖ” Ginny Weasley might have taken all the blame. No one would ever have been able to prove she hadnвҖҷt acted of her own free will. вҖҰвҖқ
Mr. Malfoy said nothing. His face was suddenly masklike.
вҖңAnd imagine,вҖқ Dumbledore went on, вҖңwhat might have hapВӯpened then. вҖҰ The Weasleys are one of our most prominent pure-blood families. Imagine the effect on Arthur Weasley and his Muggle Protection Act, if his own daughter was discovered attackВӯing and killing Muggle-borns. вҖҰ Very fortunate the diary was disВӯcovered, and RiddleвҖҷs memories wiped from it. Who knows what the consequences might have been otherwise. вҖҰвҖқ
Mr. Malfoy forced himself to speak.
вҖңVery fortunate,вҖқ he said stiffly.
And still, behind his back, Dobby was pointing, first to the diВӯary, then to Lucius Malfoy, then punching himself in the head.
And Harry suddenly understood. He nodded at Dobby, and Dobby backed into a corner, now twisting his ears in punishment.
вҖңDonвҖҷt you want to know how Ginny got hold of that diary, Mr. Malfoy?вҖқ said Harry.
Lucius Malfoy rounded on him.
вҖңHow should I know how the stupid little girl got hold of it?вҖқ he said.
вҖңBecause you gave it to her,вҖқ said Harry. вҖңIn Flourish and Blotts. You picked up her old Transfiguration book and slipped the diary inside it, didnвҖҷt you?вҖқ
He saw Mr. MalfoyвҖҷs white hands clench and unclench.
вҖңProve it,вҖқ he hissed.
вҖңOh, no one will be able to do that,вҖқ said Dumbledore, smiling at Harry. вҖңNot now that Riddle has vanished from the book. On the other hand, I would advise you, Lucius, not to go giving out any more of Lord VoldemortвҖҷs old school things. If any more of them find their way into innocent hands, I think Arthur Weasley, for one, will make sure they are traced back to you. вҖҰвҖқ
Lucius Malfoy stood for a moment, and Harry distinctly saw his right hand twitch as though he was longing to reach for his wand. Instead, he turned to his house-elf.
вҖңWeвҖҷre going, Dobby!вҖқ
He wrenched open the door and as the elf came hurrying up to him, he kicked him right through it. They could hear Dobby squealing with pain all the way along the corridor. Harry stood for a moment, thinking hard. Then it came to him вҖ”
вҖңProfessor Dumbledore,вҖқ he said hurriedly. вҖңCan I give that diВӯary back to Mr. Malfoy, please?вҖқ
вҖңCertainly, Harry,вҖқ said Dumbledore calmly. вҖңBut hurry. The feast, remember. вҖҰвҖқ
Harry grabbed the diary and dashed out of the office. He could hear DobbyвҖҷs squeals of pain receding around the corner. Quickly, wondering if this plan could possibly work, Harry took off one of his shoes, pulled off his slimy, filthy sock, and stuffed the diary into it. Then he ran down the dark corridor.
He caught up with them at the top of the stairs.
вҖңMr. Malfoy,вҖқ he gasped, skidding to a halt, вҖңIвҖҷve got something for you вҖ”вҖқ
And he forced the smelly sock into Lucius MalfoyвҖҷs hand.
вҖңWhat the вҖ” ?вҖқ
Mr. Malfoy ripped the sock off the diary, threw it aside, then looked furiously from the ruined book to Harry.
вҖңYouвҖҷll meet the same sticky end as your parents one of these days, Harry Potter,вҖқ he said softly. вҖңThey were meddlesome fools, too.вҖқ
He turned to go.
вҖңCome, Dobby. I said, come.вҖқ
But Dobby didnвҖҷt move. He was holding up HarryвҖҷs disgusting, slimy sock, and looking at it as though it were a priceless treasure.
вҖңMaster has given a sock,вҖқ said the elf in wonderment. вҖңMaster gave it to Dobby.вҖқ
вҖңWhatвҖҷs that?вҖқ spat Mr. Malfoy. вҖңWhat did you say?вҖқ
вҖңGot a sock,вҖқ said Dobby in disbelief. вҖңMaster threw it, and Dobby caught it, and Dobby вҖ” Dobby is free.вҖқ
Lucius Malfoy stood frozen, staring at the elf. Then he lunged at Harry.
вҖңYouвҖҷve lost me my servant, boy!вҖқ
But Dobby shouted, вҖңYou shall not harm Harry Potter!вҖқ
There was a loud bang, and Mr. Malfoy was thrown backward. He crashed down the stairs, three at a time, landing in a crumpled heap on the landing below. He got up, his face livid, and pulled out his wand, but Dobby raised a long, threatening finger.
вҖңYou shall go now,вҖқ he said fiercely, pointing down at Mr. MalВӯfoy. вҖңYou shall not touch Harry Potter. You shall go now.вҖқ
Lucius Malfoy had no choice. With a last, incensed stare at the pair of them, he swung his cloak around him and hurried out of sight.
вҖңHarry Potter freed Dobby!вҖқ said the elf shrilly, gazing up at Harry, moonlight from the nearest window reflected in his orb-like eyes. вҖңHarry Potter set Dobby free!вҖқ
вҖңLeast I could do, Dobby,вҖқ said Harry, grinning. вҖңJust promise never to try and save my life again.вҖқ
The elfвҖҷs ugly brown face split suddenly into a wide, toothy smile.
вҖңIвҖҷve just got one question, Dobby,вҖқ said Harry as Dobby pulled on HarryвҖҷs sock with shaking hands. вҖңYou told me all this had nothing to do with He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named, remember? Well вҖ”вҖқ
вҖңIt was a clue, sir,вҖқ said Dobby, his eyes widening, as though this was obvious. вҖңWas giving you a clue. The Dark Lord, before he changed his name, could be freely named, you see?вҖқ
вҖңRight,вҖқ said Harry weakly. вҖңWell, IвҖҷd better go. ThereвҖҷs a feast, and my friend Hermione should be awake by now. вҖҰвҖқ
Dobby threw his arms around HarryвҖҷs middle and hugged him.
вҖңHarry Potter is greater by far than Dobby knew!вҖқ he sobbed. вҖңFarewell, Harry Potter!вҖқ
And with a final loud crack, Dobby disappeared.
Harry had been to several Hogwarts feasts, but never one quite like this. Everybody was in their pajamas, and the celebration lasted all night. Harry didnвҖҷt know whether the best bit was Hermione runВӯning toward him, screaming вҖңYou solved it! You solved it!вҖқ or Justin hurrying over from the Hufflepuff table to wring his hand and apologize endlessly for suspecting him, or Hagrid turning up at half past three, cuffing Harry and Ron so hard on the shoulders that they were knocked into their plates of trifle, or his and RonвҖҷs four hundred points for Gryffindor securing the House Cup for the second year running, or Professor McGonagall standing up to tell them all that the exams had been canceled as a school treat (вҖңOh, no!вҖқ said Hermione), or Dumbledore announcing that, unВӯfortunately, Professor Lockhart would be unable to return next year, owing to the fact that he needed to go away and get his memВӯory back. Quite a few of the teachers joined in the cheering that greeted this news.
вҖңShame,вҖқ said Ron, helping himself to a jam doughnut. вҖңHe was starting to grow on me.вҖқ
The rest of the final term passed in a haze of blazing sunshine. Hogwarts was back to normal with only a few, small differences вҖ” Defense Against the Dark Arts classes were canceled (вҖңbut weвҖҷve had plenty of practice at that anyway,вҖқ Ron told a disgruntled Hermione) and Lucius Malfoy had been sacked as a school goverВӯnor. Draco was no longer strutting around the school as though he owned the place. On the contrary, he looked resentful and sulky. On the other hand, Ginny Weasley was perfectly happy again.
Too soon, it was time for the journey home on the Hogwarts ExВӯpress. Harry, Ron, Hermione, Fred, George, and Ginny got a comВӯpartment to themselves. They made the most of the last few hours in which they were allowed to do magic before the holidays. They played Exploding Snap, set off the very last of Fred and GeorgeвҖҷs Filibuster fireworks, and practiced disarming each other by magic. Harry was getting very good at it.
They were almost at KingвҖҷs Cross when Harry remembered something.
вҖңGinny вҖ” what did you see Percy doing, that he didnвҖҷt want you to tell anyone?вҖқ
вҖңOh, that,вҖқ said Ginny, giggling. вҖңWell вҖ” PercyвҖҷs got a girlfriend.вҖқ
Fred dropped a stack of books on GeorgeвҖҷs head.
вҖңWhat?вҖқ
вҖңItвҖҷs that Ravenclaw prefect, Penelope Clearwater,вҖқ said Ginny. вҖңThatвҖҷs who he was writing to all last summer. HeвҖҷs been meeting her all over the school in secret. I walked in on them kissing in an empty classroom one day. He was so upset when she was вҖ” you know вҖ” attacked. You wonвҖҷt tease him, will you?вҖқ she added anxВӯiously.
вҖңWouldnвҖҷt dream of it,вҖқ said Fred, who was looking like his birthday had come early.
вҖңDefinitely not,вҖқ said George, sniggering.
The Hogwarts Express slowed and finally stopped.
Harry pulled out his quill and a bit of parchment and turned to Ron and Hermione.
вҖңThis is called a telephone number,вҖқ he told Ron, scribbling it twice, tearing the parchment in two, and handing it to them. вҖңI told your dad how to use a telephone last summer вҖ” heвҖҷll know. Call me at the DursleysвҖҷ, okay? I canвҖҷt stand another two months with only Dudley to talk to. вҖҰвҖқ
вҖңYour aunt and uncle will be proud, though, wonвҖҷt they?вҖқ said Hermione as they got off the train and joined the crowd thronging toward the enchanted barrier. вҖңWhen they hear what you did this year?
вҖңProud?вҖқ said Harry. вҖңAre you crazy? All those times I couldвҖҷve died, and I didnвҖҷt manage it? TheyвҖҷll be furious. вҖҰвҖқ
And together they walked back through the gateway to the Muggle world.
